## Phase 8: Standard Library — Floor

> **Note on phase split (2026-04-29):** roadmap.md splits stdlib work across Phase 8 (floor — universal modules every program needs) and [Phase 11](#phase-11-standard-library--long-tail) (long-tail — numerical/data-science stack, security types, embedded primitives, codegen IR optimization). v1 release = end of Phase 11. The items below mix floor and long-tail because this working tracker predates the split — the **`### Numerical and data-science stdlib`** sub-section and the embedded-primitives / `std.secret` items belong to Phase 11; everything else is floor (Phase 8). The roadmap.md phase headings are the authoritative split.

> **v64 reshape (2026-05-09):** the backend platform stdlib bundle (`std.http`, TLS, WebSocket, `std.tracing`, HTTP/2, `std.regex`, `std.process`, protobuf, `Pool[T]`, backpressure primitives) was lifted from Phase 11 long-tail into Phase 8 floor under the [backend-first lead-persona decision](../../brainstorming/archive/v64_backend_first_v1_concurrency.md). Tracked under § Backend Platform (v64-lifted) below.

### Backend Platform (v64-lifted)

> Lifted from Phase 11 under the v64 backend-first decision (2026-05-09). Spec at [`design.md § v1 Positioning — Backend-First`](../design.md#v1-positioning--backend-first); roadmap pointer at [`roadmap.md § Phase 8 > Backend Platform`](../roadmap.md#backend-platform-v64-lifted).

- [ ] **P0 — `std.http` (HTTP/1.1 server + client) — stable v1 surface + `#[unstable]`-gated extensions.** Stable surface: `Server::bind` / `Server::serve` / `Request` / `Response` / `Client::get` / `Client::post`, body streaming, header manipulation, basic routing, keep-alive, chunked transfer, Host routing. Advanced surface (gated `#[unstable]` per [syntax.md § 8](../syntax.md#8-attributes)): connection-level customization, custom transport, low-level frame access. Pre-lock audit of API shape against Go `net/http`, Rust `hyper` + `axum`, Node `http` for known footguns (Go middleware composition, Rust body-ownership in handlers, Node error propagation through promise chains). Effects: `sends(Network)` / `receives(Network)` on every call into the network surface; routes through the event loop via Phase 6.3.
  - [x] **Request inbound-header read — `Request.header(name) -> Option[String]`.** Case-insensitive lookup per RFC 7230 § 3.2. Runtime extern `karac_runtime_http_request_header(req, name_ptr, name_len) -> *const c_char` (null on miss; runtime-owned cstring on hit — explicitly-empty header values return a zero-length cstring, not null, so `Some("")` is distinguishable from `None`). Codegen `compile_request_header` PHI-merges a strlen+malloc+memcpy String aggregate into `Option[String]`; interpreter mirrors the type shape (always `None` for the interpreter's stub Request value). Tests: typechecker (`test_http_request_header_ok`), interpreter (`test_server_serve_handler_request_header_returns_none`), three E2E round-trips in `tests/http_server.rs` covering present / case-insensitive / absent.
  - [x] **`Request.headers()` and `Request.query()` (full-map iteration) — `-> Vec[(String, String)]`.** Both return a `Vec` (not a `Map`) so repeated header names and duplicate query keys (`?a=1&a=2`) survive in request order. `headers()` walks the parallel `headers_keys` / `headers_vals` arrays hyper already populates (names hyper-normalized lowercase); `query()` reads percent-decoded (`+` → space, `%XX`) pairs the runtime parses once at request-translation time into new `query_keys` / `query_vals` arrays on `KaracHttpRequest` (`parse_query_pairs` + `decode_form_component`, lenient on malformed `%`). Six indexed FFI accessors (`karac_runtime_http_request_{headers,query}_count` + `_{header,query}_{key,val}_at`); codegen `compile_request_pairs` drives a counted loop building a `Vec[(String, String)]`, copying each borrowed cstring into a fresh owned String (`build_owned_string_from_cstr`, same per-call ownership contract as `header(name)`) so the Vec outlives the request struct. Interpreter mirrors the shape (empty Vec on the stub Request). Tests: 6 runtime parser units, typechecker (`test_http_request_headers_ok` / `_query_ok`), interpreter (`test_server_serve_handler_request_headers_and_query_return_empty`), two E2E round-trips in `tests/http_server.rs` (`_iterates_headers` proves both the custom + Host header iterate; `_reads_query_param` proves `+`-decode + multi-param). NB: the E2E handlers use `==` comparisons; building result strings by concatenation also works now that the `String + String` typechecker gap this surfaced is fixed (see the dedicated § entry below).
  - [x] **Server response-header manipulation — handler-set response headers.** Shipped via a positional-third-field convention on the user's `Response` struct: if the handler returns `Response { status, body, headers: Vec[(String, String)] }`, codegen's `emit_http_handler_shim` extracts field 2 and emits one `karac_runtime_http_response_set_header` call per pair. The 2-field shape `Response { status, body }` continues to work unchanged — the shim's field-count check skips the headers loop when the struct has fewer than three fields. Runtime: new `karac_runtime_http_response_set_header` extern accumulates pairs into a thread-local `PENDING_RESPONSE_HEADERS` staging buffer; `serve_request`'s `invoke` closure drains it before returning, and feeds the headers to `hyper::Response::builder`. User-set `Content-Type` overrides the smoke-path default `application/json`; other defaults are not added. Both `karac_runtime_serve_http` and `karac_runtime_serve_https` share `serve_request`, so HTTPS automatically picks this up. Test: `tests/http_server.rs::test_server_serve_handler_sets_response_headers` returns three headers (X-Custom-Header, X-Trace-Id, Content-Type) and a sync TCP client parses them back. Not in scope here: a fluent `Response.builder()` surface, structured header types, multi-value headers — all additive future work.
  - [x] **Basic routing + Host routing — manual dispatch ratified at v1.** Design call resolved: `Server.serve(handler)` continues to hand every request to one user-supplied handler, which dispatches manually on `req.path()` / `req.method()` / `req.header("host")`. No stdlib router primitive at v1. **Rationale.** (1) The TLS / HTTPS / Request / Response surfaces shipped above expose every input a router needs (path, method, host, query, headers); a stdlib router would be a thin layer of conveniences, not a load-bearing primitive — and once shipped it would be hard to evolve without breaking. (2) Precedent: Go's `net/http` core is the same shape — `ServeMux` is a thin add-on, and production code typically pulls in a community router (chi, gorilla/mux, echo, axum-style trait routing in Rust) chosen to fit the workload. Kāra's package ecosystem is the right venue for those, not the stdlib floor. (3) v1's launch focus is the *backend platform* (HTTPS, WebSocket, std.tracing, Pool, std.process, etc.), and a router is the most easily-replaced surface among those — pulling it in would slow v1 without unblocking real demos. **Karac-new template (line 28).** Will scaffold a small `match req.path() { … }` dispatch table in its default `Server.serve(handler)` body so new projects see the manual-dispatch shape immediately. **Post-v1 path.** A `Router` primitive (path patterns + method match + Host vhost) can land additively once a real consumer signal materializes; tracked at `deferred.md § Router` when the demand exists. Parent line 11's "basic routing + Host routing" claim remains true: those capabilities ARE available — just via direct accessors rather than a stdlib router type.
  - [x] **keep-alive + chunked transfer — verified hyper-provided.** Split out from the original "keep-alive + chunked + streaming" umbrella (streaming is the genuinely-absent piece — see the new sub-entry below). hyper's `http1` connection handles both persistent connections and chunked request/response framing at the protocol layer transparently; nothing in `serve_request` adds plumbing for either. The previous smoke tests used `Connection: close` + fixed `Content-Length` so neither was exercised. Two new E2E tests pin both: `test_server_serve_handler_keep_alive_persistence` opens one TCP socket, issues two HTTP/1.1 GETs (first without `Connection: close`, second with), parses each response with `Content-Length` framing, and asserts both round-trip with the right echoed path — proves the server holds the connection open across requests. `test_server_serve_handler_chunked_request_body_decode` POSTs a `Transfer-Encoding: chunked` body of two chunks (`"hello"` + `" world"`); the handler echoes `req.body()` and the test asserts the response body is `"hello world"` — proves hyper assembles chunks before the handler sees them, and that `serve_request`'s `body.collect().await` pipeline handles chunked framing correctly. No runtime / codegen changes needed.
  - [ ] **Body streaming — incremental request reads + chunked / streamed response writes.** Genuinely absent: `serve_request` drains the entire request body into `bytes::Bytes` before invoking the handler, and the response is a fixed `Full<Bytes>`. For large / long-lived bodies (file uploads, server-sent events, long-polling, gRPC streaming, …) the handler needs to read the request body incrementally and write the response body incrementally too. Surface design open: (a) extend the `Request` opaque pointer with `req.read_chunk(buf)` / `req.read_to_end(buf, max)` style methods and replace the body's eager-collect path with a chunked pull; (b) replace `Response { status, body, headers }`'s `body: String` field with a writer-handle that the handler can `.write(bytes)` / `.flush()` on, feeding hyper's `http_body_util::StreamBody` or equivalent. Both halves need cancel-safety analysis (state-machine yields between read/write rounds preserve handler position). Deferred until a real consumer signals demand — the fixed-Full-body path covers the v1 backend-first launch demos (Demo 1 uses WebSocket frames, Demo 3 is a data pipeline). Tracked separately in `deferred.md § HTTP body streaming` if/when the trigger fires.
  - [x] **`Client.get` / `Client.post` — real network client.** Shipped end-to-end across runtime + codegen, 2026-05-29. Both `Client.new().get(url)` and `.post(url, body)` compile against `karac build` and resolve `Result[Response, HttpError]` with the runtime's actual network response (success → `Ok(Response { status, body })`, transport failure → `Err(HttpError { message })`). E2E pin: `tests/http_server.rs::test_client_get_end_to_end_against_rust_origin` spawns a Rust-side one-shot origin, compiles a karac client binary that does `Client.new().get(url)` against it, and asserts the binary's stdout contains the echoed body. Slice breakdown below.
    1. **Runtime FFI via `ureq`.** Shipped. `ureq = { version = "2", default-features = false, features = ["tls"] }` added to `runtime/Cargo.toml` (pulls rustls + `ring` — matches the runtime's existing crypto posture; `json` feature dropped from the originally-specced set, not needed for v1). Two externs landed in `runtime/src/lib.rs`: `karac_runtime_http_client_get(url_ptr, url_len, out_status, out_body_ptr, out_body_len, out_err_ptr, out_err_len)` and `_post` with the additional `body_ptr, body_len` input pair. Status discriminant: `> 0` = HTTP transaction completed, `0` = transport error. Body / error-message buffers are libc::malloc-allocated so the Kāra-side `String { data, len, cap }` Drop frees them via plain `free(data)`; `cap = len` convention pinned by the runtime's tightly-packed copy. 3 runtime unit tests cover GET success, GET transport error (ECONNREFUSED via drop-the-listener), and POST round-trip with body forwarding.
    2. **Codegen `Client.get` / `Client.post` dispatch.** Shipped. Both externs declared in `Codegen::new`. `Client.new()` lands as an `assoc_call.rs` arm returning the empty-struct undef so `let c = Client.new()` populates `var_type_names[c] = "Client"`. Method dispatch in `src/codegen/method_call.rs` routes Client-receivers to `compile_client_http_method` in `src/codegen/http.rs`: alloca 5 out-param slots, extract URL (and body) String `(ptr, len)`, call the extern, branch on `status > 0`. **Result-payload packing — corrected from original spec.** Result is a 5-word `{tag, w0, w1, w2, w3}` aggregate; Ok arm packs `Response { status, body }` as `w0=status, w1=body.data, w2=body.len, w3=body.cap`; Err arm packs `HttpError { message }` as `w0=msg.data, w1=msg.len, w2=msg.cap, w3=0`. The original spec said "w0 zeroed, message at w1..w3" — that was wrong: `pattern_payload_word_count` for `e: HttpError` slices the first 3 payload words for the `{ String }` shape, so the destructure expects `data, len, cap` to start at w0, not w1. Three IR-grep tests in `tests/http_client_codegen.rs` pin the wiring.
    3. **Struct-type seed + Response/HttpError accessors.** Shipped via two surfaces, not the originally-specced "remove `#[compiler_builtin]` + add field-access body" path. (a) `seed_builtin_struct_types` in `src/codegen/declarations.rs` registers `Client`, `Response { status: i64, body: String }`, and `HttpError { message: String }` in `struct_types` — baked stdlib structs don't reach codegen's `declare_structs` pass (only user `program.items` do), so `pattern_payload_word_count` for `Ok(resp)` / `Err(e)` was falling back to the i64-default and truncating multi-word payloads to a single i64. The seed lets the pattern destructure rebuild the right-shaped LLVM aggregate. (b) `compile_response_accessor` / `compile_http_error_message` in `src/codegen/http.rs` emit method-call → struct-field translation: `status` is a primitive i64 GEP+load; `body` / `message` route through `karac_string_clone` so the caller's String doesn't alias the receiver's field. (c) `reconstruct_payload_value` in `src/codegen/control_flow_match.rs` extended to walk nested struct fields per word-count (was hard-coded to 1 i64 word per LLVM field; now handles the `{ ptr, i64, i64 }` String aggregate embedded in `Response.body` / `HttpError.message`). The `#[compiler_builtin]` attribute stays — removing it would require stdlib impl-block bodies to reach codegen, which they don't.
    4. **E2E test.** Shipped as a single-process variant of the originally-specced two-process design: `tests/http_server.rs::test_client_get_end_to_end_against_rust_origin` spawns a Rust-side `std::net::TcpListener` in a background thread that responds to one request with a fixed `200 OK / Content-Length: 18 / hello-from-origin` canned response. The karac client binary calls `Client.new().get("http://127.0.0.1:<port>/test")`, destructures `Ok(resp)`, and prints `resp.body()`. Test asserts stdout contains `hello-from-origin`. The single-process variant covers the same code paths as the originally-proposed two-binary build (compile + link + run karac client; HTTP round-trip through `ureq`; pattern destructure on `Result[Response, HttpError]`; deep-clone via `karac_string_clone`; `println` on the resulting String) without the per-test cost of building a second karac server binary.
    5. **Doc split for the deferred surface.** Carved out into separate `[ ]` sub-entries below the parent so they're tracked but don't gate the v1 get/post minimum: chained header/body/timeout builders; `Request.send()`; `Response.text()` / `.bytes()` (string-vs-bytes return-type split); `Response.header(name)` (needs Response to carry headers); TLS / public-CA trust (the `webpki-roots` default the parent line-22 already deferred to a follow-on once `Client.get("https://...")` lands — that follow-on is now this entry's responsibility, since `Client.get` is shipped). See the dedicated `[ ]` sub-entries for each.
  - [x] **`Client` chained header / body / timeout builders.** Shipped 2026-05-29 via the both-signatures option: eager `Client.get(url)` / `Client.post(url, body)` (line 22) stay unchanged, and a new `Client.request(method, url) -> RequestBuilder` entrypoint returns a chained-builder descriptor. Surface: `c.request("GET", url).header(name, value).body(b).timeout(ms).send() -> Result[Response, HttpError]`. The chained methods are `self`-by-value (owned-self mirror of `Command.arg` / `.env`); `.send()` consumes the builder. **Implementation shape — opaque-handle, not value-typed.** `RequestBuilder { handle: i64 }` wraps a runtime-side `HTTP_BUILDERS: Mutex<HashMap<i64, BuilderState>>` entry; each chained Kāra method routes through a `karac_runtime_http_builder_*` extern that mutates the state by handle and returns the same handle wrapped in a fresh struct value. Owned-self semantics on the Kāra side, shared state on the runtime side. `.send()` removes the entry on every code path so handles are bounded; abandoned builders leak their runtime entry until process exit (a known v1 limitation resolved when `impl Drop for RequestBuilder` becomes wired through codegen). Slice breakdown below.
    1. **Runtime FFI — 5 handle-based externs.** `runtime/src/lib.rs`. `karac_runtime_http_builder_new(method_ptr, method_len, url_ptr, url_len) -> i64` mints a positive handle (or `0` on alloc failure — downstream `_builder_*` calls treat that as a no-op entry); `_builder_add_header(handle, key_ptr, key_len, val_ptr, val_len)` appends to the headers Vec; `_builder_set_body(handle, body_ptr, body_len)` replaces the body bytes; `_builder_set_timeout(handle, ms)` configures the request deadline; `_builder_send(handle, *mut i64 status, *mut *mut u8 body_ptr, *mut i64 body_len, *mut *mut u8 err_ptr, *mut i64 err_len)` drives the configured request through `ureq::request(method, url).set(...).timeout(...).call() / .send_bytes(body)` and removes the entry. Same out-param ownership convention as `_client_get` (libc::malloc'd buffers freed by Kāra-side String Drop; `status > 0` discriminant). Unknown handle on `_builder_send` yields a descriptive transport-error message via the err_ptr buffer. 1 runtime unit test (`test_http_builder_send_consumes_handle_and_round_trips_state`) pins both the round-trip (origin sees POST + custom header + body) and the entry-lifecycle invariant (second send with the same handle yields unknown-handle err). The earlier-shipped flat-args `karac_runtime_http_client_send` extern also stays (3 unit tests) — exercises the same ureq paths via a different ABI, useful as a sanity backstop.
    2. **Stdlib — `RequestBuilder` + impl block.** `runtime/stdlib/http.kara`. Single-field `struct RequestBuilder { handle: i64 }` declared above `impl Client` so the `Client.request(...)` signature finds it at impl-block registration time. `impl Client` gains `request(ref self, method: String, url: String) -> RequestBuilder` (`#[compiler_builtin]`, stub body). `impl RequestBuilder` declares all four chained methods as `#[compiler_builtin]` (no real Kāra body — codegen lowers each, see slice 4): `header(self, name, value) -> RequestBuilder`, `body(self, b) -> RequestBuilder`, `timeout(self, ms) -> RequestBuilder`, `send(ref self) -> Result[Response, HttpError]`. `RequestBuilder` added to `PRELUDE_TYPES` in `src/prelude.rs` so user code can name the type without a `use`. `baked_http_carries_inherent_impl_with_compiler_builtin_methods` test extended to assert the new methods exist with `#[compiler_builtin]`.
    3. **Typechecker — hardcoded dispatch for the stdlib HTTP types.** `src/typechecker/stdlib_io.rs::infer_http_client_method` extended with a `"request"` arm returning `RequestBuilder`; new `infer_http_request_builder_method` handles `header` / `body` / `timeout` / `send` with the right return types and arg-count checks. `src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs::infer_method_call`'s hardcoded `Client` / `Response` / `HttpError` dispatch arm (~line 1410) extends to also dispatch `RequestBuilder` — necessary because `register_baked_stdlib` does register the impl block but the resolved-method-dispatch fallthrough returns `Type::Error` for prelude types (the lax-fall-through rule in `is_user_defined`), so the chained `.send()`'s `Result[Response, HttpError]` return type would never reach `pattern_binding_types` and the `Ok(resp)` arm's `resp.body()` would miss the Response-dispatcher arm in codegen. The hardcoded path is the same pattern Client/Response/HttpError already use; adding RequestBuilder restores type propagation.
    4. **Codegen — handle-based lowerings + non-identifier-receiver path.** `src/codegen/declarations.rs::seed_builtin_struct_types` adds `RequestBuilder { handle: i64 }` to `struct_types` (same seeding rationale as Client/Response/HttpError). `src/codegen.rs::Codegen::new` declares the 5 `karac_runtime_http_builder_*` externs. `src/codegen/http.rs` adds three lowerings: `compile_client_request_builder` (extracts method + url Strings, calls `_builder_new`, packs the handle into a fresh `RequestBuilder` aggregate); `compile_request_builder_setter` (handles `header` / `body` / `timeout` — loads the handle from the receiver's slot, extracts the arg payloads, calls the matching `_builder_*` extern, and returns the receiver unchanged); `compile_request_builder_send` (loads the handle, allocates the 5 out-param slots, calls `_builder_send`, then packs the result into `Result[Response, HttpError]` using the same `{tag, status, body.data, body.len, body.cap}` layout as `compile_client_http_method`'s Ok/Err arms). `src/codegen/method_call.rs::compile_method_call` adds two dispatch surfaces: an identifier-receiver arm matching `var_type_names == "RequestBuilder"` for the let-binding case (`let r = c.request(...); r.send()`); and a non-identifier-receiver arm right before the dispatch-fail Err that detects `RequestBuilder`-shaped struct values returned from chained calls, stashes them in a synthesized alloca, registers the synth name in `var_type_names`, and re-dispatches through the identifier path — necessary because `c.request(...).header(...).timeout(...).send()` has each call's receiver as the prior call's `ExprKind::MethodCall` return value, not an identifier.
    5. **Tests.** 3 IR-grep codegen tests in `tests/http_client_codegen.rs`: `test_ir_http_builder_runtime_ffis_declared` pins the 5 extern declarations; `test_ir_request_builder_chain_dispatches_through_handle_ffi` pins the full chain (`_builder_new` + `_add_header` + `_set_timeout` + `_builder_send` calls in `main`, plus the `rb.send.ok` / `rb.send.err` branch labels from the Result packing); `test_ir_request_builder_body_dispatches_to_set_body_ffi` pins the `.body(...)` arm distinctly. 1 E2E smoke test in `tests/http_server.rs::test_client_request_builder_chain_end_to_end`: spawns a capturing Rust origin, compiles + runs a karac client binary that does `c.request("GET", url).header("X-Trace-Id", "trace-zzz").send()`, asserts both stdout (`hello-from-origin` round-trips through `Ok(resp).body()`) and the captured wire bytes (origin observed `x-trace-id: trace-zzz`). Runtime-side: 1 new unit test (above) plus 3 earlier-shipped `karac_runtime_http_client_send` tests stay as ABI-symmetry coverage for the flat-args path that the handle-based externs wrap.
    
    Known v1 limitations carved as separate `[ ]` follow-ups: (a) handle leak when send is never called — needs `impl Drop` codegen wiring; tracked alongside the broader Drop-codegen story. (b) Other chained-client surface (`Response.text()` / `.bytes()` split, `Response.header(name)`, public-CA trust default, `#[unstable]` advanced surface) — see the dedicated sub-entries below.
  - [x] **`Response.text()` / `.bytes()` — return-type split.** Shipped 2026-05-30 via the **single-buffer, raw-byte capture** approach (not the originally-specced parallel `karac_runtime_http_client_get_bytes` FFI). Surface mirrors Python `requests` / Rust `reqwest`: `Response.text() -> String` (string view of the entity; `.body()` retained as its alias from line 18), and `Response.bytes() -> Vec[u8]` (raw-byte view that does NOT go through UTF-8 validation, so image / protobuf / file-transfer payloads survive intact). **Key realization — one buffer, two views.** `String` and `Vec[u8]` share the same `{ptr, len, cap}` codegen aggregate and both scope-exit cleanups `free(data)` identically, so `.text()` and `.bytes()` need no separate fetch: they reinterpret the single entity buffer the `Response` already carries, differing only in surface type. The only required change was making that buffer hold *raw* bytes — pre-fix all four client fetch sites ran `resp.into_string().unwrap_or_default()`, which collapsed any non-UTF-8 body to empty, so `.bytes()` on a binary response would have surfaced nothing. Slice breakdown below.
    1. **Runtime — raw-byte capture.** `runtime/src/lib.rs`. New `read_response_body_bytes(resp) -> Vec<u8>` reads the entity via `resp.into_reader().read_to_end(...)` (no UTF-8 validation; lenient on mid-stream read error, mirroring `unwrap_or_default`'s stance). All four `into_string().unwrap_or_default()` body-capture sites — `karac_runtime_http_client_get` / `_post` / `_client_send` (flat-args) / `_builder_send` — now route through it. `Response.text()` / `.body()` reinterpret the buffer as a `String` verbatim (valid UTF-8 for the common text response, raw bytes otherwise — matching reqwest's lossy-`text` posture; no behavior change for text responses since their bytes are already valid UTF-8). 1 runtime unit test (`test_http_client_get_returns_raw_bytes_for_non_utf8_body`) pins that a `0xFF 0xFE 0x00 0x41` body survives as 4 bytes rather than collapsing to empty.
    2. **Stdlib — `impl Response`.** `runtime/stdlib/http.kara`. Added `fn text(ref self) -> String` and `fn bytes(ref self) -> Vec[u8]` (both `#[compiler_builtin]`, stub bodies `""` / `Vec.new()`); `body()` stays as the `text()` alias. `baked_http_carries_inherent_impl_with_compiler_builtin_methods` extended to assert both.
    3. **Typechecker.** `src/typechecker/stdlib_io.rs::infer_http_response_method`: `body | text` → `String`, `bytes` → `Vec[u8]` (`Type::Named { "Vec", [u8] }`). The hardcoded `Response` dispatch arm in `expr_method_call.rs` already routes here, so no change there. The `Vec[u8]` return flows through the existing `record_pattern_inner_type` → `pattern_binding_types`/`_inner_types` path, so `let b = resp.bytes()` registers `b` in codegen's `vec_elem_types` the same way `Request.headers()`'s `Vec` return already does.
    4. **Codegen.** `src/codegen/method_call.rs` dispatch arm extended to `status | body | text | bytes`; `src/codegen/http.rs::compile_response_accessor` routes `body | text | bytes` through the existing `clone_string_field` (`karac_string_clone`-backed deep clone of field 1). No new lowering — the clone is layout-identical for both view types; the binding's surface type (String vs `Vec[u8]`) comes from the typechecker, and the `Vec[u8]` drop frees the cloned buffer via the same libc `free` the String drop uses (verified ASAN-clean by the existing string-clone + vec-free sanitizer coverage, and end-to-end by the E2E binary exiting clean).
    5. **Interpreter.** `src/interpreter/method_call_http.rs`: `body | text` return the body String; `bytes` returns a `Vec[u8]` array of the body's UTF-8 bytes (best-effort parity — the interpreter captures bodies via `into_string`, so true binary preservation is codegen-only). Pinned by the existing `test_http_response_methods`.
    6. **Tests.** Runtime unit (above); codegen IR-grep (`test_ir_response_text_and_bytes_clone_entity_buffer` — both methods compile + emit ≥2 `karac_string_clone` calls); E2E (`tests/http_server.rs::test_client_get_bytes_end_to_end_binary_body` — origin returns invalid-UTF-8 bytes, karac binary does `resp.bytes()` and prints `len() == 4`, proving raw bytes survive the full client→Result-destructure→accessor→`Vec[u8]`-bind→drop path).
  - [x] **`Response.header(name) -> Option[String]`.** Shipped 2026-05-30 via the **Result-widening + side-table-handle** approach. `Response.header(name)` does a case-insensitive (RFC 7230 §3.2) lookup of a response header, returning `Some(value)` on a hit — including on empty-body responses (204 / 301 redirects / 401), where response headers matter most — and `None` on a miss. **Design fork resolved.** `Response` was exactly 4 words (`status` + `body` String `{ptr,len,cap}`), which filled the `Result[Response, HttpError]` payload (w0..w3) exactly — so attaching headers forced a choice: (A) widen the global Result payload + carry a headers handle on `Response`, or (B) a runtime side-table keyed by the body buffer pointer with no ABI change. **Chose A.** B returns `None` for *every* header on a null-body response (the body-ptr key is null) — exactly the redirect/204/401 cases where reading response headers is the point — so it ships a `.header()` that silently lies where it's most used. A blast-radius pass confirmed A is contained: the `Option` 1→3 widening is proven prior art, and par-blocks / drops / pattern destructure / the HTTP packing sites all compute payload width dynamically (`count_fields()` / `pattern_payload_word_count`), so the change is backwards-compatible by construction (narrower Results just carry one unused trailing word; the `?`-operator error-reconstruction reads ≤3 words and needed no change). Slice breakdown below.
    1. **Result widening 4 → 5 payload words.** `src/codegen/declarations.rs`: the seeded `Result[T,E]` LLVM aggregate grew `{tag,w0..w3}` → `{tag,w0..w4}` (`result_payload_words 4 → 5`). The HTTP client packing sites already guarded every payload store with `if total_fields > N` + a zero-fill tail loop, so they absorbed the extra word automatically. `src/codegen/json.rs`'s `Result[Json, JsonError]` Err arm now explicitly zero-fills w4 (`JsonError`'s message `cap`) so the 5-word `Err(e)` destructure reads a deterministic 0 — preserving the historical "cap lost → message leak" behavior — rather than an undef stack word (which would free a garbage-cap buffer under the wider payload). One IR test (`par_codegen::..._result_typed_let_emits_slot_and_cancel_store`) that pinned the literal 5-field Result shape was updated to the 6-field shape.
    2. **Runtime — response-headers side-table.** `runtime/src/lib.rs`: new `HTTP_RESPONSE_HEADERS: Mutex<HashMap<i64, Vec<(String, CString)>>>` + monotonic id. `capture_response_headers(&resp)` reads every header off the live `ureq::Response` (BEFORE `read_response_body_bytes` consumes it) into the table and returns a fresh positive handle; all four fetch sites (`_client_get` / `_post` / `_client_send` / `_builder_send`) gained a trailing `out_headers_handle: *mut i64` out-param, written on the Ok path (`0` on Err). New accessor `karac_runtime_http_response_header(handle, name_ptr, name_len) -> *const c_char` does the case-insensitive lookup (response-side mirror of `_http_request_header`), null on miss / unknown handle. Values stored as `CString` for a stable null-terminated return pointer; entries leak until process exit — the same bounded v1 trade-off as `HTTP_BUILDERS`, resolved when `impl Drop for Response` is wired through codegen. 1 runtime unit test (`test_http_client_get_captures_response_headers_for_lookup`).
    3. **Codegen — hidden `headers` field + accessor.** `seed_builtin_struct_types` grows the (client-only, seeded) `Response` to `{ status: i64, body: String, headers: i64 }`. The stdlib `struct Response` declaration stays 2-field — its methods are all `#[compiler_builtin]`, so the client `Response` is never constructed from a literal and the seed alone drives its codegen layout. The two client packing sites (`compile_client_http_method` / `compile_request_builder_send`) pass a sixth out-param slot and pack the minted handle at w4. New `compile_response_header` loads the handle from Response field 2, calls the runtime accessor, and wraps the borrowed cstring in `Option[String]` via a new shared `build_option_string_from_borrowed_cstr` helper (extracted from `compile_request_header`, now used by both header paths). Dispatch arm added in `compile_method_call` for `Response` + `header` + 1-arg; extern declared in `Codegen::new`.
    4. **Handler-shim guard tightened.** `emit_http_handler_shim`'s positional "field 2 = response headers `Vec[(String,String)]`" convention (phase-8 line 14) now additionally requires field 2 to be a struct aggregate (the Vec shape), so the client `Response`'s new i64 handle field can't be misread as a Vec base pointer should a server handler ever return the seeded client `Response`.
    5. **Surface already present.** The stdlib `impl Response { fn header(ref self, name: String) -> Option[String] }`, the typechecker arm (`infer_http_response_method`'s `"header"` → `Option[String]`), and the interpreter parity arm were all already shipped (stubbed) — this entry wired the codegen + runtime under them.
    6. **Tests.** Runtime unit (above); codegen IR-grep (`test_ir_response_header_dispatches_to_runtime_lookup` — pins the extern decl + dispatch + the `karac_runtime_http_response_header` call); E2E (`tests/http_server.rs::test_client_get_header_end_to_end` — origin returns `X-Custom: custom-value`; the karac binary's `resp.header("x-custom")` resolves it case-insensitively and prints the value, plus the `None` arm for an absent name). Full regression pass green under the widened Result: `cargo fmt --check`, `clippy --all-targets --features llvm -D warnings`, full non-llvm suite, codegen (916) + par_codegen, http_server / http_client_codegen / json, and memory_sanitizer (72 ASAN tests).
    
    Resolved sub-items (a, b done; c is a scope note): (a) **side-table-handle leak — FIXED 2026-05-30 via move-aware Drop.** The seeded client `Response` and `RequestBuilder` now get a synthesized scope-exit Drop (`emit_struct_drop_synthesis` + a new `HttpHandleFree` field kind, guarded on `handle != 0` and on the LLVM field actually being `i64` so a user server-side `Response` whose field 2 is a headers-Vec is never misread) that frees the side-table entry via `karac_runtime_http_response_headers_free` / `karac_runtime_http_builder_free` (idempotent/total removes). This also fixes the latent `Response.body` and `HttpError.message` String leaks (the seeded `Response` / `HttpError` had no Drop at all before; the same synth drop now frees those String fields via the existing Vec logic). Registration: `struct_field_type_names` seeded for `Response` / `RequestBuilder` / `HttpError`; the `Ok(resp)` / `Err(e)` pattern bindings register the `Response` / `HttpError` StructDrop, the `let rb = …` binding auto-registers `RequestBuilder`. An *abandoned chained* builder — `c.request(url).header(...);` discarded as a statement with no `.send()` and no binding (a temporary, which Kāra has no general drop for) — is freed by a targeted `StmtKind::Expr` hook (`expr_is_live_request_builder_temp` detects a `.request(...)`-rooted, not-`.send()`-ed chain and calls `karac_runtime_http_builder_free` on the discarded value's handle; pinned by `test_ir_abandoned_request_builder_frees_handle`). **Move-safety** across every exit site (`let g = f`, match-arm tail, `return`, by-value arg, struct/tuple field) comes from extending the single shared `suppress_source_vec_cleanup_for_arg` to zero the i64 handle on move (so the moved-from value's Drop no-ops) — and from closing a *pre-existing* gap it surfaced: the struct `let g = f` move-suppression only covered Vec/String fields, never struct-level `StructDrop`, so a tracked struct moved via `let g = f` double-freed; now the source struct's heap-field state (caps + handle) is zeroed on that move too (benefits any user struct with heap fields, not just HTTP). Tests: runtime units (`test_http_response_headers_free_removes_entry`, `test_http_builder_free_removes_entry`), codegen IR-grep (`test_ir_response_drop_frees_headers_handle`, `test_ir_http_error_drop_frees_message`), and the double-free/premature-free regression E2E (`test_client_get_header_survives_move_out_of_match` — moves the Response via `let resp2 = resp` then queries `header()`; pins single-free + still-resolves). Full regression green incl. memory_sanitizer (72 ASAN). (b) **`Response.headers() -> Vec[(String, String)]` full-map iteration — shipped 2026-05-30.** Mirror of `Request.headers()`: the side-table value type widened to `(CString, CString)` (so names round-trip as stable pointers); three runtime accessors (`_response_headers_count` + `_response_header_{key,val}_at`); codegen `compile_response_pairs` loads the hidden handle and drives the shared `build_string_pairs_vec` counted loop (extracted from `compile_request_pairs`, now used by request + response surfaces); stdlib `impl Response { fn headers() }` + typechecker `Vec[(String, String)]` arm + interpreter parity. Tests: runtime unit (`test_http_client_get_response_headers_iteration`), codegen IR-grep (`test_ir_response_headers_iterates_via_runtime_accessors`), E2E (`test_client_get_headers_iteration_end_to_end` — origin returns two custom headers, the karac binary `for (k, v) in resp.headers()` round-trips both). (c) **Scope note (not a task):** `Response.header(name)` / `.headers()` are wired for all three real consumer paths — eager `Client.get` / `Client.post` and the chained `RequestBuilder.send`; the flat-args `_client_send` backstop also captures headers but has no codegen consumer (it's a runtime-test-only ABI-symmetry path).
  - [x] **Public-CA trust default (`webpki-roots`).** Shipped 2026-05-30. **Original-premise correction.** The pre-shipped entry claimed `Client.get("https://...")` "works today only if the platform's default CA bundle is reachable via ureq's default rustls config (which is what ships)" — that was wrong. ureq 2.12.1's `tls` feature (`default-features = false, features = ["tls"]`) already pulls `webpki-roots` in transitively and selects the `#[cfg(not(feature = "native-certs"))]` `root_certs()` branch (`ureq-2.12.1/src/rtls.rs:82`), which builds a `RootCertStore` from `webpki_roots::TLS_SERVER_ROOTS`. ureq's own docs (`lib.rs:318-321`) confirm: "When you use rustls (`tls` feature), ureq defaults to trusting webpki-roots, a copy of the Mozilla Root program that is bundled into your program." So HTTPS GETs against any public host *already* worked on stripped images at the head this entry opened against; the premise's failure mode never existed. **What actually shipped — pin the design intent in our code.** Even with the premise corrected, the entry has real value: today we depend on ureq's default behavior staying webpki-roots-based, and a future ureq release flipping to `rustls-native-certs` would silently move us to system CAs. So all 4 ureq client fetch sites in `runtime/src/lib.rs` (`_client_get` / `_post` / `_client_send` / `_builder_send`) now route through a shared `ureq::Agent` returned by a new `http_client_agent()` (cached in a `OnceLock`) whose rustls `ClientConfig` is built explicitly via the same recipe as `runtime/src/tls.rs::build_client_config` — `ring` provider + `with_safe_default_protocol_versions` + `with_root_certificates(RootCertStore { roots: webpki_roots::TLS_SERVER_ROOTS.to_vec() })` + `with_no_client_auth`. New direct dep on `webpki-roots = "0.26"` in `runtime/Cargo.toml` (was transitive via ureq; now also direct so the choice is in our deps, with a comment block citing this entry). Tests: 1 runtime unit (`tests::test_http_client_agent_uses_explicit_webpki_roots_and_is_shared`) asserts the Mozilla bundle is non-empty AND `http_client_agent()` returns the same `&'static` agent across calls (proves OnceLock caching); plus 1 `#[ignore]`'d network test (`tests::test_https_round_trip_against_public_origin`) that does a real `Client.get("https://example.com/")` and asserts a non-zero HTTP status — runs only in the new CI job (next bullet) and locally with `cargo test -- --ignored`. **CI matrix entry** added to `.github/workflows/ci.yml § stripped-image-https`: runs the runtime's test binary in a `rust:alpine` container, builds with `ca-certificates` present (cargo needs it for crates.io fetch), then `apk del ca-certificates` BEFORE the test runs and verifies `/etc/ssl/certs/ca-certificates.crt` is gone, then executes `tests::test_https_round_trip_against_public_origin --include-ignored`. Proves the embedded webpki-roots (not the OS bundle) is what's keeping HTTPS working. All gates green: `cargo fmt --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full http_server + http_client_codegen suites (21 tests). **Observation — pre-existing failure, now fixed.** `cargo test -p karac-runtime --lib event_loop::tests::ffi_round_trip_register_poll_deregister_wake` was failing reproducibly at `runtime/src/event_loop.rs:3372` ("expected at least one fd-readiness wakeup, got 0") on `main` at SHA `e0a76306`; not regressed by this entry. Resolved 2026-05-30 — see [`phase-6-runtime.md` Slice 9f](phase-6-runtime.md) (network-event-loop list entry 15) for root cause + fix.
  - [x] **`#[unstable]` attribute machinery — shipped 2026-05-30.** Prereqs 1–4 from the original blocker landed end-to-end (parser recognition + AST payload, symbol-table sidecar + use-site dispatch, `unstable_api` lint registry entry, `kara.toml` `[lints].allow_unstable_api` opt-in). The shipped surface is **the machinery, not the gated APIs**: connection-level customization / custom transport / low-level frame access remain absent from the stdlib at v1 per the original "not added at v1 even as private types" stance — adding them is now an additive `#[unstable]`-tagged item-by-item decision rather than a missing primitive. Audit pass (original prereq 5) folds into the broader pre-lock API-shape audit below (line 56). Slice breakdown:
    1. **Parser recognition.** `runtime/stdlib`-recognized at `src/attribute_validator.rs::RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES` (new `"unstable"` entry — silences `E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE`). New `Parser::scan_unstable_attr` in `src/parser/items.rs` mirrors `scan_deprecated_attr`'s shape: bare `#[unstable]`, shorthand `#[unstable = "note"]`, long form `#[unstable(note: "...")]`. Unknown named keys (e.g. future `feature` / `issue`) are silently ignored so a future RFC can extend the surface without a source break; positional args emit `E_UNSTABLE_POSITIONAL_ARG`; duplicates emit `E_UNSTABLE_DUPLICATE`. Called from every parser site that calls `scan_deprecated_attr` (13 sites across `src/parser/items.rs` + `src/parser/items_trait.rs`) so the attribute attaches to every item kind that supports `#[deprecated]` — Function, StructDef, UnionDef, EnumDef, EnumVariant, TraitDef, TraitMethod, TraitAliasDef, MarkerTraitDef, ConstDecl, ModuleBinding, TypeAliasDef, DistinctTypeDef. AST: new `Unstable { span, note: Option<String> }` payload in `src/ast/items.rs`; `pub unstable: Option<Unstable>` field added next to every existing `deprecation` field on the same item kinds (13 sites, plus 6 synthetic-construction sites in `prelude.rs`, `test_main_synth.rs`, `cli.rs`, `effectchecker.rs`, `effectchecker/bounds.rs`, `typechecker/items.rs`).
    2. **Symbol-table sidecar.** `src/resolver.rs::SymbolTable` grows a `unstables: HashMap<SymbolId, Unstable>` sidecar (same shape rationale as `deprecations` — out-of-band storage because most symbols carry no annotation). New `record_unstable` / `unstable_for` methods. `src/resolver/collect.rs::record_unstable_if_present` mirrors `record_deprecation_if_present`; called at every `record_deprecation_if_present` site (13 call points, all bundled into the same `Ok(id) => { ... }` arm so the existing 5 inline-Ok-arm sites become blocks).
    3. **Use-site lint emission.** New `TypeErrorKind::UnstableApi` in `src/typechecker.rs`; routed to `DiagnosticClass::LintWarning` and assigned codes `W0255` / `E0255` (when promoted via `#[deny]`). New `TypeChecker::check_unstable_use_at` mirrors `check_deprecated_use_at` (per-span resolution map, falling back to global-scope name lookup). Called from the same five reference-site emission points as deprecated: `expr_ops.rs::infer_identifier` (function-name + constant lookups), `fields.rs` (union-literal + struct-literal sites), `lowering.rs::lower_path_type` (type-position path resolution). The message surfaces the optional `note` and points at both `#[allow(unstable_api)]` (per-item) and `[lints].allow_unstable_api = true` (project-wide).
    4. **`unstable_api` lint registry.** New entry in `src/lints.rs::STARTER_LINTS` with `default_level: LintLevel::Warn` and a description quoting the two opt-in paths. `starter_set_covers_spec_listed_lints` test extended so the registry stays the single source of truth.
    5. **`kara.toml` `[lints]` table.** New `ManifestLints` struct in `src/manifest.rs` (currently one field: `allow_unstable_api: bool`); new `Manifest.lints` field; new `parse_lints_table` recogniser (unknown sub-keys soft-warn so future fields are additive; non-bool values for known keys hard-error so a typo'd `= "true"` surfaces immediately). Two stub-Manifest construction sites in `dep_graph.rs` / `dep_resolver.rs` updated. New `CliLintOverrides::apply_manifest_lints` helper installs a per-name `Allow` for `unstable_api` when the manifest opts in (only when CLI hasn't already named the lint, so explicit `-D unstable_api` still wins). Wired into the typecheck pipeline at three sites: `cmd_check` (line 3460), `cmd_build_project` (line 4466, via a refactored `typecheck_modules(&tree, &lint_overrides)` signature), and `cmd_test` (line 7825, same path). Cascade precedence is preserved: source `#[deny(unstable_api)]` beats the manifest opt-in because the per-item `lint_override_stack` lands earlier than the cascade fall-through to `CliLintOverrides`.
    6. **Tests (45 new across 3 files).** Parser: 9 tests in `tests/parser.rs` covering bare / shorthand / long-form / unknown-key-silently-ignored / struct + enum capture / duplicate-rejection / positional-arg-rejection / `attribute_validator` recognition. Typechecker: 11 tests in `tests/typechecker.rs` covering call-site warning / shorthand-note surfacing / long-form-note surfacing / `#[allow(unstable_api)]` suppression / `#[deny(unstable_api)]` error promotion / non-unstable-fn no-fire / type-position emission / struct-literal emission / const emission / manifest-opt-in suppression / source-deny-beats-manifest-opt-in. Manifest: 4 tests in `tests/manifest.rs` covering `allow_unstable_api = true` lift / absent-table default / non-bool hard-error / unknown-key soft-warn. Plus 1 extension to the `starter_set_covers_spec_listed_lints` registry test in `src/lints.rs`. Two pre-existing `tests/missing_*_lint.rs` test helpers got `unstable: None,` field additions for the `Function` AST struct.

    **Carved follow-ups — the actual gated surfaces the original blocker named are now individually trackable.** The machinery shipped; the *uses* of it are item-by-item additive decisions. None have a current consumer signal — all stay `[ ]` until a real demand surfaces.
    - [ ] **`std.http` connection-level customization — `#[unstable]`-tagged surface.** The canonical `#[unstable]` candidate the parent line 11 names (alongside the line 25 `[unstable]` parent's TLS twin). Surface scope when added: per-connection keep-alive timeout, max-in-flight requests, header-size caps, idle-connection eviction policy — knobs that bypass hyper's defaults. Each method declared `#[unstable]` with a short `note` pointing here. No design lock at v1; ship behind the attribute so the API shape can move without semver concern. Trigger: a user (typically the demo or a downstream consumer) asks for one of the knobs; add only the requested knob, leave the rest unbuilt.
    - [ ] **`std.http` custom transport — `#[unstable]`-tagged surface.** Replacement of the default TCP+hyper transport with a user-supplied `impl Transport` (Unix-domain sockets for sidecar IPC; in-memory for tests; QUIC once HTTP/3 lands). API shape unknown; v1 doesn't have an `Io` trait, so the design needs work first. Trigger: a consumer needs UDS or in-memory transport for testing; pull a minimal `Transport` trait shape from real-usage shape.
    - [ ] **`std.http` low-level frame access — `#[unstable]`-tagged surface.** Direct read/write of HTTP/2 frames (HEADERS, DATA, RST_STREAM, etc.) for advanced consumers (gRPC servers wanting trailers, server-push experiments). Gated on the HTTP/2 entry shipping first (parent line 11 `P1`). Surface stays absent until HTTP/2 lands and a consumer asks; `#[unstable]` from day one when added.
    - [ ] **`std.tls` low-level certificate-verifier customization — `#[unstable]`-tagged surface.** The TLS twin of `std.http` connection-level customization. Canonical example from design.md: custom `ServerCertVerifier` that overrides webpki's default chain walk (pinning a specific leaf cert, opting into hostname-mismatch acceptance for testing, plugging in HSM-backed verification). Today rustls's `dangerous_configuration` feature is the closest equivalent; the Kāra surface would expose a trimmed `impl Verifier` trait `#[unstable]`-tagged. Trigger: a consumer needs cert pinning or HSM integration; today the only opt-out is `NoVerify` in test code (`tests/http_server.rs`), which is acceptable for testing but not for production.
    - [ ] **Stdlib pre-lock `#[unstable]` audit pass (original prereq 5).** Walk every `pub fn` / `pub struct` / `pub enum` in `runtime/stdlib/*.kara` and decide per-item: stable at v1 / `#[unstable]`-tagged / private (drop from the public surface). The machinery now exists; this is the design-review pass that uses it. Output: a one-line stability commitment per public item, materializing as either zero `#[unstable]` tags (if the audit concludes the v1 surface is all stable-ready) or as a delta of additions across `runtime/stdlib/`. Folds into and partially executes the parent line 56 "Public-surface freeze list" sub-bullet — execute that sub-bullet's walk by reading each item and asking "would this carry `#[unstable]`?". Reviewer-gated; no code execution required if the answer is "all stable", just the audit notes.
    - [ ] **User-side `#[unstable]` RFC (post-v1).** Today the parser/resolver/typechecker handle `#[unstable]` on user items as a side-effect of the symbol-table-driven dispatch (a user who tags their own item `#[unstable]` and uses it without `#[allow(unstable_api)]` correctly sees the warning fire — acceptable signal). The spec marks formal user-side use as "future RFC" — questions to settle: should the lint be promoted to `Deny`-by-default for user items (more friction, clearer signal)? should `#[unstable]` carry a `since`-like "first unstable at" version field for SemVer interaction? should the attribute reject placement on `pub(crate)`/private items where stability is meaningless? Defer until v1.x or v2 — no consumer signal at v1, and the current "works incidentally" surface is non-breaking either way.
  - [x] **Pre-lock API-shape audit. RATIFIED 2026-05-31** (formal design-owner sign-off). Prerequisites mostly met — Request reads (lines 12–13), response-header manipulation (line 14), routing (line 15), keep-alive + chunked (line 16a), and the HTTP Client minimum (`Client.get` / `Client.post` core, line 18) are all `[x]`. Remaining open: body streaming (16b, deferred); the additive client surface (chained builders / `Response.text/.bytes` / `Response.header` / public-CA trust, each their own `[ ]` sub-entry below line 18); and the `#[unstable]`-gated surface (line 25). Audit before the v1 API locks; design-review gate (not code) — execution needs a reviewer. **Concrete checklist** (split each entry as findings land):
    - **API surface walk vs three references.** Compare every public type and method against Go `net/http` (the imperative-first baseline), Rust `hyper` + `axum` (the strong-typing baseline), and Node `http` (the ergonomics-first baseline). Decision per item: keep, rename, change shape, or remove.
    - **Footgun-specific reviews** — the three the parent line 11 names:
      - **Go middleware composition** — Go's `http.Handler` middleware composes via wrapping, which has known footguns around handler reuse and request-scoped state. Confirm Kāra's `Server.serve(handler)` shape doesn't ship the same trap (the manual-dispatch v1 answer per line 15 actually sidesteps this — review for v1.x router-primitive plans).
      - **Rust body-ownership in handlers** — hyper's `Body` ownership rules cause borrow-checker friction. Kāra's `Request.body() -> String` (line 13's full-collect path) avoids the friction at v1 by giving the handler an owned String, but the body-streaming follow-on (line 16b) reopens the question. Decide handler-side ownership before streaming ships.
      - **Node error propagation** — Node's promise-chain pattern silently swallows handler errors when not awaited. Kāra's `Result[Response, HttpError]` plus the v1 panic-aborts-process posture (no per-handler recovery) gives an honest fail-loud answer. Document this contrast in the locked API doc.
    - **Effect annotations.** Every public method that touches the network must declare `sends(Network)` / `receives(Network)`; confirm none slipped past unmarked (the audit pass should walk `runtime/stdlib/http.kara` exhaustively). **[x] Walked + bug found & fixed 2026-05-30.** The audit's first concrete pass surfaced a real propagation bug: *the entire `std.http` network surface was invisible to network-effect propagation* — a caller of any HTTP method got an empty inferred network effect set (verified via `karac query effects`, contrasted against `File.open` correctly propagating `reads(FileSystem)`). Two independent root causes: **(1)** the client instance methods (`Client.get` / `Client.post` / `RequestBuilder.send`) — `Client.get`/`post` *were* hand-seeded in `seed_builtin_effects` but the effect-inference walker's `MethodCall` arm resolved instance methods by name only (the `method_bodies` `.ends_with` search + `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP`), neither of which can map `get`/`post`/`send` without tainting `map.get()` / `sender.send()`, so the seed was unreachable; `RequestBuilder.send` wasn't seeded at all. **(2)** the server entry points (`Server.serve` / `serve_tls` / `serve_static`) — `serve`/`serve_tls` *declare* `with sends(Network) receives(Network)` in the stdlib `.kara`, but baked-stdlib `with` clauses are **not** consumed for caller propagation (same reason `File.*` is hand-seeded); `serve_static` had neither a declaration nor a seed. **Why it matters:** phase-6 line 17 (effect-routed task parking) keys the auto-yield state-machine transform off `sends(Network)`/`receives(Network)`; a surface that never emits the effect is invisible to it, to effect-conflict analysis, and to `karac explain` / `query effects`. **Fix (committed under this slice):** (a) the typechecker's hardcoded `Client` / `Response` / `HttpError` / `RequestBuilder` dispatch arm now records the precise `Type.method` callee in `method_callee_types` (it returns early without going through the resolved-method path that records it elsewhere); (b) the effect-inference `MethodCall` arm now consults that precise key (`resolve_method_callee_key`) and pushes it — additive and collision-free, since the typechecker-resolved receiver distinguishes `client.get()` from `map.get()`; (c) `seed_builtin_effects` now seeds all six HTTP methods (`Client.get`/`post`, `RequestBuilder.send`, `Server.serve`/`serve_tls`/`serve_static`) — the `Server.*` static calls resolve by qualified path directly (like `File.open`), so seeding suffices for them. Regression tests: `tests/effectchecker.rs::http_network_effects_propagate_to_callers` (all six methods propagate the `sends`+`receives(Network)` pair to a caller) and `::http_network_effect_resolution_does_not_taint_same_named_methods` (`map.get()` stays Network-free). Full gate green (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm suite, codegen 935 / par_codegen 74 / http_server 21 / http_client_codegen 12 / concurrency 105). **Extended to the full stdlib network surface (TCP / TLS / WebSocket) — follow-up commit, same day.** Continuing the audit walk past `http.kara` into `tcp.kara` / `tls.kara` / `ws.kara` showed the bug was *not* http-specific: every network method there (`TcpListener.accept`, `TcpStream.{read,write,write_all}`; `TlsListener.accept`, `TlsStream.{connect,read,write,write_all}`; `WebSocket.{accept,accept_tls,recv_text,send_text,recv_binary,send_binary,send_text_masked,send_binary_masked}` — 17 methods) *declares* `with sends(Network) receives(Network)` in stdlib but, being baked-stdlib, never propagated it (verified: a caller of `TcpListener.accept()` had an empty inferred effect set). These types have no hardcoded typechecker dispatch arm — they resolve through the normal resolved-method path that already records `method_callee_types` — so the precise `MethodCall` resolution from the http slice reaches them with no typechecker change; the fix is purely extending the `seed_builtin_effects` list to all 17 (the static `WebSocket.accept`/`accept_tls` and `TlsStream.connect` resolve by qualified path, like `File.open` / `Server.*`). `bind` / `bind_tls` / `from_fd` are intentionally excluded — local socket setup, no network round-trip. Regression test `tests/effectchecker.rs::tcp_tls_ws_network_effects_propagate_to_callers` (all 17 via 7 representative callers, exercised both before the seed — confirmed empty — and after). Full gate green again (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm suite, codegen 935 / par_codegen 74 / http_server 21 / http_client_codegen 12 / concurrency 105 / memory_sanitizer 73). Cross-refs: TLS entries (lines 78–79), WebSocket entry (line 92). **Known related quirk (not this slice):** `karac query effects` runs `effectcheck()` *without* `typecheck()`, so `method_callee_types` is empty there and the *tool* still under-reports instance-method network effects (the `build`/`test` pipelines typecheck first, so real compilation is correct); tracked as its own `[ ]` follow-up below.
    - **`Result` vs sentinel returns. [x] DECIDED + MIGRATED 2026-05-30 — unify on `Result`.** The audit found the network-construction surface returned `T { fd: -1 }` sentinels (`TcpListener.bind` / `.accept`, `TlsListener.bind_tls` / `.accept`, `TlsStream.connect`, `WebSocket.accept` / `.accept_tls`) while the same types' `read`/`write` already returned `Result`, and all three references (Rust `io::Result`, Go `(conn, error)`, Node throw/reject) put accept/connect failure in the error channel. Under the no-workarounds policy the `fd: -1` C-ism was migrated to `Result[T, E]`: `bind`/`accept` → `Result[…, TcpError]`, `bind_tls`/`accept`/`connect` → `Result[…, TlsError]`, `WebSocket.accept`/`accept_tls` → `Result[WebSocket, TcpError]`. Codegen packs via a shared `build_fd_construct_result` helper (`Ok(struct{fd})` on `fd >= 0`, else `Err(<E>.<variant>(-1))`); `bind_tls`'s 2-field `TlsListener` uses a dedicated packer that also frees the rustls config on the error path (the old sentinel relied on `Drop` for that). All call sites in `examples/ws_idle_holder` + the tcp/tls/ws test suites migrated to `.unwrap()` / `match`. **Two latent compiler bugs surfaced and fixed by this migration (both their own slices below):** a codegen chained-call span-collision mis-dispatch, and a single-field-struct `Result.Ok` destructure gap. Gates green incl. memory_sanitizer (ASAN) for the fd-close drop path. **Carried follow-up:** the construction FFIs return a bare `-1`, so the `Err` payload errno is always `-1` (information-equivalent to the old sentinel); enriching the runtime FFIs to return `-errno` is a separate `[ ]` below.
    - [x] **Codegen chained-call span-collision mis-dispatch — fixed 2026-05-30 (surfaced by the Result migration).** The parser sets `MethodCall.span == receiver.span`, so in `recv.inner().outer()` the inner and outer calls share one `method_callee_types` key; it resolves to the *inner* call's `Type.method` (the effect-checker relies on that). `compile_method_call`'s compiler-builtin / state-machine dispatch keyed off that span directly, so compiling the `unwrap` of `listener.accept().unwrap()` saw `key == "TcpListener.accept"` and re-lowered `accept` on its own result — a double-lowering + LLVM type mismatch ("Call parameter type does not match function signature"). Before the migration this never fired because yield-bearing network calls returned a bare value (never consumed via `.unwrap()` / `match`). Fix: a `dispatch_key` in `src/codegen/method_call.rs` that requires the resolved key's method segment to equal THIS call's `method` before it drives a builtin/state-machine lowering (the conservative cancel-check still uses the raw key). Sibling typechecker fix: the `method_callee_types` skip for the BUILTIN Option/Result unwrap-family (so the inner effectful key survives) is now gated on the receiver being `Option`/`Result`, not the method *name* — a user `impl X { fn unwrap(self) }` still records its key (regression `use_classifier::tests::owned_self_on_field_consumes_root`).
    - [x] **Single-field-struct `Result.Ok` destructure — fixed 2026-05-30 (surfaced by the Result migration).** `match res { Result.Ok(listener) => … }` where `listener: TcpListener { fd: i32 }` (a one-primitive-field struct) bound `listener` to the raw i64 payload word instead of reconstructing the `{ i32 }` aggregate — the binding slot was sized i64 while `var_type_names` said `TcpListener`, so the next `.method()` extracted a struct field from an i64 and tripped module verification. Multi-field structs (e.g. `Response`) already worked because they span >1 payload word and take the struct-building path. Fix: `reconstruct_payload_value` (`src/codegen/control_flow_match.rs`) routes any struct-typed binding (looked up via `pattern_binding_types` ∩ `struct_types`) through the struct-building path regardless of word count. The five network structs (`TcpListener`/`TcpStream`/`TlsStream`/`WebSocket`/`TlsListener`) are seeded in `seed_builtin_struct_types` (struct_types + field names + field type names) so the destructure resolves their shape; `struct_field_type_names` is safe alongside their user `impl Drop` because all fields are primitive/pointer → `emit_struct_drop_synthesis` returns `None` (no synthesized drop shadows the fd-close).
    - [x] **Network construction errors carry a branchable cause, not bare `-1` — shipped 2026-05-30.** Follow-up to the `Result` migration: `bind` / `accept` / `connect` failures used to surface `Err(TcpError/TlsError.Other(-1))` — the `Result` shape existed but the cause was always `-1`. A `supervised_echo` kata gave the consumer signal (a server that picks another port on `AddrInUse`, a client that retries on `ConnectionRefused`), and prerequisite-building it surfaced that there was no plain-TCP client at all (`TcpStream.connect` shipped first, commit `0ed78d94`). **Design correction to the original "-errno" sketch.** Raw `-errno` is the wrong surface: errno numbers are platform-specific (`EADDRINUSE` is 48 on macOS, 98 on Linux), so a `fd == -48` decode baked into codegen would be wrong on Linux. Instead the runtime maps `std::io::ErrorKind` (which already normalizes the OS errno into platform-independent names) to a small Kāra-stable code space, and codegen decodes the *code*, never a raw errno. **Implementation.** (1) Runtime `net_construct_error_code(&io::Error)` maps `AddrInUse → -2`, `ConnectionRefused → -3`, `PermissionDenied → -4`, everything else `→ -1`; applied at the `bind`/`listen`/`accept`/`connect` failure paths in `karac_runtime_tcp_bind` / `_tcp_accept` / `_tcp_connect` and the TCP-connect leg of `_tls_client_connect` (TLS bind delegates to `_tcp_bind`, inheriting the codes). (2) Stdlib `TcpError` / `TlsError` grew fieldless named variants `AddrInUse` / `ConnectionRefused` / `PermissionDenied`; `Other(i32)` stays the catch-all. (3) `build_fd_construct_result` (codegen) replaced its fixed `Other(-1)` Err packing with a `select` chain decoding the stable code into the matching variant tag, payload = the code sign-extended (meaningful for `Other`, unread for the fieldless variants), falling back to the caller's default variant (`Other` for TCP, `Protocol` for TLS) for any unclassified code — and degrading to "always default" for any future enum lacking the named variants. **Pre-existing gap fixed in passing:** `TcpError` was never in `PRELUDE_TYPES` (only `TlsError` was, from the line-24 work; the read/write surface only ever used `Err(_)`, so naming `TcpError.<variant>` in a `match` was never exercised) — added to scope-0 so its variants are nameable without import. **Pre-existing gap tracked (not fixed):** binding a payload from an enum nested inside `Result.Err` — `match r { Result.Err(TcpError.Other(c)) => … }` — drops the inner binding in codegen (`Undefined variable 'c'`), reproducible with a plain user enum; the line-74 named causes are fieldless so they're unaffected, and the gap is a general match-codegen issue tracked in [`phase-7-codegen.md`](phase-7-codegen.md) (nested enum-payload bind). Tests: runtime units (`net_construct_error_code_maps_io_error_kinds`, `net_construct_error_codes_surface_from_real_syscalls` — closed-port connect → -3, in-use rebind → -2), codegen IR-grep (`test_ir_fd_construct_result_classifies_named_causes`), E2E (`test_tcp_stream_connect_err_is_connection_refused`, `test_tcp_bind_err_is_addr_in_use`). Full gate green (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm + runtime suites, codegen / tcp_stream / tcp_listener / tls_codegen / http_server under llvm, memory_sanitizer ASAN). Closes the consumer arc with the `supervised_echo` kata (kara-katas).
    - **Compose-with-TLS audit.** `Server.serve` and `Server.serve_tls` are parallel; confirm a handler written against one works unchanged against the other (the `Request` / `Response` ABI is transport-independent, but verify no implicit assumption sneaked in).
    - **Public-surface freeze list. [x] DRAFTED 2026-05-30 — reviewer ratification pending.** Every exported item in `runtime/stdlib/http.kara` with a one-line v1 stability commitment. Outcome: the whole surface is **stable v1 except `Server.serve_static`** (the lone `#[unstable]`); no item is dropped to private. **Two pre-lock refinements applied while freezing** (see the Response and serve_static rows): the `Response.text()` alias of `body()` was *removed* (one-name-per-concept), and `status() -> i64` was *locked* (typed `StatusCode` ruled out). The surface is well-formed — the API-walk-vs-three-references pass (above) concluded "mostly keep", and this freeze confirms it.

        | Item | Commitment | Note |
        |---|---|---|
        | `struct Client` / `.new()` | stable v1 | no-arg constructor, matches Go `&http.Client{}` / reqwest `Client::new()` |
        | `Client.get(url)` / `.post(url, body) -> Result[Response, HttpError]` | stable v1 | eager convenience, matches Go `client.Get/Post` |
        | `Client.request(method, url) -> RequestBuilder` | stable v1 | builder entrypoint, matches reqwest |
        | `struct RequestBuilder` / `.header` / `.body` / `.timeout` / `.send` | stable v1 | owned-self chain; `.send() -> Result[Response, HttpError]` |
        | `struct Response` / `.status` / `.body` / `.bytes` / `.header` / `.headers` | stable v1 | **read surface = `body()` + `bytes()`** — the `text()` alias of `body()` was dropped 2026-05-30 (one name per concept; `body()` matches the `body` field server handlers construct, and `text()` implied a charset decode v1 doesn't do). **`status() -> i64` is locked** — the return type can't change non-breakingly, and a bare int matches Go/Node (the imperative-first baseline); a typed `StatusCode` is **off the table** (it would fight the friction-zero positioning), but `is_success()`-style **predicates** are a non-breaking v1.x-additive option |
        | `struct HttpError` / `.message() -> String` | stable v1 | message-only; `.kind()` discrimination is a v1.x-additive candidate, not a freeze blocker |
        | `struct Server` (opaque marker) | stable v1 | |
        | `Server.serve(addr, handler) -> Result[Unit, HttpError]` | stable v1 | matches Go `ListenAndServe` |
        | `Server.serve_tls(addr, cert_pem, key_pem, handler) -> Result[Unit, HttpError]` | stable v1 | PEM-contents (not file paths like Go) — documented divergence |
        | `Server.serve_static(addr, body) -> Result[Unit, HttpError]` | **`#[unstable]`** (decided keep, not remove, 2026-05-30) | strict subset of `serve(handler)`, matches no reference API. Removal was considered (zero real consumers) but **reversed**: it is now load-bearing as the **sole `#[unstable]` baked-stdlib method**, so it is the test specimen for the line-96 `#[unstable]`-baked-method enforcement (3 E2E tests: warn / `#[allow]`-suppress / `#[deny]`-promote). Removing it would delete that coverage or force a synthetic stdlib test fixture — more wart than the mild "two ways to serve a fixed response" cost. Stays `#[unstable]`; revisit at v1 lock only if a real `#[unstable]` consumer appears to take over the canary role |
        | `struct Request` / `.path` / `.method` / `.body` / `.header` / `.headers` / `.query` | stable v1 | matches the request-read surface across all three references |
        | `effect resource Network` | stable v1 | unifies sends + receives per the stdlib `Stdin`/`Stdout`/`FileSystem` shape |

        **`#[unstable]` applied** to `Server.serve_static` in `runtime/stdlib/http.kara` (with a `note` pointing callers to `serve(handler)`). **The tag now enforces** at the call site as of 2026-05-30 — the method / assoc-fn use-site lint gap (the dedicated `[x]` entry below) is closed, so `Server.serve_static(...)` call sites emit an `unstable_api` warning carrying the note, suppressible with `#[allow(unstable_api)]` / `[lints].allow_unstable_api = true` and promotable with `#[deny(unstable_api)]`. The `http_server` smoke suite (21 tests) and the `serve_static` smoke test still pass with the tag applied.

        **Scope note:** this freeze covers `http.kara` (the line-64 audit's subject). The `tcp.kara` / `tls.kara` / `ws.kara` public surfaces are now `Result`-uniform after the construction-method migration (their detailed freeze belongs to the TLS P0 entry, line ~96, when that surface locks).
    - [x] **`#[unstable]` / `#[deprecated]` use-site lint at method / assoc-fn call sites — shipped 2026-05-30.** Surfaced by the `serve_static` `#[unstable]` tagging in the freeze list above. The name-based use-site lint (`check_unstable_use_at` / `check_deprecated_use_at`) fires only from `expr_ops.rs::infer_identifier` (free-fn-name + constant), `fields.rs` (struct/union-literal), and `lowering.rs::lower_path_type` (type-position) — never from a method or associated call, so `#[unstable]` / `#[deprecated]` on a method (including `Server.serve_static`) was inert. Now closed, **unblocking enforcement of the entire `#[unstable]`-tagged-method surface** (lines 58/59/60/61 `std.http` / `std.tls` candidates, the line-62 stdlib audit's per-method tags, and the freeze-list `serve_static` tag). **Investigation correction to the original fix sketch.** The sketch ("thread `method_callee_types` into a check that looks up the method symbol's unstable/deprecation sidecar") was only half-right: it works for *user-authored* impl methods (their attributes land in the symbol-table `unstables`/`deprecations` sidecars via `collect_impl` → `record_unstable_if_present`), but **baked-stdlib methods never reach `collect_impl`** — they live in `STDLIB_PROGRAMS`, walked by the typechecker directly (`register_baked_stdlib` → `env_add_impl`), and `env.impls`' `ImplInfo.methods` stores only `FunctionSig`, which drops the attributes. So `serve_static`'s tag was nowhere in any sidecar. **Implementation (two payload sources, one emitter).** (a) New `prelude::STDLIB_METHOD_STABILITY: LazyLock<HashMap<"Type.method", (Option<Unstable>, Option<Deprecation>)>>` — the baked-stdlib mirror of the symbol-table sidecars, built once from the parsed stdlib AST's impl blocks (any future stdlib stability tag is picked up with no further wiring). (b) New `TypeChecker::check_method_stability(type_name, method, span)` consults the user-method sidecar (`SymbolTable::lookup_method` → `unstable_for` / `deprecation_for`) first, then the baked-stdlib side-table; both routes funnel through the refactored `emit_unstable_warning` / `emit_deprecated_warning` helpers (factored out of the name-based checks so message + cascade are identical). (c) Two call sites: `expr_method_call.rs` for instance methods (`recv.method()` — at the central `method_callee_type_name` resolution point, so the hardcoded HTTP/TCP/TLS/WS arms are covered too) and `expr_ops.rs::resolve_path_type`'s assoc-fn-from-impl arm for static calls (`Type.method()`, which never touches `method_callee_types`). Note the original sketch's `method_callee_types` threading proved unnecessary — `check_method_stability` keys directly off the resolved `(type_name, method)` at each call site, avoiding the chained-call span-collision hazard entirely. Tests: 8 in `tests/typechecker.rs` — baked-stdlib `serve_static` (warn + note, `#[allow]` suppress, `#[deny]` promote), stable stdlib `Server.serve` no-fire, user instance-method `#[unstable]`, user assoc-fn `#[unstable]`, user instance-method `#[deprecated]`, stable user method no-fire. Full gate green (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm suite, codegen + http_server + http_client_codegen + tcp_listener + tls_codegen under llvm). **Known cosmetic gap (not this slice):** `karac check` does not print lint warnings to stderr at all (only errors) — the new warnings live in `TypeCheckResult.warnings` and surface under `karac build` / `test` cascades and the test harness, exactly like every other lint; a `check`-prints-warnings change is a separate diagnostics-surface follow-up, untracked until a consumer wants it.
    
    Execution requires a reviewer (one of the API-design owners). **Ratified 2026-05-31** — the design-owner pass ran and closed clean; all findings had already split into their own tracker entries. Three reversible-before-lock judgment calls were put to the owner and confirmed: (1) **`status() -> i64` locked** — typed `StatusCode` stays off the table, `is_success()`-style predicates remain a v1.x-additive option; (2) **`serve_static` kept `#[unstable]`** — retained as the sole `#[unstable]` baked-stdlib method / line-96 enforcement canary, removal reversed; (3) **`HttpError.kind()` deferred** to a v1.x-additive method, built when a real HTTP-client kata demands error-cause branching (the line-74 `TcpError`-causes precedent). The freeze-list table (lines 78–91) was verified byte-accurate against `runtime/stdlib/http.kara` at sign-off time — no drift between the committed surface and the freeze. No compiler work was blocking; this was the formal sign-off only.

    **Audit walk status (2026-05-30): all six checklist items executed; down to reviewer ratification.** **RATIFIED 2026-05-31** — design-owner sign-off complete (see the gate note below for the three confirmed judgment calls). Entry now `[x]`. (1) *Effect annotations* — found + fixed a real propagation bug across the whole network surface (`[x]`, shipped). (2) *API surface walk vs three references* — drafted, verdict "mostly keep". **Pre-lock surface refinements applied 2026-05-30** (the freeze made concrete): (a) dropped the `Response.text()` alias of `body()` — v1 read surface is `body()` + `bytes()`; (b) locked `status() -> i64` (return-type change is breaking; bare int matches Go/Node) — typed `StatusCode` ruled out, `is_success()`-style predicates remain a v1.x-additive option; (c) `serve_static` **kept** `#[unstable]` (removal reversed — it's the sole `#[unstable]`-baked-method test specimen for line 96). The one genuinely-deferred v1.x-additive candidate is `HttpError.kind()` (adding a method to a struct is non-breaking; build it when a real HTTP-client kata demands error-cause branching, exactly as line 74's `TcpError` causes were kata-driven). Down to formal sign-off. (3) *Footguns* — all three (Go middleware / Rust body-ownership / Node error propagation) answered, documented, no code change. (4) *`Result` vs sentinel* — decided + migrated to `Result` (`[x]`, shipped; surfaced two latent codegen bugs, both fixed). (5) *Compose-with-TLS* — closes clean. (6) *Public-surface freeze list* — drafted (`[x]`): all stable v1 except `Server.serve_static` (`#[unstable]`). Findings split into their own tracked entries: the `#[unstable]`/`#[deprecated]` method-call-lint gap (now `[x]`, shipped 2026-05-30 — `serve_static`'s tag enforces), plus the still-open `query effects` typecheck gap and construction-FFI `-errno` enrichment. The parent stays `[ ]` only for the reviewer's formal ratification of the design-judgment calls (the freeze-list commitments and the keep/rename verdicts) — no further compiler work is blocking it.
- [x] **`karac query effects` runs effect-check without typecheck — under-reports instance-method effects. Fixed 2026-05-30.** Split out of the line 70 effect-annotation audit. `cmd_query`'s `QueryKind::Effects` arm called `pipeline.effectcheck()` directly after `resolve()`, skipping `pipeline.typecheck()`. Because `effectcheck()` sources its `method_callee_types` table from `self.typed` (None when typecheck didn't run), the effect-inference walker's `MethodCall` arm couldn't resolve instance-method callees to their precise `Type.method` key — so `query effects` reported an empty/under-approximated effect set for any function whose effects come through an instance method (`c.get(...)` showed no `Network`, even though the same code under `karac build` / `karac test` correctly propagates it, because those pipelines typecheck before effect-checking). Not a miscompile — codegen is driven by the typechecked pipeline, which is correct — purely a diagnostic-tool accuracy gap. **Fix:** the Effects query now runs `pipeline.typecheck()` + `pipeline.lower()` before `effectcheck()`. **Correction to the original sketch — the `Concurrency` query arm had the *same* defect, not the clean reference the sketch assumed.** The sketch said to mirror "the `Ownership` / `Concurrency` arms that already typecheck first"; on inspection only `Ownership` (and `CostSummary` / `Queries` / `Monomorphization`) typecheck first — `Concurrency` ran `effectcheck()` → `concurrencycheck()` with no typecheck/lower, so concurrency analysis consumed the same under-reported effect set. Both arms are fixed in this slice (typecheck + lower before effectcheck). Reproduced before + after with a `c.get(...)` program: effects went from `inferred_effects:[]` to the `sends`+`receives(Network)` pair; `File.open` (qualified-path, already correct) unchanged. Regression test `tests/cli.rs::test_query_effects_resolves_instance_method_network_effect` runs the real binary end-to-end. Full gate green (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm suite incl. cli + effectchecker).
- [x] **P0 — TLS — vendored rustls + `ring` crypto provider (v1). CLOSED 2026-06-01.** `std.tls` API: cross-platform server + client surface; modern-TLS-only (no SSLv3, no insecure ciphers). `ring` shipped at v1 — see the dedicated § entry below for the aws-lc-rs reconciliation. rustls-provider plug points private at v1 (no public crypto-provider extension API, revisited at v2 if FIPS / post-quantum forces an aws-lc-rs swap).
