Audit posture: rustls + `ring` already audited upstream, but the FFI binding layer + `std.tls` API + verification callbacks + certificate-chain handling + error-mode coverage are new code and need their own audit pass before v1 ship. **CLOSED 2026-06-01:** all five implementation sub-slices (lines 103–107) shipped; the pre-lock new-code audit (line 108) ratified clean by the owner security-reviewer pass; and both carved follow-ups are shipped — the line-124 serve-loop slowloris hardening (`9f7f03da`) and the line-125 raw-`accept` blocking-handshake doc-note (`033d2e18`). No remaining TLS compiler / runtime / audit work blocks v1. (The v2-trigger crypto-provider swap to aws-lc-rs stays tracked in `deferred.md`, gated on FIPS / post-quantum needs.)
  - [x] **Server-side TLS transport — `TlsListener` / `TlsStream` + rustls FFI.** Shipped under [Phase-6 line 236](phase-6-runtime.md) (all 5 sub-slices, 2026-05-27): 7 `karac_runtime_tls_*` externs in `runtime/src/tls.rs` (config-new from PEM, bind, accept+synchronous handshake, read/write/close), `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara` types (`TlsConfig` / `TlsListener.bind_tls` / `TlsListener.accept` / `TlsStream.read`/`write`/`write_all` + `Drop`), codegen lowerings in `src/codegen/tls.rs` + externs in `src/codegen.rs`, `WebSocket.accept_tls` (WS-over-TLS), and 9 runtime unit tests. Crypto provider is rustls 0.23 + `ring`. Server-side only — no client auth, no custom roots. Verified E2E by the Demo 1 `wss://` round-trip.
  - [x] **Client-side TLS transport — `TlsStream.connect` + handshake.** Shipped as a static method on the existing `TlsStream` (no new `TlsClientStream` type — mirrors the `TcpStream` convention where the same stream type carries both directions). `TlsStream.connect(addr, server_name, roots_pem) -> TlsStream`: TCP connect + sync rustls handshake against `server_name` (SNI + cert verification) trusting only the certs in `roots_pem`. No fallback to webpki / system roots at v1 — minimal explicit-PEM posture matching `TlsListener.bind_tls`. Runtime: new `karac_runtime_tls_client_connect` extern; `TlsSession.conn` widened from `ServerConnection` to the `rustls::Connection` enum so the shared per-fd `SESSIONS` map carries both directions and the existing `karac_runtime_tls_read` / `_write` / `_close` paths reuse unchanged (`drive_read` / `drive_write` and `TlsConnIo` in `event_loop.rs` now operate on `rustls::Connection`; both inner variants delegate the called methods). Codegen: extern decl in `Codegen::new`; `lower_tls_stream_connect` in `src/codegen/tls.rs` + dispatch arm in `assoc_call.rs`. Tests: 3 runtime units (`round_trip_via_client_connect_ffi` proves end-to-end handshake + read/write through the new FFI; `client_connect_with_bad_addr_returns_minus_one` and `_with_garbage_roots_returns_minus_one` pin failure modes) + an IR-grep codegen test (`test_ir_tls_stream_connect_dispatches_to_runtime_ffi`). Public-CA trust (webpki-roots default) is left for a follow-on once `Client.get("https://...")` lands — at that point the trust-root question is resolved by the HTTP client's surface, not here. **Effect propagation (2026-05-30):** the TLS network methods (`TlsListener.accept`, `TlsStream.{connect,read,write,write_all}`) declare `with sends(Network) receives(Network)` in `tls.kara`, but baked-stdlib declarations aren't consumed for caller propagation — they were seeded in `seed_builtin_effects` alongside the http/tcp/ws surface under the line-70 effect-annotation audit so callers actually inherit the network effect (regression: `tests/effectchecker.rs::tcp_tls_ws_network_effects_propagate_to_callers`).
  - [x] **HTTPS for `std.http` `Server.serve` — std.http × TLS bridge.** Shipped via parallel `Server.serve_tls(addr, cert_pem, key_pem, handler)`. Runtime: `karac_runtime_serve_https` mirrors `karac_runtime_serve_http` but each accepted TCP stream is wrapped in `tokio_rustls::TlsAcceptor` before feeding hyper; PEM parsing reuses `tls::build_server_config` (now `pub(crate)`) — rustls 0.23 + `ring` provider, modern TLS only. Per-connection handshake failures are swallowed so one bad client cannot break the accept loop. The handler shim (`Request` / `Response` ABI) is transport-independent, so codegen reuses `emit_http_handler_shim` and replicates the `Server.serve` rc → `Result[Unit, HttpError]` translation. Same `BOUND_PORT=<n>` stdout convention as plain `serve`. New runtime dep: `tokio-rustls = "0.26"` (features mirror `rustls`'s `ring` setup). Test: `tests/http_server.rs::test_server_serve_tls_https_smoke` reads the `tests/fixtures/tls/{cert,key}.pem` fixtures, embeds them in a Kāra source calling `Server.serve_tls`, performs an HTTPS GET via a hand-rolled sync-rustls client, and asserts the handler ran through the TLS layer (chain validation is disabled in the test client because the fixture has `CA:TRUE`; the smoke proves karac's serve_tls wiring, not rustls verification).
  - [x] **`TlsError` enum + error-mode coverage.** Shipped: `enum TlsError { Interrupted, Other(i32), Protocol(i32) }` in `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara`. `TlsStream.read` / `.write` / `.write_all` now return `Result[i64, TlsError]` (replaces `Result[i64, TcpError]`). Codegen: `wrap_tls_io_result` mirrors `wrap_tcp_io_result` but classifies the runtime's `n == -1` sentinel as `Protocol(-1)` instead of `Other(1)`; `lower_tls_stream_write_all`'s err_exit block applies the same classification before the `Result.Err` build. The enum is layout-seeded next to `TcpError` and added to `PRELUDE_TYPES` for scope-0 visibility. **Honest v1 framing:** rustls 0.23 does NOT distinguish handshake failure / cert-verify failure / renegotiation attempts at the API surface — `Connection::complete_io` and `process_new_packets` collapse them into opaque errors — so v1 ships ONE `Protocol(code)` variant rather than the originally-proposed four dead variants. The carried i32 is currently always `-1` and reserved for finer-grained classification if rustls grows a richer error API. Known v1 quirk: `n == -1` from `io_err_to_neg` with EPERM (errno=1) mis-classifies as `Protocol(-1)` rather than `Other(1)` — EPERM during a TLS socket read/write is exceedingly rare; a runtime sentinel rework that disambiguates lands if a real workload surfaces it. Tests: `test_ir_tls_stream_read_wraps_with_tls_io_result` + `test_ir_tls_stream_write_all_classifies_protocol_in_err_exit` pin the codegen routing.
  - [x] **Crypto provider — `ring` at v1, aws-lc-rs deferred to v2+.** Resolved by choosing `ring` (over the originally-named aws-lc-rs) and amending the line-20 parent wording to match shipped reality. Rationale: `ring` ships in pure-Rust + asm with no nasm build dependency (`runtime/Cargo.toml` strips `aws_lc_rs` for exactly this); both providers are upstream-audited and rustls treats them as interchangeable behind `CryptoProvider`. Same `ring` provider is installed explicitly at every `ServerConfig::builder_with_provider` / `ClientConfig::builder_with_provider` site (`runtime/src/tls.rs::build_server_config` / `build_client_config`), so there's no process-global `install_default` state to migrate later. **v2 trigger** stays as documented on the parent: FIPS-certified deployments or post-quantum cipher requirements would force aws-lc-rs; the provider plug-points stay private at v1 so the migration is an internal swap rather than an API break. Tracked separately in `deferred.md` if the trigger fires.
  - [x] **Pre-lock new-code audit. RATIFIED 2026-06-01** (owner security-reviewer pass — items 1–4 & 6 confirmed clean against current source, item 5's finding already carved to line 124, plus one new doc-note carved below).     - **FFI safety contracts** — every `#[no_mangle] unsafe extern "C" fn karac_runtime_tls_*` in `runtime/src/tls.rs` + `karac_runtime_serve_https` in `runtime/src/lib.rs`: documented `# Safety` clause matches the caller-side codegen invariants; null-pointer / negative-length / invalid-utf-8 paths all reject with the documented sentinel; no use-after-free across the `SESSIONS` map's `register` / `lookup` / `close` lifecycle.
    - **`std.tls` public API shape** — `TlsListener` / `TlsStream` / `TlsConfig` field opacity (no field-access escape hatch); `bind_tls` / `accept` / `connect` / `read` / `write` / `write_all` signatures match TCP siblings for predictability; `Drop` for `TlsListener` frees the config + closes fd, `Drop` for `TlsStream` closes fd (no double-free, no leaked sessions).
    - **Verification callbacks + cert-chain handling** — `build_server_config` accepts only valid PEM via `rustls-pemfile`; private-key formats (PKCS#8 / RSA / SEC1) all parse correctly; `build_client_config` builds a root store from supplied PEM only (no implicit webpki / system roots); rustls's `with_safe_default_protocol_versions` is the only `ProtocolVersions` setter (no SSLv3 / TLS1.0 / TLS1.1 surface).
    - **`TlsError` coverage** — the three variants (`Interrupted` / `Other` / `Protocol`) are exhaustive for the runtime's negative-return scheme; no information leakage in the `Protocol(code)` payload (the `-1` carried today is generic); EPERM-vs-Protocol ambiguity (line 24 known quirk) is documented and acceptable for v1 or warrants the runtime sentinel rework.
    - **HTTPS-via-tokio-rustls integration** — per-connection handshake failures (`acceptor.accept(tcp_stream).await` Err arm in `karac_runtime_serve_https`) drop the connection silently without leaking session state or opening a DoS through repeated bad handshakes; tokio-rustls's `TlsAcceptor` carries the same `Arc<ServerConfig>` the existing `tls.rs` builds (no provider/version drift between the WS-over-TLS and HTTPS-server paths); the runtime's `BOUND_PORT=<n>` stdout leak (tests-only convention) is documented as such.
    - **Test-cert fixture posture** — `tests/fixtures/tls/{cert,key}.pem` are clearly marked self-signed CN=localhost test-only material (README + script); the `NoVerify` rustls `ServerCertVerifier` lives only in test code (`tests/http_server.rs`), not in any runtime path.

    **New-code audit walk (2026-05-31): all six checklist items executed; five close clean (one with a doc-drift fix), one split a real finding into its own `[ ]` entry. Down to security-reviewer ratification.** **RATIFIED 2026-06-01** — owner security-reviewer pass re-verified every clean verdict against current source (not just the walk's prose). Two dispositions recorded: line 124 severity confirmed (pre-public-v1, not Demo-1-blocking), and one new doc-note finding carved out of item 5's re-read (raw-`accept` blocking handshake — the `[ ]` below line 124).
    1. *FFI safety contracts* — **clean.** Every `karac_runtime_tls_*` + `karac_runtime_serve_https` carries a `# Safety` clause matching its codegen invariants; null / non-positive-length / invalid-UTF-8 inputs all reject with the documented sentinel (`null` config / `-1` fd / `0`-byte I/O return — verified at `config_new` / `tls_accept` / `tls_client_connect` / `tls_read` / `tls_write`); `config_free` is null-idempotent (double-free is documented UB, resolved by codegen's single-`Drop` guarantee); the `SESSIONS` register/lookup/close lifecycle has no use-after-free in the documented one-I/O-op-per-connection-at-a-time posture (the inner per-fd `Mutex` serialises read/write; the read/write paths use the borrow-the-fd `from_raw_fd` + `into_raw_fd` pattern so no spurious `close(2)` fires). **Documented v1 limitation (not a bug):** `tls_close` removes the session + closes the fd *without* taking the inner `Mutex`, so a `close` racing an in-flight I/O on the same fd would be a fd-reuse hazard — unreachable from the parking primitive's per-connection serial dispatch, called out in the `tls.rs` module doc. **Ratification note (2026-06-01):** the in-house re-check deepened this past the walk's original name-narrow grep (which only matched the `NoVerify` *type name*) — confirmed zero `dangerous()` / `with_custom_certificate_verifier` / `set_certificate_verifier` / `DangerousClientConfig` / `ServerCertVerifier` anywhere in `runtime/`, and zero bare `ClientConfig::builder()` / `ServerConfig::builder()` sites (every config uses `builder_with_provider`, so no `install_default` global-provider reliance). Verdict holds; the original *method* was too narrow to use as precedent for future verifier-absence checks.
    2. *`std.tls` API shape* — **clean after a doc-drift fix** (`[x]` below). Field opacity holds (`TlsConfig` empty, `TlsListener {fd, config}`, `TlsStream {fd}` are codegen-only structs with no user field-access path); `bind_tls`/`accept`/`connect`/`read`/`write`/`write_all` mirror the TCP siblings; `Drop` for `TlsListener` frees config + closes fd and `Drop` for `TlsStream` closes fd (single-free — the i32 handle is zeroed on move, no double-free, the session entry is removed on close).
    3. *Verification callbacks + cert-chain* — **clean, fails-secure.** `build_server_config` accepts only `rustls-pemfile`-valid PEM and `private_key()` covers PKCS#8 / RSA / SEC1; `build_client_config` builds the root store from the supplied PEM **only**, with NO implicit webpki / system-root fallback, and an empty / unparseable roots set fails *closed* (`NoCertsFound` → `-1`, never the "trust-nothing degrades to trust-all" footgun); `with_safe_default_protocol_versions` is the sole protocol setter at all four config sites (`tls.rs` ×3 + `lib.rs` http-client agent), so there is no SSLv3 / TLS1.0 / TLS1.1 surface; no insecure verifier exists in any runtime path (`NoVerify` is confined to `tests/http_server.rs` + `tests/coro_e2e.rs`, grep-confirmed).
    4. *`TlsError` coverage* — **clean.** `Interrupted` / `Other(errno)` / `Protocol(code)` (+ the line-74 construction causes) are exhaustive for the negative-return scheme; no information leakage in `Protocol(code)` (the carried `-1` is generic); the EPERM-vs-`Protocol` ambiguity (line 24 known quirk) is documented and acceptable for v1.

    - [x] **`std.tls` API-doc drift — stale `fd: -1` sentinel language. Fixed 2026-05-31 (surfaced by item 2 of this walk).** After the line-71 `Result` migration, `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara`'s docstrings still described `TlsListener.accept` / `TlsStream.connect` / `TlsListener.bind_tls` as returning a `TlsStream { fd: -1 }` / `TlsListener { fd: -1, config: 0 }` sentinel in four spots (file-header summary + each of the three method docstrings) — directly contradicting the migrated `Result[T, TlsError]` signatures a few lines below in the same docstring. Corrected to describe the `Ok(...)` / `Err(TlsError.*)` shape (with the `connect` path noting the line-74 branchable TCP-connect causes). Comment-only change to a `.kara` stdlib file — no codegen / behaviour change, Rust + codegen test surface unaffected; `cargo fmt --all -- --check` clean.
    - [x] **P0 — server accept-loop resource bounds (handshake/header timeout + bounded connection concurrency). Shipped 2026-06-01 (`9f7f03da`).** Surfaced by item 5 of this audit walk. All three `karac_runtime_serve_*` accept loops (`serve_http` `lib.rs` ~4292, `serve_https` ~4407, `serve_http_static` ~4503) do an **unbounded `tokio::spawn` per accepted connection with no timeout on the handshake / first-request-header read and no cap on concurrent in-flight connections.** A slowloris-style client that opens many TCP connections and either (HTTPS) never completes the TLS `ClientHello` — leaving each spawned task awaiting `acceptor.accept(tcp_stream).await` indefinitely — or (plain HTTP) dribbles request headers, exhausts tokio tasks / socket fds / memory. **Not TLS-specific:** the unbounded-spawn pattern is shared across all three serve paths and hyper's http1 builder ships no default header-read timeout, so the plain-HTTP path carries the symmetric exposure — a TLS-only patch would be a workaround (no-workarounds policy). **v1 framing:** severity is deployment-dependent (loopback Demo 1 is unaffected; an internet-facing backend is exposed), but the friction-zero-backend positioning means it must be hardened before a public-facing v1 (it does NOT block Demo 1). **Fix shape:** wrap the handshake / first-header read in a `tokio::time::timeout`, and gate each `tokio::spawn` behind a `tokio::sync::Semaphore`-bounded connection permit (configurable, sane default), applied uniformly to all three serve loops; add a slowloris-style regression test (open N stalled connections, assert a healthy connection still completes + bounded task/fd growth). Cross-ref: the plain HTTP server surface (line 15 routing / line 16a keep-alive). **Severity ratified 2026-06-01 (owner):** pre-public-v1 hardening, does **NOT** block Demo 1 — Demo 1 is 1M *completed-handshake* idle connections over loopback/controlled clients, which never exercises the incomplete-handshake threat. The connection-cap half of the fix carries a mild Demo-1 robustness angle (fd/task backpressure at 1M conns with no cap), but that's tuning, not the DoS, and doesn't change the non-blocking call. **Shipped as `ServeLimits` (read once per serve call), applied uniformly to all three loops.** `header_timeout`: **on by default** (10 s; `KARAC_HTTP_HEADER_TIMEOUT_MS` overrides, `0` disables) — plain HTTP via hyper's `TokioTimer`-backed `header_read_timeout`, HTTPS additionally wraps `acceptor.accept()` in `tokio::time::timeout` (the primary HTTPS vector). `conn_permits`: **off by default** (unbounded; `KARAC_HTTP_MAX_CONNS=<n>` bounds it), permit acquired *before* `accept` so reaching the cap applies backpressure at the OS accept backlog rather than spawning unbounded. The on/off default posture was the owner's call (timeout on, cap off — never silently breaks the 1M-idle workload). Parse logic split into pure `ServeLimits::from_raw` for env-free unit testing; `tokio` gains the `time` + `sync` features. **9 runtime unit tests:** `from_raw` parse matrix (default / explicit / `0`-disables / garbage-falls-back / whitespace-trim, cap on/off), semaphore backpressure (cap=1 blocks until released; no-cap never blocks), and two behavioral tests driving real hyper connections — a slow-header connection is reaped by the timeout, a healthy request still succeeds under it. Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets` ±`llvm`, full non-llvm suite, `http_server` (21 E2E), `http_client`/`tcp`/`ws` codegen. (One pre-existing unrelated failure on `main`: `tls_codegen::test_ir_websocket_accept_tls_parks_then_calls_runtime_ffi` — confirmed failing without this change too, not in scope.)
    - [x] **Doc-note — `TlsListener.accept` blocking handshake (carved from the 2026-06-01 audit ratification, item-5 re-read). Shipped 2026-06-01 (`033d2e18`).** The raw `std.tls` server path's `karac_runtime_tls_accept` (`runtime/src/tls.rs:325`) runs the rustls handshake **synchronously** via `conn.complete_io(&mut sock)` on the calling thread. This is correct, by-design semantics for a low-level blocking-socket primitive (mirrors Go's `tls.Conn.Handshake()`), but it means a user-authored accept loop built on `TlsListener.accept()` lets one stalled/malicious client block the **entire** accept loop — a strictly worse shape than the line-124 managed-serve-loop slowloris, which only parks one tokio task. **Deliberately NOT folded into line 124:** these are different layers. The three `karac_runtime_serve_*` loops are karac's loops (karac owns the accept policy → karac hardens them), whereas `TlsListener.accept` is the raw you-own-the-loop primitive — injecting a forced timeout/semaphore there would bake accept policy into a primitive whose contract is that the caller sets policy. **Fix = doc-only:** a one-line `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara` docstring on `TlsListener.accept` stating the handshake is blocking and that user-built accept loops must spawn-per-connection and/or apply their own handshake timeout. No codegen / behaviour change. **Shipped:** added an *Availability note — you own the accept loop* paragraph to `TlsListener.accept`'s docstring conveying exactly the above (synchronous handshake ⇒ a stalled/malicious peer blocks the whole user-built accept loop; by-design, mirrors Go's `tls.Conn.Handshake()`; cross-refs the managed `Server.serve`/`serve_tls` line-124 hardening). Comment-only; stdlib parse + typecheck verified.

    Execution requires a security reviewer; this entry stays `[ ]` until that pass runs and findings either close clean or split into their own tracker entries. **Walk run 2026-05-31** — five of six items confirmed clean (item 2 with a doc-drift fix, now `[x]` above); item 5 split one real finding (server accept-loop resource bounds) into its own `[ ]` P0 above. **RATIFIED 2026-06-01 — owner security-reviewer pass complete; entry now `[x]`.** Every clean verdict was re-verified against current source rather than the walk's prose: items 2/3/4 by reading `tls.rs`'s config builders + accept paths (all `builder_with_provider` + `with_safe_default_protocol_versions`; `build_client_config` fails closed on empty/garbage roots; 8 unsafe externs carry substantive `# Safety` clauses); item 1 deepened past the walk's name-narrow grep to confirm no rustls verifier-disabling escape hatch exists in any runtime path (margin note on item 1). Two dispositions: (a) line-124 severity confirmed pre-public-v1 / not-Demo-1-blocking; (b) a new doc-note finding (raw-`accept` blocking handshake) carved as its own `[ ]` below line 124 — kept separate from line 124 by design (raw primitive vs. managed loop). No further compiler/runtime work blocks the audit itself; the two carved `[ ]` items (line 124 slowloris hardening + the raw-`accept` doc-note) are what now gate the line-102 parent.
- [x] **P0 — WebSocket — RFC 6455. CLOSED 2026-06-01.** Server-side framing (continuation, ping/pong, close), handshake, message/binary distinction, fragmentation, masking. Built on `std.http` upgrade handshake. The canonical idle-keep-alive workload — Demo 1 (1M+ idle connections) is shaped around this surface. **CLOSED:** all RFC 6455 framing/handshake sub-slices (9e.1–9e.4 + WS-over-TLS) shipped and verified; the compliance audit walk + three-lens reviewer ratification ran clean; both v1-blocking handshake gaps (§4.2.1 validation + the residual dribble-slowloris) are fixed, and the only remaining carves (close-frame conformance sub-P1, subprotocol negotiation, `recv_text` UTF-8 validation) are genuinely-additive post-v1 items that do not gate v1. No remaining WS compiler/runtime work blocks v1. Effects: same `sends(Network)` / `receives(Network)` as `std.http` — and as of 2026-05-30 the WebSocket network methods (`accept` / `accept_tls` / `recv_text` / `send_text` / `recv_binary` / `send_binary` / `send_text_masked` / `send_binary_masked`) actually *propagate* that effect to callers, via the `seed_builtin_effects` extension recorded under the line-70 effect-annotation audit (the stdlib `with` clauses alone were decorative — baked-stdlib declarations aren't consumed for propagation).

    **RFC 6455 compliance audit walk (2026-06-01).** The framing + handshake surface shipped incrementally across Phase-6 slices 9e.1–9e.4 (text/binary frames, FIN/opcode/payload-length encoding, masked send, continuation-frame fragmentation reassembly, ping/pong/close control frames, the SHA-1 + base64 `Sec-WebSocket-Accept` handshake, and WS-over-TLS via `accept_tls`); the runtime FFI lives in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (`karac_runtime_ws_*`) with codegen lowerings in `src/codegen/tcp.rs` + `src/codegen/tls.rs`. The audit walked the implemented surface against the RFC and confirmed the framing/fragmentation/masking layers are wire-correct, with the control layer correct on the data-bearing path but carrying a close-frame conformance gap surfaced at ratification (see the `[ ]` close-frame entry) (38 runtime unit tests in `event_loop.rs` + 18 codegen IR-grep tests in `tests/ws_framing.rs`). It surfaced **two genuine v1-blocking gaps in the *handshake* path** (both fixed this slice, see the `[x]` sub-entries) plus two genuinely-post-v1-additive gaps (carved `[ ]` below), and added the **first end-to-end compiled-binary round-trip coverage** for the plain-TCP path (previously only WS-over-TLS had an E2E test; the plain path was IR-grep-only per the `tests/ws_framing.rs` header note).

    **Reviewer ratification (2026-06-01) — RATIFIED with two carve-outs.** A three-lens reviewer pass (correctness / security-DoS / RFC-6455-conformance) re-verified the walk's verdicts against current source rather than the prose. Net: the change is a correct improvement — RFC §4.2.1 validation is wire-conformant, the handshake-timeout clear-on-success path is exactly right (established idle connections never inherit the deadline, so Demo 1 is structurally safe), no fd / TLS-session leak on any reject path, no info disclosure (the runtime-side request `preview` is `eprintln`-to-stderr, env-gated, never sent to the client), and there are **zero hard MUST-violations on the normal client-masked server-role path**. Two findings were carved (both consistent with the line-124/125 dispositioning — neither blocks Demo 1): (1) the handshake read-timeout is a *per-read* `SO_RCVTIMEO`, not a whole-request wall-clock bound, so a **dribble-slowloris** survives it (bounded only by the 8 KiB request cap; the TLS handshake pool's unbounded work-queue amplifies the blast radius) — carved as a pre-public-v1 P0 below, and the overstated "bounds the handshake" wording corrected here and in the runtime comments; (2) **close-frame handling** does not echo the peer's close status code, does not validate the inbound close body, and TCP-drops on protocol error instead of sending Close 1002 (§5.5.1 / §7.4.1) — carved as a sub-P1 below. The minor §5.2 64-bit-length MSB-zero check is absent but harmless (the `out_max_len` bounds check rejects any oversize length first); folded into the close-frame entry's scope. **Parent closed `[x]` 2026-06-01** once the carved residual-slowloris P0 shipped (the `[x]` entry below) — mirroring how the TLS P0 (line 102) closed after its carved line-124/125 follow-ons landed; the additive deferrals (subprotocol, UTF-8, close-frame) do not gate v1 on their own and remain `[ ]` as post-v1 work.
    - [x] **Handshake hardening — RFC §4.2.1 header validation + slowloris read-timeout (this slice).** Both server handshake paths (`karac_runtime_ws_accept` plain TCP, and `ws_handshake_conn_tls` → `ws_drive_upgrade_handshake` for WS-over-TLS) previously accepted **any** request carrying a `Sec-WebSocket-Key`, ignoring the other RFC §4.2.1-mandated request headers (`Upgrade: websocket`, `Connection: Upgrade`, `Sec-WebSocket-Version: 13`) — a real RFC-6455-conformance gap for a P0 labelled "RFC 6455", and a slowloris exposure symmetric to the line-124 managed-serve-loop hardening (the blocking handshake read had no timeout, so a peer that completed the TCP connect but stalled/dribbled the upgrade request could pin the accept indefinitely). **Fix (`runtime/src/event_loop.rs`):** new pure `ws_validate_handshake(request) -> Result[&key, WsHandshakeReject]` checks Upgrade/Connection (token-in-comma-list, so `Connection: keep-alive, Upgrade` matches) then `Sec-WebSocket-Version` (token-in-list offering `13`) then key-presence, in RFC order; a non-conforming request is answered with `400 Bad Request` (missing Upgrade/Connection/Key) or `426 Upgrade Required` + `Sec-WebSocket-Version: 13` (unsupported version, per RFC §4.4) **rather than upgrading anyway**. The two handshake paths were de-duplicated — `karac_runtime_ws_accept` now drives the same generic `ws_drive_upgrade_handshake<S: Read + Write>` the TLS path uses (its cfg gate relaxed from `feature = "tls"` to plain `unix`, since it carries no TLS types), so both transports get identical validation + rejection-status behaviour. A `set_read_timeout` is applied to the socket for the **pre-`101` phase only** and cleared the instant the upgrade completes (so post-upgrade framed I/O, which parks through the event loop, never inherits the deadline) — configurable via `KARAC_WS_HANDSHAKE_TIMEOUT_MS` (**on by default, 10 s**; `0` disables). The default-on posture is safe for Demo 1: it governs only the handshake, never an established idle connection, so the 1M-idle-connection workload is structurally unaffected (unlike the line-124 connection-*cap*, which stayed off-by-default for exactly that reason). **Ratification correction:** this is a *per-read* inactivity deadline (`SO_RCVTIMEO`), which reaps a silently-stalled peer but not a byte-per-interval *dribbler* — it does **not** bound total handshake duration; the whole-request wall-clock deadline is the carved residual-slowloris P0 below. The deliberately-unenforced request-line / `Host` checks are documented as a non-gap (every real client sends them; rejecting buys no protocol safety). **Tests:** 12 new runtime unit tests (validation accept + each rejection class, token-in-list for Connection + Version, case-insensitive header names, the 400/426 response-status shapes, the timeout parse matrix `default`/`explicit`/`0`-disables/`whitespace`/`garbage`-falls-back, a behavioral `ws_read_http_request`-reaps-stalled-peer timeout test, and a full `karac_runtime_ws_accept` round-trip asserting a real `426` for a bad version). The stale "v1 limitation" comment block in `event_loop.rs` was rewritten to describe the now-enforced validation + timeout knob.
    - [x] **End-to-end compiled-binary round-trip tests for the plain-TCP path (this slice).** `tests/ws_framing.rs` was IR-grep-only for the plain path (its header documented that the historical blocker — stdlib `stream.fd` field access returning const 0 — was lifted by the `WebSocket.accept(listener)` builder, which the WS-over-TLS coro E2E already exploits). Added two real link-and-run tests to `tests/coro_e2e.rs` (reusing its `compile_link_coro` / `BOUND_PORT` harness, gated on `--features llvm` + the runtime archive): `e2e_plain_websocket_text_echo_roundtrip` compiles a kara `WebSocket.accept` → `recv_text`/`send_text` echo server, drives a hand-rolled masked-frame client against the real binary, and asserts the payload echoes back (proving the runtime framing FFI + codegen wiring round-trips, not just the IR shape); `e2e_plain_websocket_handshake_rejects_bad_request` drives the line-128 handshake validation through a real binary — an unsupported `Sec-WebSocket-Version` gets `426`, a request missing `Upgrade`/`Connection` gets `400`, never a spurious `101`. Existing WS-over-TLS coro E2E (`coroutine_ws_over_tls_handler_executes` + the concurrent-handlers regression) re-verified green under the handshake changes.
    - [x] **P0 — residual handshake slowloris (per-read vs whole-request deadline + unbounded TLS handshake-pool queue). Carved + SHIPPED 2026-06-01.** The line-131 handshake read-timeout is `SO_RCVTIMEO`, a *per-read* inactivity deadline that re-arms on every successful `read(2)` — so it reaps a silently-stalled peer but **not** a peer that dribbles one byte per `(timeout − ε)` interval, which keeps the clock reset indefinitely. Such a connection is bounded only by `ws_read_http_request`'s 8 KiB `MAX_REQUEST_SIZE` cap (≈ 8192 × timeout worst case → ~22 h at the 10 s default). **Blast radius is transport-dependent:** the plain path (`karac_runtime_ws_accept`) runs one dribbler per codegen-parked accept task (no per-connection concurrency cap, the line-124 `conn_permits` analog is absent here), but the **TLS path is worse** — `ws_handshake_pool_for` runs a *fixed* worker pool (`max(32, 2×cpus)`) draining an **unbounded `VecDeque<i32>` work queue**, so ~32 dribblers saturate every worker and the queue then grows without bound, stalling the whole WS-over-TLS accept pipeline (the line-125 "one stalled peer blocks the loop" shape, amplified to N peers blocking the pool). **Severity: pre-public-v1 hardening, does NOT block Demo 1** (which is completed-handshake idle connections over loopback/controlled clients — the dribble vector needs adversarial clients and never fires there) — same disposition as line-124/125. **Fix shape:** capture `Instant::now()` at handshake entry and enforce a whole-request wall-clock deadline inside both `ws_read_http_request`'s read loop and the TLS `complete_io` phase (so per-read inactivity *and* total duration are bounded), plus a per-listener in-flight-handshake cap on the TLS pool's work queue (reject/backpressure beyond N pending, mirroring line-124's `conn_permits`); add a dribble-slowloris regression test (the existing `test_ws_read_http_request_times_out_on_stalled_peer` only covers the silent-stall case). Reuse the `KARAC_WS_HANDSHAKE_TIMEOUT_MS` knob for the wall-clock bound; a new `KARAC_WS_MAX_PENDING_HANDSHAKES` for the pool cap. **Shipped (`runtime/src/event_loop.rs`):** (a) **whole-request wall-clock deadline** — `ws_read_http_request` gained a `deadline: Option<Instant>` checked before every read; both accept paths derive it from the handshake timeout (`now + t`) so the per-read `SO_RCVTIMEO` (reaps a silent stall) and the deadline (reaps a dribbler) together bound total handshake-read time to ≈ `2t`. The TLS `complete_io` (dribbled-`ClientHello`) phase is bounded by a new `DeadlineStream<S>` `Read`/`Write` adapter that fails reads with `TimedOut` past the deadline; the upgrade phase is bounded by the same deadline inside `ws_read_http_request`. On by default (the timeout is), cleared on success, so Demo 1's established idle connections are untouched. (b) **TLS handshake-pool in-flight cap** — `WsHandshakePool` gained a `max_pending: Option<usize>` from `KARAC_WS_MAX_PENDING_HANDSHAKES` (**off by default**, mirroring the line-124 connection-cap disposition); the `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls` accept-drain checks it *before* each `accept(2)` and stops draining at the cap, leaving excess connections in the OS accept backlog (true backpressure, nothing dropped). With the deadline reaping dribblers in ≈ `2t`, workers free promptly even with the cap off; the cap is defense-in-depth against a fresh-connection flood. **Tests:** `test_ws_read_http_request_deadline_reaps_dribbler` (a 50 ms/byte dribbler past a 300 ms deadline is reaped < 900 ms, not held to the 8 KiB cap), `test_ws_max_pending_from_raw_parse_matrix` (off/​`0`-off/​positive/​garbage/​negative), plus the existing silent-stall + WS-over-TLS concurrent E2E re-verified green. Gate: fmt, clippy `--all-targets` ±`tls`, runtime WS units (tls 40 / no-tls 38), llvm `coro_e2e` WS (plain + TLS).
    - [ ] **Close-frame conformance — status-code echo + inbound close-body validation + protocol-error Close 1002 (§5.5.1 / §7.4.1). Carved at 2026-06-01 ratification.** On receiving a client Close (0x8), `ws_recv_data_frame_inner` replies with an **empty** Close frame and returns 0 — it does not echo the peer's 2-byte status code (§5.5.1 SHOULD), does not parse/validate the inbound close body (a 1-byte close body is malformed per §5.5.1; reserved codes 1005/1006/1015 in the body are invalid), and every decoder protocol-violation TCP-drops (returns `-1`) rather than sending a Close frame with code **1002** (§7.4.1 SHOULD). These are SHOULD-level gaps (no hard MUST-violation on the data path), but the audit's "wire-correct control layer" wording overclaimed them, so they are tracked here. **Also folded in (minor):** the §5.2 64-bit extended-length MSB-must-be-zero check is absent — harmless because the `out_max_len` bounds check rejects any oversize length first, but it's a literal §5.2 conformance miss. Build alongside an Autobahn-style conformance pass if/when WS conformance becomes a v1 marketing claim; until then these are low-real-world-impact niceties.
    - [ ] **Subprotocol / extension negotiation (`Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` / `Sec-WebSocket-Extensions`).** The `101` response never echoes a negotiated subprotocol or extension. RFC 6455 permits a server to ignore these (a client that *requires* one will fail its own check), so this is post-v1-additive, not a v1 blocker. Build when a real consumer needs subprotocol routing (e.g. a kata that multiplexes `graphql-ws` vs a custom protocol on one endpoint) — the handshake response builder in `ws_drive_upgrade_handshake` is the single insertion point.
    - [ ] **`recv_text` UTF-8 validation (RFC §8.1 / §8.2).** A text frame's payload is currently passed through verbatim without validating it is well-formed UTF-8 (the runtime returns raw bytes; `recv_binary` deliberately passes through, and the two share the frame-decode path). RFC §8.1 requires text frames carry valid UTF-8 and §8.2 mandates failing the connection with close code 1007 on a violation. Deferred as a strictness nicety — it risks rejecting existing callers that (ab)use `recv_text` as a byte channel, and the conformance value is low for a server that hands payloads to user code. Revisit if Autobahn-style conformance becomes a v1 marketing claim.
- [ ] **P0 — `karac new <name>` default project template — backend HTTP server skeleton.** Default scaffolding: `std.http` + `std.tracing` + `/health` endpoint + `/ws` WebSocket route. `--lib` for libraries, `--cli` for CLI tools, `--data` for data-pipeline scaffolding (Kafka consumer + processor + sink shape). Default-being-backend reinforces the positioning at the friction-zero entry point.
  - [x] **`karac new <name>` command + `--backend` (default) / `--lib` / `--cli` flags + backend HTTP skeleton + `/health` endpoint.** Shipped 2026-05-29. `karac new my_api` creates `./my_api/` with `src/main.kara` carrying `Server.serve("127.0.0.1:8080", handle)`, manual `req.path()` dispatch per the v1 routing answer (phase-8 line 15), and a `/health` endpoint returning `200 OK / ok`. Effect declarations (`sends(Network) receives(Network)`) propagated through `main` so the generated source effectchecks cleanly. `karac init --backend` joins the existing `karac init` template menu so the bare-cwd init form gets the same skeleton. `--cli` maps to the existing `Template::Bin` (the hello-world scaffold; renaming the enum would have broken every existing test). 9 new tests: 4 scaffold unit tests in `src/scaffold.rs::tests` (anchors in the body, placeholder test shape, scaffold-writes-files, opposite-entry-collision); 4 integration tests in `tests/scaffold.rs` (writes-expected-files, parses-resolves-typechecks-effectchecks, test-file-parses) + 1 codegen E2E (compiles + links to a real executable, gated on `--features llvm` and the runtime archive). Full v1 flow verified manually: `karac new my_api && cd my_api && karac build` produces a working backend binary on first try.
  - [ ] **`--data` Kafka pipeline scaffold.** Reserved in the `karac new` parser with a structured `"deferred"` diagnostic. Blocked on a Kafka client surface that doesn't exist yet — the entry implies a `kafka-rs` (or equivalent) dep + `std.process` integration for the pipeline-stage harness. Lands once a data-engineering consumer signals demand; until then `karac new --data` rejects loudly so users get a "planned, not yet" signal instead of "unknown flag".
  - [ ] **`/ws` WebSocket route on the HTTP server — the original "one new arm" plan was infeasible against the shipped surface; re-scoped 2026-06-01.** The WebSocket RFC 6455 surface shipped (line 128, CLOSED 2026-06-01), but it does **not** compose with `Server.serve`'s request handler the way this entry originally assumed. The shipped WS entry points are `WebSocket.accept(listener: TcpListener)` / `accept_tls(listener: TlsListener)` — a **separate accept loop** (see `examples/ws_idle_holder`, the Demo-1 flagship, which runs exactly this standalone loop and never touches `Server.serve`). `Server.serve(addr, handler)` is a hyper request/response loop: the handler receives an **opaque `Request`** (`path`/`method`/`body`/`header`/`headers`/`query` only — no socket access) and returns a `Response`, with no upgrade hook (line 15 ratifies this one-handler-dispatch model). So there is no `WebSocket.accept(req)` and no way to add a `/ws` arm inside the `Server.serve` handler — the original "no scaffold reshape, just one new arm" claim was wrong. **Two genuinely-separate things were conflated:** (a) a real `Server.serve` WebSocket-upgrade integration (carved as its own `[ ]` below — the actual gate for a `/ws`-on-the-same-HTTP-server route), and (b) merely demonstrating the *standalone* WS idiom in the scaffold. (b) is deliberately NOT done: `Server.serve` blocks the calling thread, so a standalone `WebSocket.accept` loop cannot coexist with it in one `main()` without spawning the server into a task — an advanced shape wrong for a default `karac new` skeleton, and the standalone idiom is already demonstrated properly in `examples/ws_idle_holder`. The backend scaffold stays HTTP-only (`Server.serve` + `/health`) until the upgrade hook below lands.
    - [ ] **`Server.serve` WebSocket-upgrade integration — the real gate for a `/ws` route on the HTTP server.** For `/ws` to be a route on the same server as `/health` (the canonical backend shape: axum, Go `net/http` + gorilla/websocket, express + ws), `Server.serve` needs an in-place upgrade path: hyper's HTTP/1.1 `Upgrade` handling detaches the raw upgraded TCP (or TLS) stream, which is then fed to the existing WebSocket framing FFI (`karac_runtime_ws_*` in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs`). **Open design question — handler signaling:** the handler is `Fn(Request) -> Response` today; upgrading needs a way for a handler arm to say "upgrade this connection and run this frame loop" rather than return a `Response`. Candidate shapes: a `req.upgrade() -> Result[WebSocket, _]` accessor that detaches the connection (mirrors hyper's `on_upgrade`), a sum return type (`Response | Upgrade`), or a distinct `Server.serve_with_ws(http_handler, ws_handler)` callback pair. This is a real runtime + surface-design slice in its own right (comparable in weight to the line-17 body-streaming or line-144 HTTP/2 work), NOT a scaffold edit. v1 has structurally treated HTTP-serve and WebSocket as two separate surfaces — Demo 1 uses the standalone loop — so this is post-Demo-1 work; build it when a real consumer needs HTTP and WS multiplexed on one port. Once it lands, the scaffold's manual `req.path()` dispatch gains a genuine `/ws` arm and entry (a) above closes.
  - [x] **`std.tracing` integration in the backend skeleton. Shipped 2026-06-02.** Was blocked on a user-visible tracing *emission* surface (the `1d172e9` data shapes were interpreter-only); that surface — `StdoutExporter` + full `std.tracing` codegen — landed in the P1 `std.tracing` entry below. The scaffold's `backend_main_body` now emits the "Listening on …" announcement through the tracing idiom (`let tracer = StdoutExporter {}; tracer.export_event(LogEvent.info("Listening on http://127.0.0.1:8080"))`) instead of a bare `println`, so a fresh `karac new` project shows the structured-logging surface from day one. `Kāra` has no `span!()`/`event!()` macros — the idiom is the builder + exporter (matching the rest of the surface), so "structured span+event" is realized as the `LogEvent.info(...)` build + `export_event` call. Verified end-to-end: `backend_main_kara_codegens_to_executable` compiles + links the new body to a real binary (it previously failed once the tracing call was added — that gap is exactly what the codegen slice closed); the per-handler span idea (emit inside `handle` without threading an exporter) waits on the ambient/registered exporter, tracked separately under the `std.tracing` P1.
- [x] **P1 — HTTP/2 — multiplexed streams + flow control. Shipped 2026-06-03.** HPACK header compression, stream prioritization, server push (default-off), `Server-Sent Events` interop. Required for gRPC (which is post-v1; see [`deferred.md § gRPC`](../deferred.md#grpc-streaming-reflection-server--client)). Sequenced after HTTP/1.1 in implementation order; ships at v1 launch. **Shipped:** the three `karac_runtime_serve_*` loops (`runtime/src/lib.rs`) no longer hardcode `hyper::server::conn::http1::Builder` — they construct hyper-util's protocol-negotiating `hyper_util::server::conn::auto::Builder` over a `TokioExecutor`, which detects the protocol **per-connection**: an HTTP/2 connection preface drives the h2 path (sent by an h2c-prior-knowledge client over plain TCP, or by an ALPN-`h2` client over TLS), and anything else falls through to HTTP/1.1 (no regression). **The headline deliverables — multiplexed streams, HPACK, flow control, stream prioritization — are all internal to hyper/`h2` and came free with negotiation**, because the per-request bridge `serve_request` was already protocol-agnostic (`hyper::Request<Incoming>` → `hyper::Response<Full<Bytes>>`, no HTTP/1-specific logic). Three pieces of wiring: **(1)** `runtime/Cargo.toml` flips on `http2` for both `hyper` (`server`/`http1`/`http2`) and `hyper-util` (`server-auto`/`tokio`/`http1`/`http2`) — reverses the original "HTTP/1 only (locked design (i))" note; `h2 0.4.14` was already in the lockfile transitively. **(2)** ALPN is advertised (`server_config.alpn_protocols = [b"h2", b"http/1.1"]`) **at the HTTPS serve site only**, not in the shared `tls::build_server_config` — that helper also backs the raw `std.tls` listener (`karac_runtime_tls_config_new`), a generic TLS socket that is not an HTTP server and must stay ALPN-free. **(3)** `apply_header_timeout` → `apply_serve_tuning`, now taking `&mut auto::Builder<TokioExecutor>` and applying the line-124 header-read timeout through the `.http1()` sub-builder — the timeout is the **HTTP/1** slowloris guard; the h2 path needs no equivalent (h2 flow control + frame-size limits bound header buffering structurally, so the unbounded-header-accumulation vector doesn't exist). **`block_in_place` under multiplexing:** sibling streams on one connection are serialized while a handler runs (the connection future can't poll them mid-`block_in_place`), but cross-connection parallelism is preserved via tokio's worker-replacement — exactly the per-connection shape HTTP/1.1 keep-alive already had; documented on `serve_request`. A fully-async handler ABI (concurrent streams per connection) is a separate, larger slice. **Tests** (`tests/http_server.rs`, gated `--features llvm`): the spawn-the-binary harness gained a real multiplexing h2 client (`hyper::client::conn::http2::handshake`, driven on a private current-thread tokio runtime — added `tokio`/`hyper` client+http2/`hyper-util`/`http-body-util`/`bytes` to the **root** crate's `[dev-dependencies]`, all dev-only so the compiler's production build is unaffected). `test_http2_h2c_prior_knowledge_handler` (path-echo over real h2c, asserts `HTTP_2` version), `test_http2_multiplexed_streams` (two concurrent streams on one h2c connection), `test_http2_alpn_over_tls` (TLS handshake offering `[h2, http/1.1]` settles on `h2`; an `http/1.1`-only client falls back — sync rustls + the existing `NoVerify` client, no async needed), `test_http1_still_served_under_auto_builder` (HTTP/1.1 no-regression pin). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets ±llvm`, runtime units (`serve_limits` behavioral timeout tests re-verified through `auto::Builder`), full non-llvm suite, `http_server` (25 E2E + 1 pre-existing ignore), codegen + memory_sanitizer.
  - [ ] **Server push (HTTP/2 `PUSH_PROMISE`).** Won't-do for v1 unless a real consumer needs it: hyper 1.x dropped server-push support entirely, browsers have deprecated/removed it (Chrome removed it in 2022), and the parent entry already specified it default-off. If a future consumer needs push, it requires a hyper-version capability that doesn't currently exist — re-evaluate then.
  - [ ] **SSE interop + true response streaming.** `Server-Sent Events` and chunked/streamed response bodies are gated on the line-17 response-body-streaming slice: the serve path returns `hyper::Response<Full<Bytes>>` (a single fully-buffered body) today, so a handler cannot emit an open-ended event stream over either HTTP/1.1 or HTTP/2. SSE is a thin content-type + framing convention on top of a streaming body, so it lands naturally once streaming bodies do — build it there. (HTTP/2 itself is ready for it; the limitation is the buffered-body handler ABI, not the protocol.)
- [ ] **P1 — `std.tracing` — structured logging + span/trace context propagation, OTel-export-ready.** Minimum surface: span creation + nesting, structured fields on spans, trace-context propagation across async boundaries (state-machine transform preserves the active span), exporter trait (default no-op exporter at v1; OTel exporter ships post-v1 as a community library on the same trait). Comptime-driven trace-context plumbing — Kāra-native opportunity, no proc-macro indirection like Rust's `tracing`.
  - [x] `Span` data shape (root + child + `with_field`), `LogEvent` (5 levels + `with_field` + `in_span`), structured fields via `SpanField` — commit `1d172e9`
  - [x] `Exporter` trait + `NoOpExporter` default impl; verified user `impl Exporter for X` dispatches correctly (`test_tracing_user_can_implement_exporter_trait`) — commit `1d172e9`
  - [x] **Emission surface — `StdoutExporter` (the first output-producing exporter) + full codegen support for `std.tracing`. Shipped 2026-06-02.** Before this, the entire `std.tracing` surface (the `1d172e9` data shapes + `Exporter` trait) was **interpreter-only** — a *compiled* `LogEvent { ... }.message` read `0` (the seeded struct layouts were absent and the impl bodies never reached codegen), and there was no exporter that actually *emitted* anything. Two pieces shipped: **(1) the emission API** — `struct StdoutExporter` + `impl Exporter for StdoutExporter` in `runtime/stdlib/tracing.kara`, rendering each span/event as one structured logfmt-adjacent line (`[level] message key=value … span_id=N` / `[span] name span_id=N parent_id=M …`, trace-context suffixes only when non-zero). Caller-plumbed, matching the surface's design (the ambient/registered exporter stays the separate `[ ]` item below). Added to `PRELUDE_TYPES`. **(2) first-ever codegen for a pure-Kāra stdlib surface** — unlike the TCP/TLS/WS stdlib (which is `#[compiler_builtin]` + hand-rolled lowerings), the tracing methods are real Kāra bodies. Codegen normally skips baked-stdlib impls (`STDLIB_PROGRAMS` reaches the typechecker but not codegen), so this slice added: seed `Span`/`LogEvent`/`SpanField` layouts via `declare_structs` over the tracing program; a cached **fully-lowered** tracing program (`TRACING_LOWERED_PROGRAM`) — the baked bodies are never type-checked anywhere, so codegen's span-keyed side tables are empty for them, fixed by running the normal pipeline over `tracing.kara` standalone (type-checks clean) and **swapping its 11 span-keyed tables in** only while emitting the tracing bodies (collision-free — tracing AST carries `tracing.kara` spans, the user program is never active during that window); declaration of every tracing impl method so dispatch's `module.get_function("Type.method")` resolves; a **usage gate** that deletes any tracing impl-method declaration left with zero call sites after user bodies compile (keeps tracing-free binaries lean — no dead `Vec`/f-string machinery — and is what lets the IR-shape codegen tests stay valid); and a `Span`/`LogEvent` non-identifier-receiver re-dispatch arm so chained builders (`LogEvent.info(...).with_field(...).in_span(n)`) lower. Tests: 2 interpreter (`test_tracing_stdout_exporter_emits_{event,span}_line`), 4 codegen E2E in `tests/codegen.rs` (`e2e_tracing_stdout_exporter_emits_{events,spans}`, `e2e_tracing_noop_exporter_is_silent`, `e2e_tracing_unused_in_program_emits_no_tracing_bodies`). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets ±llvm`, codegen, par_codegen (105), scaffold (29), memory_sanitizer (73 ASAN), full non-llvm suite. **Update 2026-06-03:** the exporter bodies use the natural multi-interpolation f-string form — they were briefly written with `+` concat to dodge a codegen miscompile this surfaced, now fixed (the `[x]` below).
  - [x] **codegen-bug — f-string accumulator inside a never-executed block freed uninitialized stack (double-free / SIGABRT). Fixed 2026-06-03.** Surfaced 2026-06-02 by the tracing emission bodies; reproduced in pure user code (no tracing). **Symptom:** a `fn ev(e: Struct)` body of the form `let mut line = f"[{e.a}] {e.b}"; for x in e.items { line = line + f"..." }; println(line)`, called ≥2×, aborted on the second call with `pointer being freed was not allocated` on a `.rodata` address (a `String` literal freed as if heap). Required all of: a 2+-interpolation first f-string over owned-struct String fields, the `for`-loop reassigning the accumulator, and the fn called ≥2× (removing any one dodged it). **Root cause:** the loop-body f-string's accumulator got a function-**entry** alloca (`create_entry_alloca`) but its `{null,0,0}` value-init was emitted at the f-string **expression site** — inside the loop body. When the loop never ran, the alloca held uninitialized stack, and the unconditional scope-exit cleanup read a garbage `cap`: fresh-0 on call 1 (skips), but a non-zero leftover from call 1's frame on call 2 → `free` of a garbage/literal pointer. **Fix (`src/codegen.rs` + `src/codegen/exprs.rs`):** new `zero_init_str_acc_at_entry` emits the `{null,0,0}` store at the entry block right after the accumulator's alloca, so a never-executed f-string leaves `cap == 0` and the `cap > 0` free guard skips it; the expression-site init stays for the re-evaluated (loop) case. The `std.tracing` exporter bodies are folded back to the natural f-string form. Regression test: `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_fstring_in_loop_no_double_free` (the minimal two-call repro, asserts clean all-three-lines output). Touches the f-string lowering used by every f-string, so re-verified across the full codegen + memory_sanitizer suites.
  - [ ] Active-span context propagation across async boundaries (state-machine transform preserves active span — codegen + ownership-pass work)
  - [ ] Comptime-driven trace-context plumbing (Kāra-native answer to Rust `tracing`'s proc-macro indirection)
  - [x] **Ambient emission — `Log.{trace,debug,info,warn,error}("...")`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** A `struct Log` namespace in `runtime/stdlib/tracing.kara` (in `PRELUDE_TYPES`) whose assoc fns each build the matching `LogEvent` and emit it through a fresh `StdoutExporter` — so a program can log a message without constructing and threading an exporter value. Because these are assoc-fn bodies over the already-codegen-capable `LogEvent` / `StdoutExporter` surface, they lower through the same tracing-codegen pass and work under both `karac run` and `karac build` (E2E `e2e_tracing_log_ambient_emission` + interpreter `test_tracing_log_ambient_emission_all_levels`). **Surfaced + fixed two codegen bugs:** (a) a struct-literal `let` binding (`let s = StdoutExporter {}`) couldn't resolve its type for method dispatch when the struct lowers to an empty `{}` (collides with every other empty struct in the LLVM-identity reverse-lookup) — fixed generally by taking the type name from the `StructLiteral` AST node (`src/codegen/stmts.rs`); (b) the tracing usage-gate deleted callees before their tracing-method callers compiled (now that tracing methods call each other) — restructured to compile all bodies then fixpoint-prune, snapshotting/restoring the builder insert block across the prune (`src/codegen.rs`). Gate green: codegen (1016), par_codegen (105), memory_sanitizer (73 ASAN), full non-llvm, fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets ±llvm`.
  - [ ] **Configurable ambient exporter — register a sink + min-level filter.** Today `Log.*` always emits to stdout via `StdoutExporter`. The configurable layer — register a different sink (`NoOpExporter` to silence, or a custom exporter) and a process-global minimum level so production can dial verbosity — needs ambient mutable state shared across call sites. v1-interpreter could carry it on a field, but the codegen path wants a runtime global (level) + dynamic dispatch (arbitrary registered exporter), the `with_provider`-shape the spec calls "natural once the network event loop lands." Build it there; the `Log.*` emission entry points are the single insertion point for the level gate.
  - [ ] OTel exporter (post-v1 community library; depends on the trait shape being stable, which lands here)
- [x] **P1 — `std.regex` — compile patterns, match / find / replace.** Lifted from Phase 11 § Scripting-critical. PCRE-like syntax (excluding backreferences for predictable runtime). Compile-once + reuse pattern; `regex.compile(s) -> Result[Regex, RegexError]`. v1 effect-free (no allocates surface — pattern compilation pre-allocates internal buffer). Shipped pre-2026-05-16 across `runtime/stdlib/regex.kara` + typechecker arm in `stdlib_io.rs` + interpreter intrinsic in `method_call_regex.rs`; 13 tests (8 interpreter + 5 typechecker). `captures(s)` from the broader 10B surface (Scripting-critical section below) is deferred.
- [ ] **P1 — `std.process` — `Command` / `Child`; `ProcessTable` effect resource.** Lifted from Phase 11 § Scripting-critical. `Command::new(prog).arg(...).env(...).spawn() -> Result[Child, IoError]`; `Child.wait()` / `Child.try_wait()` / `Child.kill()`. Effects: `sends(ProcessTable)` on spawn; effect-routes through the event loop for non-blocking wait.
  - [x] Type surface: `Command` (builder), `Child` (pid), `ExitStatus`, internal `EnvVar` row type, `ProcessTable` effect resource registered in `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES` — commit `efc565c`
  - [x] Pure-Kāra builder methods: `Command.new(prog) / .arg(a) / .env(k, v)` with state preserved across owned-self chain
  - [x] `sends(ProcessTable)` declared on `spawn` / `wait` / `try_wait` / `kill` signatures; verified through a user wrapper declaring the same effect (`test_process_user_can_declare_sends_process_table_effect`)
  - [x] Real `Command.spawn()` via `std::process::Command` interpreter intrinsic — bodies flipped to `#[compiler_builtin]`, dispatch through `try_eval_process_method` in `src/interpreter/method_call_process.rs`. Pid-keyed `child_table: HashMap<i64, std::process::Child>` on the Interpreter struct holds the live handles between calls. Commit `d379b56`.
  - [x] Real `Child.wait()` / `try_wait()` / `kill()` intrinsics — same dispatch path. `wait` removes the table entry on success; `try_wait` removes only when the child has exited; `kill` leaves the entry in place per spec (caller still needs `wait` to reap). 7 new integration tests covering real spawn + wait, try_wait still-running, kill + wait, env var propagation, and unknown-child wait → IoError.NotFound. Commit `d379b56`.
  - [ ] Execution verbs: `blocks` on the synchronous `wait` form; `suspends` on the future async form (depends on the network event loop)
  - [x] **`stdin` / `stdout` / `stderr` redirection builder methods on `Command`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** New `enum Stdio { Inherit, Null }` (in `PRELUDE_TYPES`) + `Command.stdin(cfg)` / `.stdout(cfg)` / `.stderr(cfg)` owned-self builders threading three `cmd_stdin`/`cmd_stdout`/`cmd_stderr` fields (default `Stdio.Inherit`). `eval_command_spawn` reads each field and calls `std::process::Stdio::null()` only on an explicit `Stdio.Null` (`Inherit` is `std::process`'s own default, left unset) — so `Stdio.Null` discards the child's stream (e.g. spawn a noisy command without polluting the parent's terminal). 2 interpreter tests (`test_process_stdio_builder_records_redirection`, `test_process_spawn_with_null_redirection_waits_clean`); existing 10 process tests re-verified green under the widened `Command` struct. **`Stdio.Piped` deliberately deferred:** capturing a stream needs `Child` to carry read/write handles + accessors, and an *unread* pipe deadlocks a child that fills the buffer — shipping it without the read side would be a footgun. Tracked as the follow-on below.
  - [ ] **`Stdio.Piped` + `Child.stdout()` / `.stderr()` / `.stdin()` handle accessors.** The capture half of redirection: `Stdio.Piped` on a `Command` stream, plus `Child` carrying the OS pipe handles and `read_to_string` / write methods so the parent can drive the child's I/O. Needs `Child` to grow handle fields (it's pid-only today) and the interpreter's `child_table` entry to retain the `std::process::Child`'s `stdout`/`stderr`/`stdin` `Option<ChildStdout>` etc. Build when a real consumer needs to capture subprocess output (the data-pipeline `--data` scaffold is a likely first caller).
- [ ] **P1 — protobuf — wire format + comptime codegen.** `.proto` schema parsing at comptime; comptime emits the message type + serialize / deserialize / merge methods. No separate codegen tool. v1 surface covers proto3; proto2 if time permits. Effects: `allocates(Heap)` on decode; pure on encode.
- [ ] **P1 — File-system event loop — io_uring on Linux, sticky kqueue on BSD/macOS.** Lifts disk-I/O ceiling beyond what epoll covers. Not load-bearing for the 1M+ socket benchmark (epoll/kqueue/IOCP are sufficient there) but matters for mixed-workload demos and disk-bound backends. Cross-platform abstraction in the runtime crate, parallels the network event loop's surface.
- [ ] **P1 — `Pool[T]` — connection-pool primitive.** `Pool::new(create_fn, max_connections, max_waiters)`; `pool.acquire(timeout) -> Result[PooledConnection[T], PoolError]` / drop releases automatically. Bounded waiters with timeout; health-check hook fires on acquire (callable's responsibility); evict-on-error pattern. Library-shape; community database drivers build on this.
  - [x] Type surface: `Pool[T]` / `PooledConnection[T]` (with `pool_handle_id` + `val: T` fields), `PoolError` enum (`Timeout` / `PoolClosed` / `CreateFailed`); `Pool.new(create_fn: Fn() -> T, max_connections, max_waiters)` signature via `impl[T] Pool[T] { ... }` syntax — commit `e694f2c`
  - [x] `acquire(timeout)` signature, plus new `release(conn)` method on `Pool[T]` for explicit slot return (until drop-on-release wires up).
  - [x] Real intrinsic via `try_eval_pool_method` + `eval_pool_new` in `src/interpreter/method_call_pool.rs`. Per-pool state in `pool_table: HashMap<i64, PoolEntry>` keyed by a monotonic `handle_id`; PoolEntry holds the create_fn closure (`Value::Function`), bounds, slot vec, active_count. Single-threaded semantics: acquire serves immediately from a free slot, or mints via create_fn if under cap, or fires `PoolError.Timeout` straight away. Commit `1552c6d`.
  - [x] Closure storage on `Pool[T]` for `create_fn` — held on `PoolEntry.create_fn` as a `Value::Function`. Closures with captures verified end-to-end (`test_pool_create_fn_can_be_a_closure_with_captures`).
  - [ ] **Real `parking_lot::Mutex` + condvar backing the semaphore** — only matters under multi-threaded execution. The single-threaded tree-walk interpreter's collapsed semantics (immediate-serve-or-timeout) is correct for v1; the codegen/runtime path is where the bounded-waiters-with-timeout machinery becomes load-bearing. Lifts here when codegen for `std.process` / `Pool[T]` lands.
  - [ ] **Drop-releases-automatically.** Needs user-`impl Drop` dispatch in the interpreter (currently `eval_stmt::run_cleanup` treats `CleanupAction::Drop` as a trace-only no-op). When that lands, `Pool[T]` gains an `impl Drop for PooledConnection[T]` calling the same release path; the explicit `pool.release(conn)` call becomes optional. Forward-compatible.
  - [ ] **Health-check hook closure** — additional closure stored on `PoolEntry` alongside `create_fn`; fires on the `slots.pop()` branch of acquire, invalidating + minting fresh on Err. Adds a fourth parameter to `Pool.new`. Deferred until a real consumer pins down the hook's signature.
- [ ] **P1 — Application-layer backpressure primitives.** `Semaphore::new(n)` with `acquire(timeout)` / `release`; `BoundedChannel[T]::new(capacity, OnFull::Block | OnFull::FailFast)`; `RateLimiter::new_token_bucket(rate, capacity)` with `try_acquire(key) -> bool` / `acquire(key) -> impl Future`. Effects: `Semaphore` + `RateLimiter` are pure-with-suspends; `BoundedChannel` follows the existing `Channel[T]` effect surface plus `suspends` on full-block. Complementary to deployment-layer providers (which handle per-provider concurrency caps); user code routinely needs application-layer backpressure too.
  - [x] **`Semaphore` — `new(permits)` / `acquire(timeout)` / `release`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** New `runtime/stdlib/semaphore.kara`: `struct Semaphore { handle_id }` + `enum SemaphoreError { Timeout }` (both in `PRELUDE_TYPES`), with `#[compiler_builtin]` `new` / `acquire` / `release` dispatched through the interpreter intrinsic (`src/interpreter/method_call_semaphore.rs`, modeled on `Pool[T]`). Permit state lives in `Interpreter.semaphore_table: HashMap<i64, SemEntry { available, max }>` keyed by handle; `acquire` decrements when a permit is free (`Ok(Unit)`) else fails closed `Err(Timeout)`, `release` increments saturating at the initial budget. **v1 collapsed single-threaded semantics** (same as `Pool[T]`): an exhausted-semaphore `acquire` returns `Timeout` immediately rather than parking — no peer can free a permit mid-call in the tree-walk interpreter; the real parking-with-`timeout` + the `suspends` execution verb land on the codegen/runtime path with the network event loop. 4 interpreter tests (grant-up-to-N-then-timeout, release-returns-a-permit, release-saturates-at-budget, hand-rolled-zero-handle-fails-closed). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets`, full non-llvm suite, llvm build.
  - [x] **`BoundedChannel[T]` — `new(capacity, OnFull::Block | OnFull::FailFast)` + `send` / `recv`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** New `runtime/stdlib/bounded_channel.kara`: `struct BoundedChannel[T] { handle_id }` + companion `enum OnFull { Block, FailFast }` / `enum ChannelError { Full }` (all in `PRELUDE_TYPES`), with `#[compiler_builtin]` `new` / `send` / `recv` through the interpreter intrinsic (`src/interpreter/method_call_bounded_channel.rs`). Buffer lives in `Interpreter.bounded_channel_table: HashMap<i64, BoundedChannelEntry { capacity, fail_fast, queue: VecDeque<Value> }>` (T erases at runtime, like `Pool[T]`); `send` enqueues when under capacity (`Ok(Unit)`) else `Err(ChannelError.Full)`, `recv` dequeues FIFO (`Some(v)` / `None`). **v1 collapsed:** `OnFull.Block` cannot park in the single-threaded interpreter (no peer drains the buffer), so a full send fails like `FailFast`; `recv` returns `None` on empty rather than blocking. The real park-on-full (`suspends`, the `Channel[T]` effect surface) lands on the codegen/runtime path with the network event loop. 3 deterministic interpreter tests (send-bounds-then-FIFO-recv, Block-collapses-to-FailFast, hand-rolled-zero-handle-fails-closed). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets`, full non-llvm suite, llvm build.
  - [x] **`RateLimiter.new_token_bucket(rate, capacity)` + `try_acquire(key) -> bool`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** New `runtime/stdlib/rate_limiter.kara`: `struct RateLimiter { handle_id }` (in `PRELUDE_TYPES`) with `#[compiler_builtin]` `new_token_bucket` / `try_acquire`, dispatched through the interpreter intrinsic (`src/interpreter/method_call_rate_limiter.rs`). Per-limiter state in `Interpreter.rate_limiter_table: HashMap<i64, RateLimiterEntry { rate, capacity, buckets }>`; each key gets a `TokenBucket { tokens, last }` that starts full (so the first `capacity` calls burst) and **lazily refills** by `elapsed * rate` (capped at capacity) on each `try_acquire`, consuming a token when `>= 1`. Monotonic time via `std::time::Instant` read directly in the intrinsic (same pattern as the `Clock`/`RandomSource` ambient resources). 3 deterministic interpreter tests (initial-burst-then-limit, per-key independence, hand-rolled-zero-handle-fails-closed). **v1 = synchronous `try_acquire` only;** the waiting `acquire(key) -> impl Future` form is event-loop dependent — carved below. Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets`, full non-llvm suite, llvm build.
  - [ ] **`RateLimiter.acquire(key) -> impl Future` — the waiting form.** Parks the caller until a token frees for `key` instead of returning `false`. Event-loop dependent (the `suspends` execution verb + the park machinery), lands on the codegen/runtime path with the network event loop. The token-bucket state and refill logic from `try_acquire` are reused; only the on-empty behavior (park-and-retry vs return-false) differs.
- [ ] **P1 — Demo 3: data-engineering pipeline (Kafka → S3 → DuckDB-shape).** Same v1 runtime, `Pool[T]`, TLS, `std.tracing`. Verification artifact for the v64 second-order claim that backend-first investment compounds into the data-engineering persona. Lives in `examples/` as `examples/data-pipeline/`; runs in CI alongside Demo 1 (HTTP+WS server) and Demo 2 (Parallax-or-lite). Cheap incremental engineering, multiplies the v1 launch story.

### v66 graduation P1 additions (2026-05-11)

> v1 P1 items promoted in the v66 general-purpose-foundation graduation. Full design + rationale at [`../../brainstorming/archive/v66_general_purpose_with_data_bonus.md`](../../brainstorming/archive/v66_general_purpose_with_data_bonus.md); canonical entries in [`../deferred.md`](../deferred.md) under each item's name.

- [x] **[→ P1] `std.cli` — argument parser, builder-style API.** `Parser::new(name) / .arg / .flag / .subcommand / .parse() -> Result[Args, CliError]`; automatic `--help` / `--version`; effect `reads(Env)` on `.parse()`. Phase 8 floor. See `deferred.md § std.cli`.
  - [x] Pure-Kāra builder surface: `Parser.new / .about / .arg / .flag`; `Arg.string() / .required() / .help`; `Args.get_string / .get_flag`; `CliError` shape — commit `7295af9`
  - [x] `parse()` walks `Env.args()` and produces real results (named-arg pairing, flag set tracking, positional bucketing, required-arg check)
  - [x] `reads(Env)` effect on `.parse()`
  - [x] `Parser.subcommand(name, sub_parser)` + subcommand-dispatch routing; `Args.sub: Option[SubcommandResult]`; `Args.subcommand_name() -> Option[String]`; `SubcommandResult.get_string / .get_flag`. One level of depth in v1 (matches the `deferred.md` example) — recursive nesting waits for a real user case. Commit `54daf4a`.
  - [x] Automatic `--help` / `-h` / `--version` / `-V` short-circuit in `parse()`; `Parser.help_text(ref self) -> String` renders USAGE / ARGS / FLAGS / SUBCOMMANDS sections from the declared shape; `Parser.version_line(ref self) -> String` renders `<program_name> <version>` (or bare program name if `.version(...)` unset). Sentinel-via-message: returns `Err(CliError { message: <text> })` rather than a new enum variant so the v1 `CliError` struct shape stays stable. Commit `54daf4a`.
- [ ] **[→ P1] `std.embeddings` — cosine similarity (scalar + batched single-query + Q×N matrix), top-k, l2-normalize, batched dot.** Six-function surface over `Tensor[f32, ...]` for RAG / semantic search / recommendation workloads. New v67 graduation: `cosine_similarity_matrix(queries, corpus) -> Tensor[f32, [Q, N]]` is the SGEMM-shaped BLAS-3 production-RAG path. Lands in Phase 11 numerical stdlib slice. See `deferred.md § std.embeddings`.

- [ ] **[→ P1] Hand-vectorized data-spine kernels (v67 §3).** Hand-write the 8 kernel families enumerated in `deferred.md § Hand-Vectorized Data-Spine Commitment` against `Vector[T, N]` rather than relying on LLVM auto-vec: `embeddings.{cosine_similarity, cosine_similarity_batched, cosine_similarity_matrix, dot_batched, l2_normalize, top_k}`, Tensor element-wise `+`/`-`/`*`/`/`, Tensor reductions (`sum`/`mean`/`min`/`max`), activations (`relu`/`sigmoid`/`tanh`/`softmax`), and transcendental routing via `std.simd.math`. **Ceiling commitment** — final scope narrows kernel-by-kernel after the auto-vec measurement on a representative kernel once Phase 7's LLVM backend can compile one (e.g., `cosine_similarity_batched` on `Tensor[f32, [10_000, 768]]`). Rows where LLVM auto-vec hits ~80% of hand-written SIMD drop into a "trust auto-vec" footnote; rows where auto-vec hits ~20% stay hand-written. Per-kernel speedup targets per the table in the deferred entry. Lands in Phase 11 numerical stdlib slice.

- [ ] **[→ P1] `std.simd.math` — SIMD-friendly transcendentals.** New sub-surface for Sleef-class polynomial approximations of `exp`, `log`, `sqrt`, `tanh`, `sigmoid` on `Vector[f32, N]` and `Vector[f64, N]`. Required because LLVM auto-vec does not substitute vectorized exp for scalar `expf` — that is a known auto-vec dead end. The transcendental rows in the v67 spine (and the softmax / GeLU / cross-entropy paths in `std.autograd`) route through these. Lands in Phase 11 numerical stdlib slice. See `deferred.md § Hand-Vectorized Data-Spine Commitment > std.simd.math sub-surface`.

- [ ] **[→ P1] `cpu-baseline` knob + `#[multiversion]` attribute.** Add `cpu-baseline = "v1" | "v2" | "v3" | "v4"` field to `kara.toml`; default `"v3"`. Map per-architecture per the table in `design.md § Portable SIMD > Multiversioning` (x86-64-v{N} on x86; armv8-a / armv8.2-a / armv8.4-a / armv8.6-a on aarch64). Add `#[target_feature("...")]` and `#[multiversion(baseline, "...", ...)]` attributes — `#[multiversion]` is sugar over duplicate `#[target_feature]`-tagged variants of a function; compiler synthesizes a dispatcher (ifunc on Linux; manual pointer-swap on macOS/Windows). Required for the v67 §3 spine kernels that ship AVX-512 / SVE2 variants alongside the v3-baseline implementation. Lands in Phase 7+ codegen / Phase 11 numerical stdlib slice. See `design.md § Portable SIMD > Multiversioning`.
- [ ] **[→ P1] `std.autograd` — reverse-mode automatic differentiation.** `shared struct Tape` with `writes(GradTape)` effect; separate `Var[T, S]` wrapper (Q8 locked); operator overloads on `Var`; activations (relu/sigmoid/tanh/softmax/gelu/silu); losses (mse/cross_entropy/bce); `grad` / `value_and_grad`; GPU-aware tape recording. Reverse-mode only at v1. Lands in Phase 11 numerical/ML stdlib slice. See `deferred.md § std.autograd`. **`std.nn` / `std.optim` decision deferred to engineering-start (Q7)** — see `deferred.md § Neural Network Framework`.
- [ ] **[→ P1] `LazyDataFrame` — Option A v1 scope.** Predicate pushdown + projection pushdown + constant folding + CSE. `df.lazy() / .filter / .select / .group_by(...).agg(...) / .join / .sort / .limit / .collect / .explain`. Target ~2-3K LOC. Lands in Phase 11 numerical/data-science slice (lifted from v1.5). Full optimizer expansion at P2 — see `deferred.md § Lazy DataFrame Query Optimizer Expansion`.
- [ ] **[→ P1] Statistical methods on `Column[T: Numeric]` / `DataFrame`.** `Column`: `mean`, `std`, `var`, `median`, `quantile(q)`, `min`, `max`, `sum`; `Column[f64]`: `corr(other)`; `DataFrame.describe() -> DataFrame`. Trait-dispatched so future `GpuColumn` / `GpuTensor` implements the same surface. Lands in Phase 11 numerical/data-science slice. See `deferred.md § Statistical Methods on Column / DataFrame`.
- [ ] **[→ P1] `docs/book/src/data.md` — data chapter.** Tensor / Column / DataFrame / lazy query / Arrow IPC / Parquet / CSV; one ~50-line end-to-end example; pointers to `std.linalg` / `std.fft` / `std.einsum` / `std.embeddings` / `std.random.distributions` / `std.autograd`. Discoverability surface for the "quiet data bonus" positioning. Lands in Phase 8.5 docs window.
- [ ] **[→ P1] `examples/data/` — worked programs.** `csv-to-parquet.kara`, `embeddings-rag.kara`, `stats-summary.kara`, `lazy-query.kara`. Double as integration tests against the data stdlib. Lands in Phase 8.5 docs window.
- [ ] **[→ P1] `kara-postgres` — canonical Postgres driver, project-owned package.** Dogfooding-grade — written to exercise effect system, `Pool[T]`, auto-concurrency, `with_provider`, structured errors. Scope: TCP, prepared statements, simple-query protocol, basic type mapping (i64/String/f64/bool/bytes/NULL/timestamp/uuid), transactions, parameter binding, `Pool[T]` integration. Stdlib position (no `std.sql`) unchanged — driver lives outside `std.*` as a project-owned package. **Handover-to-community policy explicitly deferred to engineering-start (Q3).** See `deferred.md § Canonical Postgres Driver (kara-postgres)`.
- [ ] **[→ P1] `kara-lsp` binary + VS Code extension (Phase 8.5 Track 3).** v1 floor: syntax highlighting, diagnostics streaming, go-to-def, hover (type + effect signature), find references, document symbols, **type-aware completion** (~4-6 weeks), formatting via LSP, signature help. v1 stretch (engineering-time-permitting): rename, code actions, semantic tokens, workspace symbols. v1.x post-launch: effect-aware completion (Kāra-specific differentiator), inline-explain / type lens, refactoring, Neovim + JetBrains plugins. Tracker in roadmap at `## Phase 8.5: V1 Ship Readiness > Track 3: Language Server`. See `deferred.md § Language Server (kara-lsp) — v1 Editor Surface`.
- [ ] **[→ P1] GPU codegen — multi-vendor v1 (wgpu primary + CUDA opt-in).** Pulled forward from Phase 10 to v1 ship gate (Q6). Multi-vendor coverage already in existing Phase 10 design — wgpu auto-selects Metal on macOS, Vulkan on Linux, DX12 on Windows, WebGPU in browser; CUDA opt-in via `--target cuda`. Implementation tasks at [`phase-10-targets.md § GPU compute shaders`](phase-10-targets.md). Vendor-neutral API design from day one is satisfied by the wgpu-primary spec.
