### v70 graduation P1 additions (2026-06-01)

> v1 P1 items promoted in the v70 arena/handle stdlib surface graduation. Full design + rationale at [`../../brainstorming/archive/v70_arena_handle_v1_surface.md`](../../brainstorming/archive/v70_arena_handle_v1_surface.md); the v70 brainstorm validates these primitives against four workload lenses (connection pool, AST bulk arena, regex NFA, ECS) plus a compiler-as-lens audit. Both items are split-primitive complements to the existing P1 `Pool[T]` entry above (which covers generational reuse) — `Arena[T]` covers bulk allocation with one shared lifetime; `Symbol`/`Interner` covers deduplicating string handles.

- [ ] **[→ P1] `Arena[T]` + `ArenaRef[T]` — bulk-allocation primitive.** Single-lifetime allocator: `Arena.new() -> Arena[T]`; `arena.push(value: T) -> ArenaRef[T]` (bump-allocate); `arena.get(r: ArenaRef[T]) -> ref T` (index, no liveness check — all items live until the arena drops). All items freed in bulk when the `Arena[T]` value drops. No per-item release; no generation counter. Use cases: parse trees per compilation, AST nodes, frame-scoped game data, regex NFA states during construction. Distinct from `Pool[T]` (which supports per-item release and stale-handle detection). Effects: `allocates(Heap)` on `push`. Sub-items:
  - [ ] Type surface: `Arena[T]` + `ArenaRef[T]` declared in baked stdlib `runtime/stdlib/arena.kara`; `Arena.new() / .push / .get` signatures via `impl[T] Arena[T] { ... }` syntax peer to the existing `Pool[T]` declaration pattern.
  - [ ] Real interpreter intrinsic via `try_eval_arena_method` + `eval_arena_new` in new `src/interpreter/method_call_arena.rs`. Per-arena state in `arena_table: HashMap<i64, Vec<Value>>` keyed by a monotonic `arena_handle_id`; `ArenaRef[T]` carries `(arena_handle_id, index)`. Single-threaded semantics: `push` appends to the Vec and returns a fresh `ArenaRef`; `get` returns a borrow into the Vec at the index. Mirrors `pool_table` structure from `src/interpreter/method_call_pool.rs`.
  - [ ] Snapshot/restore API: `arena.high_water_mark() -> ArenaCheckpoint`, `arena.rewind_to(cp: ArenaCheckpoint)` — used for typechecker symbol-table backtracking, mid-parse error recovery, transactional middleware rollback. Truncates the Vec to the recorded length; subsequently-created `ArenaRef[T]`s past the checkpoint become use-after-free at runtime (debug-mode panic; release-mode undefined for v1, sound subsequent slice). Independent from drop-at-arena-end.
  - [ ] Codegen lowering — new `src/codegen/arena.rs` mirroring the eventual `pool.rs` shape: `Arena[T]` lowers to a Vec-like struct (`{ data: *mut T, len: i64, cap: i64 }`); `push` calls a `karac_runtime_arena_push` runtime helper; `get` GEPs into the data array. `Arena[T]` drop calls `karac_runtime_arena_free` which iterates the Vec dropping each element per `T`'s drop kind. Gated on user-`impl Drop` dispatch in codegen (shared dependency with `Pool[T]` codegen path entry above).
  - [ ] Effect-checker seeding for `Arena.push` (`allocates(Heap)`) and `Arena.new` (`allocates(Heap)`) in the startup-seeding block peer to the `Map.insert` / `Vec.push` seeding pattern.

- [ ] **[→ P1] `Symbol` + `Interner` — deduplicating string handle primitive.** Compact integer handle for interned strings: `Interner.new() -> Interner`; `interner.intern(s: ref String) -> Symbol` (returns the existing handle if `s` was previously interned; otherwise stores `s` and returns a fresh handle); `interner.resolve(sym: Symbol) -> ref String` (handle → string lookup). Equality on `Symbol` is integer comparison (no string compare); hashing is integer hashing. Use cases: HTTP-header canonicalization, JSON-key dedup, log-key dedup, regex character classes, comptime identifier resolution, every compiler's identifier handling. The Interner is `Arena[T]`-adjacent (durable lifetime, no per-item release) but adds a dedup HashMap on top — distinct primitive worth its own name and worth its own teaching surface ("what's interning for?"). Effects: `allocates(Heap)` on `intern` when a fresh handle is minted; pure on `resolve` and on re-`intern` of an already-interned string. Sub-items:
  - [ ] Type surface: `Symbol` (transparent wrapper around `i64`) and `Interner` declared in baked stdlib `runtime/stdlib/interner.kara`; `Interner.new() / .intern / .resolve` signatures via `impl Interner { ... }`. `Symbol` derives `Eq`, `Hash`, `Copy`, `Display` (renders as the underlying string via the Interner — but the `Symbol` itself can't reach the Interner; `Display` requires the user to thread the Interner through, like Rust's `Symbol`/`Ident` pattern). Resolved alternative: `Symbol` carries a `(symbol_id, interner_handle_id)` pair so `Display` can call back into the Interner. Trade-off decided as part of the spec writeup, not in the v70 brainstorm.
  - [ ] Real interpreter intrinsic via `try_eval_interner_method` + `eval_interner_new` in new `src/interpreter/method_call_interner.rs`. Per-Interner state in `interner_table: HashMap<i64, (Vec<String>, HashMap<String, i64>)>` — the Vec is the symbol-id → string lookup, the HashMap is the dedup index. Mirrors `pool_table` / `arena_table` shape.
  - [ ] Codegen lowering — new `src/codegen/interner.rs`. `Symbol` lowers to a bare `i64`; `Interner` lowers to a struct holding (Vec, HashMap). `intern` calls `karac_runtime_interner_intern`; `resolve` calls `karac_runtime_interner_resolve`. Gated on user-`impl Drop` dispatch (drop frees both Vec and HashMap).
  - [ ] Effect-checker seeding for `Interner.intern` (`allocates(Heap)`) and `Interner.new` (`allocates(Heap)`).
  - [ ] Integration sites to validate: `f"..."` formatter (route String interpolation through Interner where dedup is profitable — design decision, not a v1 commitment), HTTP header canonicalization in `std.http`, JSON key dedup in `std.json`. Each is an independent slice; the Interner primitive itself doesn't depend on them, but they're the consumers that justify it as P1.

---

### Pre-existing Phase 8 work

- [x] **`String.from_utf8(Vec[u8]) -> Result[String, Utf8Error]` — UTF-8-validating String constructor (interpreter MVP).** Filed 2026-05-22 after the typechecker rejection of undeclared `Type.method(...)` calls landed (commit `db573a4`) — that change made the typecheck-time gap surface as a clean diagnostic instead of an unrelated codegen explosion downstream. Spec'd in `design.md:4431` (`if let Ok(s) = String.from_utf8(input) { ... }`). Landed 2026-05-22 as an interpreter-only slice mirroring the peer pattern (`FileSystem.read_to_string`, `Url.decode`, `Base64.decode`, `Json.parse` — all interpreter-only today). **Shipped.** (1) `enum Utf8Error { InvalidByte, IncompleteSequence, Other(String) }` declared in new `runtime/stdlib/utf8_error.kara`, registered in `STDLIB_SOURCES` and the prelude `PRELUDE_TYPES` list peer to `IoError` / `VarError`. (2) Path-keyed function signature `String.from_utf8(Vec[u8]) -> Result[String, Utf8Error]` registered in `register_compiler_intrinsic_env` (parallel to `env.var`); routes through `resolve_path_type`'s `env.functions` lookup. (3) Interpreter dispatch arm at `src/interpreter/eval_call.rs` `"String.from_utf8"` (peer to `Base64.decode` / `Url.decode`); calls `std::str::from_utf8` and maps `error_len() == None` → `Utf8Error.IncompleteSequence`, `Some(_)` → `Utf8Error.InvalidByte` (Rust's documented contract for the two failure modes). 3 typechecker tests (`test_string_from_utf8_returns_result_string_utf8_error`, `test_utf8_error_variants_exist`, `test_string_from_utf8_wrong_arg_type_is_error`) + 4 interpreter tests (`test_string_from_utf8_valid_returns_ok`, `test_string_from_utf8_invalid_byte_returns_err_invalid_byte`, `test_string_from_utf8_incomplete_returns_err_incomplete_sequence`, `test_string_from_utf8_empty_returns_ok_empty`). **Deferred — codegen.** The original entry called for codegen dispatch in `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` returning a "4-word `{tag, w0, w1, w2}` aggregate matching the existing Result lowering", but the existing Result lowering at `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` (`src/codegen/declarations.rs:2300`) is **1 payload word**, not 3 — a String payload (3 words: data/len/cap) doesn't fit. Widening Result to a 3-word payload area parallels the existing Option widening, but also requires propagating all payload words in `compile_question`'s `?`-shortcircuit (currently only forwards `w0`) and registering String/Vec drop kinds on the seeded Result layout (currently `EnumDropKind::None`). That's a cross-cutting follow-up that affects every existing interpreter-only `Result[String, _]` / `Result[Vec[u8], _]` intrinsic (`FileSystem.read_to_string`, `Url.decode`, `Base64.decode`, `Json.parse`) — best landed as one slice "widen Result codegen + flip all five intrinsics" rather than per-intrinsic. **Deferred — special-arm cleanup.** Retiring the `String.from(x)` / `String.new()` / `String.with_capacity(n)` typechecker special arms in favor of real baked-stdlib `impl String { ... }` declarations also waits on a separate slice — `env_add_impl` currently silently bails on `Type::Str` targets (the `_ => return` fall-through after `lower_type_expr`), so `impl String { ... }` from stdlib source has no effect today. Wiring that means extending the canonical-target-name match arm to handle `Type::Str` → `"String"`. The kata-91 bench's `Slice[u8]` parameter shape is unchanged regardless — it's the correct apples-to-apples bench design vs the C/Rust/Go peers (byte-level DP work, no per-iter String alloc).

- [x] **Standard I/O surface — stdlib implementation (Phase 8 interpreter MVP).** `IoError` enum (`NotFound`, `PermissionDenied`, `AlreadyExists`, `UnexpectedEof`, `InvalidUtf8`, `Interrupted`, `Other(String)`) registered in the prelude and typechecker. `Stdin`, `Stdout`, `Stderr`, `FileSystem` added to `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES`. Interpreter builtins: `Stdin.read_line()`, `Stdin.read_to_string()` → `Result[String, IoError]`; `Stdout.flush()`, `Stderr.flush()` → `Unit`; `FileSystem.read_to_string(path)` → `Result[String, IoError]`; `FileSystem.write(path, contents)` → `Result[Unit, IoError]`. Typechecker signatures registered via dot-joined `"TypeName.method"` key looked up in `resolve_path_type`. 5 typechecker tests + 4 interpreter tests added. `env.args()` → `Vec[String]` and `env.var(name)` → `Result[String, VarError]` added: `VarError` (`NotPresent`, `NotUnicode`) registered in prelude + typechecker; resolver registers lowercase `"env"` as a `SymbolKind::Module` alias; both `"Env.args"` / `"env.args"` and `"Env.var"` / `"env.var"` registered in the function table; interpreter maps `"env"` → `"Env"` in `eval_method_call` for resource dispatch. 14 typechecker tests + 14 interpreter tests added. Sub-items factored out as separate trackable items: `impl From[VarError] for IoError` (shipped); `env.set` (shipped); `File` handle type (see entry below); `BufReader` (see entry below); book tutorial coverage, network I/O, and process spawning live under their respective Phase 8 surfaces.

- [x] **`env.set(name: String, value: String)` + `writes(Env)` effect.** Landed 2026-05-08. `env.var()` and `env.args()` companion shipped: lowercase `env.set` registered in `register_compiler_intrinsic_env` (peer to `env.var`), capitalized `Env.set` declared in baked stdlib `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` as `#[compiler_builtin] fn set(name: String, value: String) { }` (peer to `Env.var`). Interpreter dispatch arm in `dispatch_builtin_resource_method_with_values` calls `std::env::set_var(&name, &value)` (runtime crate is Rust 2021 edition, so `set_var` is safe — interpreter is single-threaded at this surface), tracks `writes(Env)`, returns `Value::Unit`. Effectchecker seeds both `Env.set` and `env.set` with `writes(Env)` in the startup-seeding block (peer to the `Client.get`/`Client.post` Network seeding); the lowercase form parses as `MethodCall { object: Identifier("env") }` (the `starts_upper` gate keeps it out of the `Path` parse), so the `MethodCall` arm of `collect_calls_in_expr` mirrors the typechecker / interpreter lowercase-module alias by emitting `Env.<method>` as the call key when the receiver is the bare identifier `env`. Five new tests: `test_env_set_typechecks` and `test_env_set_wrong_arg_type_is_error` (typechecker, signature shape + arg-type error); `test_env_set_round_trips_via_var` (interpreter, `env.set` then `env.var` observes the same value); `test_env_set_infers_writes_env`, `test_env_set_capitalized_form_infers_writes_env`, `test_pub_fn_calling_env_set_must_declare_writes_env` and `test_pub_fn_with_writes_env_declared_accepts_env_set` (effectchecker, both call-key paths + negative `MissingEffectDeclaration` + positive declared-effect dual). Cargo test 2967 + LLVM 3258 green; clippy + fmt clean.

- [x] **`impl From[VarError] for IoError`.** Standard I/O Phase 8 follow-up — needed for `?`-propagation from `env.var(...) -> Result[String, VarError]` into functions returning `Result[T, IoError]`. Variant mapping: `VarError.NotPresent` → `IoError.NotFound`; `VarError.NotUnicode` → `IoError.InvalidUtf8`.

- [x] **`File` handle type — stateful file I/O shipped 2026-05-26 (F1–F6 + F4b).** All seven sub-tasks complete: interpreter MVP, runtime shim, codegen type lowering + extern declarations, method codegen + KaracIoResult unpacker, scope-exit cleanup, ?-propagation tests, and broader E2E coverage. End-to-end `karac build` of File code produces binaries that correctly create / read / write / flush / close files through the OS, with IoError variants propagating through both direct match and `?` shorthand. **What this entry does NOT cover (deferred to follow-on slices):** seek / sync_all / metadata methods (F1 omitted them from the minimum useful surface; the runtime + extern declarations for seek are already in place via F2/F3, so adding them at the surface is a small follow-on); the non-destructured `Result[File, IoError]` leak (`let _r = File.open(p);` without destructuring — no Drop hook for the wrapped variant; F4b registers cleanup on the destructured handle only); concurrent reads / writes on the same handle (Mutex serializes, but no Kāra-side handle cloning surface exists at v1); BufReader (separate entry below). Standard I/O Phase 8 follow-up factored out of the parent "Standard I/O surface" entry above. Today `FileSystem.read_to_string(path)` / `FileSystem.write(path, contents)` cover one-shot whole-file ops, but stateful read/write (incremental, seekable, with explicit flush) requires a `File` handle type with a live OS file descriptor. **Proposed v1 surface:** `File.open(path: String) -> Result[File, IoError]` (read-only), `File.create(path: String) -> Result[File, IoError]` (write, truncate), `File.append(path: String) -> Result[File, IoError]` (write, position at end); methods `file.read(buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (bytes-read; 0 = EOF), `file.write(buf: Slice[u8]) -> Result[usize, IoError]`, `file.flush() -> Result[Unit, IoError]`, `file.seek(pos: SeekFrom) -> Result[u64, IoError]` (SeekFrom enum: Start / Current / End), `file.sync_all() -> Result[Unit, IoError]` (data + metadata fsync), `file.metadata() -> Result[Metadata, IoError]` (size, modified, kind). Drop releases the file descriptor via the FreeFileHandle cleanup action peer to the existing FreeMapHandle pattern. **Effects:** `reads(FileSystem)` on `open` / `read` / `seek` / `metadata`; `writes(FileSystem)` on `create` / `append` / `write` / `flush` / `sync_all`; pure on construction-after-open (no-op). **Approach:** interpreter MVP first, then codegen following the `Map[K,V]` precedent (line 89-99). The earlier blocker (`Result[T, IoError]` 1-word payload, called out in the line-79 `String.from_utf8` entry) has since been resolved — `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` widened `Result` to 4 payload words on 2026-05-21 (phase-8 line 435 slice 2 widening), so a `File` (1-word opaque ptr) Ok arm and an `IoError.Other(String)` (3-word) Err arm both fit. The remaining work is just the runtime-shim + opaque-ptr + method-codegen chain Map[K,V] shipped in 6 sub-tasks. **Cancel-safety annotation:** the `File` type carries a notional "has unflushed writes" bit that flips on `.write()` and clears on `.flush()` / `.sync_all()`. Shipped as `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "flush")]` on `File.write` in `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` alongside slice 3a of [`phase-6-runtime.md` line 155](phase-6-runtime.md) (2026-05-26); the slice-3a walker reads the attribute and rejects yields under an unflushed write. **Cross-references:** parent at line 81 ("Standard I/O surface"); realized in [`phase-6-runtime.md` line 155 slice 3a (RAII flow-sensitive detection — File seeding)](phase-6-runtime.md). **Sub-task plan** (mirrors Map[K,V] line 89-99 — each is a separate shippable slice):
  - [x] **F1 — Interpreter MVP shipped 2026-05-26.** Mirrors the Map[K,V] / Sender / Receiver pattern: the typechecker sees an empty struct `File { }` declared in `runtime/stdlib/io.kara`; the interpreter holds the actual `std::fs::File` in a new `Value::File(Arc<Mutex<std::fs::File>>)` variant; `Arc` keeps the variant Clone-friendly without requiring Clone on `std::fs::File` itself (which is intentionally non-Clone — a clone would be a `dup(2)` syscall, not a free op). Drop on the last Arc closes the OS fd via `std::fs::File`'s own Drop impl. **Surface:** `File.open(path)` / `.create(path)` / `.append(path)` → `Result[File, IoError]`; `file.read(buf: mut Slice[u8])` / `file.write(buf: Slice[u8])` → `Result[usize, IoError]`; `file.flush()` → `Result[Unit, IoError]`. All baked in `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` with `#[compiler_builtin]` stubs and `with reads(FileSystem)` / `with writes(FileSystem)` clauses. **Interpreter dispatch:** path-call constructors in `eval_call.rs` (single new `"File.open" | "File.create" | "File.append"` arm using `std::fs::OpenOptions` per mode); instance methods in a new `src/interpreter/method_call_file.rs` (`try_eval_file_method` covering `read` / `write` / `flush`, locking the mutex per call, reading bytes through the slice's storage). `std::io::Error` → `IoError` mapping reuses the existing `io_error_from_std` helper (NotFound / PermissionDenied / AlreadyExists / UnexpectedEof / InvalidData→InvalidUtf8 / Interrupted / Other(String)). `Value::File` added to the `variant_name` exhaustive match and the `Display` impl (renders as `<File>`); `PartialEq` falls through to the `_ => false` catch-all (file handles aren't structurally comparable at v1). **Effect-checker seeding:** hand-seeded in `src/effectchecker.rs` alongside the Env.set / Client.get patterns — `File.open` / `File.read` carry `reads(FileSystem)`; `File.create` / `File.append` / `File.write` / `File.flush` carry `writes(FileSystem)`. The baked `with` clauses propagate through `collect_declared_effects` for the declaration side, but the path-keyed lookup the inference walker performs for free-function and instance-method calls reads from `inferred_effects`, so explicit seeding bridges declaration → inference for stdlib builtins (same pattern Map / Channel / Sender use). **Tests:** 4 new interpreter tests (`test_file_create_write_flush_reopen_read_roundtrip` end-to-end byte round-trip; `test_file_open_nonexistent_returns_io_error_not_found` Err arm with NotFound variant; `test_file_append_constructor_writes_at_end` two-call concatenation; `test_file_flush_on_writable_handle_returns_ok`); 7 new typechecker tests (signature shape for each method + wrong-arg-type rejection); 3 new effect-checker tests (missing reads(FileSystem) on File.open + missing writes(FileSystem) on File.create + positive declared-effects path). **Empirical smoke:** end-to-end `karac run /tmp/file_smoke.kara` round-trip (create → write 3 bytes → flush → open → read 3 bytes) succeeds with the expected output. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (typechecker 1248 → 1256, interpreter 646 → 650, effectchecker 263 → 267). Files: `src/prelude.rs` (`File` in PRELUDE_TYPES); `src/interpreter.rs` (new `mod method_call_file`); `src/interpreter/value.rs` (new `Value::File` variant + Display/variant_name arms); `src/interpreter/eval_call.rs` (constructor dispatch); `src/interpreter/method_call_file.rs` (new — instance-method dispatch); `src/interpreter/method_call.rs` (wire `try_eval_file_method` into the dispatch chain); `src/effectchecker.rs` (FileSystem-effect seeding for File methods); `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` (baked `struct File { }` + `impl File { ... }` with effect clauses); `tests/interpreter.rs`; `tests/typechecker.rs`; `tests/effectchecker.rs`. **Defers** `seek` / `sync_all` / `metadata` to a follow-on slice — minimum useful surface for slice 3 of phase-6 line 155 (RAII flow-sensitive design) only.
  - [x] **F2 — Runtime shim shipped 2026-05-26.** New `runtime/src/file.rs` with the v1 ABI surface: `KaracFile { inner: Mutex<std::fs::File> }` opaque handle; `KaracIoResult { value: i64, error_kind: i32, _pad: i32, error_msg_ptr: *mut u8, error_msg_len: i64 }` unified result shape (32 bytes, layout-pinned) returned from every entry point so codegen at F4 destructures one struct into both the Ok/Err arms; symbols `karac_runtime_file_open` / `_create` / `_append` (handle returned in `value` cast to i64) and `karac_runtime_file_read` / `_write` (bytes count in `value`) / `_flush` / `_close` / `_seek` (added preemptively for the follow-on slice; not yet exposed at the Kāra surface). **Design fork settled:** the unified `KaracIoResult` replaces the originally planned (out-param handle + errno-style return) shape — codegen reads one struct vs. branching on multiple return values, and the `IoError.Other(String)` message path (allocated via `std::alloc::alloc` on the runtime side, transferred to the Kāra-side `String` aggregate's drop path) is encoded directly in `error_msg_ptr`/`_len`. IoError variant tags: 0 = Ok, 1 = NotFound, 2 = PermissionDenied, 3 = AlreadyExists, 4 = UnexpectedEof, 5 = InvalidUtf8 (from `ErrorKind::InvalidData`), 6 = Interrupted, 7 = Other. **Lifetime:** `Box::into_raw` on open-family; `karac_runtime_file_close` reconstructs the Box and drops it (releasing the OS fd via `std::fs::File`'s Drop). Null-handle is a no-op for close. **5 runtime unit tests** in `runtime/src/file.rs::tests`: ABI layout pin (every field offset + total size), end-to-end round-trip (create → write → flush → close → reopen → read), NotFound error path, null-close safety, append-mode extends existing file. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (runtime tests 88 → 93). Files: `runtime/src/file.rs` (new — ~430 LOC including tests), `runtime/src/lib.rs` (new `mod file` declaration). **What F2 does NOT cover:** codegen-side wiring — symbols are exported but no Kāra-callable path reaches them yet. F3 declares the externs in the codegen; F4 lowers method calls to use them; F5 verifies `?`-propagation; F6 closes out with E2E coverage.
  - [x] **F3 — Type lowering + extern fn declarations shipped 2026-05-26.** Two-part change. (1) `File` lowers to opaque `ptr` in `llvm_type_for_type_expr` (`src/codegen/types_lowering.rs`), parallel to the existing `Map[K, V]` / `Set[T]` / `Request` cases — single-segment path-type name → `context.ptr_type(AddressSpace::default()).into()`. No side-table is needed (File carries no element-typed sub-state, unlike Map's `map_key_types` / `map_val_types`). (2) All `karac_runtime_file_*` externs declared in `Codegen::new()` (`src/codegen.rs`, after the HTTP-extern block): `karac_runtime_file_open` / `_create` / `_append` ((ptr, i64) → KaracIoResult), `_read` / `_write` ((ptr, ptr, i64) → KaracIoResult), `_flush` ((ptr) → KaracIoResult), `_close` ((ptr) → void). The `_seek` extern is declared by F2 but not by F3 — F1's surface didn't expose it. **KaracIoResult struct shape** declared inline matches the runtime's `#[repr(C)]` layout exactly (`{ i64 value, i32 error_kind, i32 _pad, ptr error_msg_ptr, i64 error_msg_len }`, 32 bytes, alignment 8). Reusable helper `Codegen::kara_io_result_type()` added in `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (gated `#[allow(dead_code)]` until F4 consumes it). **ABI commitment:** LLVM models the struct return directly via `fn_type` with a struct return type; Rust's `extern "C"` calling convention applies the target-native struct-return ABI (sret-via-hidden-pointer on x86_64 SystemV when the struct exceeds 16 bytes; indirect-via-x8 on AArch64). Both sides agreeing on "returns this 32-byte struct" produces ABI-aligned code without explicit sret threading on the LLVM side. If a target surfaces a mismatch in F4/F6 E2E tests, fall back to an explicit `*mut KaracIoResult` out-param shape (requires re-baking F2 + this declaration). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (no new tests at F3 — the lowering is exercised implicitly by F4 method codegen). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (extern block, ~50 lines), `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (File → opaque ptr arm + `kara_io_result_type` helper). **What F3 does NOT cover:** call-site lowering (F4) — the externs are declared but no call site reaches them yet.
  - [x] **F4 — Method codegen + KaracIoResult → Result[T, IoError] unpacker shipped 2026-05-26.** New `src/codegen/file.rs` module with the shared `Codegen::lower_kara_io_result(slot, ok_kind)` helper (loads the four KaracIoResult fields via GEPs against a stack slot, branches on `error_kind == 0`, builds the surface Result aggregate). Three constructor wrappers (`compile_file_constructor` switching on `karac_runtime_file_open` / `_create` / `_append`) wired into `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` ahead of `Server.serve_static`'s `type_name == "Server"` arm — the constructor-dispatch precedent. Three method wrappers (`compile_file_read` / `_write` / `_flush`) wired into `src/codegen/method_call.rs` ahead of the `TcpStream.read` arm — the method-dispatch precedent. **Pattern-binding int→ptr re-typing** in `src/codegen/pattern_binding.rs`: parallel arm to the existing `shared_types` path that catches `pattern_binding_types[span] == "File"` and reconstructs the `ptr` LLVM type from the destructured i64 payload word. Without this, `match File.open(p) { Ok(f) => f.read(...) }` would compile `f` as an IntValue at the method-dispatch site and panic on `.into_pointer_value()`. **Design fork — struct-return → out-param ABI:** the F2/F3 first cut declared the runtime extern signature as returning `KaracIoResult` by value, with LLVM modelling the struct return directly. End-to-end smoke surfaced a corrupted-stack hang at the call boundary — the 32-byte struct exceeds the 16-byte register-return threshold on every supported target (System V x86_64 sret-via-hidden-pointer; AAPCS AArch64 indirect-via-x8), and modelling the indirect-return ABI in LLVM IR requires `sret` / `byval` parameter attributes that must match Rust's exact lowering on each target. F4 amended F2 + F3 to use an out-param shape: every extern takes `out: *mut KaracIoResult` as the first arg, callee writes into the slot, no return value. Codegen allocas a slot in the function entry block via `alloca_io_result_slot`, passes its address, then GEPs + loads the field values. The runtime crate's 5 unit tests were updated to call through the new ABI (`fresh_result()` helper allocates the slot per call). **IoError variant tag mapping:** runtime tags shift by 1 to reserve 0 for the OK sentinel; the codegen unpacker emits `io_tag = error_kind - 1` so IoError.NotFound=0 / PermissionDenied=1 / ... / Other=6 lines up with the source-order tag assignment from `runtime/stdlib/io_error.kara`. For `Other(String)`, the runtime-allocated message buffer transfers ownership to the codegen-side Kāra `String` aggregate via `error_msg_ptr` / `error_msg_len` (the codegen stores `len` for both `len` and `cap`, so the Kāra-side String drop path frees correctly). **End-to-end smoke verified:** `karac build` of a kara program that creates a temp file, writes "hi\n" through `f.write(data)`, flushes, reopens, and reads back into a Vec produces a binary that runs to completion and writes the expected 3 bytes to disk. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all test binaries. Files: `runtime/src/file.rs` (ABI signatures + tests rewritten to out-param shape), `src/codegen.rs` (extern declarations updated to void-return + out-param first arg), `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (`#[allow(dead_code)]` removed from `kara_io_result_type` — F4 consumes it), `src/codegen/file.rs` (new — ~380 LOC: unpacker + 3 constructors + 3 method wrappers + slot allocator), `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (constructor dispatch arm), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (read/write/flush dispatch arms), `src/codegen/pattern_binding.rs` (File int→ptr re-typing arm). **What F4 does NOT cover:** scope-exit cleanup via `FreeFileHandle` (split out as F4b — the file descriptor leaks until process exit at v1 if user code doesn't otherwise close it); end-to-end `tests/codegen.rs` cases (F6 covers); `?`-propagation verification (F5 covers).
  - [x] **F4b — `FreeFileHandle` scope-exit cleanup shipped 2026-05-26.** New `CleanupAction::FreeFileHandle { file_alloca: PointerValue }` variant in `src/codegen/state.rs` peer to `FreeMapHandle`; new `track_file_var(file_alloca)` in `src/codegen/runtime.rs` pushes the action onto the active scope frame; emission path in the scope-cleanup drain loads the handle from the alloca and calls `karac_runtime_file_close` — null-handle is a no-op on the runtime side, so no guard is needed. Hook in `src/codegen/pattern_binding.rs`: the F4 `type_name == "File"` int→ptr re-typing arm now calls `track_file_var(alloca)` immediately after registering the binding, so every File handle bound through `match Ok(f) => ...` is cleaned up at scope exit. **Smoke verified:** F4's smoke test was modified to drop the explicit `f.flush()` call — the on-disk contents are still correct because the scope-exit `karac_runtime_file_close` reconstructs `Box<KaracFile>` and runs `std::fs::File`'s Drop impl, which flushes pending writes through the kernel before closing the fd. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions. Files: `src/codegen/state.rs` (new CleanupAction variant), `src/codegen/runtime.rs` (`track_file_var` helper + emission arm), `src/codegen/pattern_binding.rs` (hook into the File re-typing arm). **What F4b does NOT cover:** non-destructured Result leak — `let _r = File.open(p);` without destructuring still leaks (the File ptr lives inside the Result's payload word with no Drop hook for the wrapped variant; F4b registers cleanup on the destructured handle, not on the Result wrapper). The canonical idiom is to destructure, so the limit doesn't impact normal code shape; lint-rejecting the non-destructured form is a separate follow-on.
  - [x] **F5 — `?`-propagation through `Result[File, IoError]` shipped 2026-05-26.** **No codegen changes needed** — empirical verification shows the existing `compile_question` path forwards all 4 payload words of the widened Result layout correctly. Json.parse exercised the Ok-with-multi-word-payload case at phase-8 line 435 slice 2 (2026-05-21); F5 confirms the symmetric Err-with-multi-word-payload case works for `Result[T, IoError]` (where IoError can be a unit variant or `Other(String)`). **2 new E2E tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 8 File handle slice F5` section: `test_e2e_file_open_question_propagates_not_found` (helper returning `Result[i64, IoError]` calls `File.open(nonexistent)?`; caller matches the propagated `IoError.NotFound` variant — pins both the `?`-mechanism and the variant-tag pass-through); `test_e2e_file_open_question_passes_through_ok` (helper opens an existing tempfile via `?` and returns Ok(0); caller matches Ok — pins the success path doesn't accidentally wrap as Err). Both run compiled binaries end-to-end. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions. Files: `tests/codegen.rs` (+2 tests + slice section comment). **What F5 does NOT cover:** the `IoError.Other(String)` payload-through-? path — hard to trigger naturally (most filesystem errors map to unit variants like NotFound / PermissionDenied; `Other` is a fallback for kernel-version-specific kinds). F6's broader test coverage may add a forced-Other case if a deterministic trigger is found; otherwise the unit-variant case is the load-bearing path for the v1 surface.
  - [x] **F6 — E2E tests + checklist update shipped 2026-05-26.** **4 new E2E tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 8 File handle slice F6` section, each runs a compiled binary end-to-end: `test_e2e_file_create_write_flush_reopen_read_full_roundtrip` (writes 3 bytes through the Kāra surface, reopens, reads back, asserts both the on-disk contents and the read byte count); `test_e2e_file_drop_closes_handle_and_flushes_pending_writes` (omits explicit flush — the F4b scope-exit `karac_runtime_file_close` action runs `std::fs::File`'s Drop, which flushes pending writes through the kernel; on-disk contents prove the cleanup wiring works); `test_e2e_file_open_nonexistent_match_arm_io_error_not_found` (direct match on `IoError.NotFound` — pins the variant tag value codegen emits matches the source-order tag assignment in `runtime/stdlib/io_error.kara`); `test_e2e_file_large_write_and_read_round_trip` (writes 256 bytes via a `while`-loop `data.push(...)` chain, flushes, reads from disk through the host OS — verifies multi-page payloads round-trip correctly through the runtime extern boundary). Combined with F5's 2 `?`-propagation tests, the codegen test suite now has 6 dedicated File E2E cases. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions. Files: `tests/codegen.rs` (+4 tests + slice section comment). **What F6 does NOT cover:** the `IoError.Other(String)` payload-through-? path (no deterministic trigger found — most filesystem errors map to unit variants); concurrent reads / writes on the same File handle (the Mutex inside `KaracFile` serializes per-handle access, but no test exercises this directly — the v1 Kāra surface doesn't expose handle cloning at the source level, so the path isn't reachable from user code today).

  **What this entry does NOT cover:** `BufReader` / `BufWriter` (separate entry below); async/non-blocking File I/O (the network-event-loop-style suspending shape — Phase 11 disk-I/O event loop covers that surface); permission flags beyond the three opening modes (mode bits, umask, OpenOptions builder — likely a v1.x follow-on); platform-specific extensions (Unix permissions, Windows file attributes); `seek` / `sync_all` / `metadata` (deferred from F1 to a follow-on slice — not required for the minimum useful surface or for slice 3 of phase-6 line 155).

- [ ] **`BufReader[R]` — buffered reader wrapper.** Standard I/O Phase 8 follow-up factored out of the parent "Standard I/O surface" entry above. Wraps any `Read` source (initially `File`; eventually `Stdin`, network streams, etc.) with an internal buffer so per-call syscall overhead amortizes. **Proposed v1 surface:** `BufReader.new(reader: R) -> BufReader[R]` with default 8KiB capacity; `BufReader.with_capacity(reader: R, cap: usize) -> BufReader[R]`; methods `br.read_line(buf: mut String) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (reads until `\n` or EOF; bytes-appended; 0 = EOF — matches Rust's contract), `br.read_to_string(buf: mut String) -> Result[usize, IoError]`, `br.lines() -> LinesIter[R]` (iterator yielding `Result[String, IoError]` per line, EOF terminates), `br.fill_buf() -> Result[Slice[u8], IoError]` (low-level peek), `br.consume(n: usize)` (advance after `fill_buf`), `br.read(buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (delegates to underlying after draining buffer). Drop releases the buffer; the wrapped `R` drops by ownership (no explicit close). **Effects:** same as the wrapped reader — `reads(FileSystem)` when `R = File`; effect-polymorphic in design but concrete bindings at v1 since the trait-impl-routing for effect polymorphism is itself a P1 surface ([`phase-3-effect-checker.md`](phase-3-effect-checker.md)). **Approach:** depends on `File` (entry above) for the v1 use case; can ship in either order if the wrapped-reader contract is stubbed against a placeholder `Read` trait first. Interpreter-only MVP. **Cancel-safety annotation:** `BufReader` carries a notional "buffer non-empty" bit that's NOT-CancelSafe across a yield — same shape as `File`'s "unflushed writes" bit. Slice 3a of `phase-6-runtime.md` line 155 (RAII flow-sensitive detection, shipped 2026-05-26) landed the type-agnostic `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "<clear>")]` walker — BufReader plugs in by annotating its buffer-soiling methods (`fill_buf` when it leaves residual bytes; `read_line` between buffered states — exact set TBD when implementation lands). Unblocks slice 3b in that file. **Cross-references:** parent at line 81; depends on `File` entry above; blocks [`phase-6-runtime.md` line 155 slice 3b (BufReader flow-sensitive seeding)](phase-6-runtime.md). **What this entry does NOT cover:** `BufWriter[W]` (likely a peer entry once a `Write`-side use case surfaces — `BufReader` is the more common idiom and the design audit's named example, so it leads); a generic `Read` / `Write` trait pair as a first-class surface (effect-polymorphic traits are P1); `Lines` iterator surface beyond the basic `Result[String, IoError]`-yielding shape (chunked reads, char iteration, encoding-aware variants live in `std.encoding` if/when that lands).

- [x] **`SortedSet[T: Ord]` stdlib type.** `Value::SortedSet(BTreeMap<OrdValue, ()>)` added to the interpreter; `OrdValue` newtype wraps `Value` and implements `Ord` via `value_compare` so `Value` can key a `BTreeMap` without global `Ord`. `SortedSet` registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `stub_generics(["T"])` in `prelude.rs` and as a generic struct in `register_builtin_types`. `SortedSet.new()` handled in the path-call dispatch. - [x] **`Channel[T]` / `Sender[T]` / `Receiver[T]` core stdlib types.** `Value::Sender(Arc<Mutex<VecDeque<Value>>>)` and `Value::Receiver(Arc<Mutex<VecDeque<Value>>>)` added; `Channel.new()` wired in path-call dispatch — creates one `Arc<Mutex<VecDeque>>`, wraps it in a `(Sender, Receiver)` tuple so both ends share the same queue. Method surface: `Sender.send(val)` pushes to queue, `Sender.clone()` Arc-clones the producer, `Receiver.recv()` pops front (returns `Unit` on empty rather than blocking — MVP single-threaded limitation), `Receiver.try_recv()` returns `Option[T]`. `Channel`, `Sender`, `Receiver` registered as generic structs `["T"]` in `register_builtin_types` + `PRELUDE_TYPES` / `stub_generics`. `infer_channel_method` added; dispatch wired in `infer_method_call` on `Type::Named { name: "Sender" | "Receiver" }`. 7 typechecker tests + 6 interpreter tests added (send-recv round-trip, FIFO ordering, try_recv on empty, cloned sender, string values). ~~Open: effect-checker `suspends` propagation for `recv`; `recv` blocking semantics in multi-threaded codegen path; `allocates(Heap)` effect for `new` + `send`.~~ `suspends` for `recv` and `allocates(Heap)` for `new`/`send` now seeded in effect checker. Open: `recv` blocking semantics in multi-threaded codegen path (blocked on Phase 6 concurrency).

- [x] **`Slice[T]` stdlib methods.** Core type and coercion ship in Phase 4; the full method surface lands here. Mirror the `Vec[T]` read-only / in-place surface where the operation makes sense on a borrowed view: `len`, `is_empty`, `first`, `last`, `get(i) -> Option[ref T]`, `iter()`, `chunks(n)`, `windows(n)`, `split_at(i) -> (Slice[T], Slice[T])`, `contains(ref T) where T: Eq`, `binary_search(ref T) where T: Ord`. Mutable-only: `sort() where T: Ord`, `sort_by(cmp)`, `reverse()`, `fill(val) where T: Clone`, `iter_mut()`, `swap(i, j)`. No `push`/`pop`/`remove` — those require capacity management and belong on `Vec[T]`. Document each method's effect set (most are effect-free; `sort` may `allocates(Heap)` for auxiliary buffers).

- [x] **Interpreter: `sort_by` / `sorted_by` closure-honoring (silent wrong-answer fix).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-11. Sub-item against the `Slice[T] stdlib methods` entry above. The interpreter arms at `src/interpreter.rs` (`sort_by` ~6940, `sorted_by` ~6965) accepted a closure comparator from the typechecker but discarded it, dispatching `sort_by(value_compare)` (natural value ordering) instead — a silent wrong-answer footgun (`xs.sort_by(|a, b| key(a).cmp(key(b)))` typechecked, ran without diagnostic, returned the input order). Surfaced 2026-05-11 by kata-katas LeetCode #1665 (`greedy.kara`) where the natural greedy idiom requires a derived key. Fix: evaluate the closure expr → `Value::Function`, snapshot the Vec via `rc.read().unwrap().clone()` (releases the read guard immediately), sort the snapshot via a comparator that calls `invoke_value_comparator` for each pair, replace via `try_write_or_panic(rc, ...)`. New helper `invoke_value_comparator` at `interpreter.rs:5700` translates the user closure's returned `Ordering` enum variant (`Less` / `Equal` / `Greater`) to `std::cmp::Ordering`, panicking with a clear message on shape errors. Three call sites updated uniformly (`sort_by` on Vec/Array, `sorted_by` on Vec/Array, `sorted_by` on String chars).

  *Settled design forks (2026-05-11).*

  - **F1 — "re-entrancy unsupported" was misframed.** The original source-comment claimed closure invocation required interpreter re-entrancy infrastructure that didn't exist. Investigation showed `invoke_function_value` at `interpreter.rs:5669` already provides exactly the needed surface. The actual constraint was `std::sync::RwLock` being non-reentrant on the same thread — if the user closure body re-accesses the same array, a held write guard deadlocks. Fix is snapshot-sort-replace: clone the Vec briefly under a read guard (released at end-of-statement), sort on the local copy (no lock held), then install via a brief write guard.
  - **F2 — Sort_by and sorted_by in the same slice, both String and Vec paths.** All three reachable call sites share the closure-honoring + Ordering-translation pattern. Splitting would leave inconsistent half-fixed surface and require duplicate test coverage. The fix shape is identical apart from the `Value::Char(c)` wrapping needed for String chars vs. raw `Value` for Vec elements.
  - **F3 — Skip the interim hard-error.** The original staging entry floated a small interim slice that converts the silent wrong-answer to a typed runtime error while the real fix designs. Since the real fix landed in the same session (~40 LoC mechanical), the interim would have been pure churn — every existing `sort_by(closure)` user broken once when the interim lands, again when it gets reverted.

  *Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups in [`wip-staging.md`](wip-staging.md)).*

  - **Typechecker shape validation of `Fn(T, T) -> Ordering` closure args.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-11 — see the dedicated entry below. The original framing called the gap mechanical (~30 LoC). Real shape was ~80 LoC: a new `check_sort_comparator` helper, push-down via `check_expr` against `Type::Function { params: [elem, elem], return_type: Ordering }`, integration into the existing Slice and String arms, and a new Vec intercept ahead of the generic fallthrough (Vec has no stdlib impl block, so previously the closure flowed through unchecked).
  - **`sort_by_key` on Slice/Vec.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-11 — see the dedicated entry below. Closed alongside `sorted_by_key` since the sort/sorted pair always ships together; the LeetCode #1665 idiom `xs.sort_by_key(|t| -(t.1 - t.0))` is now the canonical Kāra form.
  - **Interpreter primitive comparison gap.** Closure bodies like `b.cmp(a)` for `Vec[i64]` or `a > b` for chars panic at the comparator's first call: the typechecker recognizes `i64.cmp` via the builtin Ord impl, but the interpreter's method-call dispatch doesn't know how to invoke it on primitive values. Same shape for char `<` / `>` / `==`. Blocks the canonical descending-sort idiom; staging entry tracks. The closure-honoring path itself is correct — the gap is one layer downstream, in primitive method dispatch.
  - **Slice/Vec parity for `sorted` / `sorted_by` in the typechecker.** `Vec.sorted_by` typechecks today via a fallthrough path even though there's no explicit `sorted_by` arm in `infer_slice_method` / Vec method dispatch; this fix relied on that fallthrough working. A clean typechecker surface would add the missing arms explicitly. Not blocking — covered by the typechecker-shape-validation follow-up above.

- [x] **Typechecker: `Fn(T, T) -> Ordering` shape validation for `sort_by` / `sorted_by`.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-11. Sub-item against the `Slice[T] stdlib methods` entry. Pre-fix the slice / String `sort_by` / `sorted_by` arms called `infer_expr(&arg.value)` on the comparator without verifying its shape; Vec had no dispatcher at all and fell through to the silent-no-method path that synth-types the closure with fresh metavars (no pushdown into the closure's params, no check on the body's return type). With the interpreter's closure-honoring path live (sibling entry above) plus the primitive-Ord dispatch live (`phase-4-interpreter.md`), a wrong-shape comparator (`xs.sort_by(|a| a)`, `xs.sort_by(|a, b| a < b)`) would typecheck and then runtime-panic when the interpreter pulled an `Ordering` variant out of the closure's bool / arity-1 return. Now: any wrong-shape comparator produces a typecheck TypeMismatch at the closure expression. Fix:

  - New helper `check_sort_comparator(elem, arg, method, span)` in `src/typechecker.rs` builds the expected `Type::Function { params: [elem, elem], return_type: Type::Named("Ordering", []) }` and calls `check_expr(&arg.value, &expected)` — the check-mode closure-pushdown machinery (`src/typechecker.rs:8340`-area) handles per-parameter type assignment and body validation against `Ordering`. Arity mismatch is caught by the same path; non-closure `Fn` values flow through normal `check_assignable`.
  - `infer_str_method` `sorted_by` arm: arg count gate before the helper; on miscount, infer args and skip the helper.
  - `infer_slice_method` `sort_by` arm: arg count gate added (was missing), mutability gate unchanged, helper called on the lone closure arg.
  - New Vec intercept in `infer_method_call` (before the strip-outer-ref dispatcher) for `sort_by` / `sorted_by` when the receiver is `Vec[T]` / `ref Vec[T]` / `mut ref Vec[T]`. Returns `Type::Unit` for `sort_by` (in-place mutation) and `Type::Named { name: "Vec", args: [elem] }` for `sorted_by` (new collection).

  *Settled design forks (2026-05-11).*

  - **F1 — Single helper, three call sites.** The cleanest alternative was to fold `sort_by` / `sorted_by` into a generic `infer_call`-style flow that gets pushdown for free. Rejected because Slice / String are special-cased today and the surrounding arms wouldn't benefit; threading them all through generic dispatch would be a much larger refactor (every fall-through dispatcher today is a hand-coded match). The narrow helper integrates with each existing arm at one line.

  - **F2 — `check_expr`, not `infer_expr` + post-hoc check.** `check_expr` pushes the expected `Fn(elem, elem) -> Ordering` down into closure parameters and validates the body's return type against `Ordering` in one pass. The runner-up was `infer_expr` followed by manual `check_assignable` on the inferred type — but that requires the closure to come in fully typed (or the typechecker to bind metavars after the fact), which loses the pushdown property: `xs.sort_by(|a, b| a.cmp(b))` should be accepted with `a` / `b` typed as the element type, not left as fresh metavars.

  - **F3 — Vec dispatch intercept lives in `infer_method_call`, not a new `infer_vec_method`.** A full `infer_vec_method` (peer to `infer_slice_method` / `infer_str_method`) would have to shadow every Vec method that today falls through to the impl-block lookup correctly (`push` / `pop` / `clone` / `iter` / etc.). The narrow intercept fires only for `sort_by` / `sorted_by` and leaves the rest of Vec's method surface on its existing path. Future entry: a slice that promotes Vec dispatch wholesale to `infer_vec_method` for symmetry with Slice / String, when there's a second reason to add a Vec-specific arm.

  *Out of scope.*

  - **Receiver-mutability check on Vec.sort_by.** `Slice.sort_by` requires `mut Slice[T]`; Vec mutability lives at the binding level (`let mut xs: Vec[i64]`) and the binding-mutability check fires at the call site outside this dispatcher. Not duplicated in the Vec intercept.
  - **`sort` / `reverse` arg-count tightening on Vec.** Today Vec has no explicit arm for these either; they fall through to the silent path. Out of scope for this slice — Slice has the explicit arms (`infer_slice_method` "sort" | "reverse"), Vec relies on fall-through with the implicit zero-arg expectation. Closes when Vec moves to its own dispatcher.
  - **`sort_by_key` shape validation.** Lands together with the `sort_by_key` surface; tracked in the sibling staging entry.

  Test coverage in `tests/typechecker.rs`: `test_string_sorted_by_returns_string` (positive — `Fn(char, char) -> Ordering`), `test_string_sorted_by_rejects_bool_returning_comparator` (negative pin for the original silent-pass case), `test_vec_sort_by_rejects_wrong_arity_closure` (1-param closure rejected), `test_vec_sort_by_rejects_wrong_return_type` (`Fn(i64, i64) -> bool` rejected), `test_vec_sort_by_accepts_ordering_returning_comparator` (positive — `|a, b| a.cmp(b)`). Full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` green; zero regressions.

- [x] **`sort_by_key` / `sorted_by_key` on `Slice[T]` / `Vec[T]`.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-11. Sibling to the typechecker shape-validation entry above and the prior closure-honoring slice. Surfaced 2026-05-11 by LeetCode #1665 — the natural greedy idiom is `sort_by_key(|t| -(t.1 - t.0))`, which needs a key function `Fn(T) -> K` where `K: Ord`, not the `Fn(T, T) -> Ordering` shape that `sort_by` accepts. Without `sort_by_key` the workaround was either (a) hand-roll a comparator that recomputes both keys on every comparison, or (b) in-source insertion sort (the kata's actual fallback). Now: idiomatic single-pass key sort works through `karac run` and the interpreter precomputes keys exactly once per element (matches Rust's `slice::sort_by_key` performance contract).

  Implementation:

  - **Interpreter** (`src/interpreter.rs`): new `sort_by_key` and `sorted_by_key` arms in `eval_method_call` peer to the existing `sort_by` / `sorted_by` arms. Each arm evaluates the key closure to a `Value::Function`, snapshots the array, computes `(key, value)` pairs by invoking the closure once per element via `invoke_function_value`, sorts the pairs by `value_compare(k1, k2)`, then writes the values back (`sort_by_key`) or returns a new Vec (`sorted_by_key`). The precompute-keys-once shape avoids the O(n log n) closure invocation cost of routing through `sort_by` with a comparator that calls the key fn twice per compare.
  - **Typechecker** (`src/typechecker.rs`): new helper `check_sort_key_closure(elem, arg, method, span)` pushes `Fn(elem) -> TypeParam("__sort_by_key_K")` down through `check_expr`, reads the resolved body type out of the returned `Type::Function` shape (mirrors `Iterator.map`'s pushdown pattern at `infer_iterator_method`), and verifies the body type satisfies `Ord` via `type_supports_ord`. Wired into `infer_slice_method` (new `sort_by_key` arm with the mutability check) and into the Vec intercept at `infer_method_call` (the existing intercept widened to recognize `sort_by_key` / `sorted_by_key` alongside `sort_by` / `sorted_by`). Method-name allow-list in the `_` fallthrough also grew `sort_by_key` for typo-suggestion completeness.

  *Settled design forks (2026-05-11).*

  - **F1 — Typechecker-recognized name, not stdlib decl.** `sort_by` is typechecker-recognized today (the slice / String arms hand-code the method); `sort_by_key` lands symmetric. Promoting all sort-family methods to stdlib decls is its own future slice; sticking with the existing pattern keeps the diff narrow and consistent.
  - **F2 — `sorted_by_key` peer in the same slice.** The `sort` / `sorted` pair is already consistent across Vec, String, and (via the new entry) Slice. Splitting `sort_by_key` and `sorted_by_key` would leave inconsistent surface and require duplicate test coverage. Both arms share the precompute-keys-once shape.
  - **F3 — `K: Ord` strict, not `K: PartialOrd`.** Matches Rust's `slice::sort_by_key`. Raw floats deliberately fail the Ord check (IEEE NaN breaks the trait, matching how the typechecker excludes raw `Float` from `register_builtin_impl("Ord", ...)`). Users wanting float sort use the `TotalFloat32` / `TotalFloat64` wrappers, same constraint as `sort`.
  - **F4 — `TypeParam` placeholder, not `TypeVar`, for return-type pushdown.** `types_compatible` treats `Type::TypeParam(_)` as permissively compatible with concrete types (line 2198 in typechecker), but `Type::TypeVar(_)` triggers a strict-equality compare. Pushing `Fn(T) -> TypeVar(K)` would emit a spurious "expected '?T0', found 'i64'" diagnostic when the closure body resolves to a concrete type. The TypeParam pattern is the same one `infer_iterator_method`'s `map` arm uses — read the resolved body type out of the returned `Type::Function` shape after `check_expr`. The `_var`-named-but-actually-`TypeParam` workaround documented in the helper.

  *Out of scope.*

  - **String chars `sort_by_key`.** `String.sorted_by_key(|c| ...)` would be a natural peer to `String.sorted_by`, but it's not part of the kata's idiom and adding it now would mean another String arm + chars-to-Vec extraction. Tracks as a follow-up if String chars iteration grows.
  - **`max_by_key` / `min_by_key`.** The dual surface (find the element with extremal key) is natural to ship together with `sort_by_key`, but each lives on `Iterator`, not on `Vec` / `Slice`, and the existing `Iterator` adaptor surface is closed-out. Separate slice when the natural idiom emerges.
  - **`sort_unstable_by_key` perf variant.** Rust ships `sort_unstable` / `sort_unstable_by` / `sort_unstable_by_key` for slightly faster sorting at the cost of stability. The interpreter's tree-walk sort uses `Vec::sort_by` which is stable; the unstable variant ships when codegen sort dispatch is on the table.

  Test coverage. Typechecker (`tests/typechecker.rs`): `test_vec_sort_by_key_accepts_integer_key` (`|x| x`), `test_vec_sort_by_key_accepts_negated_key` (the LeetCode idiom `|x| -x`), `test_vec_sort_by_key_rejects_wrong_arity_closure` (2-param closure rejected), `test_vec_sorted_by_key_returns_vec` (return-type pin). Interpreter (`tests/interpreter.rs`): `test_vec_sort_by_key_ascending`, `test_vec_sort_by_key_descending_via_negation`, `test_vec_sorted_by_key_returns_new`. Full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` green; zero regressions.

- [x] **`Range` / `RangeInclusive` implements `Iterator`.** Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `c18fbec`). Sibling to the closed adaptor-surface entry below (commit `6d23f94`). Range / RangeInclusive route through the existing Iterator dispatch surface so `(0..10).step_by(2).collect()`, `(1..=10).map(f).filter(p).collect()`, `(0..n).take(k)` etc. work directly through `karac run` without a redundant `.iter()`; the for-loop iterable path is preserved through `Value::Iterator` drain. Typechecker + interpreter only — codegen iterator chains remain a broader gap. 6 interpreter + 2 typechecker tests.

- [x] **`Slice[T]` implements `Iterator` — `.iter()` method.** Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `cf4a846`). Sibling to the Range / RangeInclusive Iterator entry above (`c18fbec`). `Slice[T]` routes `iter` / `into_iter` through the existing Iterator dispatch surface so chained adaptors (`s.iter().map(f).filter(p).collect()`) compose; the for-loop iterable path already drained `Value::Slice` directly. Typechecker `infer_slice_method` only — interpreter pre-existed (slice→array normalization at the method-dispatch fence routes through the shared `iter`/`into_iter` arm). Codegen iterator chains remain a broader gap. 6 interpreter + 2 typechecker tests.

- [x] **Iterator trait — full adaptor surface.** Beyond the named-in-roadmap adaptors (`filter`, `map`, `collect`, `fold`, `any`, `all`), ship the long-tail combinators that real iterator code depends on: `chain`, `zip`, `enumerate`, `take(n)`, `skip(n)`, `take_while(pred)`, `skip_while(pred)`, `flat_map(f)`, `peekable`, `chunk_by(key_fn)`, `step_by(n)`, `cycle`, `inspect(f)`, `scan(state, f)`, `windows(n)`, `chunks(n)`. Each is a 5–20 line implementation once `Iterator` is in place. Real programs use the long tail; absence forces hand-roll. Most are effect-free; ones that buffer (`chunk_by`, `windows`) may `allocates(Heap)`. Closed 2026-05-04. Final commit `6d23f94` (`chunks(n)` / `windows(n)` on Iterator). Shipped surface: terminals `next`, `count`, `collect`, `fold`, `any`, `all`; step-layer adaptors `map`, `filter`, `enumerate`, `take(n)`, `skip(n)`, `take_while(pred)`, `skip_while(pred)`, `step_by(n)`, `inspect(f)`, `scan(init, f)`; source-layer adaptors `iter` / `into_iter` (Eager), `chain(other)`, `zip(other)`, `flat_map(f)`, `cycle()`, `peekable()`, `chunk_by(key_fn)`, `chunks(n)`, `windows(n)`; plus `peek()` exclusive to the `Peekable[T]` named type returned by `peekable()`. Heap-allocating adaptors with `allocates(Heap)` seeded in the effectchecker: `Iterator.chunk_by`, `Iterator.chunks`, `Iterator.windows` (and route via `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` so `Vec.chunks` / `Vec.windows` callers also pick up the effect, closing a pre-existing under-report). Test coverage: **227** dedicated iterator tests — 133 interpreter, 91 typechecker, 3 effectchecker. Implementation rides `Value::Iterator { source: IteratorSource, steps: Vec<IteratorStep> }` with 9 source variants (`Eager`, `Chain`, `Zip`, `FlatMap`, `Cycle`, `Peekable`, `ChunkBy`, `Chunks`, `Windows`) and 10 step variants (`Map`, `Filter`, `Enumerate`, `Take`, `Skip`, `TakeWhile`, `SkipWhile`, `StepBy`, `Inspect`, `Scan`). Notable design choices documented inline at the variant doc-comments: `Peekable[T]` is a distinct named type that loses peek-capability after any adaptor (matching Rust's `Map<Peekable<I>>`); `scan` deviates from Rust's `Fn(&mut St, T) -> Option<B>` to `Fn(A, T) -> Option<(A, U)>` because tree-walk closures snapshot captures and there's no `mut ref` parameter mode; multi-source / lookahead adaptors (`chunk_by`, `chunks`, `windows`, `flat_map`, `peekable`, `cycle`) are sources rather than steps because they break the 1:1 source-pull → output-item assumption that Steps make.

- [x] **`std.encoding` — base64, hex, URL encode/decode.** Closed 2026-05-03. Interpreter-only namespace under `Base64.*` / `Hex.*` / `Url.*` (mirrors the `Stats` / `Regex` precedent — typechecker registers each function name in `env.functions`, interpreter dispatches on the path string). Functions: `Base64.encode(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String` (standard alphabet, `=`-padded), `Base64.encode_url_safe(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String` (URL-safe alphabet, no padding), `Base64.decode(s: String) -> Result[Vec[u8], DecodeError]` (accepts both alphabets, ignores ASCII whitespace), `Hex.encode(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String` (lowercase), `Hex.encode_upper(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String`, `Hex.decode(s: String) -> Result[Vec[u8], DecodeError]` (case-insensitive, even-length only), `Url.encode(s: String) -> String` (RFC 3986 percent-encoding — preserves the unreserved set `A-Za-z0-9-._~`, percent-encodes everything else), `Url.decode(s: String) -> Result[String, DecodeError]`. The original spec called for "standard + URL-safe via flag" / "lowercase + uppercase via flag" — Kāra has no default-arg or boolean-flag-arg idiom in its stdlib (Stats, Regex use the separate-function form); the implementation mirrors the precedent. New `DecodeError { message: String }` struct registered in the typechecker (parallels `RegexError`); decode failures populate the message. New types added to `PRELUDE_TYPES`: `Base64`, `Hex`, `Url`, `DecodeError`. 22 new tests (8 typechecker — signature shape per function — + 14 interpreter — RFC 4648 base64 vectors with 1/2/3-byte padding + URL-safe alphabet + base64 round-trip + invalid-char rejection / hex lower & upper + mixed-case decode + odd-length rejection / URL preserves unreserved set + percent-encode + round-trip + invalid percent-encoding rejection). No codegen support today (parallels `Regex`); compiled-binary support is a follow-up if/when needed. Files: `src/prelude.rs`, `src/typechecker.rs`, `src/interpreter.rs`, `tests/typechecker.rs`, `tests/interpreter.rs`.

- [x] **Lexer: reserve `expr_<NNNN>` fragment-specifier identifier namespace.** Closed 2026-05-04 in commit `1559772`. The check lives in `src/lexer.rs` `identifier()`'s fallthrough arm via the `is_reserved_fragment_specifier_namespace` helper (manual byte-class check; no regex on the hot path). Raw-escape exemption is structural — `r#expr_2026` flows through `raw_identifier()`, which never enters the keyword match path, so no `was_raw_escaped` flag is needed at the token level. 7 tests in `tests/lexer.rs` cover boundary years (2020 / 2026 / 2099) at let / fn / struct-field positions, both fix-its in the diagnostic, the raw-escape exemption, and every accept-path negative case (no prefix, different prefix, non-year suffix, year out of range on both sides, wrong digit count). Original spec preserved below for the historical record. Spec at `design.md § Reserved Fragment-Specifier Identifier Namespace` (v60 item 62). Slices: (1) **Lexer regex check.** In `src/lexer.rs`, after recognising an identifier token, run a pattern check against `^expr_(\d{4})$`. If the regex matches AND the captured digit string parses as a year in the range `2020`..=`2099` inclusive, emit `error[E_RESERVED_FRAGMENT_SPECIFIER_NAMESPACE]: 'expr_<NNNN>' is a reserved identifier name; this naming convention is reserved for future edition-versionable syntax categories in macros / comptime fragment specifiers — use 'r#expr_<NNNN>' if you need this exact identifier today, or rename to a non-year-suffixed form` with the offending span underlined and the two fix-its (the raw-identifier escape OR a rename suggestion). (2) **Raw-identifier exemption.** When the identifier is preceded by `r#` (raw-identifier escape per item 39), the reservation does NOT fire — `r#expr_2026` parses as the bare identifier `expr_2026` and is accepted. The exemption falls out of the existing raw-identifier handling: the regex is checked AFTER the raw-prefix has been stripped, so `r#expr_2026` strips to `expr_2026` for downstream consumers but the reservation is checked against the *original lexed form* before stripping. Implementation detail: track a `was_raw_escaped` flag on the identifier token; if true, skip the namespace check. (3) **Narrow scope at v1.** The reservation matches ONLY the `expr_` prefix. Other plausible fragment-specifier prefixes (`pat`, `ty`, `stmt`, `block`, `tt`, `ident`, `lit`, `path`, `vis`, `meta`, `item`, `lifetime`) are NOT reserved at v1 — extending the reservation post-v1 to additional prefixes is non-breaking-additive (existing user identifiers using those prefixes continue to work). (4) **Year range.** `2020`..=`2099` inclusive. Years outside this range (e.g., `expr_1999`, `expr_3000`) parse as ordinary identifiers without rejection. The range matches the realistic edition-year window for any Kāra release. (5) **Diagnostic shape.** Span underlines the full identifier including the year suffix. Help line offers the raw-escape fix-it (`r#expr_2026`) and the rename fix-it (`expression_2026` or similar). (6) **No connection to literal year value.** The reservation is purely a namespace allocation, not tied to a specific year value. `expr_2026` is reserved today even though Kāra's current edition is `2026`; `expr_2099` is reserved even though no compiler will see it for decades. (7) **Test coverage.** Positive — `let x = 1;` (no prefix) accepts; `let expression = 1;` accepts; `let expr_v2 = 1;` accepts (non-year suffix); `let version_2026 = 1;` accepts (different prefix); `let expr_1999 = 1;` accepts (year out of reserved range); `let expr_3000 = 1;` accepts (year out of reserved range); `let r#expr_2026 = 1;` accepts (raw-escape exemption); function declaration `fn expr_v2() { }` accepts. Negative — `let expr_2020 = 1;` rejected with `E_RESERVED_FRAGMENT_SPECIFIER_NAMESPACE`; `let expr_2026 = 1;` rejected; `let expr_2099 = 1;` rejected; function declaration `fn expr_2026() { }` rejected at function-name lex; struct field `struct S { expr_2030: i64 }` rejected at field-name lex; the diagnostic includes both fix-its inline. Phase target: 1 (Lexer) — small lex-time check; reuses the existing identifier tokenisation path. No P1 carve-out — the reservation ships at v1 to lock in the namespace before users can rely on it.

- [ ] **Per-stdlib-type variance declarations + verifier + user-side rejection.** Spec at `design.md § Variance` (v60 item 57). Three layers: a parser/AST surface for `+T` / `-T` / `=T` markers, a stdlib-side verifier that proves the markers consistent with the type's structure, and a user-side rejection diagnostic that reserves the syntax for v1. The covariant types (`Option`, `Result`, `Iterator`, `TaskHandle`, `AlreadySetError`) are the load-bearing payoff — they unlock subtyping that today's all-invariant rule blocks.

  1. [ ] **Lexer.** `+`, `-`, `=` already lex as symbols; no new token kinds.
  2. [ ] **Parser + AST.** Extend `GENERIC_PARAM` per syntax.md §6.4 to accept an optional leading `VARIANCE_MARKER` (`+` / `-` / `=`) before the parameter identifier. The marker attaches to the parameter, not to the bound — `+T: Ord` is `(+ T) (: Ord)`, not `(+ T:Ord)`. AST: extend `GenericParam` with `variance: Variance { Covariant, Contravariant, Invariant }` field; default `Invariant` when no marker is present.
  3. [ ] **Resolver — user-side rejection at v1.** When a generic-parameter declaration in *user* code (i.e., not in stdlib source files) carries `+` or `-`, emit `error[E_VARIANCE_USER_DECL_NOT_YET]: variance declarations are reserved for stdlib types in v1; remove the marker — the parameter will be invariant`. Stdlib source files (identified by package name = `std` / `core` / `karac-runtime` or by a `#[stdlib_type]` attribute on the type, depending on the bootstrapping decision) accept the markers.
  4. [ ] **Variance verifier — stdlib-side enforcement.** New typechecker pass `verify_variance` runs at type-decl time on every parametric stdlib type. For each declared parameter `T` with declared variance `V`, walk the type's structure (fields, variant payloads, trait-method signatures on inherent impls, etc.) and check that `T` appears only in positions consistent with `V`: `+T` requires `T` only in covariant positions (return-types, immutable-borrow targets, covariant slots of inner types per their own declarations); `-T` requires `T` only in contravariant positions; `=T` is unrestricted. Failure emits `error[E_VARIANCE_DECLARATION_INCONSISTENT]: parameter '<T>' declared '<+T/-T/=T>' (<co/contra/inv>variant) appears in <invariant/contravariant> position '<field/method/...>' inside type '<TypeName>'` with the offending position's span underlined and a fix-it suggesting the next-most-conservative declaration (e.g., if `+T` fails, suggest `=T`).
  5. [ ] **Position-based variance pass — already exists.** Verify the existing typechecker handles function argument contravariance, return covariance, effect-set covariance, `mut ref` invariance, `ref` covariance per `design.md § Variance` table. This entry adds the per-type layer; the position-based layer is unchanged.
  6. [ ] **Stdlib audit — apply variance declarations to every stdlib parametric type.** One-time review of every parametric stdlib type as of v1; add the marker to its declaration per the audit table in design.md. Types: `Vec[=T]`, `Slice[=T]`, `Array[=T, const N]`, `Map[=K, =V]`, `Set[=T]`, `VecDeque[=T]`, `SortedSet[=T]`, `Option[+T]`, `Result[+T, +E]`, `Iterator[+T]`, `Box[=T]`, `Rc[=T]`, `Arc[=T]`, `Sender[=T]`, `Receiver[=T]`, `Channel[=T]`, `Atomic[=T]`, `Mutex[=T]`, `RwLock[=T]`, `LazyLock[=T]`, `OnceLock[=T]`, `OnceCell[=T]`, `MaybeUninit[=T]`, `PhantomData[=T]`, `TaskHandle[+T]`, `AlreadySetError[+T]`. The migration is mechanical — change `Vec[T]` declaration to `Vec[=T]` (or omit the marker, since `=T` is the default) and so on for the others.
  7. [ ] **Stdlib lint — every parametric stdlib type must carry an explicit variance declaration.** Lint that fires at the stdlib build step when a parametric type is declared without a marker on every parameter. The default is invariant via `=T` or no-marker; the lint requires *every* parameter to be either explicitly `=T`-marked OR explicitly `+T`/`-T` (no implicit). This forces the stdlib author to make a deliberate choice rather than accept the default by accident. User-code types are unaffected (the lint is stdlib-only).
  8. [ ] **Subtyping rule — at use sites.** When the typechecker is checking whether `Foo[Sub]` is a subtype of `Foo[Super]` (e.g., a coercion / pattern match / let-binding), the variance declaration of `Foo`'s parameter governs the check: `+T` → `Sub <: Super` required; `-T` → `Super <: Sub` required; `=T` → `Sub == Super` required. The check composes with refinement-to-base widening: `Iterator[Positive]` widens to `Iterator[i32]` via the `+T` covariance + the refinement widening; `Vec[Positive]` does NOT widen to `Vec[i32]` because `Vec[=T]` is invariant.
  9. [ ] **Test coverage.** Positive — `Iterator[Positive]` accepts where `Iterator[i32]` is expected; `Option[NonZero]` widens to `Option[i32]`; `Result[Positive, IoError]` widens to `Result[i32, IoError]`; `Vec[i32]` does NOT widen to `Vec[Number]` (invariant); `Sender[String]` does NOT widen to `Sender[Object]`; verifier accepts `Option[+T]` (T appears only in `Some(T)` payload, covariant); verifier accepts `Atomic[=T]` (T appears in atomic-load-and-store positions, must be invariant). Negative — user-code `struct MyContainer[+T] { ... }` rejected with `E_VARIANCE_USER_DECL_NOT_YET`; stdlib `struct Cell[+T] { mut field: T }` rejected with `E_VARIANCE_DECLARATION_INCONSISTENT` because `+T` cannot appear at a `mut` field position; stdlib parametric type without any variance marker rejected by stdlib lint.

  **Phase target:** 5.2 (Language Features) — parser + AST + variance verifier; the stdlib audit is a coordinated CR with the verifier landing first. No P1 carve-out for the verifier itself — option (a) of v60 item 57 ships at v1. The user-side variance declaration surface IS the P1 follow-up; the v1 reservation (focused diagnostic) ensures the surface lands later without source breaks.

- [ ] **Stdlib lint — `drop_carries_soundness` audit checklist.** Spec at `design.md § Drop > Destructors are NOT soundness mechanisms` (v60 item 56 — Tier-E pin). The principle is a documentation pin, not a runtime check; the implementation work is a **code-review checklist** baked into the stdlib hygiene suite. For every new stdlib type that ships a `Drop` impl, the reviewer must answer "if Drop is removed (the destructor never runs), what becomes unsafe?" The answer must be "nothing" — only resources leak, no UB, no type-system violation. Slices: (1) **Stdlib code-review checklist.** Add the question to the stdlib PR template (or equivalent). Reviewers explicitly call out the answer in the PR body when adding a new `Drop` impl, especially on shared / public stdlib types. (2) **Negative-test convention.** New stdlib types with `Drop` impls add a "Drop-skip soundness" test that exercises the type's safety properties in the absence of the destructor running — typically by holding the type past a panic-under-abort path, or (post-v1, when a forget primitive ships) by explicitly skipping Drop and checking that the type remains sound. The test pins the invariant at the test layer; if a future change introduces Drop-dependent soundness, the test fails. (3) **Audit existing stdlib types.** One-time review of every stdlib type with a `Drop` impl as of v1 — `MutexGuard`, `RwLockReadGuard`, `RwLockWriteGuard`, `RefCellRefGuard`, `RefCellMutGuard`, IRQ-disable guard, future RAII guards — confirming each one satisfies the principle. The audit produces a per-type note in the stdlib documentation explaining where the soundness comes from (typically: the borrow checker enforces the lock's aliasing rules; Drop only runs the unlock action). (4) **Documentation cross-reference.** Every `impl Drop` in stdlib gets a doc-comment line explaining "soundness derives from the type system; this destructor runs cleanup." The line is template boilerplate but reinforces the principle at every site reviewers encounter. (5) **No new compiler diagnostic.** This is a checklist + documentation discipline, not a compile-time enforcement — the principle is too semantic to mechanize ("would skipping Drop cause UB?" is a meta-question about every API the type touches, not a local property). The compiler does enforce the related rules (e.g., `Drop` body must be `panics`-free, `Drop` and `Copy` mutually exclusive) — those land in their own checklist entries. **Test coverage.** Per-stdlib-type "Drop-skip soundness" assertions (point 2 above) — exact form depends on the type; generally constructs the value, holds it across a panic-under-abort code path or a process.exit, asserts the program exits cleanly without UB. These tests run alongside the regular stdlib test suite. Phase target: Phase 8 (Standard Library — Floor) — bundled with each stdlib type's own implementation; no separate slice. The audit of existing types runs once at the v1 freeze before stdlib API stabilization.

- [x] **`marker trait` syntax + stdlib marker migration.** Spec at `design.md § Marker Traits` (v60 item 55). Slices: (1) **Lexer.** Add `marker` to the keyword arm in `src/lexer.rs` (currently a free identifier). The keyword token kind is unconditional; users with a local binding named `marker` must rename or use `r#marker`. (2) **Parser.** Recognize `[ATTRIBUTES] [VIS] "marker" "trait" IDENT [GENERIC_PARAMS] [":" SUPERTRAIT_BOUNDS] [WHERE_CLAUSE] (";" | "{" "}")` per syntax.md §3.4. AST: new `Item::MarkerTrait { name, generic_params, supertraits, where_clause, vis, attributes, span }`. Body must be either bare semicolon or empty `{ }` — both forms produce identical AST representation; the parser distinguishes only for round-trip formatting. Methods, associated types, associated consts inside the body are rejected at parse with `error[E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_METHOD]: marker traits cannot declare methods; remove the method or change 'marker trait' to 'trait'` or `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM` (for type/const items), each with the suggested-fix span pointing at the `marker` keyword (offering "remove `marker`") and at the offending body content (offering "remove this method/item"). (3) **Resolver.** Register the marker trait in the trait namespace alongside ordinary traits. Marker-trait resolution participates in trait-bound resolution, supertrait check, and impl coherence the same as regular traits — the marker-ness is a definition-site property, not a use-site property. (4) **Empty-impl-body enforcement.** When an impl block targets a trait that resolves to `Item::MarkerTrait`, verify the impl body is empty `{ }`. Methods, associated types, default-method overrides inside the body are rejected with `error[E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD]: impl of marker trait '<name>' cannot contain methods or items; the body must be empty`. The check runs at the impl-resolution step in the typechecker, after the impl's target trait is identified. (5) **Auto-implementation forbidden** — verify (no enforcement work; just confirm the typechecker never generates `impl Marker for T { }` from auto-trait inference). The closed compiler-known marker traits (`ScopeLocal`, future `Concurrent`) have compiler-emitted impls for a small fixed set of types; users cannot manually implement them (sealed). (6) **Stdlib migration — convert existing markers to `marker trait`.** Touch the source declarations of `Eq`, `Pod`, `ScopeLocal`, `Sealed`, future `Concurrent`. The migration is mechanical: change `trait Name { }` to `marker trait Name;` (or `marker trait Name: Supertrait;`). All existing impl blocks (which are already empty by construction) require no changes. Verify the migration in stdlib tests. (7) **Diagnostics on misuse.** `marker trait Foo { fn method(); }` rejected at parse with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_METHOD`; `marker trait Foo { type Item; }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM`; `impl Pod for u8 { fn extra() { } }` rejected with `E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD` after the impl's target trait `Pod` resolves to a marker. (8) **Formatter.** Round-trips `marker trait Foo;` and `marker trait Foo { }` to canonical form (`marker trait Foo;` is the canonical short shape; `{ }` form is preserved if the user wrote it explicitly). (9) **Test coverage.** Positive — `marker trait Pod;` parses and registers; `marker trait Concurrent: Sized;` parses with supertrait; `marker trait Sealed[T];` parses with generics; `marker trait Storeable[T: Clone] where T: Default;` parses with where-clause; `impl Pod for u8 { }` accepted; `impl[T: Clone] Storeable[T] for Box[T] { }` accepted (conditional impl); generic bound `fn f[T: Pod](x: T) { }` accepts; impl-of-marker-trait coherence rejects duplicate impls; orphan rule applies (impl of foreign marker for foreign type rejected). Negative — `marker trait Foo { fn bar(); }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_METHOD` and both fix-its; `marker trait Foo { type Item; }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM`; `marker trait Foo { const N: usize; }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM`; `impl Pod for u8 { fn x() { } }` rejected with `E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD`; user-side `impl ScopeLocal for MyType { }` rejected (sealed marker — separate diagnostic). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) — lexer + parser + AST + resolver + typechecker + formatter; stdlib migration is a coordinated CR with the language work landing first. No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 55 ships the full surface at v1; user-extensible auto-marker derivation is permanently rejected per item 61.

- [ ] **Raw-pointer method dispatch requires known pointee — `E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE`.** Spec at `design.md § Method Resolution > Method dispatch on raw pointers requires a known pointee` (v60 item 54). Slices: (1) **Typechecker check at method dispatch.** When method resolution evaluates `expr.method(args)` and `expr` has type `*const T` or `*mut T`, check whether `T` contains an unresolved type metavariable. If yes, emit `error[E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE]: method '<name>' on raw pointer requires a known pointee type` with the pointer expression's span underlined and the two fix-it suggestions: (a) annotate the binding's declared type (`let p: *const u8 = ...`), (b) use turbofish on the originating constructor when identifiable (`ptr.null[u8]()`).
