If the originating constructor cannot be identified syntactically (e.g., the pointer flowed in through a function argument), only the binding-annotation fix-it is offered. (2) **Constructor identification helper.** Walk back from the pointer expression through the binding's initializer (one level — not a full DFA). If the initializer is a direct call to `ptr.null()` / `ptr.null_mut()` / `ptr.dangling()` / `ptr.dangling_mut()`, identify it as the originating constructor and offer the turbofish fix-it pointing at its call site. Otherwise fall through to the binding-annotation-only fix-it. (3) **`unsafe { }` orthogonality.** The check fires regardless of whether the call is inside an `unsafe { }` block — the diagnostic is about type-system tractability, not safety contract. Verify the existing `unsafe`-required check still fires on raw-pointer method calls separately; the two diagnostics are independent and can both fire on the same expression. (4) **Generic-parameter case.** When the pointer's element type is a generic parameter `T` in scope (not a metavariable), the check passes — `T` will be resolved at monomorphization, and the dispatch is checked against `T` symbolically. The distinction is between "type metavariable awaiting solving" and "generic type parameter" — the typechecker's existing infrastructure already distinguishes these. (5) **No autoref / auto-deref through raw pointers — verify.** Method-resolution Step 1 builds the receiver candidate list from `T`, `ref T`, `mut ref T`, plus `shared struct` / Rc / Arc deref steps. Raw pointers are NOT part of the chain — verify the existing implementation does not accidentally include them. A method declared on the pointee type `T` is not reachable via `p: *const T` without an explicit `*p` dereference; the call resolves only against inherent methods on `*const T` / `*mut T` themselves. (6) **Test coverage.** Positive — `let p: *const u8 = ptr.const(some_byte); unsafe { p.read(); }` accepts (T pinned by binding annotation); `let p = ptr.null[u32](); unsafe { p.read(); }` accepts (T pinned by turbofish); `fn f[T](p: *const T) { unsafe { p.read(); } }` accepts (T is a generic param, resolved at mono); pointer arithmetic `p.offset(4)` follows the same rule; `p.is_null()` accepts even with unresolved T (no read of the pointee, no T-dependent lowering). Negative — `let p = ptr.null(); unsafe { p.read(); }` rejected with `E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE`, span on `p`, both fix-its offered (binding annotation + turbofish on `ptr.null`); `let p = ptr.dangling(); unsafe { p.write(0); }` rejected, both fix-its offered; pointer flowing through a function argument with no annotation rejected with binding-annotation fix-it only; pointer in a `Vec[*const _T]` whose element type is unsolved rejected at the `.read()` site. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) — typechecker-only work; reuses the existing metavariable / generic-parameter distinction infrastructure. No P1 carve-out — the rule is a single typechecker check; the diagnostic + fix-it are the only new compiler emission.

- [x] **Trait method parameters require names — focused diagnostic for anonymous-parameter form.** Spec at `design.md § Trait method parameter names — required` (v60 item 53). The grammar already enforces this — `PARAM = IDENT ":" TYPE | PATTERN ":" TYPE` per syntax.md §3.1, no anonymous alternative — so the rule fires automatically as a generic parse error today. This entry's work is the **focused diagnostic upgrade**: when the parser sees a type token in parameter position with no preceding name, recognize the user intent and emit `E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM` (or `E_FN_ANONYMOUS_PARAM` for free functions) with the type-only span underlined and the `_: i32` / `arg: i32` fix-it suggestion inline. Slices: (1) **Parser recognition.** In `parse_param` (or wherever parameters parse), detect the case where the token sequence starts with a type-class-looking IDENT not followed by `:` (or, more broadly, any token sequence that would form a valid TYPE in this position without a preceding name+colon). When this pattern matches, recover the type from the token stream as if a name had been provided, then emit the focused diagnostic naming the missing-name span and the type. (2) **Diagnostic shape.** `error[E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM]: trait method parameters require a name` (or `E_FN_ANONYMOUS_PARAM` for free functions, which fall under the same rule but a slightly different help line — the trait diagnostic mentions "trait method", the free-fn one says "function"). Span underlines the offending type-only token range. Help line: `write '_: <type>' for an unused parameter, or 'arg: <type>' for a meaningful name`. The `<type>` placeholder is filled with the recovered type so the fix-it is exactly applicable. (3) **Recovery — keep parsing.** After emitting the diagnostic, recover by treating the missing-name case as if `_` had been written; the parser produces a `_`-pattern parameter and continues. This lets the rest of the trait method (and the rest of the file) parse so the user sees every error in one pass rather than cascading parse failures. (4) **Distinguish from other parse errors.** When a parameter genuinely has malformed syntax (unbalanced parens, missing comma, etc.), the focused anonymous-param diagnostic must NOT fire — it should only fire on the specific shape "valid type in parameter position, no preceding name+colon, would parse as a type if positioned in a return-type slot." The detection is: peek ahead, attempt a type parse; if it succeeds and consumes tokens up to a `,` or `)`, the user wrote a type-only parameter — emit `E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM`. Otherwise fall through to the generic parse-error path. (5) **Test coverage.** Positive — `trait V { fn visit(ref self, node: Node); }` parses; `trait V { fn visit(ref self, _: Node); }` parses; `trait V { fn visit(ref self, _: i32, _: i32); }` parses (multiple `_` in the same signature accepted); `fn free(_: i32) { }` parses (free-fn equivalent); `impl V for X { fn visit(ref self, n: Node) { ... } }` accepts the impl using a different parameter name than the trait declared (names are local). Negative — `trait V { fn visit(ref self, Node); }` rejected with `E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM`, span on `Node`, help line offering `_: Node` and `node: Node`; `fn free(i32) { 0 }` rejected with `E_FN_ANONYMOUS_PARAM`; multiple anonymous params in one signature emit one diagnostic per occurrence. Phase target: Phase 2 (Parser & AST) — parser diagnostic upgrade. Verify the existing parser already produces *some* error on the type-only form (it should, via the generic "expected `:` after identifier" path); this entry replaces that with the focused diagnostic. No P1 carve-out — the change is parser-local; the grammar-level rule is already in place, only the diagnostic needs sharpening.

- [~] **`@` binding semantics — match-arm-mode propagation + composition checks.** Spec at `design.md § @ Bindings` (v60 item 52). Phase 2 parser already supports `@` bindings (`PatternKind::AtBinding` recognized in `parse_pattern`); this entry covers the typechecker semantics and composition rules. Slices 1–3, 5–8 verified or shipped (drive-by refutable-let fix: `let PAT = expr;` previously accepted refutable patterns silently — now rejects via `is_irrefutable_param_pattern`, which `AtBinding` inherits transparently from its inner pattern). 7 new parser tests + 5 new typechecker tests cover positive shapes, refutable-let rejection (including the `@`-bound-with-refutable-inner case), and per-form regression. Slice 4 (`E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME`) is the only remaining work — needs ownership-pass integration to detect overlapping consume claims between outer name and inner sub-patterns.

  1. [x] **Verify parser handles all positions.** `IDENT @ PATTERN` parses at top level (match arm), nested inside struct/tuple-variant patterns (`Response { status: code @ 500..=599, body }`), inside or-patterns (`x @ A | x @ B`), and inside `let` patterns (`let x @ Foo { a } = foo`). The existing parser already covers these; each case has a parser test.
  2. [x] **Typechecker — type assignment.** The `@` binding's `IDENT` takes the type of the scrutinee at its position in the pattern tree. For top-level `x @ pattern`, `x` has the scrutinee type; for nested `Response { status: code @ ... }`, `code` has the field type. Existing pattern-typechecking machinery handles this; the AtBinding arm in `infer_pattern` propagates the type correctly.
  3. [x] **Match-arm binding mode propagation.** Tie the `@` binding into the existing scrutinee-mode-propagation pass (`design.md § Match Arm Binding Modes`): owned scrutinee → `@` binding consumes; `ref T` scrutinee → `@` binding is `ref T`; `ref IDENT @ PATTERN` annotation → borrows even under owned scrutinee. The propagation pass already runs over all bindings; AtBinding nodes participate the same as regular IDENT bindings.
  4. [ ] **Cannot-double-consume rule (`E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME`).** When the scrutinee is owned and an `@` binding's outer IDENT would consume the value while a sub-pattern binding inside it would also consume the same field, reject with `error[E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME]: cannot bind both '<outer>' and '<inner>' as owned — '<outer>' would consume the whole value while '<inner>' would consume a field; use 'ref <outer>' to borrow, or omit one of the two bindings`. The check runs as part of the existing partial-move analysis on match arms — when the outer binding's claim is "consume whole" and an inner binding's claim is "consume sub-field", the conflict surfaces at the existing partial-move check site with an enriched diagnostic for the `@`-binding-specific case. **This is the only remaining slice.**
  5. [x] **Refutability for `let` patterns.** Drive-by fix: existing irrefutable-pattern check on `let` and `let ... else` now handles `@` bindings transparently — the `@` itself is irrefutable, so the inner pattern's refutability determines the whole pattern's refutability. `let x @ Some(y) = opt;` is rejected by the refutability check; `let x @ Foo { a } = foo;` is accepted.
  6. [x] **Or-pattern alignment.** `x @ Some(_) | x @ None` accepts (same name, same type); `x @ Some(_) | y @ None` rejects with the existing or-pattern "every alternation must introduce the same set of names" diagnostic enriched to mention the `@`-binding sites.
  7. [x] **`mut` rejection inside patterns.** `mut x @ pattern` rejected at parse with the existing "mut not valid inside patterns" diagnostic; suggested fix-it points at `let mut x = ...` rebind in the arm body.
  8. [x] **Nested `@` bindings.** `outer @ Foo { field: inner @ Bar(value) }` binds three names with correct types; the partial-move check fires at the right granularity if both `outer` and `inner` would consume an overlapping subtree.

  **Test coverage** (mirrored against the slices above). Positive — `match val { x @ Some(_) => ... }` binds `x: Option[T]`; `match val { Response { status: code @ 500..=599, body } => ... }` binds `code: i32` and `body: ...`; `match val: ref Foo { x @ Foo { field } => ... }` binds `x: ref Foo` and `field: ref FieldType` (via match-ergonomics); `ref x @ Some(y) => ...` over an owned scrutinee binds `x: ref Option[T]` without consuming; nested `outer @ Foo { field: inner @ Bar(v) }` binds three names; `x @ Some(_) | x @ None` accepts (same name + same type); `let x @ Foo { a } = foo` accepts (irrefutable); `n @ MIN_AGE..=MAX_AGE` accepts with const-expression range bound (composition with item 51). Negative — `x @ Some(y)` with owned scrutinee where `y` would consume a field that `x` already owns rejected with `E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME` (slice 4); `let x @ Some(y) = opt` rejected with refutability diagnostic; `mut x @ pattern` rejected at parse; `x @ Some(_) | y @ None` rejected with or-pattern same-names diagnostic; `x @ Some(_) | x @ Some(true)` (different inner types in alternation reaching the same name) rejected.

  **Phase target:** 5.2 (Language Features) — typechecker-only work; the parser already supports the form and the existing match-arm-binding-mode pass handles the propagation. No P1 carve-out — option uniform-with-existing-rules ships the full surface at v1.

- [~] **Half-open range patterns + const-expression bounds.** Spec at `design.md § Range Patterns` (v60 item 51). The five-form coverage and exhaustiveness rules are already specced; this entry covers verifying the parser/typechecker for half-open forms and adding the const-expression-bound extension. Slice 1 shipped with two real fixes — bounded-exclusive `lo..hi` was missing from integer/char range arms (parse path now disambiguates `lo..` vs `lo..hi` by peeking for a literal after `..`); and `match value_class_var { ..lit => ... }` previously misparsed as struct-update because `looks_like_struct_literal` matched `{ ..ident }` for any identifier (now gated on `starts_upper(name)`). Interpreter `try_match_pattern` for `RangePattern` was also a "simplified" stub returning true unconditionally; replaced with proper `value_in_range_pattern` handling all five forms via i128 keys. 4 parser + 1 typechecker + 3 interpreter tests. Slices 2–7 (const-expression bounds via `QUALIFIED_PATH`) remain — needs a new `RangeBound { Literal | Path }` AST split + const resolution in the typechecker.

  1. [x] **Verify parser already accepts all five forms.** The grammar in `syntax.md §5.6` covers `CONST_PAT_BOUND ".." CONST_PAT_BOUND`, `CONST_PAT_BOUND "..=" CONST_PAT_BOUND`, `CONST_PAT_BOUND ".."` (unbounded above), `".." CONST_PAT_BOUND` (exclusive end), `"..=" CONST_PAT_BOUND` (inclusive end). All five forms now recognized in `parse_pattern`; the bounded-exclusive and value-class-scrutinee fixes shipped here.
  2. [ ] **AST representation for range patterns.** `Pattern::Range { lo: Option<RangeBound>, hi: Option<RangeBound>, inclusive: bool, span: Span }` with `RangeBound { kind: Literal | Path, ... }`. The `Option`s capture the half-open variants (`None` for the missing bound).
  3. [ ] **Const-expression-bound resolution at typecheck.** When a range pattern's bound is a `QUALIFIED_PATH`, the typechecker resolves it via the existing module-level-const lookup machinery (the same one that powers const-eval for default parameter values, refinement-type bounds, and module-level-binding initializers). On resolution success, the const value is folded into the AST as a literal-equivalent for downstream exhaustiveness and bound-ordering checks. On resolution failure: emit `error[E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_CONST]: range pattern bound '<path>' must resolve to a module-level integer or char const` with the specific failure mode (path not found / resolves to a non-const / wrong type / not at module scope).
  4. [ ] **Bound-ordering check after resolution.** Existing rule (`9..=0` rejected) applies after const-resolution — bounds named via `QUALIFIED_PATH` are compared by their resolved values, so `MAX..=MIN` (where MAX < MIN) is rejected with the same diagnostic the literal form produces.
  5. [ ] **Type-matching check after resolution.** Existing rule applies — both bounds must resolve to the same primitive type (integer width or `char`). Mixed-type bounds (one literal-typed `i32`, one path-resolved `i64`) rejected with the existing same-type diagnostic enriched to name both resolved types.
  6. [ ] **Exhaustiveness — no change beyond existing rule.** Range patterns count toward exhaustiveness only by their resolved-value span; the existing Maranget-style algorithm already operates on resolved literal values, so const-expression bounds slot in transparently after the resolution step.
  7. [ ] **No function-call expressions in pattern position (`E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE`).** Reject anything more complex than `LITERAL` or `QUALIFIED_PATH` in pattern position with `error[E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE]: range pattern bound must be a literal or a path to a module-level const; arbitrary expressions are not accepted at pattern position`. The check runs at parse — the grammar production limits the shape upfront.

  **Test coverage.** Positive — bounded `0..=9` accepts; bounded `'a'..='z'` accepts; half-open `..0`, `0..`, `..=0`, `0..=10` all parse and match (slice 1 ✓); const-bound `match age { MIN_AGE..=MAX_AGE => ... }` resolves and matches (slice 3); const-bound + or-pattern `0..=9 | TEEN_MIN..=TEEN_MAX => ...`; const-bound + `@` binding `n @ MIN_AGE..=MAX_AGE => ...` (composition with item 52); mixed literal + const `0..=MAX_AGE` resolves correctly. Negative — `MAX..=MIN` (where MAX < MIN as resolved values) rejected with bound-ordering diagnostic (slice 4); mixed-type `0i32..=MAX_I64` (where MAX_I64: i64) rejected with same-type diagnostic naming both resolved types (slice 5); non-const path `match age { local_var..=10 => ... }` rejected with `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_CONST` (slice 3); arbitrary expression `match age { (10 + 5)..=20 => ... }` rejected at parse with `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE` (slice 7); float bounds `match x { 1.0..=2.0 => ... }` rejected (existing rule); bare `..` as a pattern rejected with the existing "use `_`" diagnostic.

  **Phase target:** 5.2 (Language Features) — typechecker-only work; reuses existing const-evaluation machinery for path resolution. No P1 carve-out — option (b) of v60 item 51 ships the const-expression-bound extension at v1; refinement and distinct-type range patterns (option c of the decision matrix) are intentionally not in v1 and are additive-later if a workload demands them.

- [ ] **Type alias bounds enforced at use sites.** Spec at `design.md § Type Aliases` (v60 item 50). Slices: (1) **Parser — already accepts bound forms.** The `GENERIC_PARAMS` rule in `syntax.md §3.12` shares grammar with struct/fn declarations, so `type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]` already parses. AST: ensure `Item::TypeAlias { generic_params: Vec<GenericParam>, ... }` records the bounds; verify the existing AST representation captures them (it should, since the same `GenericParam` shape is used elsewhere). (2) **Typechecker — bound substitution and check at use sites.** The existing alias-expansion machinery already substitutes the alias's body when a use site is type-checked. Extend the substitution to walk the alias's generic-parameter bounds in the same pass: for each `GenericParam { name, bounds }`, after binding `name` to the use-site's concrete argument, check each bound against the bound argument via the existing trait-resolution machinery (the same code path that handles `fn foo[T: Ord]` use-site bound checks). On failure, emit `error[E_TYPE_ALIAS_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED]: '<arg>' does not satisfy '<bound>' required by alias '<alias_name>'` with the use-site span as the primary, the alias declaration's span as the note, and the standard "type does not implement trait" help line. (3) **Redundant-bound lint.** When the typechecker resolves the alias body and discovers that a declared bound is already implied by the underlying type's existing bounds (e.g., `type SortedKeyMap[T: Ord] = TreeMap[T, i32]` — TreeMap already requires K: Ord), emit `warning[redundant_alias_bound]: bound '<bound>' on alias '<alias_name>' is implied by the underlying type '<body>'; consider removing` with a fix-it removing the bound. The lint is suppressible via `#[allow(redundant_alias_bound)]` on the alias declaration. (4) **Composition with refinement `where`.** The existing refinement-predicate check at `where REFINEMENT_PRED` is value-level and orthogonal; the new bound check is type-level. Both run at independent times: bound check at use-site type-resolution, refinement at construction. No interaction beyond co-existence on the same alias declaration. (5) **Cross-package surface.** `pub type` alias bounds are part of the API contract — verify the exporter pass records the bounds in the package's interface descriptor so downstream consumers see them; weakening a bound is non-breaking, tightening is breaking (same rule as `pub fn` signatures). (6) **TAIT interaction.** Bounds on a type-alias-`impl Trait` declaration (`type IterOf[T: Display] = impl Iterator[Item = T]`) are checked at every use-site of `IterOf[U]` against `U`; the check is independent of the witness-inference machinery (which is P1). The v1 stub for TAIT (per item 41) already produces the `E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` diagnostic at witness-dependent use sites; bounds on the alias's generic parameters fire the bound check first, then the TAIT stub if the bound passes. (7) **Test coverage.** Positive — `type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]; let x: Index[String] = HashMap.new();` accepts `String` (satisfies `Eq + Hash`); `type SortedVec[T: Ord] = Vec[T]; let v: SortedVec[i32] = Vec.new();` accepts `i32` (satisfies `Ord`); generic alias with multi-bound `type Cache[K: Eq + Hash, V: Clone] = Map[K, V]; let c: Cache[String, Vec[i32]] = Map.new();` accepts when both bounds hold; aliases without bounds (`type UserId = i64`, `type Callback = Fn(Event) -> Result[(), Error] with _`) continue to work unchanged; bound-on-alias composition with refinement (`type SortedNonEmpty[T: Ord] = Vec[T] where self.len() > 0`) parses, and use-site `SortedNonEmpty.try_from(some_vec)` runs both the bound check (compile-time) and the refinement (run-time). Negative — `type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]; let x: Index[Vec[i32]] = HashMap.new();` rejected at the use site with `E_TYPE_ALIAS_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED` naming `Vec[i32]` and the missing `Hash` bound; redundant `type SortedKeyMap[T: Ord] = TreeMap[T, i32]` emits `warning[redundant_alias_bound]` (suppressible); cross-package — exporter declares `pub type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]`, downstream consumer's use site fails the bound check with the alias-declaration span surfaced in the diagnostic note. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) — typechecker-only work; reuses existing trait-resolution machinery for bound checking. No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 50 ships the full surface at v1; the spec is a single typechecker rule, not a multi-phase rollout.

- [~] **Saturating float→int + every-`as`-cast-pair fully defined.** Spec at `design.md § Numeric Semantics > as-cast semantics` (v60 item 49). Two halves: typechecker cast-pair rules (which pairs are accepted/rejected and with which fix-its) and codegen lowering (saturating LLVM intrinsics + four method families on `f32`/`f64`). Slice 1 shipped — bool→int and char→{i32,u32,wider} now accepted; the four rejection diagnostics fire as specced. Slices 2 (stdlib method families) and 4 (codegen lowering) remain; slices 5–9 are existing-behavior verifications.

  1. [x] **Typechecker — cast-pair rejection rules.** Four new error codes for the rejected forms specced in design.md: `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` (rejected at `char as u8/u16/i8/i16` — fix-it suggests `c as u32 as uN` for explicit truncation OR `c.encode_utf8(buf)` for proper UTF-8 encoding), `E_INT_AS_CHAR` (rejected at `iN/uN as char` — fix-it suggests `char.try_from(n)`), `E_INT_AS_BOOL` (rejected at `iN/uN as bool` — fix-it suggests `n != 0`), `E_FLOAT_AS_BOOL` (rejected at `f32/f64 as bool` — meaningless). Each rejection runs at the typechecker's cast-resolution step; the existing redundant-cast lint (`bool as bool` etc.) is preserved.
  2. [ ] **Stdlib — float→int method families.** `f.saturating_to_iN()` / `f.wrapping_to_iN()` / `f.checked_to_iN() -> Option[iN]` / `f.trunc_to_iN()` on every `f32` / `f64` × every signed (`i8`..`i128`) and unsigned (`u8`..`u128`, `usize`, `isize`) target type. Plus the symmetric `i.to_f32()` / `i.to_f64()` for all integer types (the implicit-widening cases work without `as` already; method versions ship for code-style consistency). The four-method family parallels the existing integer arithmetic `checked_*`/`wrapping_*`/`saturating_*`/`overflowing_*` family at the spec level. Methods register in the typechecker's primitive-method table; effect-free except `trunc_to_iN()` which carries `panics` (the trapping-on-out-of-range form).
  3. [x] **`AllocError`-style not-needed.** Out-of-range float→int conversions saturate at the `as` site, so no error type is required for the default form. The `checked_to_iN()` method returns `Option[iN]` (using the existing `Option` type) for users who want the explicit-failure form; no new error type. Decision recorded; no implementation work.
  4. [ ] **Codegen — Phase 7 lowering.** `f as iN` lowers to LLVM `fptosi.sat` (signed target) or `fptoui.sat` (unsigned target) — single instruction per call, available since LLVM 12 on every supported target. `f.saturating_to_iN()` lowers to the same intrinsic — alias-method optimization folds the call to the same IR. `f.wrapping_to_iN()` lowers to `fptosi`/`fptoui` (the un-saturated raw instructions); on targets where the raw instruction's modular-overflow semantics deviate from the documented Kāra rule (currently only some legacy ARM cores per LLVM's documentation), emit a software polyfill that performs the conversion via integer-bit-manipulation to ensure target-independent semantics. `f.checked_to_iN()` emits a pre-check (`fcmp` against the integer's representable range, plus `fcmp uno` for NaN detection) and selects `None` or `Some(saturating-cast-result)` via a `phi` node. `f.trunc_to_iN()` emits the same pre-check and panics on out-of-range or NaN; the panic carries `#[track_caller]` and produces a "float-to-int out of range" message in the panic record.
  5. [ ] **Int→int casts** (existing — verify spec compliance). Bitwise truncation of low M bits on narrowing; sign-extend on signed-source widening (already implicit, not via `as`); zero-extend on unsigned-source widening. Verify codegen emits `trunc` / `sext` / `zext` LLVM instructions matching the documented behavior.
  6. [ ] **Int→float casts** (existing — verify). IEEE 754 round-to-nearest-even via `sitofp` / `uitofp`; integer source > 2^53 may round; never panic.
  7. [ ] **Float→float casts** (existing — verify). Widening is implicit (no `as` required); narrowing via `as` uses `fptrunc` (round-to-nearest-even); overflow produces `±Infinity` per IEEE 754.
  8. [x] **Bool→int casts.** `false as iN/uN` produces `0`; `true as iN/uN` produces `1`. Codegen emits `zext` from `i1` (the LLVM bool type). Accepted as of slice 1.
  9. [x] **Char→int casts (wide targets).** `char as u32` and `char as i32` produce the Unicode scalar value (range `0..=0x10FFFF`, fits in 21 bits); codegen emits `zext` from the `i32`-internal char representation. Wide-target casts accepted as of slice 1; narrow-target casts (`char as u8/u16/i8/i16`) rejected via `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` (slice 1).

  **Test coverage.** Positive — `f64.NAN as i32 == 0`; `f64.INFINITY as i32 == i32.MAX`; `f64.NEG_INFINITY as i32 == i32.MIN`; `1e30f64 as i32 == i32.MAX`; `(-1e30f64) as i32 == i32.MIN`; `1e30f64 as u8 == 255`; `(-1.0f64) as u8 == 0`; `3.7f64 as i32 == 3`; `(-3.7f64) as i32 == -3`; `(2_i64.pow(60)) as f64` rounds to nearest; `i64.MAX as f64` rounds upward past i64.MAX; `0x1FFi32 as u8 == 0xFFu8`; `(-1i32) as u8 == 0xFFu8`; `300i32 as i8 == 44i8`; `(-1i8) as u8 == 255`; `'A' as u32 == 65`; `'A' as i32 == 65`; `false as u8 == 0`; `true as u8 == 1`; `f.saturating_to_i32() == f as i32`; `f.NaN.checked_to_i32() == None`; `1e30f64.checked_to_i32() == None`; `1.5f64.checked_to_i32() == Some(1)`. Negative — `'A' as u8` rejected with `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` and the two fix-its; `'A' as i16` rejected; `65u8 as char` rejected with `E_INT_AS_CHAR` and the `char.try_from` fix-it; `1i32 as bool` rejected with `E_INT_AS_BOOL` and the `n != 0` fix-it; `1.0f64 as bool` rejected with `E_FLOAT_AS_BOOL`; `f.NaN.trunc_to_i32()` panics with the "float-to-int out of range" message and a `#[track_caller]` source location at the call site, not inside the stdlib.

  **Phase target:** Phase 5.2 (typechecker rejection rules + new error codes — slice 1 shipped); Phase 7 (codegen `fptosi.sat` / `fptoui.sat` lowering + the four method families — slices 2/4). No P1 carve-out — v60 item 49 ships the full saturating + every-pair-defined surface at v1; the additional method families on `f32` / `f64` parallel existing integer method-family ergonomics and require no new infrastructure beyond the codegen step.

- [ ] **Fallible-allocation API split — `try_*` companions on every alloc-bearing method + `panic_on_alloc_failure` profile flag.** Spec at `design.md § Fallible Allocation API and OOM Handling` (v60 item 46). Full v1 implementation. Two parallel surfaces: (a) the `try_*` companion methods on every alloc-bearing stdlib type, available always; (b) a profile flag that, when `false`, rejects every panicking-alloc call site at typecheck. Hard mode for embedded/kernel-adjacent profiles; opt-in elsewhere.

  1. [ ] **`AllocError` prelude type.** Register two-variant enum `enum AllocError { OutOfMemory { requested_bytes: usize }, CapacityOverflow }` in the typechecker prelude (parallel to `IoError`, `VarError`, `AlreadySetError`). Implements `Debug`, `Display`, `Eq`, `Copy`. Available everywhere without import; `Result[(), AllocError]` and `Result[T, AllocError]` need no qualification.
  2. [ ] **`try_*` companion methods on every alloc-bearing collection type.** `Vec`: `try_with_capacity`, `try_push`, `try_insert`, `try_extend`, `try_reserve`, `try_reserve_exact`, `try_append`, `try_resize`, `try_clone`, `try_from_iter`. `String`: `try_push`, `try_push_str`, `try_with_capacity`, `try_reserve`, `try_clone`. `Map`/`Set`/`VecDeque`/`SortedSet`: `try_with_capacity` (where applicable), `try_insert`, `try_reserve`, `try_clone`. `Box`/`Rc`/`Arc`: `try_new`. Interpreter implementation reuses the existing alloc paths and wraps with `Result`-on-null at the host-allocator layer (the interpreter rarely actually OOMs; tests can inject failure via a `with_provider`-style allocator hook scheduled with the codegen runtime work below). Typechecker dispatch added to each per-collection `infer_*_method` function. Methods carry the same `allocates(Heap)` effect as their panicking counterparts; the only signature difference is the return type.
  3. [ ] **Profile flag — `panic_on_alloc_failure`.** New field in `[profile]` table parsed by `src/manifest.rs`; `bool`, default `true`. Threaded through `Pipeline.profile` to the typechecker like the existing per-profile knobs (`bounds_checks`, etc.). The flag is rejected (parse error) on profiles that already forbid heap entirely (`embedded`, `kernel`, `isr` — i.e., profiles whose `no_effects` contains `allocates(Heap)`); the diagnostic explains that the flag is moot when heap is forbidden.
  4. [ ] **Panicking-allocator rejection check (`E_PANICKING_ALLOC_REJECTED`).** Typechecker pass under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` walks every call site, operator site, and collection-literal site against a hardcoded **panicking-alloc registry**: every entry of the table in design.md (Vec.push / Vec.with_capacity / String.push / Box.new / etc.) plus the lowering primitives behind `+= on String`, `f"..."` interpolation, `[1, 2, 3]` Vec-literal, `{ k: v }` Map-literal, `Vec.collect`, `Clone.clone` synthesized bodies. Each rejection emits `error[E_PANICKING_ALLOC_REJECTED]: 'Vec.push' may panic on allocation failure; use 'Vec.try_push' instead under panic_on_alloc_failure = false` with the type-swap fix-it inline. The registry is constructed at typechecker init time and keyed by fully-qualified method/operator/lowering name.
  5. [ ] **`#[derive(Clone)]` rejection under fallible-alloc (`E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES`).** When `panic_on_alloc_failure = false`, the derive validator walks each derived `clone` body's call sites; if any reach a panicking allocator (anything in the registry), reject with `error[E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES]: '#[derive(Clone)]' on type 'T' generates a 'clone' that may panic on allocation failure (field 'name' of type 'F' allocates); write a manual 'try_clone' method instead, or suppress with '#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]' if you accept the panic`. Pure-`Copy` types and types whose fields all impl `Clone` infallibly (primitives, refs, single-field newtypes around primitives) are unaffected.
  6. [ ] **Auto-RC fallback rejection (`E_RC_FALLBACK_ALLOCATES_UNDER_FALLIBLE_PROFILE`).** The ownership pass already records `RcEntry` records at sites where the compiler would emit `Rc.new(...)` per Part 4. Under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false`, the diagnostic kit converts each `RcEntry` into `error[E_RC_FALLBACK_ALLOCATES_UNDER_FALLIBLE_PROFILE]: auto-RC fallback at this site emits 'Rc.new(...)' which may panic on allocation failure; restructure to remove the fallback or use 'Rc.try_new(...)?' with explicit '?'-propagation` with the standard restructuring menu (`shared struct`, lifetime adjustment, ownership reshape) inlined into the help line. The check piggybacks on the existing RC-fallback recording pass — no new dataflow is needed; the rejection is a profile-flag-gated diagnostic transformation at the cost-summary emission step.
  7. [ ] **`?`-propagation through `AllocError`.** `AllocError` participates in the standard `From`-chain; user code that calls `try_*` and uses `?` must include `AllocError` in the function's error type's `From` arm or use a top-level `Result[T, AllocError]` return type. No new mechanism — same rule as every other propagated error.
  8. [ ] **Codegen — runtime allocator wrappers.** Phase 7 work — runtime allocator wrapper exposes `kara_alloc_fallible` returning a non-null `*mut u8` on success and `null` on failure; the panicking variant is `kara_alloc_or_panic` which calls the fallible variant and panics on `null` via a `#[track_caller]` helper. Both are emitted into `karac-runtime`. Stdlib generic code is parameterized once and the two API entry points dispatch to the appropriate runtime symbol.
  9. [ ] **`#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]` lint suppression.** Registered as a structured per-binding allow attribute (parallels existing `#[allow(rc_fallback)]`). User opts in to "I'm fine with the derived clone panicking on OOM here" at the type definition; the suppression is per-type, not project-wide.

  **Test coverage** (typechecker + interpreter + codegen, Phase 8 stdlib + Phase 7 runtime). Positive — under `panic_on_alloc_failure = true` (default), `Vec.push(42)` and `Vec.try_push(42)?` both type-check and run; `AllocError` is in the prelude scope without import; `try_with_capacity(usize.MAX)` returns `Err(AllocError.CapacityOverflow)`; `try_clone` available on every alloc-bearing collection. Under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` — `Vec.try_push(42)?` accepted; `Vec.push(42)` rejected with `E_PANICKING_ALLOC_REJECTED` and the fix-it; `s += other` on String rejected; `let v: Vec[i64] = [1, 2, 3]` collection literal rejected; `f"hello {name}"` rejected; `Box.new(x)` rejected; `let v: Vec[i64] = (0..1024).collect()` rejected; `#[derive(Clone)] struct S { v: Vec[i64] }` rejected with `E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES`; auto-RC fallback site rejected with `E_RC_FALLBACK_ALLOCATES_UNDER_FALLIBLE_PROFILE`; same struct under `#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]` accepted with the lint suppression visible in `karac query lint-suppressions`. Profile-flag interaction — `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` on the `embedded` profile (which forbids heap) rejected at manifest parse with the moot-flag diagnostic.

  **Phase target:** Phase 8 (stdlib types + diagnostics + manifest flag); Phase 7 (runtime allocator wrapper). No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 46 ships the full surface at v1; the optional future `#[derive(TryClone)]` companion derive (a sibling that produces fallible `try_clone`) is non-breaking-additive and is not on the v1 critical path.

- [ ] **`panic = "unwind" | "abort"` profile flag + per-profile defaults + abort-mode codegen.** Spec at `design.md § Panic Strategy: panic = "unwind" | "abort"` (v60 item 47). The narrative spec already exists across 6+ scattered references in design.md; this entry consolidates the implementation work behind the new dedicated section. Slices: (1) **Manifest parsing.** `src/manifest.rs` recognizes `panic = "unwind" | "abort"` in `[profile]` blocks. Default value is profile-dependent: `app`/`lib` → `unwind`; `embedded`/`kernel`/`isr`/`gpu` → `abort`. Custom profiles default to `unwind` unless explicitly set. Unknown values produce `error[E_INVALID_PANIC_STRATEGY]` naming the valid set. The setting is threaded through `Pipeline.profile` to the typechecker, effect checker, and codegen. (2) **Panic-strategy threading at compilation entry.** `Compilation.panic_strategy: PanicStrategy { Unwind, Abort }` field populated at pipeline init from the active profile. Available to every downstream phase via the existing `Pipeline` reference. (3) **Library-vs-binary advisory check.** When linking a library whose declared `panic` differs from the leaf binary's setting, emit `warning[W_PANIC_STRATEGY_MISMATCH]: package 'foo' declares panic = "...", this build uses panic = "..."` with the library's name and both settings. The library is recompiled under the binary's setting; the warning is informational. Detection happens at the build-system layer (`cmd_build_project`), not at the typechecker — it requires multi-package context. (4) **`catch_panic` rejection under abort** — already specced at `design.md § Catching Panics`; the typechecker check that gates `catch_panic` calls reads `Compilation.panic_strategy` and rejects with `E_CATCH_PANIC_REQUIRES_UNWIND` under `Abort`. (5) **`extern "C-unwind"` rejection under abort** — already specced at `design.md § FFI`; both declarations and calls are rejected at parse with `E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_UNWIND_PROFILE` under `Abort`. (6) **Effect-checker pass — drop-body panic-freedom enforcement** is unchanged (`Drop` body must be `panics`-free regardless of strategy; the existing rule already covers this). (7) **Custom panic handler attribute.** `#[panic_handler]` on a free function is recognized when `panic_handler = "custom"` is set in the active profile. The handler signature is fixed: `fn(info: ref PanicInfo) -> ()` (or `Never`). The handler must itself be `panics`-free (effect checker rejects otherwise — same rule as `Drop`); under abort, it's the only user code that runs between panic site and termination. Multiple `#[panic_handler]` declarations across the project's source tree produce `error[E_DUPLICATE_PANIC_HANDLER]` naming all spans. Zero declarations + `panic_handler = "custom"` set produces `error[E_MISSING_PANIC_HANDLER]` with a fix-it skeleton. (8) **Default panic handler** — when `panic_handler` is unset (the default), the runtime supplies a built-in handler. Under `unwind`, it walks the stack via the unwinder and writes the JSON crash report per `design.md § Crash Report Format`. Under `abort`, it emits a single-`write(2)` line containing panic site, panic kind, and panic message to stderr, then calls `__kara_abort()`. Both are provided by `karac-runtime`. (9) **Codegen — Phase 7.** Under `Compilation.panic_strategy = Unwind`, the existing LLVM `invoke` + personality + landingpad lowering applies (already part of the catch_panic / drop / RC-fallback / extern-C-unwind work). Under `Compilation.panic_strategy = Abort`, switch to plain `call` instructions and skip personality function attachment, skip cleanup landingpad emission, skip DWARF unwind-table emission (`.eh_frame`, `.gcc_except_table`). Panic-emitting primitives (`unwrap`, `expect`, index-OOB, divide-by-zero, explicit `panic()`) compile to `call __kara_panic_handler(info)` followed by `call __kara_abort()` (the latter marked `noreturn` so LLVM dead-code-eliminates everything past the panic site). RC decrements at scope exit are still emitted under abort (they happen on normal exit paths); the difference is they are not reached on panic paths because there is no unwind. (10) **Build-system — link-time panic-strategy check.** When the build links a binary, verify all participating object files were compiled under the same `panic_strategy`; emit `error[E_PANIC_STRATEGY_LINK_MISMATCH]` if mismatched. This is a defensive check — the per-binary-recompile rule should make mismatches impossible at v1, but the check guards against future ABI-stable library distribution. (11) **Manifest-flag interaction with `no_effects = ["panics"]`** — when the active profile already forbids the panics effect, the `panic` setting still applies to runtime-internal panics (allocator failures from non-fallible code, double-panic on the abort path). Setting `panic = "unwind"` on a `no_effects = ["panics"]` profile is legal but unusual; emit a hint pointing out that user code cannot generate panics so the unwind tables are mostly dead weight. (12) **Composition with `panic_on_alloc_failure`.** The two flags are orthogonal; the typechecker pass for OOM rejection runs independently of the panic strategy. A profile setting both `panic = "abort"` and `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` is the canonical fault-tolerant-system shape. **Test coverage** (typechecker + manifest + codegen, Phase 7 + Phase 8): positive — `panic = "abort"` parsed in `[profile]`; `panic = "unwind"` parsed; default for `app` profile is `unwind`; default for `embedded` is `abort`; default for `kernel` is `abort`; custom profile defaults to `unwind`; `[profile] name = "small_server" panic = "abort"` parses and applies; panic strategy threaded to typechecker; `#[panic_handler]` recognized; LLVM IR under unwind contains `invoke` + personality + landingpads; LLVM IR under abort contains plain `call` + no personality + no `.eh_frame`. Negative — `panic = "fast"` rejected with `E_INVALID_PANIC_STRATEGY`; `catch_panic` under abort rejected with `E_CATCH_PANIC_REQUIRES_UNWIND` (existing test, verified still passes); `extern "C-unwind"` under abort rejected with `E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_UNWIND_PROFILE` (existing test, verified); two `#[panic_handler]` decls rejected with `E_DUPLICATE_PANIC_HANDLER`; missing handler with `panic_handler = "custom"` rejected with `E_MISSING_PANIC_HANDLER` and the fix-it; `#[panic_handler]` body that calls a `panics`-effect function rejected with the existing `panics`-in-handler diagnostic; library declaring `panic = "abort"` linked into `unwind` binary emits `W_PANIC_STRATEGY_MISMATCH` warning. Phase target: Phase 7 (codegen split — invoke vs call, personality, landingpads, DWARF emission); Phase 8 (manifest parsing, profile defaults, threading, advisory warnings, `#[panic_handler]` attribute). No P1 carve-out — option (X) of v60 item 47 ships the full surface at v1; the cleanup-contract semantics under abort match Rust precedent and don't require a Kāra-specific cleanup-walk path.

- [x] **P0 — Module-level `let` / `let mut` bindings — implementation per design.md §1278-1330.** Slice 1 (parser surface) landed 2026-05-21; slice 3 (resolver) landed 2026-05-22; slice 4 (typechecker compile-time-constant initializer rule) landed 2026-05-22; slice 5 (typechecker binding-type inference + mutability check) landed 2026-05-22; slice 6 (effect-checker synthetic per-binding resources + `#[thread_local]` resource wrapping) landed 2026-05-22 — the new `src/effectchecker/modbind_synth.rs` submodule owns the surface: `collect_module_let_mut_bindings` walks `program.items` once, capturing each `let mut BINDING`'s resource name (`<NAME>_resource` for the bare case, `ThreadLocal[<NAME>_resource]` when `#[thread_local]` is present per §1330) into a new `EffectChecker.modbind_let_mut: HashMap<String, ModBindingInfo>` field; immutable `let` bindings declare no synthetic resource and are skipped (reads remain free per §1322). `seed_modbind_synth_effects` seeds `inferred_effects` with a per-binding pair of synthetic callee keys (`__modbind_read.<NAME>` carrying `reads(<resource>)`, `__modbind_write.<NAME>` carrying `writes(<resource>)`) so the existing call-graph propagation machinery (`get_callee_effects` → `infer_function_effects`) carries the synthetic effect through callers without any change to the propagation logic. The body walker `collect_modbind_synth_calls_in_block` is a fresh shadow-aware traversal: a `ModBindingSynthWalker` maintains a `Vec<String>` shadow stack seeded with the function's parameter names, then pushes/pops as it enters `let` / `let-else` / `if-let` / `while-let` / `for` / `match-arm` / `closure-param` scopes — a local binding of the same name as a module binding suppresses the synthetic attribution (mirrors the slice-5 typechecker behaviour where local shadow takes precedence over the module-binding LHS-mutability check). The walker treats bare `Identifier(name)` (and single-segment `Path { segments }`) as a read site; `Assign { target: Identifier(name), value }` is a pure write (no spurious read on the LHS) while `CompoundAssign { target: Identifier(name), value, .. }` contributes both reads and writes (`COUNTER += 1` is load+store at codegen). The walker is invoked from `infer_function_effects` after the existing `collect_calls_in_block`, and its synthetic call entries are merged into the shared `calls` vec — the call-graph filter in `build_call_graph` naturally excludes them (the synthetic keys aren't in `all_fn_names`), so SCC detection and the polymorphic-callee classification remain unchanged. Per-binding granularity is preserved (`COUNTER_resource` and `FLAG_resource` are distinct resources — two writers don't serialize against each other), and reader-writer-across-functions correctly produces the asymmetric effect sets that slice 7's par-block conflict rule will consume. `#[thread_local]` lands the resource wrapping at declaration time (the per-task disjoint-instance semantics per §1330; `Atomic[i64]`-vs-`#[thread_local]` is a user choice between shared-cell and per-task storage). Gpu-profile rejection of `#[thread_local]` per §1330 ("permitted in every profile except `gpu`") is **deferred until the `Gpu` variant of `CompileProfile` lands** — the current enum has only `Default` / `Embedded` / `Kernel`, so there's no profile state to dispatch against; the rejection lives as a single-line `if profile == Gpu` site when the variant arrives. Slice 5's prior surface (env_build module-binding type registration + the §1284 `StringSlice` carve-out + the §1297 heap-`String` rejection + the immutability check) is unchanged. Slice 4's const-init structural walk + heap-`String` rejection on declared types are unchanged. Slice 2 (AST + formatter) was rolled into slice 1. **Slice 7** (par-block conflict rule §1328) landed 2026-05-22 — `check_modbind_par_conflicts` runs as the final Phase B step in `effectchecker.rs::check()`. Each function/method body is walked via `collect_par_blocks_in_block` to find every `ExprKind::Par(block)` (nested par blocks included), and each par block's transitive effect set is computed via `collect_calls_in_block` + slice-6 `collect_modbind_synth_calls_in_block` → `get_callee_effects`. Any `writes(<resource>)` resolving (via the new `lookup_modbind_by_resource` helper) to an unwrapped `let mut` binding — neither a concurrency primitive (root type-name match: `Atomic` / `Mutex` / `RwLock` / `Arc`, detected by the new `is_concurrency_primitive` flag on `ModBindingInfo` populated at collection time from the binding's `ty` AST) nor `#[thread_local]` (`ThreadLocal[<NAME>_resource]` resources are filtered by prefix — per-task disjoint instances by construction never conflict) — fires `error[E_MODULE_BINDING_WRITE_IN_PAR]` (code `E0408`) with the §1328 verbatim fix-it text (`wrap in Atomic[T], Mutex[T], or use #[thread_local] for per-task state`) and the binding-decl line embedded in the message (the secondary span lives in the message text — adding a structured secondary span would require expanding the shared `EffectError` struct beyond slice 7's scope; the line-in-message form preserves the locator information). `ModBindingInfo` gained `decl_span` and `is_concurrency_primitive`. Deduplication: one diagnostic per offending binding per par block, not one per write site (two `COUNTER = …` writes in the same par block produce one error). Reader+reader stays legal (the rule fires on `writes` only); reader+writer cross-branch is caught via the writer branch's write; writer+writer fires once per offending binding (two distinct bindings → two diagnostics). **Known limitation (deferred):** the par-block check's synth walker doesn't track function-level local shadows introduced before the par block — the slice-6 walker's shadow stack is per-walk, and the slice-7 sub-block walk starts fresh, so a function-local `let counter` declared before a `par { counter = 1; }` would spuriously over-attribute the synthetic write onto a module binding named `COUNTER`. Module bindings are Const-class (SCREAMING_SNAKE_CASE); local Const-class shadows are exotic in practice — a focused follow-up if real-world code surfaces the corner case. Slice 6's prior surface (synthetic-resource attribution + `#[thread_local]` resource wrapping) is unchanged. **Slice 8** (`pub fn` synthetic-resource rejection §1326) landed 2026-05-22 — `verify_pub_fn_no_synthetic_resource` runs as a new Phase-B step in `effectchecker.rs::check()`, right after `verify_declarations`. Only fires under `public_effects = "declared"`; iterates `function_bodies` + `method_bodies`, filters to `function_visibility[name] == true`, and walks each public function's inferred effect set looking for synthetic per-binding resources (decoded via the slice-7 `lookup_modbind_by_resource` helper). Each `(public fn, offending binding)` pair fires `error[E_PUB_FN_SYNTHETIC_RESOURCE]` (code `E0409`) with the §1326 verbatim escape-hatch text (the four concurrency primitives spelled out — `Atomic[T]`, `Mutex[T]`, `RwLock[T]`, `Arc[shared struct S]` — plus the `public_effects = "inferred"` project-level escape) and the binding's decl line embedded in the message. Concurrency-primitive escape (§1326 path (a)): `is_concurrency_primitive` from slice 7's `ModBindingInfo` short-circuits the rejection so a `pub fn` against an `Atomic[i64]` / `Mutex[T]` / `RwLock[T]` / `Arc[...]` binding is accepted without further annotation. `#[thread_local]`: the `ThreadLocal[BINDING_resource]` resource is per-task disjoint by construction, so the public-boundary synchronisation concern doesn't apply — `verify_pub_fn_no_synthetic_resource` filters those resources by prefix, matching the slice-7 pattern. `Inferred` policy escape (§1326 path (b)): the entire pass returns early under `PublicEffectsPolicy::Inferred` — synthetic effects continue to participate in conflict analysis (slice-7 par-block rule still fires), they just aren't declaration violations. Deduplication: `seen: HashSet<String>` keyed by binding name guarantees one diagnostic per `(function, binding)` pair, so a pub fn that both reads and writes the same binding produces one diagnostic, while a pub fn that touches two distinct synthetic bindings produces two. **Filter wiring in `verify_declarations`:** the new `EffectChecker::is_synthetic_modbind_resource(resource)` helper (sibling to `lookup_modbind_by_resource`) is threaded into all four arms of `verify_declarations` (Polymorphic / PolymorphicWithFixed / Explicit / None) so synthetic-modbind effects are skipped from the generic `MissingEffectDeclaration` / over-declared paths — the "Add: writes(COUNTER_resource)" fix-it from the None arm would otherwise suggest a name the user cannot legally write in source. Slice 8's dedicated rejection owns those diagnostics end-to-end. The `EffectErrorKind::PubFnSyntheticResource` variant and the `E0409` JSON dispatch arm in `src/cli.rs` complete the wiring. 13 slice-8 tests in `tests/effectchecker.rs` cover: direct-write rejection, direct-read rejection (reads carry the synthetic resource just as writes do), transitive write via private callee, inferred-policy escape, `Atomic`/`Mutex`/`RwLock` concurrency-primitive escapes, `#[thread_local]` escape, immutable-`let` no-rejection, private-fn no-rejection, two-binding-two-diagnostic dedup, single-binding-reads+writes single-diagnostic dedup, no-double-fire-with-MissingEffectDeclaration, and pub-method (impl-block) coverage. **Slice 9** (codegen lowering) landed 2026-05-22 — the new `src/codegen/module_bindings.rs` submodule owns the surface. `declare_module_bindings` runs once at the start of `compile_program` (after `Item::ConstDecl` collection, before any function compilation) and emits one LLVM global per `Item::ModuleBinding`: immutable `let X: T = INIT` → `@X = internal constant T INIT` (set via `set_constant(true)`); `let mut X: T = INIT` → `@X = internal global T INIT` (`set_constant(false)`); `#[thread_local]` attribute → `set_thread_local_mode(Some(GeneralDynamicTLSModel))` on the global (portable across ELF/Mach-O). Internal linkage on both shapes so the binding doesn't escape the translation unit. The `ModuleBindingInfo<'ctx> { global, llvm_ty, is_mut }` carrier lives in `Codegen.module_bindings: HashMap<String, ModuleBindingInfo>`. Initializer surface for v1: the primitive literal shapes (Integer / Float / Bool / Char / Byte) lower via the existing `const_int_for_suffix` / `const_float_for_suffix` / `bool_type().const_int` helpers; `StringLit` (with or without an explicit `StringSlice` annotation per §1284) lowers to a `(ptr, len, cap=0)` aggregate constant — the byte payload becomes its own `internal constant` global named `modbind.str.<index>` so the runtime scope-exit cleanup never frees the static buffer (the `cap=0` marker is the same convention `Vec`/`String` literals use); `Unary { op: Neg, operand: Integer/Float }` is recursively unwrapped so negative-literal initialisers work. Composite initialisers (struct / enum / tuple / special-form constructors) return `None` from `module_binding_init` and are deferred to slice 10's wrapper-type coordination — the typechecker (slice 4) already rejects shapes outside the permitted surface, so the codegen surface only needs to handle the shapes that reach it. **Identifier read path** in `compile_expr` Identifier arm gains a `try_load_module_binding(name)` short-circuit positioned AFTER the local-variable check (so local shadowing works) and BEFORE the `consts` / `try_unit_enum_variant` / external-function lookups — when the name resolves to a module binding, `builder.build_load(info.llvm_ty, info.global.as_pointer_value(), "modbind.load")` returns the loaded `BasicValueEnum`. **Identifier write paths** in `StmtKind::Assign` and `StmtKind::CompoundAssign` gain a parallel `try_store_module_binding(name, val)` short-circuit that fires before the local-slot store; CompoundAssign also routes its load through `try_load_module_binding` because `load_variable` errors when the name has no entry in `self.variables`. The typechecker (slice 5) rejects writes to immutable bindings before codegen runs, and LLVM's `constant` global flag catches any missed case as a verifier error — no silent corruption surface. 13 slice-9 codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs` cover: immutable-let read, let-mut read+write across functions, compound-assign (`+=` / `-=` / `*=`), StringSlice literal, `#[thread_local]` read+write, bool let-mut, float immutable-let, negated int literal, two independent let-mut bindings, write-then-read-from-callee global-state visibility, local-shadow precedence; plus 2 IR-shape tests that assert `@X = internal constant i64 100`, `@COUNTER = internal global i64 0`, and the `thread_local` keyword on the `#[thread_local]` global. **Slice 10** (cross-coordination + composite-initialiser codegen) landed 2026-05-22 — the const-init special-form recognition was already wired in slice 4 (`module_binding_call_is_special_form` in `src/typechecker/items.rs` recognises `LazyLock.new(|| …)`, `OnceLock.new()`, `OnceCell.new()`, `Atomic.new(LITERAL)`, `Mutex.new(LITERAL)`); slice 10 reaudited the surface and confirmed no additional wiring was needed at the typechecker layer (the OnceLock/OnceCell entry directly below + the `Atomic[T]` / `Mutex[T]` entries elsewhere in this file own their own codegen-side const-init lowering when they ship — the typechecker side is already permissive). The codegen composite-initialiser surface in `src/codegen/module_bindings.rs` gained the slice-10 forms: `ExprKind::Tuple` → anonymous struct constant (heterogeneous field types preserved via `context.const_struct`); `ExprKind::ArrayLiteral` → `[N x T]` constant via the `array_type_of` / `const_array_of` BasicTypeEnum-variant dispatchers (homogeneous element type re-validated at the value level so a typechecker miss surfaces as `None` rather than an LLVM panic); `ExprKind::RepeatLiteral { type_name, value, count }` → `[N x T]` constant with the element constant replicated, count-folded from an `Integer` literal (other shapes return `None`); `ExprKind::StructLiteral` → `struct_ty.const_named_struct` driven by `struct_types[Name]` + `struct_field_names[Name]` so source-order `{ b: …, a: … }` field listings land each value in the correct LLVM slot; `ExprKind::Path { segments: [EnumName, UnitVariant] }` → enum layout's struct constant with the tag in field 0 and the payload words zero-initialised (payload-bearing `EnumName.Variant(args)` deferred — its word-stream encoder is builder-driven). The string-literal arm now serves nested positions as well (a `StringSlice` field inside a struct lowers through `modbind_string_slice_const`); the new helpers `array_type_of` / `const_array_of` / `basic_zero_const` dispatch over `BasicTypeEnum` variants so any element type the value-recursion produces (Int / Float / Bool / Pointer / Struct / Array) is supported uniformly. **Cross-function visibility fix:** `ModuleBindingInfo` gained a `declared_type: Option<TypeExpr>` field, and a new `reseed_module_binding_side_tables` helper re-registers `var_type_names` / `vec_elem_types` / etc. at the start of every function body (`compile_function` and `compile_mono_function` clear those tables per function — module bindings live for the program's lifetime but their codegen-side registrations would otherwise be invisible inside function bodies). The path-expression dispatcher in `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_path_expr` gained a leading module-binding arm: `Path { segments: [BINDING, field] }` where `BINDING` resolves to a module binding routes to a `load + extractvalue` against the global (the parser emits `CFG.field` as a 2-segment Path because the leading segment is Const-class; without this arm the access would have fallen through to the enum unit-variant path's silent-`0` placeholder). The Array fast path in `src/codegen/collections.rs::compile_index` gained a fall-back from the local-variable lookup to `self.module_bindings.get(name)` so `ARR[0]` against a module-bound `Array[T, N]` uses the global's pointer + `llvm_ty` for the GEP. **Remaining (deferred, non-blocking):** the `#[thread_local]` gpu-profile rejection still waits on `CompileProfile::Gpu` (the current enum has only `Default` / `Embedded` / `Kernel`); the par-block-walker function-level-shadow tracking still waits on a real-world surface for the corner case; codegen lowering for the special-form constructors (`LazyLock.new` / `OnceLock.new` / `OnceCell.new` / `Atomic.new` / `Mutex.new`) lands under each wrapper type's own codegen entry (typechecker accepts them; codegen returns `None` from `module_binding_init` for now, deferring to those entries). 9 slice-10 codegen tests in `tests/codegen.rs` cover: struct literal field access, source-order != declaration-order field listings, fixed-size array literal indexed read, repeat literal with summed access, enum unit-variant match against two distinct modules bindings, struct with negative-int field via `Unary { Neg }` recursion; plus 2 IR-shape tests asserting `@CORNER = internal constant { i64, i64 } { i64 3, i64 7 }` and `@ARR = internal constant [3 x i64]`. Spec is already complete in design.md and (post-slice-5) the parser + resolver + typechecker accept the form; the effect-checker / par-block / codegen wiring is the remaining gap. Surfaced 2026-05-21 by backend-kata probes (see `wip-todo-api-kata.md § Decisions log 2026-05-21` for the empirical write-up — every approach to shared mutable state across HTTP handler calls bottoms out at the same parser rejection, and the existing corpus (`examples/parallax/`, `examples/elevator/`) uses only `const` at module scope, so this work also has no regression baseline beyond `const`). **Why P0 v1:** the OnceLock/OnceCell entry directly below and the `LazyLock` / `Mutex` / `Atomic` / `Arc[shared struct S]` primitives (each their own existing or implied stdlib entry) all declare as `let X: LazyLock[T] = LazyLock.new(...)` at module scope and are unbuildable until module-level `let` works; the synthetic-per-binding effect resources at §1322 are core to the v1 effect system and feed conflict analysis (Feature 2) for any code touching global state; every backend kata in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` axes 1-3 (backend-service, CLI, systems / data-pipeline) needs at least one of these surfaces; and embedded-profile MMIO / DMA / hardware-register patterns per §1320 ("primarily intended for embedded and bare-metal code") have no alternative. Slices: (1) **Parser** — replace `src/parser/items.rs:1439 reject_top_level_let`'s hard-rejection with a real module-binding parse arm. Accept `[ATTRIBUTES] [VIS] let [mut] IDENT [: TYPE] = CONST_EXPR ;` at item position, reusing the existing statement-form `let`-binding parser for the body shape but treating the result as an `Item::ModuleBinding { name, mutable, vis, attributes, ty: Option<Type>, init: Expr, span }` rather than a `Stmt::Let`. The `parse_const_expr` machinery already used by `Item::Const` parses the RHS. Item-recovery: same skip-to-next-item dance the current hard-reject uses, so a malformed module binding doesn't poison downstream item parsing. (2) **AST + formatter** — `Item::ModuleBinding` with fields above; formatter emits `[attrs] [pub] let [mut] NAME[: TYPE] = INIT;` with the same one-space-around-`=` convention as `const`. (3) **Resolver** — register the binding's identifier in the Const-class namespace per design.md §273 + §300; enforce that the identifier matches the Const-class naming convention (all-caps with optional digits and underscores) and emit `error[E_MODULE_BINDING_NAMING]` naming the offending identifier if a lowercase form is used (parallels the existing const-naming check). Visibility forms (`pub`, `pub(crate)`, default-private) round-trip per the existing rules; module bindings participate in import resolution exactly like consts. Shadowing within a module is rejected at parse — same identifier declared twice at module scope is `E_DUPLICATE_MODULE_BINDING`. (4) **Compile-time-constant initializer rule** per design.md §1280-1297 — new typechecker pass that walks the `init` expression and rejects if any sub-expression requires runtime evaluation. Permitted forms: literals of any primitive type (with the §1284 rule that string literals have type `StringSlice` at module scope rather than the function-body default `String` — `String` itself is heap-allocated and forbidden per §1297); references to other module-level bindings (same module or imported); arithmetic, boolean, and comparison ops applied to permitted forms; struct constructors whose every field is a permitted form; enum variant constructors whose every payload is a permitted form; tuple / fixed-size array literals over permitted forms; the compiler-recognized constant-init special forms `LazyLock.new(|| ...)`, `OnceLock.new()`, `OnceCell.new()`, `Atomic.new(LITERAL)`, `Mutex.new(LITERAL)` — recognized at the path-call dispatch in a way parallel to today's `LazyLock.new` recognition (see entry directly below for the OnceLock/OnceCell side). Rejected: any function call that is not a recognized special form; any method call; any allocator-touching construct including bare `Vec.new()` / `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` / `String.from` (use `LazyLock[Vec[T]]` etc. as the §1297 work-around); effectful calls per §1309 — emit `error[E_MODULE_BINDING_EFFECTFUL_INIT]: module-level binding initializer cannot carry effects ('NAME' carries 'effect_set')` with the offending sub-expression's span. (5) **Typechecker — binding type inference and mutability check** — when `: TYPE` is absent, infer from `init`; reject reassignment of immutable `let` bindings via the existing assignment-LHS check extended to recognize module-scope `let` (versus `let mut`). (6) **Effect-checker — synthetic per-binding resources** per design.md §1322. For every module-level `let mut BINDING` (immutable `let` declares no synthetic resource — there's nothing to write), declare an internal `effect resource BINDING_resource;` that is not exportable and not nameable in user source. Read sites contribute `reads(BINDING_resource)` to the enclosing function's inferred effect set; assignment sites contribute `writes(BINDING_resource)`. The synthetic resource participates in normal conflict analysis: `reads` + `reads` is non-conflict, `reads` + `writes` is conflict, `writes` + `writes` is conflict. The per-binding granularity (not a single `GlobalModule` bucket) is deliberate per the design — otherwise every module-level mutation serializes against every other. **`#[thread_local]` variant** per §1330: when the binding carries `#[thread_local]`, the synthetic resource is `ThreadLocal[BINDING_resource]` (a parameterized resource that never conflicts with itself across tasks because each task holds a disjoint instance). Reject `#[thread_local]` under the `gpu` profile (no thread-local execution-model analog). (7) **Par-block conflict rule** per design.md §1328 — extend the existing `par { }` checker so any branch whose transitive effect set contains `writes(BINDING_resource)` for a `let mut BINDING` whose type is not an explicit concurrency primitive (`Atomic[T]`, `Mutex[T]`, `RwLock[T]`, `Arc[shared struct S]`) is rejected with `error[E_MODULE_BINDING_WRITE_IN_PAR]: module-level let mut 'BINDING' cannot be written from inside par { } — wrap in Atomic[T], Mutex[T], or use #[thread_local] for per-task state` with the par-block span and the binding-decl span both labeled. Reader-reader across branches stays legal; reader-writer across branches is rejected by the existing conflict analysis once the synthetic resource is in the effect sets. The diagnostic copies the fix-it from §1328 verbatim. (8) **`pub fn` and synthetic resource** per design.md §1326 — a `pub fn` that directly mutates a module-level `let mut` cannot satisfy `public_effects = "declared"` because the synthetic resource is not nameable in the public declaration. Two supported paths: (a) wrap the binding in a named concurrency primitive (`Atomic[T]`, `Mutex[T]`, `RwLock[T]`, `Arc[shared struct S]`) and declare effects on those well-known resources at the public surface; (b) `public_effects = "inferred"` at the project level (the `embedded`-profile device-driver escape hatch) — the synthetic resource is then displayed in `karac explain` output but does not need to appear in the declaration. Diagnostic at the `pub fn` decl when the function's inferred effect set contains a `writes(SYNTH_resource)` and the project is on `public_effects = "declared"`: `error[E_PUB_FN_SYNTHETIC_RESOURCE]: pub fn 'NAME' writes module-level 'BINDING' whose synthetic resource cannot appear in a declared effect set — wrap 'BINDING' in Atomic/Mutex/RwLock/Arc[shared struct], or switch the project to public_effects = "inferred"` with the function decl + binding decl spans both labeled and the two fix-its enumerated in the help. (9) **Codegen** — lower immutable module-level `let X: T = INIT;` to an LLVM `@X = internal constant T INIT` global with the appropriate constant initializer for the permitted-form expression tree (literal → LLVM constant; struct constructor → LLVM struct constant; etc.). Lower `let mut X: T = INIT;` to `@X = internal global T INIT`. The synthetic-resource analysis from slice (6) does not change codegen — it lives in the effect system only. `#[thread_local]` lowers to an LLVM `thread_local` global with the platform-appropriate TLS model. Reads in function bodies lower to LLVM `load`; writes lower to LLVM `store`. The compiler-recognized special-form initializers (`LazyLock.new(|| ...)`, `OnceLock.new()`, etc.) emit the runtime-side cell representation per the existing/forthcoming stdlib entries — coordinate with the OnceLock/OnceCell entry below so the closure-as-function-pointer storage for `LazyLock.new(|| ...)`'s initializer fits the synthetic-resource model. (10) **Cross-coordination with `OnceLock`/`OnceCell`/`LazyLock`/`Mutex`/`Atomic` entries** — the slice that wires the const-init permitted-special-forms list to the compiler-recognized constructors is the touch point with the entry directly below (and with the `Atomic[T]` / `Mutex[T]` / `RwLock[T]` entries elsewhere in this file once they're filed). Land slice (1)-(5) first as the parser-through-typechecker foundation; (6)-(8) as the effect-system layer; (9) as the codegen layer; (10) as the integration with the wrapper-type entries. **Test coverage**: positive — `let MAX: i64 = 100;` parses, resolves, type-checks, lowers; `let mut COUNTER: i64 = 0;` + free-fn that increments + read at module scope works end-to-end (a single binary that prints the incremented counter); `let GREETING: StringSlice = "hello";` works (StringSlice type, no heap allocation); `let mut TODOS: LazyLock[Mutex[Vec[Todo]]] = LazyLock.new(|| Mutex.new(Vec.new()));` parses + resolves once the wrapper-type entries land; `#[thread_local] let mut TLS_COUNTER: i64 = 0;` parses + emits as thread-local + non-conflicting across tasks; `pub fn bump() { COUNTER = COUNTER + 1; }` accepted under `public_effects = "inferred"`, rejected under `"declared"`; reader+reader across `par { }` branches accepted; reader+writer rejected. Negative — `let mut V: Vec[i64] = Vec.new();` rejected with `E_MODULE_BINDING_EFFECTFUL_INIT` (or the heap-allocation rejection diagnostic — final code name to be decided during impl); `let mut S: String = "x".to_owned();` rejected per §1297; `let mut N: i64 = compute();` rejected because `compute()` is not a recognized special form; immutable `let X: i64 = 0; ... X = 1;` rejected at the assignment site with the existing immutable-reassignment diagnostic; same-name `let mut X` declared twice at module scope rejected with `E_DUPLICATE_MODULE_BINDING`; lowercase identifier `let mut counter: i64 = 0;` rejected with `E_MODULE_BINDING_NAMING`; `writes(COUNTER_resource)` from inside a `par { }` branch when `COUNTER: i64` (not wrapped) rejected with `E_MODULE_BINDING_WRITE_IN_PAR`; `pub fn bump()` under `"declared"` with no concurrency wrapper rejected with `E_PUB_FN_SYNTHETIC_RESOURCE`; `#[thread_local]` under the `gpu` profile rejected with `E_THREAD_LOCAL_INVALID_PROFILE`. **Probe fixtures already on disk** at `/tmp/kara-probes/q1_module_let_mut.kara`, `q1c_const_mut.kara`, `q3_module_vec.kara`, `q4_lazylock.kara` — minimal regression seeds for slices (1)-(4). Phase target: 5.2 (parser, AST, resolver — slices 1-3); Phase 3 (typechecker + effect-checker — slices 4-8); Phase 7 (codegen — slice 9); Phase 8 (stdlib coordination — slice 10). Cross-reference: design.md §1278-1330 (spec); §1322 (synthetic-resource rule); §1328 (par-block conflict rule); §1330 (`#[thread_local]`); §1343 (`LazyLock`); §1374 (`OnceLock`); `src/parser/items.rs:1439 reject_top_level_let` (current hard-reject — replaced by slice 1); `examples/parallax/bench/kara/server.kara` + `examples/elevator.kara` (existing `const`-only corpus — regression baseline); `kara-katas/PLAN.md` Priority 1 (backend-service kata that needs this); entry directly below (`OnceLock`/`OnceCell`) and `LazyLock`/`Mutex`/`Atomic` entries (downstream consumers of the const-init special-form recognition); `wip-todo-api-kata.md § Decisions log 2026-05-21` (probe results that surfaced this gap).

- [x] **`Vec.new()` / `VecDeque.new()` as module-binding const-init.** First wrapper-type follow-on to the §1278-1330 umbrella above — the slice-10 doc-comment listed these as deferred ("wait on the wrapper-type entries"). Landed 2026-05-22 at `d92f3da` as a focused two-edit slice: (1) `src/typechecker/items.rs::module_binding_call_is_special_form` gained a `"Vec" | "VecDeque" => args.is_empty()` arm alongside the existing `OnceLock` / `OnceCell` / `Atomic` / `Mutex` arms, and the `E_MODULE_BINDING_EFFECTFUL_INIT` diagnostic message gained the two new forms in its enumeration; (2) `src/codegen/module_bindings.rs::modbind_init_from_value` gained an `ExprKind::Call { callee, args } if args.is_empty()` arm delegating to a new `modbind_empty_vec_const` helper that recognises 2-segment Path callees `Vec.new()` / `VecDeque.new()` and emits LLVM `const_struct({ptr null, i64 0, i64 0})` matching `vec_struct_type` — the runtime invariant for an empty Vec (`{ptr=null, len=0, cap=0}` per `assoc_call.rs:1256`'s shared `Vec/VecDeque && method == "new"` arm). LLVM prints this aggregate as `zeroinitializer`. No heap allocation needed; the value is a true compile-time constant. `Map.new()` was investigated and explicitly excluded — the runtime calls `karac_map_new` to install hash seeds, so it can't be a compile-time constant. Filed as the `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` module-binding entry directly below (different mechanism — static-init prologue rather than const struct). Regression tests: `tests/typechecker.rs::test_module_binding_vec_new_init_accepted` (positive — Vec.new(), VecDeque.new(), immutable form); `tests/typechecker.rs::test_module_binding_vec_new_with_args_rejected` (negative — `Vec.new(1)` still rejected); `tests/codegen.rs::test_ir_modbind_vec_new_emits_empty_aggregate` + `test_ir_modbind_vecdeque_new_emits_empty_aggregate` (IR shape pins). The old `test_module_binding_vec_new_init_rejected` was flipped to the positive case. **Why P1 v1:** the §1278-1330 umbrella ships without a way to declare an empty growable global Vec — every backend kata in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` axis 1 (backend-service) needs at least an in-memory store pattern, and `LazyLock[Vec[T]]` adds ceremony that visibly weakens the Go-comparison story. Cross-reference: design.md §1278-1330 (umbrella); `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs:1256` (Vec.new() runtime lowering); umbrella entry directly above (slice-10 deferral note); the uppercase-receiver method dispatch entry directly below (remaining kata blocker); `wip-todo-api-kata.md § Blockers` (kata's blockers list).

- [x] **Uppercase-receiver method dispatch — typechecker + lowering + codegen rewrite.** Pre-existing latent bug surfaced 2026-05-22 while probing the kata's planned shape `let mut TODOS: Vec[Todo] = Vec.new(); TODOS.push(t)`. The parser at `src/parser/exprs.rs:1298-1326` greedily consumes Path segments after an uppercase-leading identifier followed by `.`, producing `Call(Path([TODOS, push]))` instead of `MethodCall(TODOS, push)`. The parser comment is explicit about the intent ("Type/Const-class idents (uppercase leading) root a path here; Value-class idents fall through to the postfix loop") but the parser can't tell at parse time whether the leading segment is a type or a value binding. Affected ANY uppercase receiver: `let F: Foo = Foo { value: 5 }; F.double()` failed identically to `TODOS.push(1)` with the misleading diagnostic `type 'Foo' is not callable`. Landed 2026-05-22 at `f41a62c` via three coordinated edits: (1) **Typechecker dispatch** in `src/typechecker/expr_call.rs::infer_call` — top-of-function arm detects `Call(Path([first, method], None))` with `first` resolving as a value binding (new `path_first_segment_is_value_binding` predicate: local-scope hit OR `env.constants` hit that is not also a known type name; locals shadow types unconditionally per Kara design), constructs a synthetic `Identifier(first)` receiver, and routes through `infer_method_call`. The call span is inserted into the new `path_call_method_dispatch: HashSet<SpanKey>` side-table on `TypeCheckResult`. (2) **Lowering rewrite** in `src/lowering.rs::try_rewrite`'s Call arm — `rewrite_path_call_to_method_call` (tried before `rewrite_bare_assoc_fn_call`) consults the side-table and mutates the AST node from `Call { callee: Path([X, method]), args }` to `MethodCall { object: Identifier(X), method, args }`. Downstream phases see the uniform method-call shape with no further special-casing. (3) **Codegen sibling block** in `src/codegen/method_call.rs::compile_method_call` — when the Identifier receiver is in `module_bindings` but not `variables`, dispatch through the same `compile_vec_method` / `compile_map_method` / `compile_set_method` paths a local Vec/Map/Set would use; `src/codegen.rs::get_data_ptr` gains a module-binding fall-back returning the global's pointer (matching the existing `collections.rs::compile_index` fall-back from slice 10). Effect / ownership / interpreter need no changes — after lowering they see `MethodCall(Identifier(X), ...)`. The `db573a4` `Type.method()` rejection ordering is preserved by the predicate's "not a known type name" guard: `Vec.new()`, `String.from(x)`, and similar Type-associated calls continue to route through `resolve_path_type` because `Vec` / `String` are in `PRELUDE_TYPES` / `env.structs`. 7 regression tests: `tests/typechecker.rs::test_uppercase_local_method_dispatch`, `test_uppercase_modbind_vec_method_dispatch` (the kata's exact shape), `test_uppercase_modbind_const_method_dispatch`, `test_vec_new_type_assoc_call_still_resolves` (negative guard against the rewrite shadowing Type-associated calls), `test_unknown_type_method_rejection_still_fires` (negative guard against regressing `db573a4`); `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_modbind_vec_push_then_len` (full end-to-end pin: 3 pushes + len through the rewrite path produces `3\n`), `test_e2e_modbind_vec_indexed_read`, `test_e2e_uppercase_local_struct_method`. Closes the backend kata's Slice 4 blocker — the kata's planned `let mut TODOS: Vec[Todo] = Vec.new(); TODOS.push(t)` shape now compiles and runs correctly. **Why P0 v1:** without this fix, the Vec.new() module-init entry immediately above was unusable — the global compiled but no method call on it worked. Every backend kata in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` axes 1-3 needing module-level state shared this blocker. **Known limitation (deferred):** field access on uppercase locals (`let F: Foo = ...; let x: i64 = F.value;`) is still broken for the same parser-greedy-Path reason — `resolve_path_type` for `Path([F, value])` returns the type of `F` (Foo) instead of the type of the field. Codegen has its own correct path so the field access works end-to-end in compiled binaries (proven by slice-10's `test_e2e_modbind_struct_literal`), but the typechecker disagrees with codegen on the field's type, and `karac build` exits on the typecheck error. Vec is empty-struct so the kata's Slice 4 doesn't need field access. Filed as the sibling-half "Uppercase-receiver field access" entry directly below. Cross-reference: `src/parser/exprs.rs:1298-1326` (greedy path-consumption site, kept as-is); `src/typechecker/expr_call.rs::infer_call` + `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs::path_first_segment_is_value_binding` (dispatch); `src/lowering.rs::rewrite_path_call_to_method_call` (AST mutation); `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (module-binding dispatch); `src/codegen.rs::get_data_ptr` (module-binding pointer fall-back); the Vec.new() entry directly above (slice 4 unblock half 1); `wip-todo-api-kata.md` (kata's planned shape — now buildable).

- [x] **`Vec[a, b, c]` literal codegen — `PrefixCollectionLiteral` compile arm.** Landed 2026-05-22 at `540cd8c`. New `compile_vec_prefix_literal` helper in `src/codegen/collections.rs`: empty `Vec[]` → `{null, 0, 0}` aggregate (matches Vec.new()); non-empty malloc `items.len() * sizeof(elem)` + per-slot GEP store + return `{buf, len, len}` (cap-equals-len; first push triggers grow).
