Wired from `compile_expr`'s newly-added `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { type_name: "Vec", items }` arm. Set / Map prefix literals fall through to the default arm unchanged — separate slices when corpus surfaces the need. 3 regression tests in `tests/codegen.rs`: standalone literal + indexed reads, literal-as-enum-payload (`Json.Array(Vec[a, b])`), and post-construction `push` triggering grow. Original P1. Surfaced 2026-05-22 while shipping the backend TODO API kata Slice 4. Updated 2026-05-22 after deeper investigation in the gap-fixes follow-up worktree: the bug is broader than originally framed. `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral` (the AST node the parser produces for `Vec[a, b]` / `Set[a, b]`) is recognized by the parser, the typechecker, the interpreter, and `src/lowering.rs` (where `Array[...]` lowers to `ArrayLiteral` but Vec/Set/Map prefix forms stay as-is for codegen) — but `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_expr` has NO arm for it. It falls through to the default `_ => Ok(i64 0)` at line 345, producing a zero value where a Vec struct should be. This affects every use site, not just enum-variant payloads: `let xs: Vec[i64] = Vec[1, 2, 3];` builds cleanly but produces a null Vec at runtime; `Json.Array(Vec[...])` lands the same null in the variant payload, hence the `stringify()` → `[]` output. The original entry mistakenly blamed enum-variant payload composition; the real root cause is the missing `PrefixCollectionLiteral` codegen arm in `compile_expr`. Slice plan: (1) add a `compile_prefix_collection_literal(type_name, items)` helper in `src/codegen/collections.rs` that, for `type_name == "Vec"`, allocates a heap buffer sized for `items.len() * sizeof(elem)`, stores each item, and returns the `{ptr, len, cap}` Vec struct. (2) Wire it from `compile_expr`'s `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { type_name, items }` arm. (3) Set / Map prefix literal codegen can follow in a sibling slice if the kata corpus surfaces a need (Map literal already has its own `compile_map_literal_stmt` at the let-stmt level — generalize to a Map prefix expression at the same time). Element-type inference comes from the enclosing expected-type carrier (`Json.Array(Vec[...])` knows the elem is `Json` from the variant's payload signature) — likely consult the typechecker's `expr_types` side-table on the literal's span, OR thread an expected-type parameter through `compile_expr`. (4) Move-semantics: the elements are moved into the heap buffer; the buffer's lifetime joins the resulting Vec value's lifetime — `track_vec_var` for let-bindings, but for transient enum-payload composition the parent value's drop machinery owns it. **Workaround in v1:** explicit `Vec.new() + .push(...)` for every site. The TODO API kata uses this inline at every JSON-building site and notes it in its README. **Why P1 v1:** every kata or production workload that builds a JSON-shaped tree (or any Vec-payloaded enum) is forced into the verbose explicit form. Cross-reference: `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_expr` (the missing arm — line 345 default fires); `src/lowering.rs:261-275` (Array→ArrayLiteral canonicalization, Vec/Set/Map stay PrefixCollectionLiteral); `src/codegen/collections.rs::compile_array_literal` (the precedent for fixed-size arrays — Vec needs heap-alloc instead of stack-alloc); `kara-katas/backend/todo-api/main.kara` (the inline workaround sites); `runtime/stdlib/json.kara` (`Json.Array` / `Json.Object` variant declarations).

- [x] **Field-receiver method GEP through a `ref T` parameter.** Landed 2026-05-22 at `32f52d2`. Root cause was narrower than the original "helper-function Json returns empty / crashes silently" framing: codegen's field-receiver method dispatch in `src/codegen/calls.rs` (`outer.field.method(...)` shape) was using `slot.ptr` directly as the GEP base for plain (non-shared) struct receivers. For `ref T` parameters the slot is an `alloca ptr` holding a pointer to the struct, not the struct itself — the GEP indexed into the alloca's first 8 bytes (the stored pointer value) and read junk past it. The bad `{ptr, len, cap}` triple for a String field was then passed to `karac_clone_String`, which dereferenced and segfaulted silently. Fix: when the variable is a ref param (`self.ref_params.contains_key(outer_name)`), load the pointer first to recover the struct's address — mirrors the existing shared-struct handle-load pattern in the same site, just extended to the ref-param case. Regression test `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_field_receiver_method_through_ref_param` pins the kata's exact helper shape (`fn todo_to_json(t: ref Todo) -> Json` with `t.title.clone()` embedded in a returned Json.Object). Original P2.

- [x] **`Vec.remove(idx)` codegen + typechecker arm.** Landed 2026-05-22 at `4de2e8e`. `compile_vec_method` had no `"remove"` arm — fell through to the default `_ => i64 0` so `xs.remove(i)` silently no-op[']d. Fix in two coordinated edits: typechecker arm in `src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs::infer_method_call` next to the pop / pop_front family, returning T for `Vec[T]` / `VecDeque[T]` receivers with i64 idx (v1 contract matches Rust — UB on OOB); codegen arm in `src/codegen/vec_method.rs` mirroring pop_front[']s load + memmove + len-- but at an arbitrary index. 4 regression tests in `tests/codegen.rs` cover middle / head / tail removal and the module-bound Vec receiver. Original P1.

- [x] **Enum-payload bool narrowing — `match Json.Bool(b) => b`.** Landed 2026-05-22 at `11ca0e1`. The enum-payload bool is encoded as i64 in the word stream; codegen now inserts a `trunc i64 → i1` at pattern-bind reconstruction when the binding[']s typechecker-recorded type is `"bool"`. Two coordinated edits: typechecker `bind_pattern_types` + `check_pattern_against` Binding arm record `"bool"` in `pattern_binding_types` for `Type::Bool`; codegen `control_flow_match.rs::reconstruct_payload_value` single-word arm narrows to i1 when the recorded type is `"bool"`. Regression test `test_e2e_enum_payload_bool_narrowing` covers Json.Bool(true), Json.Bool(false), and the default-arm Json.Number fall-through. Original P2.

- [ ] **Uppercase-receiver field access — typechecker `resolve_path_type` walk.** P1 v1. Sibling-half of the shipped uppercase-receiver method-dispatch entry directly above. Same parser-greedy-Path root cause at `src/parser/exprs.rs:1298-1326`: `let F: Foo = Foo { value: 5 }; let x: i64 = F.value;` parses `F.value` as `Path([F, value])`, then `resolve_path_type` for the 2-segment path falls through to `resolve_identifier_type("F")` and returns `Foo` (the value's type) instead of walking the path to resolve the field's type as `i64`. Symptom is `expected 'i64', found 'Foo'` at any annotated binding (or downstream `println()` Display-mismatch when there's no annotation — what slice 10's `test_e2e_modbind_struct_literal` would have surfaced if the test pipeline didn't bypass typecheck-fatal-error gating). Codegen has its own correct path (`compile_path_expr`'s `Path([BINDING, field])` arm against `module_bindings`), so compiled binaries produce the right value — the slice-10 test passes vacuously through `run_program_capturing_inner` which doesn't honour typecheck errors. But `karac build` from the CLI exits on the typecheck error, so users see the wall. Slice plan: (1) **Extend `path_first_segment_is_value_binding`** (already added for the method-dispatch entry) into a richer `resolve_path_type_for_value_first_segment` helper, or add a sibling arm in `resolve_path_type` directly. When `segments.len() == 2` and `segments[0]` is a value binding (the same predicate the method-dispatch rewrite uses), look up the binding's type, then resolve `segments[1]` as a field of that type. For a struct receiver, consult `env.structs[name].fields` for the matching `(name, ty)` pair and return the field's type. For non-struct receivers (tuple, primitive, etc.), fall through to the existing diagnostic path. (2) **Ordering against the method-dispatch rewrite** — the method-dispatch arm in `infer_call` already covers Call(Path) shapes; this new arm covers bare-Path shapes (field access has no `(args)` suffix). The two are disjoint by callee context. (3) **No codegen changes needed** — the slice-10 codegen path already handles `Path([BINDING, field])` correctly via `compile_path_expr`'s module-binding arm. The fix is typechecker-only. (4) **No lowering rewrite needed** — unlike method-dispatch, field access doesn't need an AST rewrite; the typechecker just needs to compute the right type. Downstream phases see the same Path AST. **Test coverage**: positive — `let mut CFG: Config = Config { max: 64, count: 7 }; let m: i64 = CFG.max; let c: i64 = CFG.count;` accepted; `let F: Foo = Foo { value: 5 }; let x: i64 = F.value;` (local) accepted; nested `OUTER.inner.field` walks through both segments. Negative — `let CFG: Config = ...; let _: i64 = CFG.nonexistent;` fires the existing `NoSuchField` diagnostic on the value's type (not "type 'Config' is not ..." misdirection). Regression — `Vec.new()` field-of-type access (none exists today but the codepath must not regress) still routes through `resolve_path_type`'s associated-fn dispatch unchanged. **Why P1 v1:** unblocks every backend / CLI kata that uses a non-empty struct module binding (config singletons, in-memory caches with named fields, registry structs); the Vec.new() entry above ships the empty-struct case, this entry ships the non-empty case. No workload in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` Priority 1 needs it today (the TODO API uses Vec, which is empty-struct), but a half-dozen backend / CLI shapes that would naturally surface as v1 demos use it. Phase target: Phase 3 (typechecker only — single focused arm). Cross-reference: `src/parser/exprs.rs:1298-1326` (greedy path-consumption — unchanged); `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs::resolve_path_type` lines 366-370 (the identifier-fallback site that drops the trailing segments); `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs::path_first_segment_is_value_binding` (the predicate already in place from slice b — reuse); `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_path_expr` (the correct codegen path that today silently disagrees with the typechecker); the uppercase-receiver method-dispatch entry directly above (sibling half, shipped); `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_modbind_struct_literal` (the slice-10 test that already exercises the codegen path — extend with a `karac build` smoke test once typechecker agrees).

- [ ] **`Map.new()` / `Set.new()` as module-binding initialisers.** P1 v1. Wrapper-type follow-on to the Vec.new() module-init entry — the slice-a rationale (kata corpus needs in-memory store patterns at module scope) applies identically to Map and Set, which are even more common shapes for backend services (config maps, in-memory KV caches, intern tables). Unlike Vec, Map's runtime invariant is NOT a zero-shaped aggregate: `runtime/src/map.rs::karac_map_new` installs per-instance hash seeds and vtable function pointers before any operation on the map can run, so the empty-Map value isn't `zeroinitializer` — it's whatever shape `karac_map_new` returns. (`Set[T]` reuses the same runtime via `karac_map_new` with `val_size = 0` per `src/codegen/stmts.rs::compile_set_new_stmt`.) Two mechanism options: **(a) Static-init prologue.** At codegen time, emit a synthesised `__karac_static_init` function that runs before `main`'s body and writes each `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` module-binding's runtime initialiser. Mirrors the C++ `__attribute__((constructor))` shape. The const-init permitted-special-forms list in `module_binding_call_is_special_form` (typechecker) gains `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` arms; the codegen module-binding emission produces a `zeroinitializer` placeholder global; a separate prologue pass walks `module_bindings`, emits per-binding `karac_map_new(...)` calls into the prologue, and wires the prologue to run before `main` (LLVM `@llvm.global_ctors` array, or a synthesised explicit call from `main`'s entry block — the latter is simpler and avoids the global-ctors-ordering question). **(b) LazyLock-style deferred init.** `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` const-init recognises the form, codegen emits a `LazyLock[Map[K,V]]`-shaped wrapper that initialises on first access. Requires `LazyLock[T]` codegen to be in place (currently deferred per the module-binding-umbrella entry's slice-10 narrative). (a) is the right v1 call — LazyLock isn't shipped yet and adding it as a transitive dep here would add scope; static-init prologue is a contained codegen extension and the runtime cost (one global ctor call per Map binding at startup) is negligible. Slice plan: (1) **Probe** — confirm whether any pre-existing static-init machinery exists in the codegen (search for `global_ctors` / `__karac_init` / similar). The `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` global pattern at codegen-program-end is the closest precedent. (2) **Typechecker** — add `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` to `module_binding_call_is_special_form` in `src/typechecker/items.rs` alongside the existing `Vec` / `VecDeque` arm. Update the diagnostic enumeration to name them. (3) **Codegen** — emit the placeholder `zeroinitializer` global at `module_bindings.rs::modbind_init_from_value` for `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` (reuse the LLVM struct type the existing local-binding `compile_map_new_stmt` / `compile_set_new_stmt` produces; map's layout is in `src/codegen/maps.rs` — find or define the shared type accessor). (4) **Static-init prologue** — synthesise an `__karac_static_init` LLVM function that runs each Map/Set module binding's runtime initialiser. Inject a call to it from `main`'s entry block (simplest) or via `@llvm.global_ctors`. (5) **Method dispatch** — the uppercase-receiver method-dispatch entry directly above already covers `REGISTRY.insert(k, v)` / `REGISTRY.get(k)` for module-binding receivers via the codegen module-binding sibling block in `compile_method_call`; no additional method-dispatch work is needed. **Test coverage**: positive — `let mut REGISTRY: Map[String, i64] = Map.new(); fn main() { REGISTRY.insert("a", 1); println(REGISTRY.get("a").unwrap_or(0)); }` end-to-end; same for `Set[T]`. Negative — `Map.new(1)` continues to be rejected (zero-arg only); `Map.with_capacity(n)` rejected (not a permitted const-init form — would need its own arm); runtime init runs exactly once per binding. Regression — local `let m: Map[K, V] = Map.new();` inside a function continues to use the existing per-statement codegen path unchanged. **Why P1 v1:** every backend kata in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` axes 1-2 (backend, CLI) needing keyed state shares this need; config maps and in-memory caches are the canonical shape; the Vec.new() entry above ships the ordered-list case, this entry ships the keyed case. Phase target: Phase 3 (typechecker) + Phase 7 (codegen + static-init prologue). Cross-reference: `runtime/src/map.rs::karac_map_new` (the runtime initialiser that has to run); `src/codegen/stmts.rs::compile_map_new_stmt` + `compile_set_new_stmt` (the local-binding codegen paths to mirror at the prologue); `src/typechecker/items.rs::module_binding_call_is_special_form` (where the typechecker arms land); the Vec.new() module-binding entry directly above (the precedent slice — same shape, simpler runtime); the uppercase-receiver method-dispatch entry directly above (covers the consumer side — method calls on the global Map work for free once init lands).

- [ ] **`OnceLock[T]` and `OnceCell[T]` lazy-init primitives.** Spec at `design.md § Module-Level Bindings > LazyLock[T] / OnceLock[T] / OnceCell[T]` (v60 item 45). Ship alongside the existing `LazyLock[T]` (already specced; unchanged by this entry). Both new primitives carry the same method surface — `new`, `set(val) -> Result[(), AlreadySetError[T]]`, `get() -> Option[ref T]`, `get_or_init(\|\| ...) -> ref T`, `is_set() -> bool` — so a type swap between the two is mechanical. The structural difference is single-task vs. cross-task safety, enforced through three explicit rules on `OnceCell[T]` rather than a `Sync` auto-trait. Slices: (1) **Stdlib types.** `OnceLock[T]` and `OnceCell[T]` registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `stub_generics(["T"])` in `prelude.rs` and as generic structs in `register_builtin_types`. `OnceLock.new()` and `OnceCell.new()` wired into the path-call dispatch (parallel to the existing `LazyLock.new` recognition). (2) **Interpreter values.** `Value::OnceLock(Arc<Mutex<Option<Value>>>)` and `Value::OnceCell(Rc<RefCell<Option<Value>>>)` — the difference is `Arc<Mutex<...>>` vs. `Rc<RefCell<...>>` to mirror the cross-task vs. single-task split (Rust-host implementation; the language-level guarantee is the structural-rule check, the interpreter implementation just needs to be racy-safe enough not to panic on the cross-task path). (3) **Method surface implementation.** `set` returns `Ok(())` on first call, `Err(AlreadySetError { rejected: val })` on subsequent calls; `get` returns the cached value via `Option`; `get_or_init` wraps both into a single race-safe call (for `OnceLock`, the lock is acquired once; if another task's `set` races, the loser's constructed value is dropped without invoking the closure twice). (4) **Typechecker dispatch.** `infer_once_lock_method` and `infer_once_cell_method` added; dispatch wired in `infer_method_call` on `Type::Named { name: "OnceLock" \| "OnceCell" }`. Methods carry no effects beyond the invocation closure's effects (which propagate through `get_or_init`'s closure type per existing trait-method effect-checking rules). (5) **`AlreadySetError[T]`** registered as a prelude error type in the typechecker (`enum AlreadySetError[T] { rejected: T }`). Conditional `Display` impl gated on `T: Display` follows the existing conditional-impl pattern. Always implements `Debug`. (6) **`OnceLock` constant-init recognition.** `OnceLock.new()` is added to the compiler-recognized constant-init special forms alongside `LazyLock.new` so it's permitted as a module-level binding's right-hand side without violating the constant-initializer rule (the ctor produces a fresh empty cell with no captured runtime state — the same property `LazyLock.new` already has). (7) **Single-task structural enforcement** (three new diagnostics targeting `OnceCell[T]` use sites): (a) **`E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE`** — typechecker check at module-level binding registration: if the declared type contains `OnceCell[T]` anywhere in its tree, reject with `error[E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE]: 'OnceCell[T]' is single-task; module-level bindings are visible to every task and must be 'OnceLock[T]' instead` and a fix-it suggesting the type swap. (b) **`E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE`** — typechecker check at `par struct` / `par enum` field type validation (the existing pass that already rejects single-task types in `par struct` fields gains `OnceCell[T]` to its rejected-type set): `error[E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE]: 'OnceCell[T]' is single-task; fields of 'par struct'/'par enum' must be 'OnceLock[T]' instead` with the offending field's span and the type-swap fix-it. `shared struct` fields accept `OnceCell[T]` (per design.md — `shared struct` itself is single-task). (c) **`E_ONCE_CELL_CROSSES_TASK_BOUNDARY`** — par-region escape analysis: when an owned binding of type `OnceCell[T]` is consumed by a `par {}` branch, a `spawn()` argument, or a `Sender[OnceCell[T]].send` call, reject with `error[E_ONCE_CELL_CROSSES_TASK_BOUNDARY]: 'OnceCell[T]' cannot cross task boundaries; replace with 'OnceLock[T]' or move the surrounding owned struct's task-local clone into the branch instead`. The check piggybacks on the existing par-region escape pass that already rejects raw `Rc[T]` from crossing into a `par {}` branch — no new dataflow pass is needed; the check adds `OnceCell` to the existing rejected-type set keyed off the type-name. (8) **Effect attribution.** First-access initialization (whether through `set` or `get_or_init`) is attributed to the *calling* function, not to the binding — same rule that already applies to `LazyLock`. The closure passed to `get_or_init` has its own effect set checked at the call site against the calling function's ceiling (existing trait-method effect-check machinery). (9) **Codegen.** Phase 7 work — both primitives lower to small heap-allocated structs (the `Once` synchronization primitive already exists in `karac-runtime` for `LazyLock`'s use; `OnceLock` reuses it; `OnceCell` is just an `Option<T>` with interior mutability). The existing `karac-runtime` `Once` API gains `set`/`get`/`get_or_init` entry points. **Test coverage** (interpreter + typechecker, Phase 8): positive — `let CFG: OnceLock[Config] = OnceLock.new();` accepted at module scope; `CFG.set(Config { ... })` returns `Ok(())` on first call; `CFG.get()` returns `Some` after `set`, `None` before; `CFG.set(other)` after first set returns `Err(AlreadySetError { rejected: other })`; `CFG.get_or_init(\|\| compute())` runs closure exactly once across multiple calls; `OnceCell[Vec[Token]]` field on a non-`par` struct accepted; `parser.tokens()` lazy-init pattern type-checks and runs end-to-end; struct containing `OnceCell` may be moved into a non-`par` block. Negative — `let X: OnceCell[i64] = OnceCell.new();` at module scope rejected with `E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE` and fix-it; `par struct Foo { cell: OnceCell[i64] }` rejected with `E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE`; `par { let cell = OnceCell.new(); cell.set(1).unwrap(); }` accepted (cell is born inside the branch, doesn't cross); `let cell = OnceCell.new(); par { cell.set(1).unwrap(); }` rejected with `E_ONCE_CELL_CROSSES_TASK_BOUNDARY`; `Channel[OnceCell[i64]]` declared then `tx.send(cell)` rejected at the send call site with the same error. Phase target: **Phase 8** (Standard Library — Floor) for stdlib types + interpreter + typechecker + structural-enforcement diagnostics; Phase 7 for codegen. No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 45 ships the full surface at v1; `LazyCell[T]` (the embedded-init non-Sync sibling) is intentionally not in v1 and is non-breaking-additive if a workload demands it later.

- [x] **Map codegen gap closure.** Several `Map[K, V]` methods that the typechecker accepts were silently miscompiled: `compile_map_method` in `src/codegen.rs:4667` ended with `_ => Ok(i64_t.const_int(0, false).into())` at line 4945, returning constant `0` for `keys`/`values`/`entries`/`merge`/`get_or` — programs ran to "success" with corrupt output. `compile_index` only handled Array/Vec/Slice so `m[k]` was wrong on compiled binaries. `Map.clear()` didn't exist. `Display` for collections was filed at line 207 of this file as a stub. Spec at `design.md § Collection Core Methods > Map[K, V]` (line 1548) and `design.md § Iteration order is unspecified` (line 1588). All subtasks closed; Display split into its own canonical bullet at `phase-7-codegen.md § Phase 7.2` since recursive Display codegen is its own scope. Closed 2026-05-04. Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Catch-all hardening** — replaced the silent fallback at `src/codegen.rs:4945` with `Err(format!("codegen: Map.{method} not yet implemented"))`. No existing test triggered the catch-all (full LLVM suite still green at 2495 tests); hardening is purely preventative against future drift between typechecker-accepted methods and codegen-implemented methods. Commit `4a3bc3e`.
  - [x] **2. `m[k]` index op (read)** — extended `compile_index` with an early dispatch (mirrors slice early-dispatch shape) keyed off `self.map_key_types.contains_key(name)` to a new `compile_map_index` helper. Helper loads the map handle, allocates key/val slots, calls `karac_map_get`, and branches on the i1: missing → `emit_panic("Map index: key not present")` + unreachable; found → load val and return. Limitation: only direct-identifier paths wired (same as slice early-dispatch). Returned value is a bit-copy of the bucket — matches existing `Map.get` behavior; proper `ref V` return is a uniform follow-up across `[]` and `Map.get`. Tests: `test_e2e_map_index_get_existing_i64`, `test_e2e_map_index_get_existing_string_key`, `test_e2e_map_index_panics_on_missing`. Commit `ca94b9f`.
  - [x] **3. `m[k] = v` index op (write)** — extended `compile_index_store` with an early dispatch to a new `compile_map_index_store` helper that lowers to `karac_map_insert_old` and discards the previous-value out-slot. Fresh-insert and overwrite are handled uniformly by the runtime call. Tests: `test_e2e_map_index_set_fresh_and_overwrite`, `test_e2e_map_index_set_string_key`. Commit `3f08a39`.
  - [x] **4. `Map.clear()`** — `karac_map_clear(map)` added to `runtime/src/map.rs` (zeroes status via `write_bytes`, resets `len` + `tombstones`; bucket capacity preserved per Rust `HashMap::clear` contract). Extern declared in `Codegen::new()`. `clear` arm added to `infer_map_method` (Unit return), `eval_method_call` on `Value::Map`, and `compile_map_method`. Tests: `test_e2e_map_clear`, `test_e2e_map_clear_string_key` (codegen), `test_map_clear` (interpreter). Commit `8806883`.
  - [x] **5. `keys()` / `values()` / `entries()` codegen** — new `compile_map_keys_values_entries` helper pre-allocates a buffer at `karac_map_len` capacity (one malloc, no growth), then drives the existing `karac_map_iter_*` loop writing each element to `buf[i]`. Returns the Vec struct `{data, len, cap=len}` directly; receiving binding's let-statement registers cleanup via existing `vec_elem_types` path. Tests: `test_e2e_map_keys_returns_vec`, `test_e2e_map_values_returns_vec`, `test_e2e_map_entries_returns_vec_of_tuples`, `test_e2e_map_keys_string_keys_len`, `test_e2e_map_keys_empty`. Surfaced separate pre-existing gap: `for s in vec_of_strings { s.len() }` returns 0 because for-loop bindings don't register String/Vec method dispatch — affects all Vec[String] iteration regardless of source. Tracked separately. Commit `b150d8c`.
  - [x] **6. `Display` for collections** — split into separate canonical bullet **Display for collections (recursive codegen)** in `phase-7-codegen.md § Phase 7.2`. Recursive Display codegen (per-type emitted Display fns, with Vec[Vec[T]] / Map[K, Vec[T]] / Tuple support) is substantial enough to warrant its own bullet rather than being subsumed under the gap-closure umbrella. The interpreter side (`src/interpreter.rs:206-307`) is already correct; the codegen side is the new bullet's scope. Closed-by-delegation 2026-05-04.
  - [x] **7. `Map[k: v, ...]` prefix-literal K/V inference** — turned out to need parser + codegen, not pure typechecker. Parser was rejecting `Map[k: v]` outright ("Expected RightBracket, found Colon"); the AST node `PrefixCollectionLiteral.items` is a `Vec<Expr>` that can't represent key-value pairs. Fix: when type_name is "Map" and first expr is followed by `:`, parser switches to key-value parsing and emits `ExprKind::MapLiteral` (same AST as the bare `["k": v]` form, so existing typechecker case applies unchanged). Codegen for MapLiteral was also missing — silent-0 catch-all at `compile_expr` line 2837 swallowed it. Added `compile_map_literal_stmt` (new + insert-loop) and a let-statement-level recognizer that dispatches both bare and prefix forms. Tests: `test_map_prefix_literal_string_keys` / `test_map_prefix_literal_int_keys` (interpreter); `test_e2e_map_prefix_literal_string_keys` / `test_e2e_map_prefix_literal_int_keys` / `test_e2e_map_bare_literal_with_annotation` (codegen). Closes `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 13. Commit `1678d0a`.

- [x] **`Set[T]` LLVM codegen.** Lower `Set[T]` to `Map[T, ()]` at the codegen layer and reuse the `karac_map_*` C runtime — the canonical implementation strategy used by Rust's `HashSet<T>` (defined as a wrapper around `HashMap<T, ()>`) and equivalent in every mainstream stdlib. The existing runtime at `runtime/src/map.rs` already handles zero-size values correctly via `(key_size + val_size).max(1)` at line 71, so no new C code is required; `Set[T]` keeps its own type identity in the parser/typechecker/interpreter/effect-checker layers and the lowering happens entirely below LLVM IR. Spec at `design.md § Collection Core Methods > Set[T]` (line 1590). Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Codegen state** — `set_elem_types: HashMap<String, BasicTypeEnum<'ctx>>`, `set_elem_type_names: HashMap<String, String>`, and `set_elem_type_exprs: HashMap<String, TypeExpr>` added next to the Map side-tables in `Codegen`. New `extract_set_elem_type`, `extract_set_elem_name`, `set_inner_type_expr` helpers parallel `extract_map_kv_types` / `extract_map_key_name` / `map_kv_type_exprs`. Side-tables populated both at the let-statement type-annotation site and via `register_var_from_type_expr` (the latter already runs for for-loop bindings). Type lowering at `llvm_type_for_type_expr` already lowers `Set[T]` to opaque `ptr` so no change there.
  - [x] **2. `Set.new()` path-call dispatch** — `is_set_new_call` predicate + `compile_set_new_stmt` added next to the Map versions. Lowers to `karac_map_new(elem_size, 0, hash_fn, eq_fn)` — the runtime's `(key_size + val_size).max(1)` keeps the bucket allocation valid for `val_size = 0`. Hash/eq fns selected via `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` so compound element shapes (tuples, derived-Hash structs) compose. Cleanup is the existing `FreeMapHandle` action; `track_map_var` is reused.
  - [x] **3. `compile_set_method`** — new function parallel to `compile_map_method`. Implements `len` → `karac_map_len`; `is_empty` → `karac_map_len == 0`; `insert(v)` → `karac_map_insert_old(map, &v, &dummy, &dummy)` then XOR with `1` (returns `true` on fresh insert, matching Rust `HashSet::insert`); `contains(v)` → `karac_map_contains`; `remove(v)` → `karac_map_remove_old(map, &v, &dummy)` returning the existed bit; `clear()` → `karac_map_clear`. The dummy unit/out is a single shared `i8` alloca per function — `val_size = 0` in the runtime makes the actual store a no-op. Method dispatch wired in the method-call routing site at `compile_method_call` alongside Map.
  - [x] **4. `for x in s`** — `compile_for_set_var` mirrors `compile_for_map_var`, swapping the val out-slot for a single shared `i8` alloca and binding the element directly (no `(k, v)` destructuring). Dispatch wired in the for-loop routing site at `compile_for`.
  - [x] **5. `union` / `intersection` / `difference`** — three new arms in `compile_set_method` route through a shared `emit_set_op_iter` helper that walks `karac_map_iter_*` over the source, optionally probes a "filter set" via `karac_map_contains`, per-element-clones survivors via `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`, and inserts into a freshly-allocated destination handle. `union` calls the helper twice — unfiltered from `self`, filtered against `self` from `other` — so duplicate elements never get double-cloned (which would leak the second clone since `karac_map_insert` overwrites in-place without freeing the prior key bytes). `intersection` uses `ContainsIn(other)`; `difference` uses `NotContainsIn(other)`. Hash/eq/elem-size pulled from the receiver's `set_elem_type_exprs` entry so compound element types compose. Result-handle scope-cleanup integration: extended the let-binding fallback path to call `track_map_var` when the RHS is a fresh-handle-producing method call (`clone` / `union` / `intersection` / `difference`); previously only `Vec`/`String` got auto-tracking, so `let n = m.clone();` was silently leaking the cloned handle on macOS (Apple ASAN has no LeakSanitizer; Linux + LSAN would have caught it). Restricted to `MethodCall` RHS so move-via-Identifier (`let n = m;`) keeps the source's existing track as the unique cleanup owner — no double-free risk. 5 codegen E2E tests (`union_i64`, `intersection_i64`, `difference_i64`, `union_string`, `difference_independent_after_source_mutation`) + 1 ASAN test (`asan_set_union_string_independent_handles`) added.
  - [x] **6. E2E codegen tests** — 9 baseline tests in `tests/codegen.rs` (search `test_e2e_set_`): `i64_insert_contains`, `i64_insert_returns_bool` (false on duplicate, true on fresh), `i64_remove`, `i64_len_is_empty`, `i64_for_loop_sum` (iteration-order-independent sum), `string_insert_contains`, `string_remove`, `string_for_loop_count`, `clear`. Plus the 5 set-op tests landed with subtask 5. Compound-key coverage (`Set[(i32, i32)]`, `Set[(String, (i32, i32))]`) deferred — Hash machinery is shared with the Map suite which already exercises both compound-key recursion and cache reuse.
  - [x] **7. ASAN test** — `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs::asan_set_new_insert_scope_exit_free` verifies the `FreeMapHandle` cleanup fires on Set drop. `asan_set_string_scope_exit_free` covers `Set[String]` with static-buffer (cap = 0) string literals to verify the bucket-array free fires while the static String buffers are correctly left alone.
  - [x] **8. `Set[v1, v2, ...]` prefix-literal element type inference** — typechecker arm added in `infer_expr` for `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { type_name: "Set", items }`. Element type is unified from items via `check_assignable`; empty `Set[]` falls to `Type::Error` for the element and recovers via the binding-site annotation per `design.md` line 1462. 4 typechecker tests: `test_set_prefix_literal_infers_i64`, `test_set_prefix_literal_infers_string`, `test_set_prefix_literal_mismatched_elements_rejected`, `test_set_prefix_literal_empty_with_annotation`. Closes `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 12 — flip that checkbox when this lands too.

- [x] **Clone trait surface for collections — vertical implementation (typechecker + interpreter + codegen + runtime).** Spec at `design.md § Iteration` line 1692: *`Vec`, `Map`, `Set`, `VecDeque`, `TreeMap`, and `SortedSet` implement `Clone`*. Today **every layer is missing** — typechecker has no `clone` method registration on these types (the only `"clone"` arm is for `Sender`); interpreter's `eval_method_call` falls through to "method 'clone' not found on type" panic; codegen has zero `"clone"` method dispatch and zero per-type clone fn emission. Compiled and interpreted binaries calling `Vec.clone()` / `String.clone()` / `Map.clone()` / `Set.clone()` fail today; this is a present-day v1 surface bug, not a future enhancement.

  **Priority: P0** — covers v1 stdlib API surface methods that currently produce wrong behavior at every layer.

  **Consumers blocked on this** (cross-references; flip their checkboxes when the relevant subtask lands):
  - ~~`Set[T] LLVM codegen` subtask 5 (`union` / `intersection` / `difference`)~~ — landed 2026-05-04 on top of `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`; per-element cloning routes through `emit_set_op_iter`.
  - `Vec.filled[T: Clone]` per `design.md § 1488` — every fill slot is a per-element clone.
  - Future stdlib generics with `T: Clone` bounds (e.g., `Vec.dedup_by_key`, `Vec.split_off` on non-Copy element types).
  - `#[derive(Clone)]` on user structs whose fields are non-Copy — the synthesized body is field-wise per-type clone.

  **Subtasks (split by layer):**

  - [x] **1. Typechecker — `clone` method registration on collection types.** Per-collection method-inference functions register `clone(ref self) -> Self` against `Vec[T]`, `String`, `Map[K, V]`, `Set[T]`, `VecDeque[T]`, `SortedSet[T]`, `TreeMap[K, V]`. The existing `infer_map_method` (`src/typechecker.rs:8275`) gets a `"clone"` arm; `Vec`/`String`/`Set` need their own (today the `Sender.clone()` arm at line 8892 is the only one in the typechecker). The `T: Clone` bound on collection element types is enforced via the existing trait-bound checking — `Vec[T]: Clone where T: Clone`. Negative test: `Vec.clone()` on a `Vec[NonCloneStruct]` rejected with the bound-violation diagnostic.

  - [x] **2. Interpreter — `clone` dispatch on collection values.** Add a `"clone"` arm to `eval_method_call` (`src/interpreter.rs`) that matches each `Value::Vec` / `Value::String` / `Value::Map` / `Value::Set` / `Value::SortedSet` shape and produces a deep copy via Rust-side `Vec::clone` / `String::clone` / etc. The Rust-side clones are correct by construction (each `Value` variant is itself `Clone`); this is purely dispatch wiring.

  - [x] **3. Codegen — per-type clone fn emission machinery (`emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`).** TypeExpr-aware emit fn paralleling `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_display_fn_for_type_expr`. New `clone_fn_cache: HashMap<String, FunctionValue<'ctx>>` keyed on `display_mangle_te(te)`. Function signature is uniform `void karac_clone_<typename>(*const T src, *mut T dst)` — caller provides both source and destination addresses, callee writes the cloned value into the destination slot. Cases:

    - **Primitive (Copy)** — `i8`/`i16`/`i32`/`i64`/`u8`/`u16`/`u32`/`u64`/`isize`/`usize`/`f32`/`f64`/`bool`/`char`/`unit` — single `load src` + `store dst`, no allocation.
    - **String** — call new runtime helper `karac_string_clone` (subtask 4 below). Receives a String struct `{data, len, cap}`; allocates `cap` bytes (or `len` if `cap == 0` for static literals — the cloned buffer needs `cap > 0` so its scope-exit cleanup fires), `memcpy`s `len` bytes, writes `{new_data, len, new_cap}` to `dst`.
    - **Vec[T]** — recursive: load `data`/`len`/`cap` from src; emit `karac_clone_<elem_mangled>` for `T` (via `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr(elem_te)`); `malloc(cap * elem_size)` for the new buffer; loop `i in 0..len` calling the elem clone fn with `src.data + i*elem_size` / `dst.data + i*elem_size`; write `{new_data, len, new_cap}` to `dst`. Empty Vecs (`cap == 0`) skip the malloc per the existing String-literal cap=0 convention.
    - **Map[K, V]** — emit `karac_map_new(key_size, val_size, hash_fn, eq_fn)` for the destination; iterate the source via `karac_map_iter_*`; for each pair, alloca'd K and V copies (clone via per-K, per-V emit_clone fns), then `karac_map_insert_old` into the destination. Hash/eq fn pointers come from `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type_expr` (already exist).
    - **Set[T]** — same as Map[T, ()] — single-element clone per iteration, val_size = 0 with shared dummy slot.
    - **Tuple `(T1, T2, ..., Tn)`** — typed entry `emit_clone_fn_for_tuple(elems)`; field-wise recurse into per-field clone fn via struct GEP. Mirror the tuple Hash/Eq/Display pattern.
    - **`#[derive(Clone)]` struct** — synthesized body is field-wise recurse. Emit at the derive-site by walking the struct's `field_types` and calling `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr` per field, then GEP+store into `dst` per field. The derived `clone` method gets registered as the user struct's `Type.clone` so method-call dispatch finds it.

  - [x] **4. Runtime — `karac_string_clone(*const String) -> String` helper.** New extern in `runtime/src/string.rs` (or a dedicated `runtime/src/clone.rs`). Allocates a fresh buffer via the runtime's allocator (same path as `karac_vec_grow`), `memcpy`s `len` bytes from the source data pointer, returns the new `{ptr, len, cap}` struct. For static literals (`cap == 0`), allocates `len`-byte buffer with `cap = len` so the cloned String's scope-exit cleanup correctly frees it (the source's `cap = 0` keeps the static buffer untouched). Declared in `Codegen::new()` alongside the existing `karac_*` externs.

  - [x] **5. `compile_method_call` dispatch wiring.** Add `"clone"` arms to each per-collection method handler — `compile_vec_method`, `compile_map_method`, `compile_set_method`, plus a String-method handler if one exists separately. Each wires the source variable's slot through to the corresponding `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr` and writes the result to a fresh stack alloca + side-table registration so the cloned value participates in scope cleanup correctly.

  - [x] **6. Scope-cleanup integration.** A cloned `Vec` / `Map` / `Set` / `String` is a fresh heap-owning value — register the appropriate `FreeVecBuffer` / `FreeMapHandle` cleanup action on its scope frame. Goes through the existing `track_vec_var` / `track_map_var` machinery; the only new piece is recognizing that `let w = v.clone()` produces a heap-owning bound name and calling the right tracker.

  - [x] **7. ASAN tests** in `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs`: `asan_vec_clone_independent_buffers` (verify the source's buffer is freed once and the cloned buffer is freed once — no aliasing); `asan_string_clone_static_literal` (source has `cap = 0`, clone has `cap > 0` and gets freed, source untouched); `asan_map_clone_independent_handle` (verify both maps free their bucket arrays separately, and any heap-bearing key/value bytes — String keys especially — clone correctly so neither map points at the other's strings); `asan_set_clone_string_elements` (per-element String clone integrity).

  - [x] **8. E2E tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` + `tests/interpreter.rs`: `vec_clone_preserves_contents`, `vec_clone_grows_independently` (mutate source after clone, verify clone unchanged), `string_clone_independent_buffer`, `map_clone_preserves_entries` (single-key cases for deterministic output; multi-key behavior verified via the cardinality-equality / per-key lookup pattern that Map tests already use), `set_clone_preserves_membership`, `derive_clone_struct_with_vec_field` (whole-struct clone produces independent inner Vec).

  - [x] **9. Empty-collection clone fast path.** `Vec.new().clone()` doesn't need to allocate; same for the other empty collections. Either special-case `len == 0` in the emitted body (skip the malloc; produce a `cap = 0` placeholder) or rely on the runtime's `malloc(0)` defined-behavior path. The former is cleaner and saves an allocation per empty clone.

- [x] **`Map.entry(k)` + `Entry[K, V]` enum — in-place insert-or-modify.** The idiomatic O(1) insert-or-modify pattern `self.table.entry(key).or_insert_with(Vec.new).push(row)` avoids the double-hash that `if !m.contains_key { m.insert(...) }` produces. Without this, every word-count / group-by / counter-style program either double-hashes or threads an explicit `match m.get(...)` / `insert` pair through the call site. Spec at `design.md § Entry[K, V]` (around line 1565). Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Parser/AST verification** — confirmed: `m.entry(k)` parses as a `MethodCall` AST node with no new grammar, and the `.or_insert / .or_insert_with / .and_modify` chain composes through the standard method-call grammar. `tests/parser.rs::test_map_entry_chain_parses` covers the four canonical chain shapes.
  - [x] **2. `Entry[K, V]` enum prelude registration** — `Entry` added to `PRELUDE_TYPES` (with `K, V` arity in `stub_generics`); `Occupied` / `Vacant` added to `PRELUDE_VARIANTS`. The full `EnumInfo` in `register_builtin_types` defines `Occupied { value: mut ref V }` / `Vacant { key: K, map: mut ref Map[K, V] }`. First stdlib type using `mut ref` on a variant payload — typechecker accepts the borrow-typed fields without changes.
  - [x] **3. `Entry` methods** — new `infer_entry_method` keyed off `Type::Named { name: "Entry", args: [K, V] }`, wired into `infer_method_call`'s named-type dispatch chain. `or_insert(default: V) -> mut ref V`, `or_insert_with(f: Fn() -> V) -> mut ref V` (closure-pushdown solves the closure return type from V), `and_modify(f: Fn(mut ref V)) -> Entry[K, V]` (returns Entry for chaining). Effect polymorphism on the closure-taking forms propagates through the existing closure-effect-checking pass.
  - [x] **4. Interpreter** — `Value::Entry { map_var: Option<String>, key: Box<Value>, slot_idx: Option<usize> }`. The `entry` arm in `eval_method_call` linear-searches `Value::Map` for the key, builds the Entry. `or_insert` / Vacant arm of `or_insert_with` push onto the live Map and write back via `env.set` (the standard interpreter mut-ref-self idiom); the Occupied arm returns the cloned slot value. `and_modify` aliases the slot via `Value::SharedCell` and runs the closure with `[SharedCell]` as the arg so `|v| { v += 1 }` mutates through. The fully-aliased pattern `m.entry(k).or_insert_with(Vec.new).push(row)` is interpreter-incompatible without invasive Map representation changes — codegen handles that case correctly.
  - [x] **5. Runtime — `karac_map_entry` and `karac_map_lookup_slot`** — two C ABI fns in `runtime/src/map.rs`. `karac_map_entry` (insert-on-vacant) is used by chains terminating in `or_insert` / `or_insert_with`; `karac_map_lookup_slot` (read-only) is used by chains terminating in bare `and_modify` so a missing key never causes an insertion side-effect. Both: out-pointer + bool-return shape mirroring `karac_map_get`, resize before probing so the slot pointer is stable for the rest of the call, pointer valid until the next mutating call (`HashMap::entry`'s lifetime contract).
  - [x] **6. Codegen** — `try_compile_entry_chain` in `compile_method_call` peels `and_modify` wrappers off the receiver and matches `m.entry(k)` at the chain root. One runtime call (terminal-driven choice between `karac_map_entry` and `karac_map_lookup_slot`) followed by branch blocks for each step, sharing a single slot pointer — exactly one hash per chain. `or_insert(d)` stores the default through the slot on Vacant; `or_insert_with(f)` uses the fat-pointer indirect-call path; `and_modify(f)` inlines the closure body directly (binds closure param to a stack alloca initialised from the slot, evaluates the body, stores back through the slot pointer) so `|v| { v += 1 }` mutates the map slot without needing closure-param-as-pointer codegen surgery. Restricted to inline `ExprKind::Closure` — named-fn forms are spec-out-of-scope at v1. The terminal-`.push(row)` form on `or_insert_with(Vec.new).push(row)` is its own piece of work that co-evolves with the per-type Clone codegen bullet (both need a slot-ptr-receiver path on `Vec.push`); the typechecker accepts that chain shape today.
  - [x] **7. Test coverage** — 11 typechecker + 7 interpreter + 7 codegen E2E tests. Codegen E2E (search `test_e2e_map_entry_`): or_insert vacant insert / occupied passthrough; or_insert_with closure fires only when vacant / skipped when occupied; and_modify runs only when occupied / skipped when vacant; the canonical `and_modify(|v| { v += 1; }).or_insert(1)` chain across three calls. Negative: `or_insert_with` closure body that re-borrows the map remains rejected by the existing borrow checker (no Entry-specific work needed since the `mut ref Map` borrow conflict is in the existing infrastructure).

- [x] **Effect-checker wiring for `Map[K, V]` and `Set[T]` methods.** ✓ DONE (2026-05-04). Wired the per-method allocator surface into `src/effectchecker.rs` via the existing seed-`inferred_effects` + `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` mechanism rather than a new `infer_*_method_effects` function (the architecture is data-driven through these tables, not per-type inference functions like the typechecker has). The typechecker registers per-method signatures for both types, but `src/effectchecker.rs` previously seeded only `Map.new` / `Map.insert` / `Set.new` / `Set.insert` and lacked dispatch entries for the other allocator methods — so a `pub fn count_words(...) allocates(Heap)` declaration that internally used `m.merge(other)` or `m.keys()` passed verification only because the effect machinery never inspected the methods. Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Map allocator effect seeding** — extended the path-call seed loop in `src/effectchecker.rs` to register `Map.with_capacity`, `Map.try_insert`, `Map.entry`, `Map.clone`, `Map.from_iter`, `Map.extend`, `Map.merge`, `Map.keys`, `Map.values`, `Map.entries` with `allocates(Heap)` (`Map.new` / `Map.insert` were already seeded). Index op `[]` already carries `panics` through the pre-existing `__builtin_index` path in `collect_calls_in_expr`. Pure reads (`get`, `contains_key`, `len`, `is_empty`) and non-growing mutators (`remove`, `clear`) get no seed — they fall through to empty effects, which is correct.
  - [x] **2. Set allocator effect seeding** — same shape: registered `Set.with_capacity`, `Set.clone`, `Set.from_iter`, `Set.union`, `Set.intersection`, `Set.difference` with `allocates(Heap)` (`Set.new` / `Set.insert` were already seeded). No index op. Pure reads (`contains`, `len`, `is_empty`) and `remove` left unseeded.
  - [x] **3. Dispatch wiring** — extended `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` in `collect_calls_in_expr` with dispatch entries for the new method names (`try_insert`, `entry`, `extend`, `merge`, `keys`, `values`, `entries`, `clone`, `union`, `intersection`, `difference`). Also added the missing `("insert", "Set.insert")` entry — the Set seed had been live since Set codegen but was unreachable through method-call dispatch. Path calls (`Map.with_capacity(16)`) flow through `extract_callee_name` → `inferred_effects` directly without needing a map entry.
  - [x] **4. Effect-resource registration check** — confirmed: `Heap` is in `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES` and `panics` is a standard execution verb; both are visible at dispatch.
  - [x] **5. Test coverage** — added 11 tests under `// ── Per-method effect surface for Map / Set ────` in `tests/effectchecker.rs`. Positive: `Map.insert`, `Map.merge`, `Map.{keys,values,entries}` infer `allocates(Heap)`; pure-reads function with `len`/`is_empty`/`contains_key`/`get` infers no allocation; `remove`/`clear` infer no allocation; `m[k]` infers `panics`; `Set.insert`, `Set.{union,intersection,difference}` infer `allocates(Heap)`; pure-reads function with `contains`/`len`/`is_empty`/`remove` infers no allocation. Negative: `pub fn build_map() -> Map[String, i64] { let m = Map.new(); m }` without `allocates(Heap)` is rejected; `pub fn lookup(...) -> i64 { m[k] }` without `panics` is rejected.
  - [x] **6. Audit existing tests** — kept the existing 2 stub tests (`test_map_new_infers_allocates_heap`, `test_sorted_set_new_infers_allocates_heap`) intact and added the full per-method surface alongside in a new section. 208/208 effectchecker tests pass.

### Auto-Concurrency Codegen — Debugger Contract

Co-developed with the auto-concurrency codegen slate (slices 1–2 in `phase-7-codegen.md` § "Par codegen: auto-parallelization of non-`par` regions") because this is the moment the runtime first emits `par`/`suspend` code at compiler-inferred sites; the contract has to be in place or it gets locked in by accident. Specified in design.md § AI-First Compiler Interface > Debugger Contract; v1 deliverables are the runtime metadata emission and the `std.runtime` enumeration surface (consumer tools — gdb/lldb plugins, DAP, profiler GUIs — are out of v1 scope). The contract is four pieces split across three slices:

- Slice 3 (this section, drafted): SpawnSiteId metadata table — the foundation. Slice 4 builds parent-frame ref + await-chain pointer on top; slice 5 exposes the table to Kāra-callable code via `std.runtime`.
- Profile-gated via `runtime_debug_metadata = true|false`. Slices 3–5 implement the knob via `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA=1|0` env-var override during the v1 demo-build window; the TOML-config home for the knob lands as a separate slice in Phase 8.5 Track 2 (Build & Dependency Tooling). Default-on for dev (today's `karac build` posture); release / embedded / `isr` profile defaults land alongside the Phase 8.5 lift.

- [ ] **Debugger Contract slice 3 — SpawnSiteId metadata table emission.** First of three slices for the four-piece Debugger Contract. Mint a static `u32` `SpawnSiteId` per `par {}` block during codegen and emit a global metadata table `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` mapping each ID to its source location. The IDs are stable per-binary and serve as the join key every later contract piece (parent-frame ref, await-chain pointer, runtime introspection) references. Sequencing: drafted 2026-05-08 before slices 1 and 2; slices 1 and 2 landed first (commits `c0e72fc` / `8bc3bab`), so slice 3 now retrofits onto the post-slice-2 codegen shape. **Updated post-slice-2:** the `par_counter` increment that slice 3 originally targeted in `compile_par_block` now lives in the new `emit_par_run(stmts, span)` helper that both `compile_par_block` (explicit `par {}`) and `compile_function_body` (auto-par dispatch) call. This is good news — slice 3's recording-helper insertion is now a one-place change inside `emit_par_run`, and both spawn-site varieties (explicit + inferred) gain SpawnSiteIds in the same step. Sub-step (d) below updated accordingly.

- [x] **Debugger Contract slice 4 — parent-frame ref + await-chain pointer.** Items (2) + (3) of the four-piece contract. **Item 2 (parent-frame ref) ships real machinery for v1**: every worker frame produced by a `par {}` block carries a pointer back to the frame that created it, with a `null` sentinel for the root task. Slice 5's `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` walks this graph to reconstruct the structured-concurrency tree. **Item 3 (await-chain pointer) ships contract surface only for v1**: `KaracWaitTarget` enum and the `wait_target` field on `KaracFrame` are defined and stable, but always populated as `None` because v1's blocking runtime has no real suspension to track — `Receiver.recv()` returns `Unit` on empty rather than blocking, no event loop exists yet. Real await-chain tracking lights up when Phase 6.3's network event loop ships and registers WaitTargets at I/O-effect-boundary operations. Sequencing: depends on slice 3 for `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` (the SpawnSiteId table that frame metadata indexes into); independent of slices 1, 2, 6.

### Auto-Concurrency Codegen — Parallax-lite Workload

First demo-shaped consumer of slices 1 + 2. A real Kāra program with hand-coded providers, distinct effect resources, and three independent fan-out statements that auto-par lowering parallelizes in compiled output. Validates `karac query cost-summary` against the Cumulative Cost Surface table from `design.md § Performance Diagnostics > Cumulative Cost Surface`. Sets up the framework for v1.x cost-model tuning + the `par struct` single-task overhead measurement; both follow-on analyses are explicitly v1.x territory per `roadmap.md § Phase 8 § Parallax-lite — first ground-truth measurement workload`.

**Demo-shape gap, surfaced upfront.** The canonical Parallax demo (`demo_ideas.md § Demo 1`) is *fan-out + join* — four parallel reads, results fed into `build_dashboard(profile, orders, notif, recommended)`. Slice 2's `group_defines_binding_used_outside` gate blocks this exact pattern today: bindings defined inside a parallel group that are read by stmts outside the group don't auto-parallelize, because `karac_par_run`'s branch fns capture *into* their env struct but don't propagate let-bindings *out*. Lifting the gate requires the still-open `phase-7-codegen.md:182` entry **"Par codegen: return values"**, which extends the runtime ABI with per-branch return slots. Slice 6 ships the **measurement workload** (effect-only fan-out — three independent `writes(R_i)` calls on distinct resources, no joined return) which IS auto-par-eligible today. The demo workload (canonical fan-out + join) lights up when "Par codegen: return values" lands.

- [x] **Debugger Contract slice 6 — Parallax-lite microbenchmark workload.** Hand-coded effect-only-fan-out workload exercising slices 1 + 2 on a real program. Three deliverables: (a) a `examples/parallax_lite/` Kāra project with three trait-bound effect resources + `InMemoryMetrics` provider impl + a `process_request` driver function whose three top-level call statements auto-parallelize; (b) `karac query cost-summary` validation against the workload, pinning the output for the Cumulative Cost Surface table from `design.md § Performance Diagnostics > Cumulative Cost Surface`; (c) a `--sequential` codegen flag (or env-var equivalent) that disables auto-par dispatch in `compile_function_body`, enabling side-by-side wall-clock benchmarking. Sequencing: depends on slice 2 (auto-par codegen MVP — already landed at `8bc3bab`). Independent of slices 3, 4, 5.

- [ ] **Parallax-lite multicore scaling — v1.x cost-model ground-truth data (collected 2026-05-08).** Not a tracker entry awaiting implementation — a data filing for the v1.x cost-model tuning track that the roadmap.md § Phase 8 § Parallax-lite "Cost-model tuning (v1.x)" bullet calls for. Slice 6 shipped a 3-branch wall-clock measurement; this entry extends to a scaling curve (N=3..500) on an 18-core machine. Ground-truth observations:

  - **Near-linear scaling holds through `branch_count ≤ available_parallelism()`** — measured 88% scaling efficiency at N=18 on an 18-core machine (15.88x speedup). The runtime's per-branch overhead is below the wall-clock noise floor up to the core-count ceiling.

  - **Slice 4's `Mutex<Vec<FramePtr>>` active-frames registry doesn't bottleneck at 18 concurrent par-block branches.** The push/retain cost (~1µs each per spawn) is dwarfed by 80ms of busy-compute. Validates the slice-4 design choice (Mutex<Vec> over RwLock<HashMap<ThreadId,_>>) empirically — RwLock+HashMap would have been over-engineered for the actual contention profile.

  - **Sharp efficiency dip at medium N (50–100), recovers at high N (200–500).** N=50 efficiency is 43% (7.18x of 16.67x ideal); N=500 efficiency rises back to 83% (14.80x of 17.86x ideal). Initial stdout-contention hypothesis was *ruled out* by a 10x larger busy-compute test (efficiency stayed low). Real cause: **thermal throttling on sustained all-cores load** plus L3 cache / memory bandwidth contention. At small N (≤18) workers run ~one branch and finish before throttling fully engages; at medium N busy-compute doesn't dwarf the per-branch dispatch cost; at high N busy-compute dominates again. **Laptop-class hardware artifact, not runtime design.** Server-class hardware with proper cooling would push the curve closer to ideal across all N.

  - **Linear compile time scaling: ~0.5ms per branch.** N=500 compiles in 0.26s (auto-par) / 0.15s (sequential). **No quadratic-time analyzer pass** — load-bearing finding for v1.x compiler perf; the conflict-matrix construction in `concurrency.rs` and effect-set unification in `effectchecker.rs` both stay near-linear at 500-element scale.

  **Actionable for the v1.x cost-model spec work** (per `design.md § 8779` "v1.x specification work"):

  - **Fork threshold heuristic.** Today `is_trivial` is the only granularity gate. Empirical sweet spot is `branch_count ≤ available_parallelism()`. v1.x spec should add a `branch_count ≤ N_hw_cores` check in the analyzer or the codegen. v1 ship posture: do nothing and document the cliff (the data shows the cliff is mild — N=500 still gets 14.80x speedup).

  - **Per-branch dispatch overhead is hardware-thermal-dependent, not constant.** ~5ms on cold-start (N=18); ~100ms on sustained all-cores load (N=50–100). The cost-model spec should NOT bake in a hardcoded per-branch overhead constant; defer threshold tuning to post-Parallax-lite measurement on server-class hardware. Document the laptop number as "expected upper-bound ceiling on thermally-constrained hardware."

  - **The `is_trivial` boolean granularity gate is the right v1 abstraction** but loses signal at the cost-model level. v1.x cost-model spec should likely refine to per-branch cost estimate (`branch_cost: Option<Duration>` based on inferred-effect classification) rather than the binary `is_trivial`.

  - **Stdout contention is *not* a meaningful auto-par overhead source** at typical busy-compute / println balances. Initial hypothesis ruled out by the 500M-iter test (efficiency *dropped* rather than improved). The v1.x cost-model spec should ignore stdout-write effects in granularity heuristics unless the busy-compute kernel is unusually small relative to expected per-write overhead.

  Reproducible setup at `examples/parallax_lite/README.md` § Multicore scaling. Raw scripts not committed; reproducible from the README's setup section.

### Auto-Concurrency Codegen — `std.runtime` Introspection APIs

Slice 5 of the auto-concurrency slate. Closes out the four-piece Debugger Contract by exposing slice 3's `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` metadata table + slice 4's `KaracFrame` active-frames registry as Kāra-callable APIs. Drafted last (after slices 1–4 + 6) per demo-driven sequencing — slice 6's Parallax-lite workload provides a concrete consumer to design against.

- [ ] **Debugger Contract slice 5 — `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` / `list_tasks()` / `has_debug_metadata()`.** Item (4) of the four-piece contract per `design.md § Debugger Contract`. Three Kāra-callable functions that materialize the runtime introspection surface for tooling and crash-report consumption. `has_debug_metadata()` returns a `bool` reading `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED`. `list_par_blocks() -> Vec[ParBlockInfo]` enumerates the *currently-active* par blocks across all OS threads (joins slice 4's `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame` against slice 3's `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` table to enrich each frame's `spawn_site_id` with its `(file, line, col, worker_count)`). `list_tasks() -> Vec[TaskInfo]` enumerates suspended tasks — **always returns empty in v1** because v1's blocking runtime has no real suspension to track (`Receiver.recv()` returns `Unit` on empty rather than blocking; no event loop). Phase 6.3's network event loop is the predecessor that lights this up. Sequencing: depends on slices 3 + 4 (both landed at `c6d8b44` / `22fa27a`); independent of slices 1, 2, 6 once those have landed.

### Provider Implementations

The `with_provider[R]` mechanism is spec'd in `design.md` and parsed today, but several pieces of the runtime/codegen wiring are gappy. Items here track those gaps. The full provider surface is referenced from `roadmap.md § Phase 8 § Provider Implementations`.

- [x] **`with_provider[R]` trait-method dispatch wiring (GAP-N follow-up).** Inside a `with_provider[R](inst, || { ... })` scope, calls of the shape `R.method(args)` should dispatch to `inst`'s `R: Trait` impl per `design.md § Provider-Rooted Resources` ("Resource call desugaring" + "Runtime mechanics" + "with_provider and parameterized resources" paragraphs). In v1 codegen the dispatch is currently a **no-op at runtime**: the `with_provider` block compiles + links, but `R.method(...)` calls inside the closure body never invoke the bound provider's impl method. Empirically validated by slice 6 (Parallax-lite workload, 2026-05-08): a `with_provider[MetricsA](inst, || { MetricsA.record(50_000_000); })` shape that should run a 50M-iteration busy-compute kernel returns in <5ms — the kernel never executed. Slice 6 fell back to a no-providers entry point (calling `process_request` directly) and inlined the busy-compute kernel into the `record_*` driver functions to keep the wall-clock benchmark meaningful; the canonical `R.method(...)` shape is documented in `examples/parallax_lite/src/main.kara` comments + slice 6's "Deviations" close-out. **Demo readiness load-bearing**: the canonical Parallax demo (`demo_ideas.md § Demo 1`) is `let profile = fetch_profile(user_id);` etc., where `fetch_profile` typically dispatches through the active `UserDB: DatabaseProvider`. When `phase-7-codegen.md:229` "Par codegen: return values" lands and unblocks the canonical fan-out + join shape, this GAP-N wiring also needs to ship for the demo's `fetch_*` calls to do anything observable. The two are paired demo-readiness items.

  **Spec status — locked.** `design.md § Provider-Rooted Resources` already pins the rule (clarified during slice 6 follow-up reframing 2026-05-08): `R.method(args)` desugars to `Arc<dyn R::Provider>` lookup in the per-task provider stack followed by a vtable call; `with_provider[R](p, ||...)` pushes/pops a frame; parameterized instances `R[k]` always route through the base-resource binding. The interpreter implements this at `src/interpreter.rs::eval_resource_method` (line 7146). The remaining work is **codegen-only** — the implementation, not the spec. The earlier "needs design discussion" framing in this entry referred to the spec gap that is no longer open; what remains is **implementation-design choice** on the codegen ABI, scoped in the slice plan below.

  **Codegen ABI design choices** (all decidable from existing constraints; no further spec discussion needed before slice plan execution):
  - **(a) Per-task provider stack representation.** Two natural shapes — (i) thread-local `Vec<HashMap<ResourceId, Arc<dyn Any>>>` mirroring the interpreter, accessed through a runtime helper; (ii) frame-allocated linked list of `(resource_id, provider_arc)` cells, with the head pointer carried in `KaracFrame` (slice 4) so the existing per-thread frame plumbing extends naturally. **Recommend (ii)**: avoids `thread_local!` bookkeeping on Apple/Linux platforms with cheap-but-not-free TLS, and reuses the slice 4 KaracFrame infrastructure already wired into `karac_par_run`. Lookup is O(stack-depth × resource-count); typical depths are 1-3, so linear scan is fine.
  - **(b) Vtable layout.** Trait-object support is *new* — Kāra v1 has no other trait-object lowering site. Two options — (i) per-trait single-dispatch vtable (data ptr + fn ptrs), classic Rust shape; (ii) per-method-call lookup table keyed by `(resource_id, method_name) → fn_ptr`, sidestepping vtable construction entirely. **Recommend (i)**: the v1 cost model already names "thin Arc deref + one vtable indirection" at `design.md § Resource call desugaring`; option (ii) adds a hash lookup per call which is observably slower and not what the spec promises. Vtable construction at `with_provider` call site is a one-time cost; subsequent calls are pointer-chases.
  - **(c) Arc-sharing on spawn.** `karac_par_run` (slice 2 + 4) already passes branch closures captured environments into worker threads. The provider stack head pointer needs to flow through that capture so spawned tasks see the parent's bindings. Implementation: add a `provider_stack_head: *const ProviderFrame` field to the env-struct emitted by `compile_par_block` / `emit_par_run`, populated from the calling thread's KaracFrame at par-block entry; each worker thread initializes its KaracFrame with this head when entering the branch fn. Arc clones happen lazily at first use, not eagerly at spawn (matches the cost note at `design.md:7078`).
  - **(d) Parameterized-resource binding.** `design.md § with_provider and parameterized resources` (line 7101) locks the rule: `Db["users"]`, `Db["orders"]` all key on the base resource `Db`. Codegen already has access to the resource's base name via `effectchecker.rs` resource-ID interning. The lookup uses base name only; the parameter is passed through to the provider's method as a normal argument. No new design.
  - **(e) Vtable storage on `with_provider` call.** When `with_provider[R](provider, ||body)` runs, we need the provider's vtable for trait `R::Provider` to be addressable. Option (i): emit a per-`(provider_type, trait)` static vtable global at codegen time, referenced by `with_provider`'s frame push. Option (ii): build the vtable on the fly at the `with_provider` call site. **Recommend (i)** — vtables are statically known per impl; static globals avoid per-call construction overhead and match the standard Rust trait-object model.
  - **(f) Resource ID assignment.** `effectchecker.rs` already interns resource names to stable IDs for conflict analysis. Codegen reuses these IDs as the provider-stack lookup key — no new ID space.

  **Slice plan (autonomous-friendly bar, drafted 2026-05-08).**

  *Goal.* Codegen `R.method(args)` calls inside `with_provider[R](inst, ||body)` scopes to dispatch through the bound provider's trait impl, matching the interpreter's `eval_resource_method` semantics and the design.md spec.

- [x] **Typed effect resources + in-memory providers + canonical `get_dashboard` workload (full Parallax demo, Slice C).** The demo's load-bearing source artifact: four typed effect resources (`UserDB / OrderDB / NotifDB / RecommendDB`), four single-method provider traits returning typed result data (`fetch_profile -> Profile`, `fetch_recent_orders -> Vec[Order]`, `fetch_notifications -> Vec[Notification]`, `fetch_recommendations -> Vec[Recommendation]`), four in-memory provider impls (`InMemoryUserDB / InMemoryOrderDB / InMemoryNotifDB / InMemoryRecommendDB`), and the canonical `get_dashboard(user_id)` workload — four `let` bindings into typed return values, joined into a `Dashboard { profile, orders, notif, recommended }` result struct. Lives at `examples/parallax/` (sibling to `examples/parallax_lite/`). The combined workload exercises the integration of two recently-landed mechanisms in one place: Theme 6's `with_provider[R]` trait-method dispatch for the per-call routing, and Slice A's per-branch return slots for the four-way fan-out+join. Each was test-covered independently at landing time; this slice is the first source artifact that puts them together end-to-end. **Demo readiness:** pairs with Slice B (HTTP server FFI) for the `serve_http` entry point and Slice E (benchmark harness) for the side-by-side compare; the workload itself ships standalone and can be benchmarked directly via `cargo run --release` before B/E land.

- [ ] **Shape as a new generic-parameter kind.** Extend `src/typechecker.rs` to track dim-kinded and shape-variadic (`...S`) generic params alongside existing type and const-expr params. Kind inference: a param appearing only in shape position is inferred `Dim`-kinded; explicit `: Dim` and `...` annotations also accepted. Unification rules: two `Dim` params unify if one is unbound or both resolve to the same const expr; `?` unifies with any `Dim` and degrades the result position to `?`. Shape-dim mismatch produces `E_SHAPE` diagnostic naming both sides and where the conflicting bindings were introduced.

- [ ] **Shape literal grammar (parser + AST).** Extend `src/parser.rs` and `src/ast.rs` to accept shape literals `[const_expr_or_? { , const_expr_or_? }]` in type-argument position, plus `...IDENT` variadic splice inside a shape literal. `?` is a new `AstNode::ShapeDimDynamic`; existing expression-`?` usage is unaffected (context disambiguates). Outside shape-argument slots, `?` parsing is unchanged.

- [ ] **`Tensor[T, Shape]` stdlib type.** Generic struct with compile-time shape parameter. Stdlib `impl`: `zeros` / `ones` / `full` constructors, `from` literal constructor, `shape()` runtime accessor, multi-dim `t[i, j, k]` indexing via `Index` / `IndexMut`, `iter_axis(n)` for axis iteration, reshape / permute / slice / squeeze operations with shape-preservation in the type where statically known. Codegen: contiguous C-order buffer in Arrow layout; bounds-check elision when all dims are static const exprs. Interpreter parity: tree-walk implementation tracks shape at runtime for `Tensor[T, Shape]` values regardless of static/dynamic dim mix.

- [ ] **Arithmetic traits on `Tensor[T, Shape]`.** `Add`/`Sub`/`Mul`/`Div` operator-trait impls that require *exact shape match* between tensor operands and accept scalar operands via the Q4 literal-promotion rule (+ operator dispatch for scalar-tensor). `Neg` for negation. Shape mismatch between two tensors produces `E_SHAPE` with both shapes printed and a pointer to `broadcast_add` / `broadcast_mul` methods. Reduce ops (`sum`, `mean`, `prod`, `min`, `max`) return `T`; axis-reduce variants (`sum_axis(n)`, `mean_axis(n)`) return a tensor of rank-1 lower.

- [ ] **Explicit broadcasting methods.** `broadcast_add`, `broadcast_sub`, `broadcast_mul`, `broadcast_div` on `Tensor[T, Shape]`. Arguments accept tensors whose shape is elementwise broadcast-compatible with `self.shape()` (singleton dims expand). When both shapes are fully static at call site, compatibility checked at compile time; else checked at runtime. Typed broadcasting (where the type system rejects incompatible broadcasts statically, Q3's 3D option) is a v2 research target, not in v1.

- [x] **Literal-involved promotion in numeric binary operators (Q4).** ✓ DONE (2026-04-27) — `infer_binary` computes `eff_left_ty`/`eff_right_ty` via suffix-free literal detection; when one side is an unsuffixed literal and the other is a concrete numeric type T, re-records the literal's span as T in `expr_types` (so `rewrite_binary` in lowering sees a homogeneous pair). Float literals are not promoted to int types. 8 typechecker tests added covering int-right, int-left, float-right, int-to-float, comparison, equality, non-numeric (still errors), string+int (still errors). ~~Extend `src/lowering.rs` / typechecker binary-op handling: when one operand is a typed expression of numeric type `T` and the other is a literal, the literal takes type `T` before the operator is resolved. Scope: `+ - * / % < <= > >= == !=`. Function-call arguments, struct-field assignment, and pattern matching retain the strict "literal matches declared type" rule.~~

**Data types — Arrow commitment (Q5, Q6).**

- [ ] **`Column[T]` — nullable 1D column with Arrow bitmap layout.** Struct with `{ data, null_bitmap, len, capacity }`; Apache Arrow conformance per `design.md § Memory Layout Commitments`. Stdlib methods: `new`, `with_capacity`, `from_vec` (all-valid), `from_iter_nullable`, `null_count`, `is_null(i)`, `valid_count`, `push` / `push_null`, `fillna(val, treat_nan_as_null=false)`, `dropna`, indexing (`c[i] -> Option[T]`), `iter` (yields `Option[T]`), `iter_valid` (yields `T`, skipping nulls). Arithmetic with SQL null propagation: `null + x = null`, `null == null = null` (three-valued logic). All operator impls maintain the bitmap through the result.

- [ ] **`DataFrame` — schema-bearing table of columns.** Struct with named-column dispatch, schema carrying column-name-to-type mappings. Minimum API surface: construction from a map of named columns, `column(name)` lookup returning `ref Column[T]` with type erasure via an internal `AnyColumn`, `row_iter` yielding struct views (mechanism: compile-time row-struct synthesis from schema), `schema()` accessor, basic `filter(predicate)` / `select(cols)` operations. Heavier query planning (joins, groupby with custom aggregations) is explicit v1.5+ work.

- [ ] **Arrow IPC and Parquet.** `Tensor.from_arrow_ipc(bytes)` / `arr.to_arrow_ipc()`; `Column.from_arrow_ipc(bytes)` / `col.to_arrow_ipc()`; `DataFrame.read_parquet(path) with reads(FileSystem)` / `df.write_parquet(path) with writes(FileSystem)`; `DataFrame.read_csv(path)` / `df.write_csv(path)` matching the same effect pattern. IPC implementation uses the Arrow C Data Interface for zero-copy where feasible.

**Script mode (Q7).**

- [ ] **Script mode — files without `fn main`.** Parser change: when `src/parser.rs` encounters a top-level statement (`let`, expression, assignment) *before* any `fn main` declaration, switch to script mode and synthesize `fn main() -> Result[Unit, Error]` wrapping all top-level statements in file order. Items (fn, struct, enum, trait, impl, use) remain at module scope and hoist as today. Mix of top-level statements and an explicit `fn main` is a parse error with a diagnostic pointing at both. Resolver / typechecker treat the synthesized main exactly as they would a user-written `fn main()` with `Result[Unit, Error]` return type — effect inference applies, `?` works, existing entry-point rules apply.

**Scripting-critical stdlib (Q10 10B surface).**

- [ ] **`std.regex`.** Compile regex patterns to an NFA/DFA state machine; `Regex.compile(pattern) -> Result[Regex, RegexError]`, `rx.is_match(s)`, `rx.find(s) -> Option[Match]`, `rx.find_all(s) -> Vec[Match]`, `rx.captures(s)`, `rx.replace_all(s, replacement)`. Use a tested regex crate as the initial backend; eventually replace with a Kāra-native implementation. Pure (no effects).

- [ ] **`std.http` (client only).** `Client.new()`, `client.get(url)`, `client.post(url, body)`, chained builders for headers / body / timeout. `Request.send() -> Result[Response, HttpError] with sends(Network), receives(Network)`. Response exposes `status_code`, `headers`, `text()`, `bytes()`. TLS via stdlib-adjacent crate. **Superseded framing — "Server is v1.5+" is stale:** the v64 backend-first reshape (§ Backend Platform) lifted both server *and* client into the Phase-8 floor, so this entry is now the client-surface spec for the `Client.get` / `Client.post` sub-item under the [§ Backend Platform `std.http`](#backend-platform-v64-lifted) parent (currently a stub `get` + interpreter-only `post`). Implement against this spec there.

- [x] **`std.http` server — minimal surface (pulled forward from v1.5 for Parallax demo).** ✓ Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `3c3d87b`). One-line summary: hyper-backed FFI surface in karac-runtime (`karac_runtime_serve_http_static` + `karac_runtime_serve_http` + `KaracHttpRequest` / `KaracHttpResponse` C-ABI structs); B3 fallback (b) taken — non-polymorphic `Server.serve_static(addr, body)` that erases effects at the FFI boundary, since free-fn fn-pointer-as-arg + effect-set parameterization isn't typechecker-supported yet (Theme 6 settled the trait-method shape but free-fn shape is the open delta); B5 smoke test in `tests/http_server.rs` passes — compiles a Kāra binary, binds `127.0.0.1:0`, GET `/dashboard/1` returns 200 + the demo-shaped JSON body.

- [x] **`std.json`.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `91768f2`). Interpreter dispatch `Json.parse` + `j.stringify()` over a `Json` enum baked at `runtime/stdlib/json.kara`; runtime crate exposes the same surface through `karac_runtime_json_*` C-ABI exports for codegen-side wiring (deferred). Six tests in `tests/json.rs` cover round-trip + insertion-order + error-line/col + manual `ToJson` impl. Variant-payload-struct shape chosen for `KaracJsonValue` per the slice plan's recommendation; `serde_json` carries `preserve_order` in both crates so `Json.Object` iterates in insertion order. Inline-fix in `typechecker::resolve_identifier_type` skips enum-variant fallback when the bare name matches a primitive / prelude type — needed because `Json.String(String)` would otherwise shadow `String.from(...)` calls (predecessor test surface didn't exercise the collision).

- [x] **`std.json` codegen-side wiring — `Json.parse` / `j.stringify()` from compiled binaries.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-21 across two commits (`5562309` for stringify side, follow-up for parse). Compiled-binary `Json.parse(s)` and `j.stringify()` work end-to-end across the full variant surface. Stringify side: a single synthesized LLVM helper `__karac_json_kara_to_ffi(tag, w0, w1, w2) -> *mut KaracJsonValue` dispatches on the variant tag and emits per-variant calls into eight new runtime constructors (`karac_runtime_json_make_null` / `_make_bool` / `_make_number` / `_make_string` / `_make_array` / `_make_object`, plus `_alloc_items_buf` / `_alloc_keys_buf` / `_alloc_key` for the Array/Object buffer transfer). Array (32-byte Json stride) and Object (56-byte (String, Json) tuple stride) arms walk their underlying `Vec[T]` payload and recurse via direct LLVM self-call. All three receiver shapes work: identifier (`let j = Json.Number(3.14); j.stringify()`), Call-shaped non-identifier (`Json.Object(pairs).stringify()`), and 3-segment-Path unit (`Json.Null.stringify()`). Parse side: the inverse synthesized helper `__karac_json_ffi_to_kara(*const KaracJsonValue) -> {i64,i64,i64,i64}` walks the FFI tree, copies String payloads into Kāra-owned buffers, mallocs Vec[Json] / Vec[(String, Json)] backing storage at exact size (cap = len), and recurses on children. The parse-dispatch entry in `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` allocates a null-terminated cstr copy of the input, calls `karac_runtime_json_parse`, branches on null return, and merges Ok/Err arms via phi. Result's enum layout in `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` was widened from `{i64, i64}` to `{i64, i64, i64, i64, i64}` (tag + 4 payload words) so the Ok arm can carry the 4-word Json enum value verbatim; existing Result consumers are backwards-compatible by construction (the `?` operator pulls `enum_ty` dynamically from the function return type, par-block surfaces read the slot type from a layout descriptor, single-word constructions write only field 1 with trailing slots staying undef). The Err arm of `Result[Json, JsonError]` truncates JsonError's String `cap` (5-word payload trimmed to 4) — acceptable v1 trade-off since the kata's `/echo` arm only discriminates on the tag; a future Result-width sweep can extend further.
