Two new cross-cutting fixes shipped alongside slice 2: (a) `pattern_payload_word_count` / `pattern_payload_llvm_type` (`src/codegen/control_flow_match.rs`) now look up `enum_layouts` after `struct_types` so enum-typed bindings (`Ok(j)` where j: Json) reconstitute as the full tagged-union struct instead of falling to the i64-default — this also unblocks any future `Result[E, E]`-style multi-word Ok payloads; (b) `reconstruct_payload_value`'s multi-word target-type pick was symmetrically extended to consult `enum_layouts`. Layout invariants pinned in runtime: `test_karac_json_value_layout_pinned` locks the 10-field 72-byte `KaracJsonValue` shape and `test_karac_json_error_layout_pinned` locks the 16-byte `KaracJsonError` shape — both feed hand-coded byte-stride GEPs in `src/codegen/json.rs`. Tests: 12 codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_json_parse_*` covering every variant (null, bool both polarities, number, string + empty-string, array + empty-array, object, deeply-nested, parse-error) plus `test_ir_json_parse_emits_lift_helper_once` pinning the single-walker-definition invariant. Existing `tests/par_codegen.rs::test_ir_par_branch_result_typed_let_emits_slot_and_cancel_store` was updated to reflect the new Result struct shape. Closes the deferral noted in the std.json shipped entry above ("runtime crate exposes the same surface through `karac_runtime_json_*` C-ABI exports for codegen-side wiring (deferred)"). Original detailed slice plan retained below for reference. Closes the deferral noted in the std.json shipped entry directly above ("runtime crate exposes the same surface through `karac_runtime_json_*` C-ABI exports for codegen-side wiring (deferred)"). Surfaced 2026-05-21 by `kara-katas/backend/todo-api/main.kara` build: `error: codegen failed: codegen: no handler for method 'stringify' on variable 'j'` (and `... on non-identifier receiver` for unbound expressions like `Json.Object(p).stringify()`). The interpreter dispatch is shipped and exercised by `tests/json.rs`; this entry adds the compiled-binary path. **Why P0 v1:** every backend kata + flagship demo that emits JSON over a real HTTP server needs `Json.stringify()` to work in compiled mode (the interpreter has no `Server.serve` arm — confirmed via probe 2026-05-21 that `karac run` on a `Server.serve` program panics with `internal error: ... path 'Server.serve' not found ... should be caught by resolver`). Slices: (1) **Lowering — `Json` enum ↔ `KaracJsonValue`.** The Kāra-side `pub enum Json { Null, Bool(bool), Number(f64), String(String), Array(Vec[Json]), Object(Vec[(String, Json)]) }` (`runtime/stdlib/json.kara:30-39`) and the runtime-side `KaracJsonValue` C struct (`runtime/src/lib.rs:1805-1822`, variant-tagged struct per locked design at line 1786) need a bidirectional lowering: a Kāra `Json` value lowered into a `*mut KaracJsonValue` to pass to runtime externs, and a returned `*mut KaracJsonValue` translated back into a Kāra `Json` value for the user. The variant-tag enum layout already exists at the LLVM IR level for ordinary Kāra enums; this slice adds the FFI-translation pair (likely a runtime-side `karac_runtime_json_from_native(...)` taking the Kāra variant tag + payload-pointer triple, and a `..._to_native(value)` for the inverse). Memory ownership per the runtime's locked rule: both `karac_runtime_json_parse` and `karac_runtime_json_stringify` allocate Boxed trees / `CString`s and the caller frees via `karac_runtime_json_free_value` / `..._free_string` (see `runtime/src/lib.rs:1769-1772`). (2) **`Json.parse(s)` codegen.** New compile-time dispatch: when a free fn call resolves to the path `Json.parse`, lower to `karac_runtime_json_parse(s.data, s.len) -> KaracJsonResult { tag, value_ptr, error_line, error_column, error_msg_ptr, error_msg_len }`. Translate `KaracJsonResult` into the Kāra-side `Result[Json, JsonError]` via the lowering from slice (1). Free the runtime allocation after translation. (3) **`j.stringify()` codegen.** New method-call dispatch: when the receiver type resolves to `Json` (whether the receiver is an identifier `j`, a let-bound variable, or a non-identifier expression like `Json.Object(pairs).stringify()`), lower to `karac_runtime_json_stringify(value_ptr) -> *mut c_char` after lowering the receiver into a `*mut KaracJsonValue` via slice (1)'s `..._from_native` helper. The returned C string is owned by the runtime; copy bytes into a fresh Kāra `String { data, len, cap }` (mirroring `compile_request_string_method` in `src/codegen/http.rs`) and call `karac_runtime_json_free_string` to release the runtime's allocation. (4) **Non-identifier-receiver path.** `Json.Object(p).stringify()` currently fires `error: codegen failed: codegen: no handler for method 'stringify' on non-identifier receiver` because the method-call dispatch falls through before any Json-typed handling is reached. Plumb the non-identifier path through the same `compile_method_call` arm as the identifier path — both lower to the same `..._from_native + extern call + String-copy` sequence; the only difference is whether the receiver value is read from a slot (identifier case) or assembled into a temp (non-identifier case). (5) **Tests in `tests/codegen.rs`.** New section `Phase 8 line 431 follow-up — std.json codegen`: positive — `let j = Json.Number(3.14); println(j.stringify());` produces `3.14`; `Json.Object([(\"a\", Json.Number(1.0))]).stringify()` produces `{"a":1.0}` (non-identifier-receiver path); `Json.parse("[1,2,3]")` round-trips via `match` + `Json.Array` destructure. Negative — `Json.parse("not json")` emits `JsonError` with non-zero line/col. The existing `tests/json.rs` (interpreter) tests stay green unchanged — this entry's tests live in `codegen.rs` and run under `--features llvm`. (6) **Reused infrastructure.** The same `..._from_native` / `..._to_native` helpers will be reused by future `#[derive(ToJson)]` codegen (v1.5 per the original `std.json` ship note's locked design (v)). Doc those helpers as the stable internal surface for that follow-up. Phase target: Phase 7 (codegen) for slices (2)-(4); Phase 8 (stdlib) for the runtime-side translation helpers in slice (1). Cross-reference: `runtime/src/lib.rs:1765-1830` (`KaracJsonValue` + ownership rules); `runtime/stdlib/json.kara` (`Json` enum decl); `src/codegen/http.rs::compile_request_string_method` (the `String`-copy pattern this slice mirrors); `tests/json.rs` (existing interpreter coverage — the v1 contract this slice extends to compiled mode); `kara-katas/backend/todo-api/main.kara` (first consumer to surface the gap); `wip-todo-api-kata.md § Decisions log 2026-05-21 (later)` (write-up of the kata's workaround pattern).

- [ ] **`std.stats` — basic statistics.** `mean`, `sum`, `prod`, `variance`, `stddev`, `percentile(p)`, `median`, `min`, `max`, `argmin`, `argmax`, `sort`, `argsort`. Trait-dispatched via `Reduce`, `ElementwiseMap`, `ElementwiseOrd` traits so `Tensor`, `Column`, and future `GpuTensor` implement the same surface without API break. Free-function forms in `std.stats` (`stats.mean(v)`) and method forms on `Tensor` / `Column` (`v.mean()`).

**GPU call-site backend — deferred to post-Phase-10.**

- [ ] **(Deferred.) Revisit GPU call-site dispatch once Phase 10 codegen has ground truth.** Expected shape: `GpuTensor[T, Shape]` mirroring `Tensor[T, Shape]` with device memory; `.on(gpu)` / `.to_cpu()` boundary ops matching CuPy / PyTorch / JAX semantics. Revisit the lazy-evaluation design alongside — whole-pipeline visibility is load-bearing for GPU kernel fusion.

**Lazy evaluation (Q8) — v1.5 feature, not v1.**

- [ ] **(Deferred to v1.5.) `.lazy()` method on `Vec`, `Tensor`, `Column` returning `LazyColumn[T]` / `LazyTensor[T]` / `Iterator[T]` specializations.** Fused filter/map/reduce pipelines with effect composition from closures. Build on top of the existing `Iterator[T]` language-level primitive. Revisit when Phase 11 stdlib is stable.

**Fallback plan:** if Phase 11 schedule slips, `regex` and `http` are the most at-risk items (real network + state-machine work); pushable to v1.1. Tensor / Column / DataFrame / stats / script mode are cheap enough to keep as v1 non-negotiables.

- [ ] **G23 — Trait coherence / orphan rules**. Decide and enforce: can you implement a foreign trait for a foreign type? Recommendation: Rust's orphan rule (must own either the trait or the type). Document the newtype workaround. Not relevant until multi-package support exists — moved from Phase 3.

- [ ] **G14 — FFI effect annotation completeness**. Create comprehensive syscall-to-effect mapping table. Review POSIX/Linux syscall man pages for composite effects (e.g., `sendfile()` needs both `reads(FileSystem)` and `sends(Network)`). Build integration tests that validate effect annotations against actual syscall behavior.

- [ ] **FFI — Kāra-to-C exports.** Enable Kāra functions to be callable from C. Requires: `#[export]` or `pub extern "C"` annotation, compiler generates C-compatible calling convention, restrictions on parameter/return types (must be C-representable). Needed for shared libraries, plugins, and embedding Kāra in C/C++ applications.

- [ ] **FFI — C header generation.** Tooling to auto-generate `.h` header files from `extern "C"` Kāra exports (like Rust's `cbindgen`). Maps Kāra types to C equivalents. Needed for C consumers of Kāra libraries.

- [ ] **FFI — `#[repr(C)]` struct layout.** Attribute to guarantee C-compatible memory layout for structs passed across FFI boundaries. Without this, Kāra's compiler is free to reorder/pad fields (especially with layout blocks). `#[repr(C)]` pins layout to match C's rules.

- [ ] **FFI — `#[repr(transparent)]` for distinct-type FFI.** Spec lives at design.md § `#[repr(transparent)]` for distinct-type FFI (v60 item 23). Sub-steps: (1) Parser — `#[repr(transparent)]` already lexes per the existing `#[repr]` infrastructure; the typechecker is the new work. (2) Typechecker carrier-shape validation at item-decl time: accept on `distinct type`, single-field `struct` (single non-zero-sized field; zero-sized companion fields are permitted iff every companion has size zero AND alignment one — `PhantomData[T]`, `()`, `[T; 0]`, an empty unit struct), and single-variant single-field `enum`. Reject multi-field struct (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_REQUIRES_SINGLE_FIELD]`); zero-field struct (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_REQUIRES_FIELD]`); enum with !=1 variant or with payload-less variant (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_ENUM_NOT_SINGLE_VARIANT]`); union (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_UNION_FORBIDDEN]`); generic carrier whose inner is a type parameter `T` without a `T: Sized` bound (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_REQUIRES_SIZED]`). Combination with any other repr (`#[repr(C)]`, `#[repr(packed)]`, `#[repr(align(N))]`, `#[repr(intN)]`) is rejected (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_EXCLUSIVE]`). (3) Layout — codegen records the wrapper as a layout-pass-through to the inner field (no separate type registered in the LLVM type table; the wrapper's LLVM type *is* the inner type). The inner type's repr passes through unchanged: a `transparent` wrapper around a `#[repr(C)]` inner has the same layout as the inner. (4) FFI ABI integration — at `extern "C"` call sites, an argument of the wrapper type whose declared `extern` parameter type is the inner type is permitted with an explicit unwrap (`.raw()` for `distinct type`, named-field access for single-field struct carriers); the type system enforces the unwrap, but codegen lowers without conversion (the bit-pattern is identical). (5) Auto-derive integration — `#[derive(...)]` walks the carrier's fields normally for `Eq`/`PartialEq`/`Hash`/`Clone`/`Copy`/`Debug`; the existing distinct-type derive rules continue to govern `distinct type` carriers. (6) Orphan-rule integration — no special handling; `transparent` is a layout claim that doesn't change the orphan-rule arithmetic (the wrapper is still a local type for orphan purposes). Test plan: positive — `#[repr(transparent)] distinct type Fd = i32` round-trips through an `extern "C" fn close(fd: i32)` signature with `.raw()`; `#[repr(transparent)] struct Tagged[T] { inner: i32, _marker: PhantomData[T] }` accepts the zero-sized companion; layout-pass-through verified via `size_of` and `align_of` on wrapper equals same on inner. Negative — multi-field `struct Wrapper { a: i32, b: i32 }` rejected; zero-field `struct Empty {}` rejected; multi-variant `enum E { A(i32), B(i32) }` rejected; `union U` rejected; `#[repr(transparent, C)]` rejected; `#[repr(transparent)] struct Tagged[T] { inner: T }` without `T: Sized` rejected. (Phase 5.2 — typechecker work; depends on `#[repr]` parsing infrastructure being stable.)

- [ ] **FFI — Callback passing.** Define how Kāra closures (or function values, G51) are passed as C function pointers. Non-capturing functions can map directly to `fn` pointers. Capturing closures need a `void* context` + function pointer pair (standard C callback pattern). Document the effect implications — C callbacks are unverified effect boundaries.

- [ ] **FFI — String marshaling.** Define conversion between Kāra `String` (UTF-8, length-prefixed) and C strings (null-terminated `*const u8`). Provide stdlib helpers: `String.from_c(ptr)` (copies, validates UTF-8), `string.as_c_str()` (appends null terminator). Handle the allocation question — who owns the memory?

- [ ] **FFI — Error code mapping.** Define stdlib pattern for converting C-style error codes (`i32` return, `errno`) to Kāra `Result[T, E]`. Provide a `CError` type or trait-based conversion. Stdlib wrappers should use this consistently for all POSIX wrappers.

- [ ] **Dynamic dispatch / trait objects.** Implement trait object support. All design decisions are settled: (1) syntax is `dyn Trait` — the explicit keyword is required, and a bare trait name in a type position is a compile error; (2) unbound `dyn T` (no trait constraint) is not allowed — erasure without interface knowledge is useless; (3) multiple bounds allowed: `dyn Shape + Display`; (4) object safety: traits with generic methods cannot be used as trait objects — compiler emits a clear diagnostic; (5) owned `dyn Trait` requires heap allocation and produces `allocates(Heap)`; `ref dyn Trait` borrows an already-allocated value and does not; (6) effect semantics use an open-world model (design.md): the programmer declares the effect bound at the trait definition (`trait Handler with reads(UserDB), sends(AuditLog) { ... }`), all impls must have effects ⊆ that bound, and call sites use the declared trait bound as the effect set — no whole-program analysis needed; (7) trait objects cannot use `layout` blocks — concrete type is unknown at compile time. Implementation tasks: vtable layout and codegen (Phase 7 prerequisite), object safety checker in the type checker, `allocates(Heap)` inference for owned `dyn Trait` positions. Depends on Phase 3 trait system and Phase 7 LLVM codegen being stable.

- [ ] **G10 — Cycle detection with generic containers and trait objects.** Document the `dyn Trait` limitation in the ownership section. The compiler can't see through `dyn Trait` to detect cycles. Recommend `shared struct` with `weak` or `Arena` for patterns where trait objects create cycles. Consider whether the compiler should warn when `dyn Trait` appears in a position that could form a cycle.

- [ ] **G24 — Compile time strategy**. Validate that `pub` boundaries as inference firewalls effectively bound compilation cost. Benchmark full compilation on non-trivial programs. Ensure architecture supports incremental compilation, cached analysis, and parallel module compilation.

- [ ] **G25 — Standard Error trait**. Define `trait Error` with `message()` and `source()` chaining. Define `trait From[T]` for error conversion via `?` operator. Implement for all stdlib error types.

- [ ] **String interpolation format specifiers.** Design and implement `{expr:spec}` syntax in `f"..."` strings. Open questions: syntax form (Rust-style `{x:.2}`, Python-style `{x:.2f}`, or Kāra-specific); whether format specifiers desugar to a `Format` trait separate from `Display`; interaction with `#[derive(Display)]`; width, precision, fill, alignment, sign, radix. The syntax space is reserved — `{expr:spec}` is a compile error until this is implemented.

- [ ] **Conversion traits (`From`/`Into`/`TryFrom`/`TryInto`).** Implement the four conversion traits and the blanket impl (`impl From[T]` → automatic `Into`). Enforce: implementing `Into` directly is a compile error. Wire `?` operator to desugar cross-error-type propagation to `From.from()`. Refinement types auto-generate `TryFrom` impls. See design.md — "Conversion Traits".
  - **Slice 1 shipped** (commit `deff0e3`): `From` dispatch via `T.from(x)` with source-type disambiguation; 19 built-in numeric widening impls; user `impl From[E1] for E2` resolves; `?` typechecker validates cross-error `From` and records conversion target in `TypeCheckResult.question_conversions`; interpreter consults that side-table and calls `<Target>.from(e)` before propagating Err.
  - **Slice 3a shipped:** `.into()` with expected-type threading. `TypeChecker` gained `check_expr(expr, expected)` that recognizes a zero-arg `.into()` method call against a Named / primitive expected type and records the target in `TypeCheckResult.into_conversions` (span → target-type name). Expected-type threading is wired at four positions: (1) `let x: T = ...`, (2) `let x: T = ...` in `let-else`, (3) `Assign { target, value }` (target-type-driven), (4) function call argument slot against the parameter type, (5) explicit `return expr;` against the current function's return type, (6) function body final expression against the declared return type (via `check_block_against`). Lowering then rewrites `x.into()` to `Target.from(x)` — the `Into` blanket impl is purely a lowering rewrite, no impl entries materialized at typecheck time. Codegen falls through naturally: numeric widening is a passthrough in `compile_assoc_call`, user-type `T.from(x)` routes to the impl-block-compiled `T.from` LLVM function. Missing `impl From[S] for T` emits a targeted diagnostic with the source and target type names. `let` codegen now uses the type annotation as a fallback type hint when the RHS shape isn't classifiable (fixes user-struct `var_type_names` registration for `let c: Cm = i.into();`).
  - **Slice 3b shipped:** user `impl Into for T` and `impl TryInto for T` rejected at the resolver. Distinct from the operator-trait restriction (those only fire on ArithOps / Index / Display); Into/TryInto use their own `ResolveErrorKind::IntoTraitImplNotAllowed` (code `E0109`) with a suggestion to implement `From` / `TryFrom` instead.
  - **Follow-ups not in slice 3:**
    - `TryFrom` / `TryInto` with associated `Error` type; numeric narrowing impls.
    - `From[T] for Option[T]` and `From[T] for Result[T, E]` wrapping.
    - `From[StringLit] for String` / from char literals.
    - `.into()` expected-type threading at more positions (match arm bodies, struct-literal field values, if/match final expressions).
    - Codegen `?` operator — currently hits the `_ => const 0` fallback in `compile_expr`. Requires `Result`/`Option` as built-in enum layouts in codegen first (`try_compile_enum_variant` currently only finds user-declared enums).

- [x] **Extend operator lowering to comparison, equality, bitwise (slice 2 of Phase 8).** `src/lowering.rs` now rewrites arithmetic (`+ - * / %`), equality (`== !=`), comparison (`< <= > >=`), bitwise (`& | ^ << >> ~`), and both unary forms of `not` (`!` on bool → `bool.not`, `~` on int → `T.not`). Short-circuit `&&`/`||` and range `..`/`..=` stay as `Binary` deliberately. Interpreter `dispatch_lowered_op` and codegen `compile_assoc_call` gained method-name maps for the new ops. `infer_closure_return_type` returns bool for `eq`/`ne`/`lt`/`le`/`gt`/`ge` and Self for bitwise/arithmetic/`not`. v1 comparison shortcut: `<`/`<=`/`>`/`>=` lower directly to `T.lt`/`T.le`/`T.gt`/`T.ge` (bool-returning), sidestepping the `Ordering` enum detour until `Ord.cmp`'s own callable path is fleshed out. Eq/Ord impls now register `ne`/`lt`/`le`/`gt`/`ge` as user-callable methods alongside `eq`/`cmp`, and type-receiver dispatch in both interpreter (`eval_method_call`) and codegen (`compile_method_call`) handles every operator method name by delegating to the shared lowered-op fast-path. User-defined `impl Eq for MyStruct` and `impl Ord for MyStruct` are now carved out of the resolver's operator-trait restriction — the lowering pass emits `Call(Path([TypeName, method]))` for Named operand types with a registered impl, and `TypeCheckResult.trait_impls` exposes the (trait, target) set so lowering can check without re-querying `env`. `!=` on user types desugars to `!T.eq(a, b)` (mirroring Rust's PartialEq default) so user impls only need to provide `eq`. Remaining follow-ups:
  - `?` codegen (task #9) remains the orthogonal blocker for full Phase 8 close-out — see the standalone entry below.

- [~] **`?` operator codegen for `Result` and `Option`.** Steps 1–4, 6, 7 shipped 2026-04-28; Step 5 deferred (needs new runtime). Ordered implementation steps:
  1. [x] **Built-in enum layout registration in codegen.** `Codegen::seed_builtin_enum_layouts` registers `Result[T, E]` (Err=0, Ok=1) and `Option[T]` (None=0, Some=1) as `{ i64 tag, i64 w0 }` layouts in `enum_layouts`. Variant-extract helpers find them via the same path as user enums.
  2. [x] **Variant constructor lowering.** `Ok(x)` / `Err(e)` / `Some(x)` / `None` route through the user-enum variant construction path; verified by all 8 `?`-codegen E2E tests round-tripping the values.
  3. [x] **`?` lowering at the call site.** `compile_question` emits the tag load + branch on `is_failure` (tag == 0) vs OK; failure block now calls `emit_scope_cleanup` (drains the full `scope_cleanup_actions` stack — Vec/String buffers, RC values, Map handles) before constructing `{ 0, w0 }` and returning. Pinned by `asan_question_drains_scope_cleanup_on_err` and `asan_question_drains_scope_cleanup_on_none` in `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs`.
  4. [x] **Cross-error-type conversion.** New `Program.question_conversions: HashMap<(usize, usize), String>` side-table populated by `lowering::lower_program` from `TypeCheckResult.question_conversions`. `Codegen::question_conversions` mirrors it; `compile_question` looks up the outer `?` span, calls the user-impl `Target.from` LLVM function on the err payload, and uses the converted value as the propagated `w0`. Pinned by `test_e2e_question_cross_error_from_conversion` (struct-payload err type, `from()` doubles `code` field, output `14` confirms the conversion ran).
  5. [x] **`error_return_trace` push at each `?` site.** ✓ DONE (2026-04-28) — runtime extern `karac_error_trace_push(file_ptr, file_len, line, col)` + `karac_error_trace_clear()` backed by a global `Mutex<ErrorTraceState>` ring buffer (depth 64); atexit handler prints to stderr at process exit in the same format as the interpreter's text mode. Note: switched from `thread_local!` to a global mutex because Rust's TLS is torn down before C atexit handlers run. Filename threading through codegen still deferred — v1 prints `<line>:<col>` only. 3 codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs`. See the standalone follow-up entry below for the deep description.
  6. [x] **Pattern-match interop regression test.** `test_e2e_question_result_match_interop` matches against built-in `Result` variants in both arms after a `?` propagates earlier in the call chain. User-enum match lowering reads the same enum layout table, so the built-in registration in Step 1 made this work transparently.
  7. [x] **End-to-end tests.** 8 codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs`: `option_some_propagates`, `option_none_propagates`, `result_ok_propagates`, `result_err_propagates`, `result_match_interop`, `question_in_loop`, `question_triggers_scope_cleanup`, `question_cross_error_from_conversion`. 2 ASAN tests in `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs` covering the cleanup-on-`?` contract for Result and Option. Files: `src/codegen.rs`, `src/lowering.rs`, `src/ast.rs`, `tests/codegen.rs`, `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs`.

- [x] **`?` codegen follow-up: `error_return_trace` push from compiled binaries.** Shipped 2026-04-28. Runtime side (`runtime/src/lib.rs`): two new externs `karac_error_trace_push(file_ptr, file_len, line, col)` and `karac_error_trace_clear()`, backed by a global `Mutex<ErrorTraceState>` (depth-64 ring buffer). Storage is mutex-protected, *not* `thread_local!` — TLS gets torn down before C `atexit` handlers run, which manifests as a "cannot access a Thread Local Storage value during or after destruction" panic; the global mutex stays valid throughout `atexit`. The first `push` lazily registers a printer via libc's `atexit`; the printer emits to stderr in the interpreter's text format (`Error return trace:\n  <file>:<line>:<col>\n...`). Codegen side (`src/codegen.rs`): `compile_question` emits a `karac_error_trace_push` at the failure block before `emit_scope_cleanup`, and a `karac_error_trace_clear` at the OK block. CLI needs no change — the binary's stderr passes through. 3 codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs`. **Filename threading follow-up shipped 2026-04-28** (round 2 — see git history `ba2dc9a`): added `compile_to_object_with_options` / `compile_to_ir_with_options` taking `Option<&str>` source filename (existing two-arg APIs delegate, so all 20+ in-tree callers keep working unchanged). `Codegen` carries the filename and a memoized `(PointerValue, len)` for a deduped global string materialized lazily on the first `?` site (`ensure_source_filename_global`). `emit_error_trace_push` consults that helper instead of always passing `(null, 0)`. CLI: `cmd_build` passes the source filename it already has on hand. 1 new E2E test (`test_e2e_question_trace_includes_source_filename_when_threaded`). **JSON / JSONL trace output mode shipped 2026-05-08** (close-out below). All planned follow-ups closed; entry flipped `[~]` → `[x]`.

  *JSON / JSONL trace output mode — close-out (2026-05-08).*

- [x] **Codegen for user impl-block methods.** Added passes over `Item::ImplBlock` in `CodegenCtx::compile` that declare and compile each method as an LLVM function named `Type.method`; `self`-taking methods get `self` prepended as an owned `Type` parameter (synthetic `Function` built by `make_impl_method_function`). `compile_assoc_call` and `compile_method_call` now fall through to `get_function("Type.method")` and call it, routing both the operator-lowered `Call(Path([T, m]))` shape and source-form receiver calls `obj.method(args)`. `compile_expr` gained an `ExprKind::SelfValue` arm that loads from the `self` local; `field_index_for` maps `self.field` via `var_type_names["self"]`. `ref self` / `mut ref self` deferred — all current call sites (Eq/Ord, constructors) take owned receivers, and wiring reference passing needs synthesizing `TypeKind::Ref` around the target type plus coupling with the existing `fn_param_ref` call-site logic. Generic methods on impl blocks also deferred (matches the existing generic-fn monomorphization gap).

- [x] **Associated types in traits.** `type Item` declarations in trait bodies, `type Item = T` bindings in impl blocks, `where C.Item = i64` equality constraints, and bounds on associated type declarations (`type Output: Display`) — all parsed and validated. **New in this CR:** `Type::AssocProjection { param, assoc }` added to the `Type` enum; `lower_path_type` recognises `I.Item` where `I` is a generic type parameter; `TypeEnv::impl_assoc_types` stores `(type_name, assoc_name) → Type` from impl blocks; `TypeChecker::resolve_assoc_projections` post-resolves after `substitute_type_params` at generic call sites; `contains_type_param` and `types_compatible` treat `AssocProjection` permissively (like `TypeParam`). 12 typechecker tests added. Open: `Iterator` / `IntoIterator` trait definitions (Step 2); `for` loop desugaring through `IntoIterator`; method dispatch on `T: Trait` via associated type return types.

- [ ] **Effect-polymorphic `Iterator.next()` + stdlib `io.lines()` / `fs.read_lines()`.** `Iterator.next()` carries a `with _` ceiling (design.md § Iterator Traits), so one trait covers pure, blocking, suspending, and remote sources — no separate `Stream` type. Implementation touches (1) typechecker: source effects on `next()` thread through `self` into adaptor result types, unioned with any closure effects per design.md § Iterator Adaptors; adaptor signatures stay as currently written (no new `E_src` slot). (2) stdlib: `io.lines() -> impl Iterator[Item = String] with reads(Stdin), blocks`, `fs.read_lines(path) -> Result[impl Iterator[Item = String] with reads(Fs), blocks, IoError]` (outer `Result` for open-time failure, per-line errors surface via `Item = Result[String, IoError]` on a fallible variant). EOF/termination keeps `Option[Item]` (S3c) — per-item errors live in the `Item` type. Error-strategy combinators (`retry_on`, `skip_errors`, `take_until_error`) deferred until a concrete use case lands. Book note added to ch10.

- [ ] **`core`/`alloc`/`std` standard library split.** Implement three-layer stdlib: `core` (always available, no OS/allocator), `alloc` (requires heap allocator), `std` (requires OS). Profile mapping: `kernel` → core only, `embedded` → core + optional alloc, default → all three. `no_alloc` context: `f"..."` interpolation unavailable, provide `format_into!` for fixed-size buffer formatting.

- [ ] **Volatile memory access (MMIO).** Implement `volatile_read[T: Copy]` and `volatile_write[T: Copy]` as `unsafe` intrinsics. Implement `VolatileCell[T: Copy]` stdlib wrapper. Effect integration: `volatile_read` → `reads(Hardware)`, `volatile_write` → `writes(Hardware)`.

- [ ] **Inline assembly (`asm` / `global_asm`).** Implement `asm` as a keyword expression inside `unsafe` blocks with the LLVM operand model. Per design.md § Inline Assembly (v60 item 21). Operand forms: `in(constraint) expr`, `out(constraint) binding | _`, `lateout(constraint) binding`, `inout(constraint) lvalue` and `inout(constraint) expr => binding`, `inlateout(...)`, `const expr` (compile-time integer substituted into the template), `sym path` (Kāra function/static linker symbol), and the ABI clobber form `clobber_abi("C", "system")`. Constraints accept `reg`, architecture-specific register classes (`reg_byte`, `freg`, `vreg`, ...), and named registers (`"eax"`, `"r0"`, ...). Options: `nomem`, `nostack`, `preserves_flags`, `pure`, `readonly`, `volatile`, `att_syntax`, and `raw` (disables `{...}` template substitution; no operands allowed when set). Effect integration: default → `reads(Hardware) + writes(Hardware)`; `options(nomem, nostack)` → no hardware effects; `options(pure, nomem, nostack)` → no effects. The `clobber_abi(...)` form expands at codegen to the per-target caller-saved register set so call instructions inside asm don't require manual register enumeration. `sym` operands lower to LLVM `s` constraints with the resolved linker symbol; `const` operands lower to the LLVM `i` constraint with the const-evaluated integer. `global_asm` as a top-level item with no operands; symbols defined in `global_asm` are referenced from Kāra via `extern` declarations and inherit the existing FFI effect annotation surface. Deferred (P1+/P2): `label(name) { ... }` blocks (asm goto — design pinned in design.md § Deferred Forms); `#[naked]` functions with `naked_asm` (design pinned in design.md § Deferred Forms — needs coherent integration with effect inference, unsafe-fn, and fn-pointer typing). Test plan when the implementation lands: per-target register-class round-trips, `clobber_abi("C")` round-trip with a stub `extern "C"` callee, `sym` reference to a Kāra `fn` with the right linker name, `const` substitution with arithmetic constant expressions, `raw` template with literal `{ }`, options-driven effect-set computation. (P1 — design surface lands at v1 per v60 item 21; implementation post-v1.)

- [ ] **`Atomic[T]` and memory ordering.** Implement `Atomic[T]` as a `shared struct` with `load`, `store`, `swap`, `compare_exchange`, `fetch_add`, `fetch_and`, `fetch_or` methods. `T` must be `Copy`. Implement `Ordering` enum (`Relaxed`, `Acquire`, `Release`, `AcqRel`, `SeqCst`). Implement `compiler_fence` (safe) and `fence` (unsafe). Available in `embedded` profile for ISR-to-main communication. **Effect-checker integration (design.md § Effect Model, under Atomic Operations):** every atomic method call (`load`, `store`, `swap`, `compare_exchange`, `fetch_add`, `fetch_and`, `fetch_or`) must contribute zero effects to the enclosing function's inferred set — the checker's transfer function treats them as no-ops for effect purposes. Memory-ordering arguments are discarded at the effect layer and forwarded to codegen. `lock` blocks are effect-transparent: their body's effects flow to the enclosing function unchanged; the lock itself contributes nothing. **Auto-concurrency integration (Phase 6):** treat atomic-only function bodies as conflict-free — two such functions may run in parallel on the same atomic value, because atomic ops are linearizable. The Phase 2 `Rc → Arc` promotion analysis handles atomic fields inside a `shared struct` uniformly with non-atomic fields — no special case needed.

- [ ] **`#[interrupt]` handler ABI.** Implement `#[interrupt(NAME)]` attribute: forces interrupt calling convention, emits vector table placement, forbids direct calls from normal code, implicitly applies ISR profile restrictions (no heap, no panics). Platform crates define `Interrupt` enum mapping names to vector positions. `extern "interrupt"` is the low-level form.

- [x] **Try block grammar — `try { ... }` (parser/AST only; typechecker pipeline is P1).** Spec at `design.md § Error Handling > Try Blocks (try { ... })` (v60 item 42). v1 work is parser-only. Slices: (1) Lexer — no change; the `try` keyword is already reserved per §1.1 of syntax.md (item 9 of v60). (2) Parser — extend `parse_prefix` (or wherever block-shaped prefix expressions are dispatched) so a `try` token in expression position consumes the `try` keyword and parses the following `BLOCK` per syntax.md §5.3 `TRY_EXPR`. The body is parsed with the existing `parse_block` function — try blocks share BLOCK semantics for statements and tail expression. AST: new `ExprKind::Try { body: Block, span: Span }` variant. (3) Resolver — walk the body normally (try blocks introduce no new name-resolution scope beyond what the inner `BLOCK` already does); record the construct on the AST for downstream typechecker consumption. (4) v1 typechecker stub — when the typechecker visits an `ExprKind::Try`, emit `error[E_TRY_BLOCK_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET]: try block syntax is recognized but the typechecker pipeline lands in P1 — extract the body into a helper function returning Result for now`. The diagnostic includes the block's source span and the help line; the typechecker still walks the body to type-check inner expressions (so unrelated errors inside the body still surface), but the block's overall type is recorded as the error sentinel and downstream uses propagate the same diagnostic. (5) Effect-checker — `try { ... }` contributes no effects of its own; effects from the body flow to the enclosing function as they would in any block. (6) Formatter — emit `try ` followed by the formatted block body. Test coverage: positive — `let r: Result[i32, MyError] = try { 42 };` parses and registers; nested try blocks parse; try block with internal `?` parses (the inner `?` is parsed by ordinary expression machinery); try block as the right-hand side of an assignment, function call argument, return expression all parse. Negative — the v1 stub diagnostic fires at every typechecker-visit of a try block; bare `try ;` (missing block) is rejected at parse. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) for parser/AST/resolver/v1-stub diagnostics. Cross-reference: `deferred.md § P1 § Try Blocks — ?-Retargeting and Error-Type Unification` for the P1 implementation slice (the actual `?`-target stack, error-type unification, From-chain coercion, T/E inference, defer/errdefer integration).

- [→ P1] **Try blocks — `?`-retargeting and error-type unification.** Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § Try Blocks — `?`-Retargeting and Error-Type Unification](deferred.md#try-blocks--retargeting-and-error-type-unification). The v1 grammar entry above lands the parser, AST, resolver, and use-site stub diagnostic; this P1 entry covers the implementation: (1) `?`-target stack (innermost-`try`-frame resolution); (2) per-block error-type unification with From-chain coercion; (3) block-level `T`/`E` inference flowing into the enclosing context; (4) empty / diverging-tail special cases; (5) `defer` / `errdefer` per-block scope integration; (6) closure-boundary rule (a `?` inside a closure body inside a `try` block does not target the outer `try`); (7) diagnostic enrichment naming the return target at `?` sites that fail unification. Replaces the v1 stub diagnostic with the real typechecker pipeline.

- [x] **Trait alias grammar — `trait NAME = bounds;` (parser/AST only; expansion is P1).** Spec at `design.md § Trait Aliases` (v60 item 40). v1 work is parser-only. Slices: (1) Lexer — no change (uses existing `trait`, `=`, `+`, `;`, identifier tokens). (2) Parser — extend `parse_trait_def` to peek for `=` after the optional `[GENERIC_PARAMS]`. If `=` is present, parse a `+`-separated `TRAIT_BOUND` list followed by an optional `WHERE_CLAUSE` and a terminating `;` per syntax.md §3.4 `TRAIT_ALIAS_DEF`. The alias's bound-list parser reuses the existing `parse_trait_bound` function used by supertrait parsing. (3) AST — new `Item::TraitAlias { name: String, generic_params: Vec<GenericParam>, bounds: Vec<TraitBound>, where_clause: Option<WhereClause>, vis: Visibility, attributes: Vec<Attribute>, span: Span }` variant. The shape is deliberately parallel to `Item::Trait` (same generic-params, same where-clause shape) so resolver reuse is mechanical. (4) Resolver — register the trait alias in the trait namespace alongside ordinary traits. The resolver records the alias's bound list verbatim — no expansion at v1. (5) v1 typechecker stub — when a use site (a bound, a `where`-clause predicate, or a `dyn` type) resolves to a trait alias, emit `error[E_TRAIT_ALIAS_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET]: trait alias 'NAME' is recognized but not yet expanded; the implementation lands in P1 — write the bound list explicitly for now`. The diagnostic includes the alias declaration's source span and the alias's bound list copy-pasted into the error so users see the workaround inline. (6) `impl TraitAlias for T { ... }` rejection — already at v1 since it would otherwise fall into the typechecker; emit `error[E_IMPL_TRAIT_ALIAS]: cannot implement trait alias 'NAME'; implement each component trait separately` with the bound-list enumeration. (7) Effect-bound-in-body rejection — at parse time, scan the alias's bound list for any effect predicate (`reads(R)`, `writes(R)`, etc.) and emit `error[E_EFFECT_IN_TRAIT_ALIAS]: effect predicates do not belong in a trait alias body; use an effect group declaration`. (8) Formatter — emit the alias declaration as `trait NAME[generic_params] = bound1 + bound2 + ... [where ...];`. Test coverage: positive — `trait Numeric = Copy + Add + Sub + Mul + Div;` parses and registers; generic alias `trait IteratorOver[T] = Iterator[Item = T];` parses; alias with where-clause `trait OrderedFloat[T] = Ord where T: Numeric + Bounded;` parses; visibility `pub trait Foo = Bar;` parses; multiple aliases in one module register independently. Negative — empty bound list `trait Foo = ;` rejected at parse; effect predicate in body rejected with named diagnostic; `impl Foo for T { ... }` against an alias rejected with named diagnostic + bound-list enumeration; use-site of declared alias produces the v1-stub diagnostic. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) for parser/AST/resolver/v1-stub diagnostics. Cross-reference: `deferred.md § P1 § Trait Aliases — Expansion` for the P1 implementation slice (the actual bound-substitution machinery, cycle detection, where-clause propagation, `dyn` handling, cross-package re-exports).

- [→ P1] **Trait aliases — expansion (substitution, cycle detection, dyn handling).** Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` § P1 § Trait Aliases — Expansion](deferred.md#trait-aliases--expansion-trait-numeric--copy--add--sub--). The v1 grammar entry above lands the parser, AST, resolver registration, and use-site stub diagnostic; this P1 entry covers the implementation of bound expansion at every use site, transitive flattening across nested aliases, generic-argument propagation, alias-`where`-clause gating, impl-of-alias rejection with bound enumeration, cycle detection (Tarjan SCC over the alias-mentions-alias graph), `dyn`-of-alias acceptance for single-method-trait expansions, effect-bound-in-body rejection, and cross-package re-export resolution. Replaces the v1 stub diagnostic with the real expansion machinery.

- [ ] **Explicit discriminants on payload variants — `enum Op { Connect { addr: u32 } = 0x05, ... }`.** Spec at `design.md § Explicit Discriminants on Payload Variants` (v60 item 43). Full v1 implementation (no P1 carve-out — there is no companion runtime-surface lift; the explicit values are declarations only). Slices: (1) Parser — extend the `VARIANT` rule per syntax.md §3.3 so each of the three variant forms (unit, struct, tuple) optionally accepts `"=" CONST_EXPR` after the payload portion. The const-expression parser is the existing `parse_const_expr` already used by module-level bindings — literals, arithmetic on literals, and references to other module-level integer constants. AST: extend the existing variant node (likely `EnumVariant { name, kind: VariantKind, discriminant: Option<ConstExpr>, span }`) with a `discriminant` field; the field is `Option<ConstExpr>` so the field-less-no-explicit-value case (`Audio,`) round-trips the same way it does today. The formatter emits `= LITERAL` after the variant body (struct `{ ... }` or tuple `(...)`) when present, with one space on either side of `=` for parity with the existing field-less formatting (`Audio = 0x01`). (2) Resolver — const-expression evaluation runs at item-resolution time so per-enum duplicate-value detection happens before downstream phases. (3) Typechecker — three new checks, all at the enum-decl site after const-eval has folded each `discriminant` to an integer literal: (a) **All-or-nothing rule.** Walk the variant list; if some variants have `discriminant.is_some()` and some don't, emit `error[E_PARTIAL_EXPLICIT_DISCRIMINANTS]: enum 'NAME' mixes explicit and implicit discriminants; declare a value on every variant or remove the explicit values and rely on declaration order` with the first explicit + first implicit variant spans labeled. (b) **Range check per `#[repr(intN)]`.** When `#[repr(intN)]` is present, every explicit value must fit the repr type's range — otherwise `error[E_DISCRIMINANT_OUT_OF_RANGE]: discriminant 'N' on variant 'V' does not fit in 'intN' (range '[MIN, MAX]')` with the offending value's span. Under `#[repr(C)]` without an `#[repr(intN)]` companion, the range is the platform's `c_int` (signed `i32` on every supported target at v1; the diagnostic should name `c_int` rather than `i32` to make the C-ABI-driven choice explicit to the reader). (c) **Duplicate-value rejection.** Build a `HashMap<i64, Span>` over the resolved values; on any insert that collides, emit `error[E_DUPLICATE_DISCRIMINANT]: variant 'V2' has the same discriminant value 'N' as variant 'V1'` with both spans labeled. The diagnostic uses the *resolved* integer value so const-expression aliasing (e.g., two variants pointing at the same module-level constant) is caught. (d) **`#[repr]` requirement on payload variants.** If the enum has at least one variant with both a payload (`VariantKind::Struct` or `VariantKind::Tuple`) and a `discriminant`, and the enum's `#[repr]` set does not contain `#[repr(intN)]` or `#[repr(C)]`, emit `error[E_PAYLOAD_DISCRIMINANT_REQUIRES_REPR]: explicit discriminants on payload variants require '#[repr(intN)]' or '#[repr(C)]'; without one, the discriminant location is unspecified and the value commitment is unreachable` at the first offending payload-variant's discriminant span. The check rejects `#[repr(transparent)]`, `#[repr(packed)]`, `#[repr(align(N))]` as repr forms that satisfy the requirement (none commits to a discriminant position). Field-less variants with `= N` under a `#[repr]`-less enum continue to be legal per the existing C-like-enum rule. (4) Runtime-surface preservation. The existing payload-enum exclusion from `.discriminant()` / `TryFrom[intN]` / `.values()` continues to apply unchanged — explicit discriminants on payload variants do not lift the exclusion. Calls to `.discriminant()` on a payload enum (with or without explicit discriminants) continue to fail with the existing diagnostic that points at the manual-`tag` workaround; the design.md cross-reference now mentions the explicit-discriminant declaration form as the source of the literal values the manual `tag` method's match arms reference. (5) Effect-checker / ownership-checker integration — none. The discriminant declarations are pure data attached to variant decls and contribute no effects, no consume tracking, no reference flow. (6) Codegen — the explicit values on payload variants are *declarations*, not layout commitments. At v1 the LLVM lowering of payload enums is unchanged: the compiler may still elide tags via niche optimization, store the discriminant non-contiguously, and otherwise treat the variant set as it does today. The declarations exist for documentation, semver-lock, and as the literal values a hand-written `tag` method's arms reference. Field-less explicit-discriminant enums under `#[repr(intN)]` continue to lower with the declared integer at the runtime-surface position, exactly as today. Test coverage: positive — `#[repr(u8)] enum Op { Reset = 0x01, Connect { addr: u32 } = 0x05, Send(Bytes) = 0x06, Disconnect = 0xFF }` parses, resolves, type-checks, formats; `#[repr(C)] enum E { A = 1, B { x: i32 } = 2 }` accepted; signed-repr negative values `#[repr(i8)] enum E { A = -1, B(u32) = 5 }` accepted; a manual `fn tag(ref self) -> u8` calling `match self { Op.Connect { .. } => 0x05, ... }` type-checks normally and is the documented consumption pattern. Negative — partial-explicit (`enum E { A = 1, B(u32) }`) rejected with `E_PARTIAL_EXPLICIT_DISCRIMINANTS`; out-of-range `#[repr(u8)] enum E { A = 256 }` rejected with `E_DISCRIMINANT_OUT_OF_RANGE`; duplicate values `#[repr(u8)] enum E { A = 1, B(u32) = 1 }` rejected with `E_DUPLICATE_DISCRIMINANT` naming both variants; payload variant with explicit discriminant on a `#[repr]`-less enum rejected with `E_PAYLOAD_DISCRIMINANT_REQUIRES_REPR`; same on `#[repr(transparent)]` rejected; `.discriminant()` call on a payload enum (regardless of explicit discriminants) continues to be rejected with the existing payload-exclusion diagnostic. Phase target: 5.2 (parser/AST/resolver/typechecker). No P1 companion — option (b) of v60 item 43 deliberately scopes the v1 work to declarations only; a future `#[derive(Discriminant)]` synthesizing `tag` from the declared values is additive-later and is not on the v1 critical path.

- [ ] **`#[derive(Default)]` and `#[default]` on enum variants.** Spec at `design.md § #[derive(Default)] and #[default] on enum variants` (v60 item 44). Full v1 implementation (no P1 carve-out — option (a) is fully achievable at v1; payload-bearing default variants are deliberately deferred indefinitely as additive-later). Slices: (1) Parser — extend the `VARIANT` rule per syntax.md §3.3 so each of the three variant forms accepts a leading `[ ATTRIBUTES ]` (the existing attribute parser handles every form already; the rule extension just records the parsed attributes on the variant AST node). AST: extend the existing `EnumVariant` node with `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` if not already present; the field defaults to empty so the no-attributes case round-trips today. (2) Attribute recognition — the parser-side attribute table (syntax.md §8) gains `#[default]`. The attribute carries no arguments; `#[default(...)]` and `#[default = ...]` are rejected at the attribute parser as malformed (existing `E_MALFORMED_ATTRIBUTE_ARGS` machinery, with the diagnostic naming `#[default]` and saying it accepts no arguments). (3) Position checker (resolver / pre-typechecker pass) — `#[default]` is legal **only** on an enum-variant decl. Applying it to a struct, struct field, function, type alias, distinct type, trait, trait method, impl block, const, or extern declaration emits `error[E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_INVALID_POSITION]: '#[default]' is only valid on a unit enum variant under '#[derive(Default)]'` with the offending item's span. The check runs before the per-derive validators so the diagnostic is location-focused rather than coming out of the derive machinery. (4) Derive registration — `Default` joins the existing derivable-traits table (the same machinery that handles `Eq` / `Clone` / `Debug`). The derive is keyed off `#[derive(Default)]` literal text; it has no derive dependencies (i.e., does not auto-derive any other trait, and is not auto-derived from any other derive). (5) **Struct derive body** — `#[derive(Default)]` on a struct generates `impl[GENERIC_BOUNDS_PROPAGATED] Default for StructName { fn default() -> Self { StructName { f1: F1.default(), f2: F2.default(), ... } } }`. Each field's `default()` resolves through the existing trait-associated-function dispatch. The bound-propagation rule mirrors `#[derive(Eq)]` — the compiler infers the minimal set of generic-param bounds (`T: Default` for every type-param `T` used in any field type) and emits them on the impl block. If any field's type does not implement `Default` (and is not a type-param with a propagatable bound), emit `error[E_DERIVE_DEFAULT_MISSING_FIELD_DEFAULT]: cannot #[derive(Default)] for 'StructName' — field 'name' of type 'T' does not implement 'Default'` with the offending field's span. (6) **Enum derive body** — `#[derive(Default)]` on an enum scans variant attributes for `#[default]` and emits four checks before generating the body: (a) **No marker**: zero variants carry `#[default]` → `error[E_DEFAULT_NO_VARIANT_MARKED]: #[derive(Default)] on enum 'StatusName' requires exactly one variant to be marked with #[default]; consider adding it to the variant that represents the starting state` with the enum-decl span labeled. (b) **Multiple markers**: ≥2 variants carry `#[default]` → `error[E_DEFAULT_MULTIPLE_VARIANTS]: #[derive(Default)] on enum 'EnumName' requires exactly one variant marked with #[default]; found markers on 'V1' and 'V2'` with both attribute spans labeled. (c) **Marked variant has fields**: the marked variant is `VariantKind::Struct` or `VariantKind::Tuple` (not unit) → `error[E_DEFAULT_VARIANT_HAS_PAYLOAD]: #[default] on enum variant 'V' requires a field-less variant; either declare the marked variant as 'V,' (no fields) or write a manual 'impl Default for E' that constructs the desired starting state` with the marked variant's payload span labeled, and the manual-impl skeleton inlined into the help line so the user sees the exact replacement. (d) **All checks pass**: emit `impl Default for EnumName { fn default() -> Self { EnumName.MarkedVariant } }` — a constant-expression body, no field walk, no generic bound propagation needed (the marked variant is field-less). Generic enums are still generic on the impl (`impl[T] Default for Box[T]` if the marker is on a unit variant — no `T: Default` bound, since the marked variant doesn't reference `T`). (7) **`#[default]` requires `#[derive(Default)]` on the enclosing enum** — an enum that does not carry `#[derive(Default)]` but has at least one variant with `#[default]` is rejected with `error[E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_WITHOUT_DERIVE]: '#[default]' on variant 'V' requires the enclosing enum 'E' to carry '#[derive(Default)]'` with both the variant attribute span and the enum-decl span labeled, and a fix-it suggesting `add #[derive(Default)] to enum E`. The check runs at type-decl time after resolver-side derive registration so dead annotations don't accumulate silently. (8) Effect-checker / ownership-checker integration — none. The derived `default` is a constructor with no effects on user-defined resources beyond what the field types' own `default()` methods carry (struct case) or zero (enum unit-variant case). (9) Composition — verify orthogonality with `#[non_exhaustive]` (the variant set may grow without changing the default), explicit discriminants from item 43 (a marked variant may also carry `= N`; the two are independent), and `#[deprecated]` on the same variant (legal — emits the existing deprecation warning at every reference site, including the synthesized `default()` body, which surfaces the marker's attribution to the user). Test coverage: positive — `#[derive(Default)] struct Point { x: i64, y: i64 }` generates `Point { x: 0, y: 0 }`; `#[derive(Default)] struct Pair[T] { a: T, b: T }` generates `impl[T: Default] Default for Pair[T]`; `#[derive(Default)] enum Status { #[default] Pending, Active, Closed }` generates `Status.default() == Status.Pending`; `#[derive(Default)] enum Mode[T] { #[default] Idle, Custom(T) }` generates `Mode[T].default() == Mode.Idle` with no `T: Default` bound; `#[non_exhaustive] #[derive(Default)] enum M { #[default] A, B }` accepted; `#[repr(u8)] #[derive(Default)] enum Op { #[default] Reset = 0x01, Send = 0x02 }` accepted with `Op.default() == Op.Reset`. Negative — `#[derive(Default)] enum E { A, B }` (no marker) rejected with `E_DEFAULT_NO_VARIANT_MARKED`; `#[derive(Default)] enum E { #[default] A, #[default] B }` rejected with `E_DEFAULT_MULTIPLE_VARIANTS` naming both; `#[derive(Default)] enum E { #[default] A(i32), B }` rejected with `E_DEFAULT_VARIANT_HAS_PAYLOAD` plus the manual-impl-skeleton help line; `#[derive(Default)] struct S { v: NonDefault }` (where `NonDefault` does not impl Default) rejected with `E_DERIVE_DEFAULT_MISSING_FIELD_DEFAULT` naming the offending field; `#[default] struct S { ... }` rejected with `E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_INVALID_POSITION`; `#[default]` on a struct field rejected with the same diagnostic; `enum E { #[default] A, B }` (no derive) rejected with `E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_WITHOUT_DERIVE`; `#[derive(Default)]` plus a manual `impl Default for T` rejected with the existing duplicate-impl diagnostic; `#[default(some)]` and `#[default = "x"]` rejected as malformed-args. Phase target: 5.2 (parser/AST/attribute-position-checker/derive). Cross-reference: design.md § `#[derive(Default)]` and `#[default]` on enum variants; syntax.md §8 attribute table row for `#[default]`.

- [ ] **Codegen hint attributes — `#[inline]`, `#[inline(always)]`, `#[inline(never)]`, `#[cold]`.** Spec at `design.md § Codegen Hint Attributes` (v60 item 38). Slices: (1) Attribute parser (Phase 5.2) — recognise the four attributes per syntax.md §8. `#[inline]` parses with no args; `#[inline(always)]` and `#[inline(never)]` parse with a single keyword arg (`always` / `never`); `#[cold]` parses with no args. (2) AST — capture inlining axis as `Option<InlineHint { Default | Always | Never }>` and a separate `is_cold: bool` on the existing `Function` node and the trait-method declaration node. Trait-decl propagation parallels `#[track_caller]`: the hint applies to every impl unless that impl carries its own override (last-writer-wins). (3) Conflict checker (Phase 5.2) — reject `#[inline]` + `#[inline(always)]`, `#[inline]` + `#[inline(never)]`, `#[inline(always)]` + `#[inline(never)]` with `error[E_INLINE_HINT_CONFLICT]` naming both attribute spans; reject `#[cold]` + `#[inline(always)]` with `error[E_COLD_INLINE_ALWAYS_CONFLICT]`. `#[cold]` + `#[inline]` and `#[cold]` + `#[inline(never)]` are accepted. Duplicate same-attribute on one fn falls through to the existing `E_DUPLICATE_ATTRIBUTE` diagnostic. (4) Position checker (Phase 5.2) — reject on closure expressions (`error[E_CODEGEN_HINT_ON_CLOSURE]`), on foreign-function declarations inside `unsafe extern { }` (`error[E_CODEGEN_HINT_ON_EXTERN_DECL]`), and on entire `impl` blocks (per-method only at v1). Allowed positions: free `fn`, methods inside inherent and trait `impl`, trait method declarations, `extern "C" fn` definitions (Kāra-side body), `impl Drop for T` destructors. (5) Codegen (Phase 7) — at LLVM IR emission time, attach the corresponding LLVM function attribute: `#[inline]` → `inlinehint`, `#[inline(always)]` → `alwaysinline`, `#[inline(never)]` → `noinline`, `#[cold]` → `cold`. The attributes are advisory at the LLVM level; LLVM honors them faithfully under all standard optimization levels but the Kāra-side compiler does not depend on them being honored — they are reported behavior, not guaranteed semantics. (6) Effect-system orthogonality — codegen hints contribute no effects to the enclosing function and do not alter the inferred set; an inlined body's effects have already been folded into the caller's inferred effects via normal effect inference. (7) `#[track_caller]` interaction — orthogonal; both attributes coexist without diagnostic. When a `#[track_caller] #[inline]` function is inlined at a call site, the hidden caller-location parameter folds into the receiver function's site (LLVM-side; no Kāra-pass change). (8) Silent-leave-out-of-line policy — when `#[inline(always)]` cannot inline (recursive call site, function-pointer call, cross-package without LTO IR available, or function body containing inlining-blocking constructs like large `asm` blocks or `#[interrupt]` ISR handlers), no diagnostic is emitted at v1. Future tooling (`karac build --perf-report`) will surface "had no inlining sites" as a hint, but the build never fails on it. Test coverage (parser/checker — Phase 5.2): each attribute parses; each conflict pair rejects with the named diagnostic; closure-expression rejection; extern-decl rejection; entire-impl-block rejection; trait-decl propagation honored by impls that don't override. Test coverage (codegen — Phase 7): emitted LLVM IR carries the expected `alwaysinline` / `noinline` / `inlinehint` / `cold` attribute; a recursive `#[inline(always)]` function still compiles cleanly; a `#[inline(always)]` function used through a function pointer still compiles cleanly; `#[cold]` placement bias visible in IR via the `cold` attribute on the function. Phase target: 5.2 (parser, AST, conflict/position checks); 7 (LLVM attribute emission). Cross-reference: design.md § Codegen Hint Attributes; syntax.md §8 attribute table rows.

- [ ] **Critical sections.** Implement `critical_section.acquire()` returning an RAII `CriticalSectionGuard` that disables/re-enables interrupts. Guard type is `#[must_use]`.

- [ ] **`std.secret` module — `Secret[T]` wrapper.** Spec is in `design.md § Secret Type (Secret[T])`. Stdlib + compiler work split:
  1. [ ] **Stdlib types.** Implement `Secret[T]` (struct wrapping `T`, private field, `Secret.new(t: T) -> Secret[T]` constructor); `ConstantTimeEq` trait (`fn ct_eq(ref self, other: ref Self) -> bool`) with impls for `String`, `Vec[u8]`, `[u8; N]`, integer primitives; `Zeroize` trait (`fn zeroize(mut ref self)`) with impls for the same set. All three in `std.secret`, not prelude.
  2. [ ] **Access methods on `Secret[T]`.** `.expose() -> ref T`, `.expose_mut() -> mut ref T`, `.clone() -> Secret[T] where T: Clone` (re-wraps), `.ct_eq(ref self, other: ref Secret[T]) -> bool where T: ConstantTimeEq`. No `.into_inner()`, no `Deref`/`Borrow`/`AsRef`.
  3. [ ] **`Drop` impl.** `impl Drop for Secret[T] where T: Zeroize` — calls `T::zeroize(&mut self.inner)` before the field destructor runs. Effect checker must allow this specific `Drop` impl to invoke `zeroize`; the call is effect-free.
  4. [ ] **Compiler-side trait blocklist.** Resolver/typechecker rejects user `impl Debug for Secret[T]`, `impl Display for Secret[T]`, `impl Serialize for Secret[T]`, `impl Deserialize for Secret[T]`, `impl PartialEq for Secret[T]`, `impl Eq for Secret[T]`, `impl PartialOrd for Secret[T]`, `impl Ord for Secret[T]`, `impl Hash for Secret[T]`, `impl Deref for Secret[T]`, `impl Borrow[T] for Secret[T]`, `impl AsRef[T] for Secret[T]`, `impl Copy for Secret[T]`. Diagnostic code `E_SECRET_TRAIT_FORBIDDEN` with a pointer to the design.md section. `#[derive(...)]` of any of those on `Secret[T]` directly is rejected with the same diagnostic.
  5. [ ] **Derive codegen — containing types.** When `#[derive(Debug)]` / `#[derive(Display)]` is applied to a struct or enum that contains a `Secret[T]` field (direct or nested through non-`Secret` types), the generated impl emits the field as the literal string `<redacted>` instead of recursing into `T`'s Debug/Display. Implement by detecting `Secret[_]` in the derive's field-walk pass.
  6. [ ] **Derive codegen — Serialize rejection.** `#[derive(Serialize)]` on a type containing `Secret[T]` (direct or nested) is a compile error `E_SECRET_SERIALIZE_DERIVE` with a diagnostic suggesting a manual `Serialize` impl calling `.serialize_expose()` or a non-secret mirror type. Implement in the derive expansion pass.
  7. [ ] **Explicit serialization methods.** `Secret[T]` exposes `fn serialize_expose[S: Serializer](ref self, s: mut ref S) -> Result[S.Ok, S.Error] where T: Serialize` and `fn deserialize_wrap[D: Deserializer](d: mut ref D) -> Result[Secret[T], D.Error] where T: Deserialize`. These are the only wire-transit paths; they are explicit and greppable.
  8. [ ] **Tests.** `tests/typechecker.rs` — every trait blocklist case produces `E_SECRET_TRAIT_FORBIDDEN`. `tests/resolver.rs` — derive rejection on containing struct. `tests/codegen.rs` — derived Debug/Display on a struct `{ name: String, token: Secret[String] }` prints `token: <redacted>`; Drop runs zeroize on the inner `String`'s heap buffer before the allocator sees the free. Integration test in `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs` under ASAN verifying zeroize behavior end-to-end.
  9. [ ] **Book coverage (P0 prose).** Add a short security chapter to `docs/book/` introducing `Secret[T]`, constant-time equality, and the "use the wrapper at the type, not at the call site" posture. Keep concise per `feedback_book_prose_concise.md`.

- [x] **Parser/AST: thread `#[attr]` and `pub` through `LayoutDef`, `ExternFunction`, `StructField`.** Preparatory scaffolding shared across several later items. Added `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` + `is_pub: bool` to `LayoutDef` and `ExternFunction`, and `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` to `StructField`. Parser (`parse_layout_def`, `parse_extern_function`, struct-field loops) now captures the `#[...]` and `pub` tokens it previously dropped on the floor. No behavior change yet — each downstream consumer reads these slots: `#[link_name]` / `#[no_mangle]` / `#[used]` / `#[link_section]` on extern (see "Linker control attributes" below), `#[interrupt]` on extern, field-level `#[must_use]` / `#[allow]`, `#[no_rc]` / `@no_rc` on layout, and `pub extern` / `pub layout` for cross-module visibility. Covered by three parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`.

- [x] **Linker control attributes.** ✓ DONE (2026-04-28) — `Codegen::apply_linker_attrs` consumes `#[link_section("name")]`, `#[no_mangle]`, and `#[used]` on `Function` / `ExternFunction` declarations: section directive set on the LLVM symbol; `#[no_mangle]` is a no-op (codegen already uses source names); `#[used]` queues into `Codegen::used_symbols` and `emit_llvm_used` produces the standard `@llvm.used` appending-linkage global in section `llvm.metadata` after all functions are declared. All permitted outside `unsafe`. `#[no_mangle]` controls symbol name only — does not imply `extern "C"` ABI. 5 IR-level tests in `tests/codegen.rs`.

- [ ] **G32 — Serialization / deserialization**. Design `Serialize` / `Deserialize` traits. Depends on G27 — Derive / compiler-synthesized traits. Support JSON at minimum, TOML for config. Attribute syntax for field customization (`#[serialize(rename: "...")]`).

- [x] **`String.sorted()` method.** ✓ DONE (2026-04-27) — `infer_str_method` dispatch in typechecker (`Type::Str` branch before generic fallthrough); `sorted`/`sorted_by` arms in interpreter `eval_method_call` (char-level sort for strings, `value_compare` fallback for arrays). 3 typechecker tests + 4 interpreter tests added.

- [x] **Typechecker accepts `+` between `String` operands.** Both backends already handled it — interpreter via the `(BinOp::Add, Value::String(a), Value::String(b)) => Value::String(a + &b)` arm in `eval_ops`, codegen via `compile_string_binop`'s `BinOp::Add` (fresh malloc + copy both → owned `{data, len, cap}`). The typechecker's `+` operand-type rule listed only numerics, so `a + b` (both `String`) errored `arithmetic operator requires numeric type, found 'String'`. Fixed by adding a String-concat case to `infer_binary`'s `Add` arm: `is_string_concat_operand(left) && is_string_concat_operand(right) -> Str`, where the helper strips `ref` / `mut ref` so all three forms (`String + String`, `String + ref String`, `ref String + String`, incl. `ref + ref`) admit — verified codegen auto-loads the borrowed pointee before the concat (`test_e2e_string_concat_ref_operands`). `String + <non-String>` and `String - String` stay rejected. Surfaced 2026-05-20 (kata-katas/leetcode/71-simplify-path sidestepped via f-strings) and again 2026-05-29 while writing the `Request.query()`/`headers()` E2E handlers. Tests: `tests/typechecker.rs` (`test_string_concat_ok`, `_with_literal_ok`, `_chained_ok`, `_ref_operand_ok`, plus `test_string_subtraction_rejected` and the existing `_no_int_promo` reject) + `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_string_concat_ref_operands`.

- [x] **`String.push(char)` end-to-end + `push_str` interpreter dispatch.** ✓ DONE (2026-05-25) — added `"push"` arm in `infer_str_method` accepting a `Char` argument and returning `Unit`; codegen arm in `compile_vec_method` gated on `string_vars` membership that calls `emit_codepoint_to_utf8` (1–4 UTF-8 bytes via `karac_string_encode_char`) and shares `push_str`'s power-of-two growth + heap-free geometry; interpreter dispatch arm in `method_call_seq.rs` rebinds the receiver via `env.set`. The same commit closed a `push_str` interpreter gap that surfaced as a side observation — `push_str` typechecked + codegened cleanly since 2026-05-23 but `karac run` panicked on the unreachable arm. Both gaps surfaced as the kata-71 follow-up after the bench showed the `out = f"{out}{c}"` self-append shape was O(n²): kata-katas/leetcode/71-simplify-path's auto-par lane went from 28.5 ms → see § Benchmarks for the post-fix delta once it's measured. 8 regression tests added (3 codegen e2e + 2 interpreter + 3 typechecker).

- [ ] **`String` substring / slicing surface.** No way to extract a sub-range of a String today. Existing String method surface enumerated in `src/typechecker/stdlib_seq.rs:172` is `bytes`, `chars`, `sorted`, `sorted_by` — none of those return a `String`. Surfaced 2026-05-20 by kata-katas/leetcode/71-simplify-path, which had to rebuild each path component character-by-character via f-string append instead of slicing the input directly. Open shape question: prefer `s[a..b]` range-indexing (lines up with design.md's range syntax and matches Rust's `&s[a..b]`) over a named `s.substring(a, b)` method. UTF-8-aware bounds check on `a`/`b` against char boundaries; on a non-boundary index, panic with `E_STRING_SLICE_NOT_AT_CHAR_BOUNDARY` (mirrors Rust's panic shape). Returns a fresh `String` (no borrowed-substring zero-copy view at v1 — `ref str` lifetime extension is its own design slice). Until this lands, the available substring-extraction shape is the char-by-char f-string append used by kata #71 (O(n) over the extracted length, identical big-O but with per-char interpolation overhead). The kata is the natural integration test once the surface ships.

- [x] **Built-in `Display` for collections.** Already in place — `type_supports_display` in `typechecker.rs:1596` recursively recognises `Vec[T]`, `Set[T]`, `SortedSet[T]`, `Option[T]`, `Map[K, V]`, `Result[T, E]`, `Tuple[..]`, `Array[T, N]`, `Slice[T]`, `Ref[T]`, `MutRef[T]` when their element types support Display; the `Value::Display` impl in `interpreter.rs:411` mirrors the recursion for runtime formatting. Codegen path lands separately under [phase-7-codegen.md § Phase 7.2 § Display for collections](phase-7-codegen.md). Regression tests in `tests/typechecker.rs` (`fstring_accepts_*`) cover Vec, nested Vec, Map, Set, Option, Result.

### Book Documentation

- [x] **Book appendix: Keywords (P1).** Add `docs/book/src/appendix-a-keywords.md` (mirrors Rust book Appendix A). Enumerate every reserved word in Kāra — `fn`, `let`, `mut`, `ref`, `own`, `pub`, `struct`, `enum`, `shared`, `trait`, `impl`, `where`, `match`, `if`, `else`, `while`, `for`, `loop`, `break`, `continue`, `return`, `yield` (reserved per design.md:6032), `defer`, `errdefer`, `par`, `seq`, `spawn`, `collect_all`, `with`, `reads`, `writes`, `sends`, `receives`, `allocates`, `panics`, `layout`, `distinct`, `type`, `as`, `use`, `mod`, `unsafe`, `extern`, `asm`, `global_asm`, `self`, `Self`, `true`, `false`. Cross-reference each to its introducing design.md section. Mirror the Rust book's split into "currently used" vs "reserved for future." Generate from a single source if possible so drift is caught at build time.

- [x] **Book appendix: Operators and Symbols (P1).** Add `docs/book/src/appendix-b-operators.md` (mirrors Rust book Appendix B). Catalog every operator and punctuation symbol — `+ - * / %` (arithmetic), `== != < <= > >=` (comparison), `&& || !` (logical), `& | ^ ~ << >>` (bitwise), `= += -= *= /= %= &= |= ^= <<= >>=` (assignment), `? ?.` (error propagation), `|>` (pipe, design.md:2479), `..` `..=` (range), `[T]` (generics), `f"..."` (interpolation), `#[...]` (attribute), `//` `///` `/* */` (comments), `->` `=>` `.` `:` `;` `,` `.` — and every Kāra-specific symbol. One row per symbol with name, example, and cross-reference.

- [x] **Book appendix: Derivable Traits (P1).** Add `docs/book/src/appendix-c-derivable-traits.md` (mirrors Rust book Appendix C). List every trait that works under `#[derive(...)]` in Kāra — `Debug`, `Display` (design.md:603), `Eq`, `PartialEq`, `Ord`, `PartialOrd`, `Hash`, `Clone`, `Copy`, `Default`, `Serialize`, `Deserialize` (deferred, design.md:911), plus any Kāra-specific additions. For each: what it generates, the field requirements (e.g., `Eq` requires all fields `Eq`), visibility interaction (design.md:603 — derive operates on all fields regardless of visibility), and known gotchas (e.g., `Copy` not inherited by `distinct type`, design.md:363-ish).

- [x] **Book appendix: Attribute Reference (P1).** Add `docs/book/src/appendix-d-attributes.md`. No Rust book equivalent — Rust scatters attributes through the Reference. Kāra has enough attribute surface (`#[derive]`, `#[must_use]`, `#[repr]`, `#[no_mangle]`, `#[used]`, `#[link_section]`, `#[interrupt]`, `#[gpu]`, `#[cyclic]`, `#[allow]`, `#[distinct]`, `#[generational_fallback]`, `#[export]`, `#[frozen_effects]` — if kept —, `#[serialize]`, `#[max_stack]`, `#[noblock]`) that users need a single reference page. For each: syntax, where it's valid, what it does, cross-reference to the introducing design.md section.

- [ ] **Book: Getting Started / Installation chapter (P1).** Add a chapter covering toolchain install, creating a new project with `kara.toml`, running `karac build` / `karac run` / `karac test`, and IDE setup. Rust book ch1 equivalent. Blocked on the build-tool CLI surface stabilizing (design.md:6036 — package manager deferred to Phase 7-8).

*Items moved to [deferred.md](deferred.md): `#[no_std]`/bare metal (P1), list comprehensions (P1), comptime (P2 — full spec at [deferred.md § Comptime — AST→AST comptime fn](deferred.md#comptime--asttoast-comptime-fn) per v60 item 31). Items already tracked in [design.md § Deferred Items](design.md#deferred-items): channels/atomics.*

- [x] **Compiler queries channel — P0 architectural commit.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. Spec at [`design.md § Specification Layers > Compiler Queries`](../design.md#compiler-queries) (graduated from brainstorm v63, 2026-05-08). Ships the channel infrastructure even with zero query catalogue entries; subsequent P1 entries are non-breaking additions that ride on this floor. Five sub-items, all P0 — all landed:

  1. [x] **Stable item identity — path-based DefId + structural-hash sub-item slots.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. New `src/def_path.rs` with `DefPath`, `SubItemHash`, `QueryId`. `collect_item_def_paths` walks every top-level Item kind and builds the index; `ResolveResult.def_paths: HashMap<String, DefPath>` carries it. Resolver-side map keeps the storage burden at item-level only (no per-AST-node field churn); sub-item slots compute their hash on demand. `SubItemHash::of_expr` is intentionally a stub returning `ROOT` for v1 — the real hashing lands with the first sub-item-addressing catalogue entry (phase-7-codegen.md line 25). Four regression tests in `tests/resolver.rs::def_paths_*` confirm the motivating property: stability under unrelated source insertions and unrelated item renames.

  2. [x] **Per-phase `queries: Vec<CompilerQuery>` field.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. New `src/queries.rs` with `CompilerQuery` struct + `QueryKind` (`non_exhaustive`, ships with one `Stub` placeholder for v1) + `QueryOption` / `Confidence` / `ResolutionSurface` / `Phase`. Empty `queries: Vec<CompilerQuery>` field added to `ResolveResult`, `TypeCheckResult`, `EffectCheckResult`, `OwnershipCheckResult`, `ConcurrencyAnalysis`. Surface lock — adding new `QueryKind` variants or populating queries from any phase is non-breaking; the `non_exhaustive` attribute forces match exhaustiveness handling for unknown variants in tools.

  3. [x] **`karac query queries` CLI surface.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. New `QueryKind::Queries` variant on the CLI enum + dispatch in `cmd_query`. Runs the full pipeline (typecheck → lower → effectcheck → ownershipcheck → concurrencycheck), collates `queries` across every phase result, and emits the JSON envelope on stdout. v1 output is `{"queries":[]}` because no phase populates yet; the empty-only emitter notes if a phase has unexpectedly pushed values so the serializer extension doesn't get skipped. `tests/cli.rs::test_query_queries_empty_envelope` locks the surface; help text lists the new kind. Streaming-mode `phase_queries` event integration deferred to the first P1.x entry that actually populates.

  4. [x] **Attribute extension surface verification.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. Future query-resolving attribute names (`prefer_rc`, `specialize`, `fork_at` — companion to existing `no_rc`) registered in `RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES`. Reserved at v1; semantic enforcement lands with their P1.x catalogue entries. Regression test `tests/resolver.rs::query_resolving_attribute_propagates_through_pipeline_without_diagnostic` confirms `#[specialize(T = i64, mode: "x")]` carrying nested named args parses, attaches to the item, and survives resolve + typecheck + ownership without any diagnostic — verifying the AST shape supports query-resolving attributes without parser changes.

  5. [x] **Multi-resolution conflict diagnostic.** ✓ Landed 2026-05-18. New `ResolveErrorKind::QueryResolutionConflict` variant; new error code `E_QUERY_RESOLUTION_CONFLICT` in the CLI mapper. Conflict-pair registry `QUERY_RESOLUTION_CONFLICT_PAIRS` in `attribute_validator.rs` lists `(cold, inline)` (P1.3 inlining query) and `(no_rc, prefer_rc)` (P1.1 RC-fallback query); both `inline` / `cold` / `likely` / `unlikely` / `inline(never)` added as reserved attribute names. The validator walks each item's attributes, detects conflict pairs, emits one error per (pair × item), anchored at the second attribute's span. Three tests in `tests/resolver.rs::query_resolution_conflict_*` cover both pairs + the negative (single attribute of a pair must not fire).

  *Out of scope for the P0 commit.* Specific query catalogue entries (P1.1–P1.6) are tracked as separate items below and in [`phase-7-codegen.md`](phase-7-codegen.md). Verifier-backed resolution (Alive2-class checks against author claims), runtime feedback into the queries report, and cross-phase deduplication are deferred to post-v1 (see `deferred.md`).

  *Cross-references.* design.md § Specification Layers > Compiler Queries (the spec); design.md § AI-First Compiler Interface > Structured Compiler Output (the JSON output discipline this joins); `src/ownership.rs:360` (P1.1 first decision site); brainstorm archive `brainstorming/archive/v63_llm_compiler_query_channel.md` (full design rationale and prior-art map).

- [ ] **Compiler queries — P1.1: RC fallback at use site.** Resolution surface for the existing RC fallback decision (`src/ownership.rs:360`, `RcFallbackNote`). Reuses the existing diagnostic infrastructure; smallest implementation surface; demonstrates the loop end-to-end. Resolution attribute pair: `#[no_rc]` already exists (per design.md § Feature 4 Part 4); add companion `#[prefer_rc]` per the previously-deferred entry in `deferred.md` (now reframed as a query channel resolution surface — see deferred.md update). Each `RcFallbackNote` emission also pushes a `CompilerQuery` onto the ownership pass result; the query enumerates `{ keep_rc | prefer_rc | no_rc }` with the compiler's rationale per option. Author-resolved annotations remove the query from the next compile's report.

- [ ] **Compiler queries — P1.2: Generic specialization on monomorphization tuple.** The typechecker monomorphization counter (already reportable via `karac query monomorphization`) emits a query at instances with notable instantiation count or bytecode-size impact: "monomorphized 14× for {T = i64, T = i32, ...}; specialize body for any of these?" Resolution: `#[specialize(T = i64)]` (new attribute). First catalogue entry that stress-tests whether the P0 identity scheme handles fan-out queries (one decision site, many monomorphizations) — successful landing validates the identity hash function over multi-instance items.

- [ ] **Compiler queries — P1.4: Effect-set narrowing.** Effect inference at function exit emits a query when the inferred effect set could be narrower if a specific branch were proven unreachable: "inferred effect set is `{reads(file), allocates}` but I could narrow to `{reads(file)}` if the allocation is gated by an unreachable branch — confirm reachable?" Resolution: existing effect declaration on the function (the author's confirmation that the broader set is correct, or a tightened declaration that proves the narrower set). Cleanest demonstrator of the channel's novel value — pure intent question PGO cannot answer.

- [ ] **Compiler queries — P1.5: Layout choice.** Layout validation pass emits a query where layout-block ambiguity exists (SoA vs AoS, field grouping alternatives the cost model considered). Resolution: existing layout-block syntax. Gated on layout-block stability (Phase 7.2 Layout codegen — already shipped).

- [ ] **Compiler queries — P1.6: Auto-concurrency fork threshold.** Concurrency cost model emits a query at fork-decision sites: "I would fork this group at N=64 estimated cost; raise/lower?" Resolution: `#[fork_at(N)]` (new attribute). Gated on the cost model graduating from "unspecified for v1" (per design.md § Reported behavior > Auto-concurrency cost-model decisions) — likely [Phase 11](phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md) at earliest.

- [ ] **Comptime — AST→AST `comptime fn` (post-v1).** Spec lives at [`deferred.md § Comptime — AST→AST comptime fn`](deferred.md#comptime--asttoast-comptime-fn) (v60 item 31, decided 2026-05-02). Four discrete implementation substrates, all post-v1: (1) **Comptime evaluator** — treewalk interpreter over the typed AST, retargeted from the existing Phase 4 interpreter to compile-time invocation; covers value-level computation in `comptime fn` bodies excluding AST/type-as-value work. (2) **`Type` as first-class value + reflection API** — expose the compiler's existing type registry as immutable `Type` values; field/variant/method iteration; size/align queries; the `Type` pseudotype is comptime-only (runtime references emit `E_TYPE_VALUE_AT_RUNTIME`). (3) **AST builder + emission** — stdlib `compiler.ast` module with typed builder API (`ast.expr`, `ast.method`, `ast.impl_block`, etc.) plus quasi-quote shim (`ast.parse_expr(string)`); module-level splicing rules for items returned from comptime fns. (4) **Derive desugaring** — `#[derive(Trait)]` resolves to a `derive_<Trait>` `comptime fn` lookup; built-in derives (`Eq`, `Hash`, `Display`, `Debug`, `Clone`, `Copy`, `PartialEq`, `PartialOrd`, `Ord`, `Arithmetic`, `Serialize`, `Deserialize`) are stdlib `comptime fn`s with no special compiler treatment beyond the lookup convention; user-defined derives use the same mechanism. Each substrate is internally complete on its own — partial deployment never leaks a half-built feature into the v1 language. Effect-system wiring (already pinned in v1 — design.md § Comptime Effect Defaults): `reads(CompileTimeEnv)` / `writes(CompileTimeEnv)` / `allocates(CompileTimeHeap)` permitted; `panics` becomes a build-time diagnostic; runtime resource verbs forbidden via `E_RUNTIME_EFFECT_AT_COMPTIME`. Resource limits (configurable via CLI flags): 2^24 instructions, 512 MiB CompileTimeHeap, 1024 frames recursion. Tooling integration: `karac doc` documents comptime fns with a "comptime" badge; `karac explain --expand <span>` prints post-expansion AST; `karac` debugger sees comptime frames as a dedicated stack; `karac query monomorphization` tracks comptime invocations alongside type/effect tuples. (Post-v1.)
